## User (2026-04-24 14:19:15)

we are trying to prove RH. see paper and work in progress files attached.

YOUR TASK:

Attack UV-023/UV-026 by localizing the first-collision derivative defect.

Context:
The amplitude-weighted non-((1,1)) cubic contribution has the expansion
[
\delta^{-2}\mathcal C_3
=======================

a^3\delta\left(
-3\kappa\mathsf B_3(L,L',L')
----------------------------

\mathsf B_3(L',L',L')
\right)
+O(\delta^2).
]
Here
[
L=L_m,\qquad L'=L_m',
]
and (\mathsf B_3) is the symmetric trilinear polarization of
[
P_3(X)=Q_{7,m}^q(\mathcal T_3(X,X,X)).
]

Target:
Compute the (L_1YR_1) contribution to the first-collision derivative
[
F_1^{(3)}(\kappa)
=================

## -3\kappa\mathsf B_3(L,L',L')

\mathsf B_3(L',L',L')
]
at the matrix/fixed-sector level.

Use the obstruction-covector reduction:
For
[
A=\ell_0I+\ell_1S+\ell_2D,\qquad
B=r_0I+r_1S+r_2D,\qquad
Y=y_0I+y_1S+y_2D+y_3J,
]
define
[
\Theta_{A,B}^{A_5}=(\theta_0,\theta_1,\theta_2,\theta_3)
]
by
[
\theta_0
========

v_5(\ell_0r_0+\ell_1r_1+\ell_2r_2)
-u_5(\ell_1r_0+\ell_0r_1),
]
[
\theta_1
========

v_5(\ell_1r_0+\ell_0r_1)
-u_5(\ell_0r_0+\ell_1r_1-\ell_2r_2),
]
[
\theta_2
========

v_5(\ell_2r_0+\ell_0r_2)
-u_5(\ell_2r_1+\ell_1r_2),
]
[
\theta_3
========

v_5(-\ell_2r_1+\ell_1r_2)
-u_5(-\ell_2r_0+\ell_0r_2).
]
Then the quotient obstruction for (AYB) is
[
y_0\theta_0+y_1\theta_1+y_2\theta_2+y_3\theta_3.
]

What to do:

1. Specialize the (L_1YR_1) obstruction to one source slot (L_m) and two source-derivative slots (L_m').
2. Compute the two quotient Hessians:
   [
   H_1^{L_1YR_1}:=\mathsf B_3^{L_1YR_1}(L,L',L'),
   ]
   [
   H_2^{L_1YR_1}:=\mathsf B_3^{L_1YR_1}(L',L',L').
   ]
3. Form the defect
   [
   D_{L_1YR_1}(\kappa)
   =
   -3\kappa H_1^{L_1YR_1}-H_2^{L_1YR_1}.
   ]
4. Decide whether:

   * (D_{L_1YR_1}(\kappa)=0) by actual coefficient identities;
   * (D_{L_1YR_1}) is canceled by the mirror family or another cubic family;
   * (D_{L_1YR_1}) is nonzero and identifies a missing package correction.

Work before (\Phi_K), before determinant scalarization, before quotient extraction shortcuts, and before diagonal merger. Do not use scalar hiding or one-pair gauge alone.

I’ll attack this as a local algebra problem first, using the uploaded draft/work files only for notation and guardrails. I’ll keep the computation pre-\(\Phi_K\), at the fixed-sector matrix level, and separate “computed” from “still requires actual coefficient tables.”

The key point I can compute without the missing coefficient tables is the exact trilinear specialization. _Thought for 2m 41s_

## Verdict

For the \(L_1YR_1\) family, the first-collision derivative defect is **not zero as a formal fixed-sector identity**. A same-sign mirror family can cancel only the \(J\)-antisymmetric part of the obstruction covector; it does **not** cancel the symmetric \(I,S,D\) channels. So, at this level, \(L_1YR_1\) remains a live UV-023/UV-026 obstruction unless the missing actual coefficient tables force the two scalar identities below, or another cubic family supplies the exact negative defect. This matches the current frontier: \(L_1YR_1\) is still waiting on \([z^r]\Lambda_{i,\pm}\), \([z^s]M_i^{[5]}\), and determinant identities against \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\). 

I use the normalized polarization convention
\[
\mathsf B_3(X,X,X)=P_3(X).
\]
If the paper uses the unnormalized polarization, multiply \(H_1,H_2\) by the same global factor; the zero/cancellation verdict is unchanged.

---

## 1. Fixed-sector specialization

Write the source slot \(L_m\) as
\[
A=\ell_0I+\ell_1S+\ell_2D,\qquad
B=r_0I+r_1S+r_2D,\qquad
Y=y_0I+y_1S+y_2D+y_3J,
\]
and the source-derivative slot \(L_m'\) as
\[
\dot A=\dot\ell_0I+\dot\ell_1S+\dot\ell_2D,\qquad
\dot B=\dot r_0I+\dot r_1S+\dot r_2D,\qquad
\dot Y=\dot y_0I+\dot y_1S+\dot y_2D+\dot y_3J.
\]

Define the obstruction scalar
\[
\mathcal O(A,Y,B)
:=
Y\cdot\Theta_{A,B}^{A_5}
=
\sum_{j=0}^3 y_j\theta_j(A,B).
\]

Set
\[
\alpha:=\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5},\qquad
\beta:=\Theta_{A,\dot B}^{A_5},\qquad
\gamma:=\Theta_{\dot A,B}^{A_5}.
\]

Then explicitly
\[
H_2^{L_1YR_1}
=
\mathsf B_3^{L_1YR_1}(L',L',L')
=
\dot Y\cdot\alpha.
\]

For one source slot and two derivative slots,
\[
H_1^{L_1YR_1}
=
\mathsf B_3^{L_1YR_1}(L,L',L')
=
\frac13\Bigl(
\mathcal O(A,\dot Y,\dot B)
+
\mathcal O(\dot A,Y,\dot B)
+
\mathcal O(\dot A,\dot Y,B)
\Bigr),
\]
hence
\[
H_1^{L_1YR_1}
=
\frac13\Bigl(
\dot Y\cdot\beta
+
Y\cdot\alpha
+
\dot Y\cdot\gamma
\Bigr).
\]

Therefore the localized \(L_1YR_1\) defect is
\[
\boxed{
D_{L_1YR_1}(\kappa)
=
-\kappa\Bigl(
Y\cdot\alpha+\dot Y\cdot(\beta+\gamma)
\Bigr)
-
\dot Y\cdot\alpha.
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
D_{L_1YR_1}(\kappa)
=
-\kappa\,Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}
-\dot Y\cdot
\Bigl(
\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}
+\kappa\Theta_{A,\dot B}^{A_5}
+\kappa\Theta_{\dot A,B}^{A_5}
\Bigr).
}
\]

This is already the localized first-collision derivative defect.

---

## 2. Expanded \(\alpha\)-slot

The pure derivative covector \(\alpha=\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}\) is

\[
\alpha_0
=
v_5(\dot\ell_0\dot r_0+\dot\ell_1\dot r_1+\dot\ell_2\dot r_2)
-
u_5(\dot\ell_1\dot r_0+\dot\ell_0\dot r_1),
\]

\[
\alpha_1
=
v_5(\dot\ell_1\dot r_0+\dot\ell_0\dot r_1)
-
u_5(\dot\ell_0\dot r_0+\dot\ell_1\dot r_1-\dot\ell_2\dot r_2),
\]

\[
\alpha_2
=
v_5(\dot\ell_2\dot r_0+\dot\ell_0\dot r_2)
-
u_5(\dot\ell_2\dot r_1+\dot\ell_1\dot r_2),
\]

\[
\alpha_3
=
v_5(-\dot\ell_2\dot r_1+\dot\ell_1\dot r_2)
-
u_5(-\dot\ell_2\dot r_0+\dot\ell_0\dot r_2).
\]

The \(\beta\) and \(\gamma\) covectors are the same formula with
\[
(\dot A,\dot B)
\mapsto
(A,\dot B)
\quad\text{and}\quad
(\dot A,\dot B)
\mapsto
(\dot A,B).
\]

---

## 3. When can this vanish?

As a polynomial identity in \(\kappa\), the defect vanishes iff

\[
\boxed{
\dot Y\cdot\alpha=0
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
Y\cdot\alpha+\dot Y\cdot(\beta+\gamma)=0.
}
\]

If one wants a stronger identity independent of the actual \(Y,\dot Y\) coefficients, then the vector-level sufficient condition is

\[
\boxed{
\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}=0,
\qquad
\Theta_{A,\dot B}^{A_5}+\Theta_{\dot A,B}^{A_5}=0.
}
\]

Nothing in the obstruction-covector algebra forces either condition. For example, take
\[
u_5=0,\quad v_5=1,\quad
A=\dot A=B=\dot B=I,\quad
Y=\dot Y=I.
\]
Then
\[
\alpha=\beta=\gamma=(1,0,0,0),
\]
so
\[
H_2=1,\qquad H_1=1,
\]
and therefore
\[
D_{L_1YR_1}(\kappa)=-3\kappa-1\neq0.
\]

So this is not a formal zero.

---

## 4. Mirror-family check

Under left/right mirror swap \(A\leftrightarrow B\), the obstruction covector satisfies

\[
\Theta_{A,B}^{A_5}+\Theta_{B,A}^{A_5}
=
2(\theta_0,\theta_1,\theta_2,0),
\]
and
\[
\Theta_{A,B}^{A_5}-\Theta_{B,A}^{A_5}
=
2(0,0,0,\theta_3).
\]

Thus a same-sign mirror \(R_1YL_1\) cancels only the \(J\)-antisymmetric \(\theta_3\) channel. It leaves the \(I,S,D\) channels doubled. An opposite-sign mirror would do the reverse: it would remove \(I,S,D\) but retain \(J\).

Therefore the mirror family does **not** generically cancel \(D_{L_1YR_1}\). Full mirror cancellation would require additional actual coefficient support, such as all surviving \(L_1YR_1\) obstruction living purely in the antisymmetric \(J\)-channel with same-sign mirror pairing, or purely in the symmetric channel with opposite-sign pairing. The current UV-026 setup explicitly requires matrix/fixed-sector work before \(\Phi_K\), determinant scalarization, quotient extraction, or diagonal merger, so that shortcut is not available. 

---

## 5. Classification of the outcome

The local computation gives:

\[
\boxed{
D_{L_1YR_1}(\kappa)
=
-\kappa\Bigl(
Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}
+\dot Y\cdot(\Theta_{A,\dot B}^{A_5}+\Theta_{\dot A,B}^{A_5})
\Bigr)
-
\dot Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}.
}
\]

So:

1. **Not zero by formal coefficient identities.** It is generically nonzero.
2. **Not canceled by the mirror family alone.** The mirror only separates symmetric \(I,S,D\) and antisymmetric \(J\) channels.
3. **Current status: live missing package correction / coefficient gate.** To close UV-023/UV-026 here, the paper needs actual coefficient tables proving
   \[
   \dot Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}=0,
   \qquad
   Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}
   +
   \dot Y\cdot(\Theta_{A,\dot B}^{A_5}+\Theta_{\dot A,B}^{A_5})=0,
   \]
   or another cubic family must contribute exactly
   \[
   +\dot Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}
   +
   \kappa\Bigl(
   Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}
   +
   \dot Y\cdot(\Theta_{A,\dot B}^{A_5}+\Theta_{\dot A,B}^{A_5})
   \Bigr).
   \]

This matches the current paper/work frontier: \(L_1YR_1\) has been reduced to coefficient tables and determinant identities, but those tables are still missing; the source-provenance audit also says the grade \(1/5/1\) cubic matrices and fixed-sector projection are not yet supplied under another notation. turn3file13

## Claim

The accepted \(L_1YR_1\) defect embeds into the seven-family cubic target as a **specific \(C_0/C_1\) obstruction pair**, not as an isolated vanishing target. With the normalization implicit in the accepted formula,

\[
D_{L_1YR_1}(\kappa)=-\kappa C_0^{L_1YR_1}-C_1^{L_1YR_1},
\]

where

\[
\boxed{
C_0^{L_1YR_1}
=
Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}
+
\dot Y\cdot
\left(
\Theta_{A,\dot B}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{\dot A,B}^{A_5}
\right)
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
C_1^{L_1YR_1}
=
\dot Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}.
}
\]

The only plausible formal cancellation route is **aggregate cancellation** across the nonlinear whitening completion, principally \(L_2YR_0+L_0YR_2\), with possible correction from \(L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2\) and pure same-point closure from \(L_3N_0R_0+L_0N_0R_3\). No single mirror or one-pair gauge shortcut is sufficient; current files already record that the seven cubic pre-\(\Phi_K\) families remain live until actual \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\) coefficients are computed. 

## Status: open

The split of \(L_1YR_1\) into \(C_0\) and \(C_1\) is proved from the accepted local formula. The aggregate cancellation is **not proved** by the current paper/work files. The current correct choice among the four options is:

\[
\boxed{\text{C. No formal cancellation exists; actual coefficient tables must prove the two identities.}}
\]

More precisely: option B is the likely positive mechanism if the missing Fréchet identities work, but it is not yet established. Option D is premature because the defect is not yet an actual-package obstruction; it is a formal fixed-sector obstruction awaiting actual coefficient tables.

## Evidence

### 1. Variable map and sign convention

Use the corrected-whitening matrix cross-effect before \(\Phi_K\). Set

\[
A=\Lambda_{-,m}^{[1]},\qquad
B=\Lambda_{+,m}^{[1]},\qquad
Y=M_m^{[5]}.
\]

Here

\[
\Lambda_{-,m}^{[1]}
=
D(G_-^{(0)}{}^{-1/2})[\delta G_{-,m}^{\lin}],
\qquad
\Lambda_{+,m}^{[1]}
=
D(G_+^{(0)}{}^{-1/2})[\delta G_{+,m}^{\lin}],
\]

and \(M_m^{[5]}\) is the normalized grade-5 mixed block input in the same \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\) normalization.

For the collision labels, I use the symmetric convention

\[
X_1(\delta)=X_m+\delta\dot X_m+O(\delta^2),
\qquad
X_2(\delta)=X_m-\delta\dot X_m+O(\delta^2).
\]

Thus

\[
\dot A=\dot\Lambda_{-,m}^{[1]},\qquad
\dot B=\dot\Lambda_{+,m}^{[1]},\qquad
\dot Y=\dot M_m^{[5]}.
\]

If the draft parameterizes the collision by \(h_1=m+\delta/2\), \(h_2=m-\delta/2\), then \(\dot X_m=\frac12\partial_hX_h|_{h=m}\). This rescales \(C_1\) consistently but does not change any quotient-vanishing or cancellation verdict.

The staged UV-025 source block is explicitly pre-whitening and does not assert \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\), \(Q_{7,m}^q\), \(\Pi_{1,1}\), or UV-026 gauge, so the present calculation remains before \(\Phi_K\), determinant scalarization, quotient extraction shortcuts, and diagonal merger. 

### 2. \(L_1YR_1\) contribution

Let

\[
\alpha:=\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5},\qquad
\beta:=\Theta_{A,\dot B}^{A_5},\qquad
\gamma:=\Theta_{\dot A,B}^{A_5}.
\]

Then

\[
H_1^{L_1YR_1}
=
\mathsf B_3^{L_1YR_1}(L,L',L')
=
\frac13
\left(
Y\cdot\alpha+\dot Y\cdot(\beta+\gamma)
\right),
\]

and

\[
H_2^{L_1YR_1}
=
\mathsf B_3^{L_1YR_1}(L',L',L')
=
\dot Y\cdot\alpha.
\]

Since

\[
D_{L_1YR_1}(\kappa)
=
-3\kappa H_1^{L_1YR_1}
-
H_2^{L_1YR_1},
\]

we get the clean split

\[
\boxed{
C_0^{L_1YR_1}=3H_1^{L_1YR_1}
=
Y\cdot\alpha+\dot Y\cdot(\beta+\gamma)
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
C_1^{L_1YR_1}=H_2^{L_1YR_1}
=
\dot Y\cdot\alpha.
}
\]

So the two scalar defects to kill are exactly

\[
\boxed{
\dot Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}
+
\dot Y\cdot
\left(
\Theta_{A,\dot B}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{\dot A,B}^{A_5}
\right).
}
\]

### 3. Aggregate seven-family embedding

Define the scalar obstruction pairing

\[
\mathcal S(P,Z,Q):=Z\cdot\Theta_{P,Q}^{A_5}.
\]

Let \(L_0,R_0,N_0\) denote the baseline left inverse-square-root, right inverse-square-root, and middle block. Let \(\mathcal L_1,\mathcal L_2,\mathcal L_3\) be the first, second, and third Fréchet outputs of the left inverse-square-root map, and \(\mathcal R_1,\mathcal R_2,\mathcal R_3\) the right analogues. With the same polarization normalization,

\[
A=\mathcal L_1(L),\quad \dot A=\mathcal L_1(L'),\quad
B=\mathcal R_1(L),\quad \dot B=\mathcal R_1(L').
\]

The other six families contribute to \(C_0,C_1\) schematically as follows.

For \(L_2YR_0\),

\[
C_0^{L_2YR_0}
=
\mathcal S(\mathcal L_2(L',L'),Y,R_0)
+
2\mathcal S(\mathcal L_2(L,L'),\dot Y,R_0),
\]

\[
C_1^{L_2YR_0}
=
\mathcal S(\mathcal L_2(L',L'),\dot Y,R_0).
\]

For \(L_0YR_2\),

\[
C_0^{L_0YR_2}
=
\mathcal S(L_0,Y,\mathcal R_2(L',L'))
+
2\mathcal S(L_0,\dot Y,\mathcal R_2(L,L')),
\]

\[
C_1^{L_0YR_2}
=
\mathcal S(L_0,\dot Y,\mathcal R_2(L',L')).
\]

For \(L_2N_0R_1\),

\[
C_0^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
\mathcal S(\mathcal L_2(L',L'),N_0,\mathcal R_1(L))
+
2\mathcal S(\mathcal L_2(L,L'),N_0,\mathcal R_1(L')),
\]

\[
C_1^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
\mathcal S(\mathcal L_2(L',L'),N_0,\mathcal R_1(L')).
\]

For \(L_1N_0R_2\),

\[
C_0^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
\mathcal S(\mathcal L_1(L),N_0,\mathcal R_2(L',L'))
+
2\mathcal S(\mathcal L_1(L'),N_0,\mathcal R_2(L,L')),
\]

\[
C_1^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
\mathcal S(\mathcal L_1(L'),N_0,\mathcal R_2(L',L')).
\]

For \(L_3N_0R_0\),

\[
C_0^{L_3N_0R_0}
=
3\mathcal S(\mathcal L_3(L,L',L'),N_0,R_0),
\]

\[
C_1^{L_3N_0R_0}
=
\mathcal S(\mathcal L_3(L',L',L'),N_0,R_0).
\]

For \(L_0N_0R_3\),

\[
C_0^{L_0N_0R_3}
=
3\mathcal S(L_0,N_0,\mathcal R_3(L,L',L')),
\]

\[
C_1^{L_0N_0R_3}
=
\mathcal S(L_0,N_0,\mathcal R_3(L',L',L')).
\]

These formulae identify exactly where the \(L_1YR_1\) defect can go.

### 4. Likely cancellation partners

The first required cancellation is

\[
C_1^{\mathrm{rest}}
=
-\dot Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}.
\]

The only families with an explicit \(\dot Y\) channel are

\[
L_2YR_0,\qquad L_0YR_2.
\]

So the minimal direct \(C_1\) cancellation identity is the vector identity

\[
\boxed{
\Theta_{\mathcal L_2(L',L'),R_0}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{L_0,\mathcal R_2(L',L')}^{A_5}
=
-\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}.
}
\]

If this identity holds, then \(L_2YR_0+L_0YR_2\) cancels the whole \(C_1^{L_1YR_1}\) defect.

The second required cancellation is

\[
C_0^{\mathrm{rest}}
=
-
Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}
-
\dot Y\cdot
\left(
\Theta_{A,\dot B}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{\dot A,B}^{A_5}
\right).
\]

The same direct \(Y\)-families would cancel the first part if

\[
\boxed{
\Theta_{\mathcal L_2(L',L'),R_0}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{L_0,\mathcal R_2(L',L')}^{A_5}
=
-\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}.
}
\]

They cancel the \(\dot Y\)-part if the mixed second-Fréchet identity

\[
\boxed{
2\Theta_{\mathcal L_2(L,L'),R_0}^{A_5}
+
2\Theta_{L_0,\mathcal R_2(L,L')}^{A_5}
=
-
\left(
\Theta_{A,\dot B}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{\dot A,B}^{A_5}
\right)
}
\]

also holds.

Thus \(L_2YR_0+L_0YR_2\) are the primary cancellation candidates.

The next pair,

\[
L_2N_0R_1,\qquad L_1N_0R_2,
\]

does not carry explicit \(Y,\dot Y\) as middle-slot data. It can still participate if the actual corrected-block coefficient tables identify the grade-5 side-block terms inside \(\mathcal L_2\) or \(\mathcal R_2\) with the grade-5 mixed input \(M^{[5]}\). In other words, these families can complete the whitening identity, but they do not by themselves carry the literal negative of

\[
\dot Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}
\]

unless the missing side-vs-middle grade-5 coefficient identity is proved.

The pure same-point pair,

\[
L_3N_0R_0,\qquad L_0N_0R_3,
\]

has no explicit \(Y\) channel. It cannot be the direct cancellation partner for the two displayed \(Y,\dot Y\) scalar defects. It can only cancel residual side-only terms introduced by the nonlinear inverse-square-root completion. This matches the current frontier: all-left/all-right families reduce to third-Fréchet coefficient identities and are not closed by generic source support or one-pair laws. 

## Exact refs

The relevant current-file facts are:

- The active UV-026 target is the actual-package cubic gauge theorem for non-\((1,1)\) type \((1,1,5)\) terms before \(\Phi_K\), requiring proportionality to \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\), not scalar invisibility. 
- The seven-family list is complete at the current working frontier, and current source only proves gauge/vanishing after a term is identified as one-pair \(K_5\), \(K_3\), or pure. 
- The \(L_1YR_1\) gate is already reduced to \([z^r]\Lambda_{i,\pm}\), \([z^s]M_i^{[5]}\), and determinant identities for \(C_{112}^{L_1YR_1}\), \(C_{122}^{L_1YR_1}\); those tables are still missing. 
- \(L_2YR_0/L_0YR_2\) are currently classified as needing second-Fréchet plus mixed-input coefficient identities, not as already source-trivial or gauge. 
- The staged UV-025 source block is only a tagged pre-whitening source lift and explicitly does not prove \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\), \(Q_{7,m}^q\), \(\Pi_{1,1}\), or the UV-026 cubic gauge theorem.

in \(\mathcal Q_m=\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\).

in \(\mathcal Q_m\), using actual coefficient tables.

The direct cancellation candidate is \(L_2YR_0+L_0YR_2\); the side-completion pairs \(L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2\) and \(L_3N_0R_0+L_0N_0R_3\) are secondary aggregate partners. ## Classification of cancellation channels

### \(C_2^{L_1YR_1}\): even-Hessian cancellation channel

The \(C_2\) piece has the structure

\[
-\Bigl(
Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}
+
\dot Y\cdot(\Theta_{A,\dot B}^{A_5}+\Theta_{\dot A,B}^{A_5})
\Bigr).
\]

This is an **even Hessian-type** obstruction: it contains two collision derivatives distributed across the two endpoint factors, plus first-derivative transport of the middle \(Y\)-slot against one differentiated endpoint.

The likely cancellation families are therefore:

\[
\boxed{
L_2YR_0,\qquad L_0YR_2
}
\]

as the primary pair, because their second-Fréchet endpoint Hessians can directly produce the negative of

\[
Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}
\]

and their mixed \(L,L'\) second-Fréchet terms can produce the negative of

\[
\dot Y\cdot(\Theta_{A,\dot B}^{A_5}+\Theta_{\dot A,B}^{A_5}).
\]

The required schematic identity is

\[
C_2^{L_2YR_0+L_0YR_2}
=
+
\Bigl(
Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}
+
\dot Y\cdot(\Theta_{A,\dot B}^{A_5}+\Theta_{\dot A,B}^{A_5})
\Bigr)
\quad\text{in }\mathcal Q_m.
\]

Secondary completion may come from

\[
\boxed{
L_2N_0R_1,\qquad L_1N_0R_2
}
\]

if the actual whitening identity couples endpoint Hessians with baseline-middle transport. These are not the direct \(Y\)-carriers, but they can modify the endpoint-Hessian contribution that \(L_2YR_0+L_0YR_2\) alone supplies.

The pure same-point third-Fréchet terms

\[
L_3N_0R_0,\qquad L_0N_0R_3
\]

are not natural \(C_2\) cancellers unless the even-Hessian identity is being packaged through a higher-order inverse-square-root completion. They are tertiary for \(C_2\).

### \(C_3^{L_1YR_1}\): odd third-derivative / amplitude-character channel

The \(C_3\) piece is

\[
\frac12\,\dot Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}.
\]

This is the **odd amplitude-character** part: all three active slots are differentiated once. In collision notation, it is the fully odd \((\dot A,\dot Y,\dot B)\) component of the cubic package.

The direct cancellation target is

\[
C_3^{\mathrm{rest}}
=
-\frac12\,\dot Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}.
\]

The most natural carriers are not merely \(L_2YR_0/L_0YR_2\), but the aggregate odd-completion families:

\[
\boxed{
L_2YR_0,\quad L_0YR_2,\quad L_2N_0R_1,\quad L_1N_0R_2
}
\]

because the odd third-derivative character can arise from differentiating a second-Fréchet endpoint term once more along the collision direction, or from coupling a second-Fréchet endpoint correction with a first-Fréchet correction on the other side.

The pure same-point third-Fréchet pair

\[
\boxed{
L_3N_0R_0,\qquad L_0N_0R_3
}
\]

is also a serious \(C_3\) candidate, because \(C_3\) is exactly where third-Fréchet endpoint completion naturally lives. These terms are less likely to cancel the literal \(\dot Y\)-middle expression by themselves, but they can cancel the residual odd amplitude-character after the \(L_2Y/L_0YR_2\) and \(L_2N_0R_1/L_1N_0R_2\) pairs are combined.

C_2^{L_1YR_1}
\text{ should be assigned to the even-Hessian cancellation problem.}

Primary cancellation partner:

## Assistant (2026-04-24 14:31:07)

I’m going to test the proposed identity at the Fréchet-calculus level rather than by symmetry. A scalar/commutative specialization is enough to refute a universal identity if it fails there.

_Thought for 53s_

Claim

The direct \(Y\)-carrying second-Fréchet identity

\[
\Theta_{\mathcal L_2(L',L'),R_0}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{L_0,\mathcal R_2(L',L')}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}
=0
\]

is **false as a formal Fréchet-calculus identity**. It already fails in the scalar diagonal base specialization \(G_0=I\). Therefore \(L_2YR_0+L_0YR_2\) alone does **not** cancel the \(Y\cdot\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}\) piece of \(C_2^{L_1YR_1}\).

The mixed derivative identity

\[
2\Theta_{\mathcal L_2(L,L'),R_0}^{A_5}
+
2\Theta_{L_0,\mathcal R_2(L,L')}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{A,\dot B}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{\dot A,B}^{A_5}
=0
\]

is likewise **not forced by second-Fréchet calculus alone**. It can hold only after including the missing baseline-middle completion families

\[
L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2,
\]

or after imposing actual coefficient-table identities not present in the current source. Current work already records that \(L_2YR_0/L_0YR_2\) require second-Fréchet plus mixed-input coefficient data, and that generic matrix algebra does not force the needed \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-gauge relation. 

Status: rejected for the direct \(L_2YR_0+L_0YR_2\) identity; open for the completed \(L_2Y/L_0YR_2 + L_2N_0R_1/L_1N_0R_2\) identity.

Evidence

Let

\[
F(G)=G^{-1/2}.
\]

At a diagonal base

\[
G_0=\lambda_+P_+ + \lambda_-P_-,
\]

the Fréchet derivatives are given by divided differences:

\[
DF_{G_0}[E]_{ij}
=
f^{[1]}(\lambda_i,\lambda_j)E_{ij},
\qquad
f(x)=x^{-1/2},
\]

and

\[
D^2F_{G_0}[E,F]_{ij}
=
\sum_k
f^{[2]}(\lambda_i,\lambda_k,\lambda_j)
\bigl(E_{ik}F_{kj}+F_{ik}E_{kj}\bigr).
\]

In the \(I,S,D,J\) convention, for symmetric fixed-sector inputs

\[
E=e_0I+e_1S+e_2D,\qquad
F=f_0I+f_1S+f_2D,
\]

this formula preserves the \(I,S,D\) sector. A \(J\)-component can only enter from noncommutative ordered products or antisymmetric commutator pieces; the even second-Fréchet symmetric expression itself is an \(I,S,D\)-sector object.

Now specialize further to the scalar diagonal base \(G_0=I\). Then

\[
DF_I[E]=-\frac12E,
\]

and

\[
D^2F_I[E,F]
=
\frac38(EF+FE).
\]

If \(\mathcal L_2\) denotes the Taylor quadratic coefficient, then

\[
\mathcal L_2(E,E)=\frac38E^2.
\]

If instead \(\mathcal L_2\) denotes the raw second Fréchet derivative, multiply the displayed \(\mathcal L_2\)-terms by \(2\). The conclusion below is unchanged.

Take the simplest legal fixed-sector test:

\[
L'=I,\qquad
R_0=L_0=I.
\]

Then

\[
\dot A=\mathcal L_1(L')=-\frac12I,\qquad
\dot B=\mathcal R_1(L')=-\frac12I,
\]

and

\[
\mathcal L_2(L',L')=\frac38I,\qquad
\mathcal R_2(L',L')=\frac38I.
\]

For any \(a,b\),

\[
\Theta_{aI,bI}^{A_5}
=
ab\,(v_5,\,-u_5,\,0,\,0).
\]

Therefore

\[
\Theta_{\mathcal L_2(L',L'),R_0}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{L_0,\mathcal R_2(L',L')}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}
\]

equals

\[
\left(\frac38+\frac38+\frac14\right)(v_5,-u_5,0,0)
=
(v_5,-u_5,0,0),
\]

not zero unless \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\), which is precisely the excluded/good-patch rank-jump case.

So the first direct \(Y\)-carrying identity is false even before any noncommutative complication.

The same scalar test also refutes the mixed identity in its direct \(L_2Y/L_0YR_2\)-only form. Take \(L=L'=I\). Then

\[
A=\dot A=B=\dot B=-\frac12I,
\qquad
\mathcal L_2(L,L')=\mathcal R_2(L,L')=\frac38I
\]

under the same Taylor-coefficient convention. Hence

\[
2\Theta_{\mathcal L_2(L,L'),R_0}^{A_5}
+
2\Theta_{L_0,\mathcal R_2(L,L')}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{A,\dot B}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{\dot A,B}^{A_5}
\]

equals

\[
\left(
2\cdot\frac38
+
2\cdot\frac38
+
\frac14
+
\frac14
\right)(v_5,-u_5,0,0)
=
2(v_5,-u_5,0,0),
\]

again nonzero generically.

Thus the direct even-Hessian cancellation does not hold.

Exact refs

The current UV ledger states that UV-026’s \(L_2YR_0/L_0YR_2\) subtarget is still to classify these terms via actual second-Fréchet inverse-square-root identities coupled to the grade-one/grade-five mixed input; it is not already proved by formal calculus. 

The findings file likewise records that UV-026 reduces to seven pre-\(\Phi_K\) whitening families and that \(L_2YR_0/L_0YR_2\) need second-Fréchet plus mixed-input identities; current source only gives gauge/vanishing after one-pair \(K_5/K_3\) or pure identification. 

The collation further records that the \(L_2YR_0/L_0YR_2\) formal witness has nonzero determinant against \(A_5=(2,5)\), so generic matrix algebra does not force the quotient-gauge identity. 

Dependencies

The exact residuals are therefore not zero. They are:

\[
\boxed{
R_{C_2}^{Y}
=
\Theta_{\mathcal L_2(L',L'),R_0}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{L_0,\mathcal R_2(L',L')}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5}.
}
\]

In the scalar-base Taylor-coefficient normalization, the obstruction test gives

\[
R_{C_2}^{Y}

(v_5,-u_5,0,0)
\]

for \(L'=I\). In raw-\(D^2\) normalization the coefficient changes, but it remains nonzero.

The mixed residual is

\[
\boxed{
R_{C_2}^{\dot Y}
=
2\Theta_{\mathcal L_2(L,L'),R_0}^{A_5}
+
2\Theta_{L_0,\mathcal R_2(L,L')}^{A_5}

\Theta_{A,\dot B}^{A_5}

In the same scalar test \(L=L'=I\),

R_{C_2}^{\dot Y}

2(v_5,-u_5,0,0)

under Taylor-coefficient normalization.

\[

\[
\boxed{
C_{2,Y}^{L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2}

-Y\cdot R_{C_2}^{Y}
\quad \text{in }\mathcal Q_m,

\[
\boxed{

-\dot Y\cdot R_{C_2}^{\dot Y}
\quad \text{in }\mathcal Q_m.
}
\]

More concretely, the missing coefficient theorem must identify the grade-5 contribution hidden inside the baseline-middle families with the same \(M^{[5]}\) normalization used in \(L_1YR_1\). Symbolically, one needs a relation of the form

\[
\Theta_{\mathcal L_2^{\{1,5\}}(\cdot,\cdot),R_1^{\{1\}}}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{L_1^{\{1\}},\mathcal R_2^{\{1,5\}}(\cdot,\cdot)}^{A_5}
=
-
R_{C_2}^{Y/\dot Y},
\]

with the braces indicating the finite-order source grades, not a new family.

Strongest objection

The scalar-base refutation proves only that the **direct** \(L_2YR_0+L_0YR_2\) identity is false. It does not refute the completed whitening identity after \(L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2\) are included. In fact, the failure pattern is exactly what one expects from differentiating the whitening constraint: the second derivative of \(G^{-1/2}\) alone does not cancel the \(L_1YR_1\) term; the baseline-middle terms are needed because the inverse-square-root map is tied to the same-point Gram block, not to a free middle \(Y\)-slot.

Needed for promotion

To promote \(C_2\), the paper needs one of the following:

1. A coefficient-level theorem proving

\[
R_{C_2}^{Y}=0,\qquad R_{C_2}^{\dot Y}=0
\]

after actual source normalization. The formal scalar test says this cannot be true for unconstrained inputs, so this would need a nontrivial actual-package constraint.

2. More plausibly, a completed second-Fréchet whitening identity:

\[
C_2^{L_2YR_0+L_0YR_2}
+
C_2^{L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2}
=
-C_2^{L_1YR_1}
\quad\text{in }\mathcal Q_m.
\]

3. A counterexample from actual coefficient tables showing the completed identity also fails. In that case the even-Hessian obstruction is live and UV-026 cannot remain a pure gauge theorem without an additional package counterterm.

Honest verdict

The direct \(L_2YR_0+L_0YR_2\) second-Fréchet identities are false. The failure is already visible at \(G_0=I\), \(L'=I\), before \(\Phi_K\), before determinant scalarization, and before any diagonal-merger assumption. The \(C_2\) problem therefore moves to the completed second-Fréchet whitening identity involving

\[
L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2.
\]

So the correct classification is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Direct }L_2YR_0+L_0YR_2\text{ cancellation: rejected.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Completed }L_2Y/L_0YR_2+L_2N_0R_1/L_1N_0R_2\text{ cancellation: open.}
}
\]

Do not move to \(C_3\) yet. The next exact target is the baseline-middle completion identity for \(R_{C_2}^{Y}\) and \(R_{C_2}^{\dot Y}\).

## Assistant (2026-04-24 14:33:52)

The direct \(L_2Y/L_0YR_2\) failure has the right shape: it is exactly the failure of differentiating the inverse-square-root factors without the baseline-middle product rule terms. I’ll test whether the \(N_0\) terms close that product-rule defect or whether they need an additional \(N_0\!\to Y\) coefficient theorem.

_Thought for 2m 4s_

Claim

The completed \(C_2\)-level identity is **not a formal consequence** of the inverse-square-root Fréchet calculus with \(N_0\) held as a baseline middle factor. The \(N_0\)-families

\[
L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2
\]

do produce the right **second-Fréchet product-rule type** terms, but they do **not literally produce the \(Y,\dot Y\) channels** needed to cancel

\[
-Y\cdot R_{C_2}^{Y}
-\dot Y\cdot R_{C_2}^{\dot Y}.
\]

So the completed \(C_2\) cancellation is **conditional** on a missing coefficient theorem identifying the grade-5 side contribution hidden in the \(N_0\)-families with the \(M^{[5]}\) / \(Y\)-slot contribution in the same \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\) normalization.

Status: open; direct formal cancellation rejected; conditional completion possible only with a missing \(N_0\)-to-\(Y\) grade-5 coefficient identity.

Evidence

Let

\[
\mathcal S_{201}(h_a,h_b,h_c)
=
\mathsf L_2[h_a,h_b]\,N_0\,\mathsf R_1[h_c],
\]

\[
\mathcal S_{102}(h_a,h_b,h_c)
=
\mathsf L_1[h_a]\,N_0\,\mathsf R_2[h_b,h_c].
\]

Use the reduced \(C_2\) operator

\[
\mathcal C_2^{\mathrm{red}}=-\sum_{i<j}D_iD_j.
\]

For \(\mathcal S_{201}\), since \(\mathsf L_2\) is symmetric bilinear and \(\mathsf R_1\) is linear,

\[
\mathcal C_2^{\mathrm{red}}\mathcal S_{201}
=
-\mathsf L_2[L',L']\,N_0\,\mathsf R_1[L]
-
2\mathsf L_2[L,L']\,N_0\,\mathsf R_1[L'].
\]

Using

\[
B=\mathsf R_1[L],
\qquad
\dot B=\mathsf R_1[L'],
\]

this contributes, in obstruction-covector form,

\[
\boxed{
C_2^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
-
N_0\cdot
\left(
\Theta_{\mathsf L_2(L',L'),B}^{A_5}
+
2\Theta_{\mathsf L_2(L,L'),\dot B}^{A_5}
\right).
}
\]

Similarly,

\[
\mathcal C_2^{\mathrm{red}}\mathcal S_{102}
=
-\mathsf L_1[L]\,N_0\,\mathsf R_2[L',L']
-
2\mathsf L_1[L']\,N_0\,\mathsf R_2[L,L'],
\]

so with

\[
A=\mathsf L_1[L],
\qquad
\dot A=\mathsf L_1[L'],
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
C_2^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
-
N_0\cdot
\left(
\Theta_{A,\mathsf R_2(L',L')}^{A_5}
+
2\Theta_{\dot A,\mathsf R_2(L,L')}^{A_5}
\right).
}
\]

Therefore the completed \(N_0\)-family contribution is

\[
\boxed{
C_2^{N_0\text{-comp}}
=
-
N_0\cdot
\Bigl[
\Theta_{\mathsf L_2(L',L'),B}^{A_5}
+
2\Theta_{\mathsf L_2(L,L'),\dot B}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{A,\mathsf R_2(L',L')}^{A_5}
+
2\Theta_{\dot A,\mathsf R_2(L,L')}^{A_5}
\Bigr].
}
\]

This is the exact output of the reduced \(C_2\) operator on

\[
L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2.
\]

The target it must equal is

\[
-Y\cdot R_{C_2}^{Y}
-
\dot Y\cdot R_{C_2}^{\dot Y},
\]

where

\[
R_{C_2}^{Y}
=
\Theta_{\mathsf L_2(L',L'),R_0}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{L_0,\mathsf R_2(L',L')}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{\dot A,\dot B}^{A_5},
\]

\[
R_{C_2}^{\dot Y}
=
2\Theta_{\mathsf L_2(L,L'),R_0}^{A_5}
+
2\Theta_{L_0,\mathsf R_2(L,L')}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{A,\dot B}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{\dot A,B}^{A_5}.
\]

These are not the same formal type. The \(N_0\)-families pair \(N_0\) against covectors involving \((B,\dot B,A,\dot A)\). The target pairs \(Y,\dot Y\) against residual covectors involving \((R_0,L_0)\) and \((\dot A,\dot B)\). Thus there is no literal formal cancellation unless \(Y,\dot Y\) are identified with grade-5 pieces hidden inside the \(N_0\)-family coefficient extraction.

This matches the current frontier: UV-026 remains a seven-family pre-\(\Phi_K\) coefficient problem, and the source only gives gauge/vanishing after a family has been identified as one-pair \(K_5\), \(K_3\), or pure; these general cubic whitening families are not yet classified. 

Exact refs

The uploaded ledger states that the \(L_2YR_0/L_0YR_2\) families remain open and require second-Fréchet outputs plus \(M_i^{[1]}\), \(M_i^{[5]}\) mixed-input lists; generic matrix algebra does not force gauge. 

The UV ledger states UV-026’s active subtargets still require coefficient lists for Fréchet inverse-square-root outputs and grade-5 mixed blocks, plus second-Fréchet identities for \(L_2YR_0/L_0YR_2\). 

The staged UV-025 block is explicitly pre-whitening and explicitly does **not** assert \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\), \(Q_{7,m}^q\), \(\Pi_{1,1}\), or the cubic \((1,1,5)\) \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-gauge theorem. 

Dependencies

The missing source identity is not just a Fréchet identity for \(G^{-1/2}\). It is a grade-5 coefficient-identification theorem.

A precise form is:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
&
N_0\cdot
\Bigl[
\Theta_{\mathsf L_2(L',L'),B}^{A_5}
+
2\Theta_{\mathsf L_2(L,L'),\dot B}^{A_5}
+
\Theta_{A,\mathsf R_2(L',L')}^{A_5}
+
2\Theta_{\dot A,\mathsf R_2(L,L')}^{A_5}
\Bigr]
\\
&\qquad =
Y\cdot R_{C_2}^{Y}
+
\dot Y\cdot R_{C_2}^{\dot Y}
\quad\text{in }\mathcal Q_m.
\end{aligned}
}
\]

Equivalently, the paper needs to prove that the grade-5 contribution hidden in

\[
\mathsf L_2^{\{1,5\}}N_0\mathsf R_1^{\{1\}}
+
\mathsf L_1^{\{1\}}N_0\mathsf R_2^{\{1,5\}}
\]

is the same \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\)-normalized object as the explicit mixed-block slot

\[
M^{[5]}=Y.
\]

In compressed wording:

\[
\boxed{
\text{hidden grade-5 side contribution from }N_0\text{-families}
=
M^{[5]}\text{ in the same }B_7^{\mathfrak f}\text{ normalization.}
}
\]

Without that theorem, \(N_0\) is merely a baseline middle factor and cannot cancel arbitrary \(Y,\dot Y\)-slot residuals.

Scalar-base test with \(N_0\)-families included

Take the same scalar base as before:

\[
G_0=I,\qquad N_0=I,\qquad L=L'=I.
\]

Then

\[
\mathsf L_1[I]=\mathsf R_1[I]=-\frac12 I,
\qquad
\mathsf L_2[I,I]=\mathsf R_2[I,I]=\frac38 I
\]

under Taylor-coefficient normalization.

The \(N_0\)-completion contributes

\[
C_2^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
-\left[
\Theta_{\frac38 I,-\frac12 I}^{A_5}
+
2\Theta_{\frac38 I,-\frac12 I}^{A_5}
\right]\cdot I
=
+\frac{9}{16}\,(v_5,-u_5,0,0)\cdot I,
\]

and

\[
C_2^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
+\frac{9}{16}\,(v_5,-u_5,0,0)\cdot I.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
C_2^{N_0\text{-comp}}
=
\frac98\,(v_5,-u_5,0,0)\cdot I.
}
\]

The prior direct residuals were

\[
R_{C_2}^{Y}=(v_5,-u_5,0,0),
\]

\[
R_{C_2}^{\dot Y}=2(v_5,-u_5,0,0)
\]

in the same scalar test.

The \(N_0\)-completion therefore does **not** cancel those residuals as a formal identity. It has no independent \(Y\) or \(\dot Y\) dependence. Even if one artificially sets \(Y=\dot Y=N_0=I\), the reduced-operator scalar coefficient does not give the required negative coefficient. The coefficient mismatch is less important than the structural mismatch: \(N_0\)-terms cannot cancel arbitrary \(Y,\dot Y\)-residuals unless a grade-5 source identity ties those slots together.

If the full operator

\[
\frac38D^2-\sum_{i<j}D_iD_j
\]

is retained, extra diagonal-gauge terms enter, but they still do not create literal \(Y,\dot Y\) channels. They can only help after the same missing \(N_0\)-to-\(Y\) coefficient theorem is supplied.

Strongest objection

The scalar-base refutation treats \(Y,\dot Y\) as independent from \(N_0\). In the actual source package they may not be independent: \(M^{[5]}\) may be tied to the grade-5 same-point perturbations entering \(\mathsf L_2^{\{1,5\}}\) and \(\mathsf R_2^{\{1,5\}}\). If such a coefficient theorem exists, the completed \(C_2\) identity could still hold.

But that theorem is not formal Fréchet calculus. It is a source-normalization theorem at the \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\) coefficient level. The current files classify exactly this kind of coefficient data as still missing. turn8file10

Needed for promotion

To promote the completed \(C_2\) cancellation, one must prove the coefficient identity

\[
\boxed{
C_2^{L_2YR_0+L_0YR_2}
+
C_2^{L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2}
=
-C_2^{L_1YR_1}
\quad\text{in }\mathcal Q_m
}
\]

by showing, before \(\Phi_K\), that

\[
\boxed{
C_2^{L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2}
=
-Y\cdot R_{C_2}^{Y}
-
\dot Y\cdot R_{C_2}^{\dot Y}.
}
\]

The exact missing finite-order theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^7]
\left(
\mathsf L_2^{\{1,5\}}N_0\mathsf R_1^{\{1\}}
+
\mathsf L_1^{\{1\}}N_0\mathsf R_2^{\{1,5\}}
\right)
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^7]
\left(
\text{the corresponding }M^{[5]}\text{-middle-slot correction}
\right)
}
\]

modulo \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\), with the same source tags and the same \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\) normalization.

Honest verdict

The completed \(C_2\) identity is not proved by inverse-square-root Fréchet calculus alone. The \(N_0\)-families produce the right kind of product-rule completion terms, but they do not literally produce the \(Y,\dot Y\) channels required to cancel the accepted residuals. The scalar-base test remains nonzero after adding \(L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2\) unless one imposes an additional source-normalization identity tying the hidden grade-5 \(N_0\)-family contribution to \(M^{[5]}\).

Classification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Completed }C_2\text{ cancellation is conditional on a missing }N_0\text{-to-}Y\text{ grade-5 coefficient identity.}
}
\]

Do not move to \(C_3\) yet. The next target is that exact \(N_0\)-to-\(M^{[5]}\) coefficient theorem in \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\) normalization.

## Assistant (2026-04-24 14:39:26)

The source variables force a sharper conclusion: \(M^{[5]}\) is a mixed-block Taylor coefficient in \((d_-,d_+,\eta)\), while the \(N_0\)-completion uses same-point grade-\((1,5)\) Fréchet data from \((d_\pm,e_\pm,g_\pm)\). Those are not identical by definition; a real coefficient theorem is needed.

_Thought for 51s_

Claim

The missing \(N_0\)-to-\(M^{[5]}\) source-normalization theorem is **not currently proved by the corrected block variables**. The actual source formulas show that

\[
M^{[5]}
\]

is a grade-5 coefficient of the **linearized mixed block** in the variables

\[
d_-,d_+,\eta
\quad\text{or equivalently}\quad
U_-,U_+,V,
\]

while the \(N_0\)-family side contribution is built from grade-\((1,5)\) pieces of the **same-point inverse-square-root Fréchet calculus**, involving

\[
d_\pm,e_\pm,g_\pm
\quad\text{or equivalently}\quad
U_\pm,E_\pm,G_\pm.
\]

Those two objects are not identical by definition. They can be equal only after a finite coefficient theorem ties the mixed-block \(V,U_-,U_+\) contribution to the same-point \(U_\pm,E_\pm,G_\pm\) contribution in the same \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\) normalization.

Status: open.

The source identity is neither proved nor refuted by the current draft. The scalar-base free-symbol counterexample is no longer decisive once \(Y,\dot Y,N_0\) are constrained by actual source variables, but the current source does not supply the coefficient tables needed to check the constrained identity.

Evidence

The canonical tagged source block defines the two-atom pre-whitening perturbation by additive substitution into

\[
d_\pm,\quad e_\pm,\quad g_\pm,\quad \eta,
\]

with

\[
q_{2,\pm}=q_{0,\pm}+d_\pm^{(2)},\qquad
q'_{2,\pm}=q'_{0,\pm}+e_\pm^{(2)},\qquad
q''_{2,\pm}=q''_{0,\pm}+g_\pm^{(2)},\qquad
\Delta_2=\Delta_0+\eta^{(2)}.
\]

It explicitly remains pre-whitening and does not assert \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\), \(Q_{7,m}^q\), \(\Pi_{1,1}\), or the UV-026 gauge theorem. 

The one-pair kernels are

\[
d_\pm(z)=\frac{z^2}{Q^4}U_\pm(z),\qquad
e_\pm(z)=\frac{z}{Q^2}E_\pm(z),
\]

\[
g_\pm(z)=G_\pm(z),\qquad
\eta(z)=\frac{z^3}{Q^6}V(z).
\]

From the corrected mixed-block formula, the linearized mixed perturbation has entries of the following form, up to the fixed \(\mathfrak D_Q\) normalization:

\[
\delta N_{11}^{\lin}
=
-\frac{2}{\pi s}\cos\Delta_0\,\eta,
\]

\[
\delta N_{12}^{\lin}
=
\frac{1}{\pi s^2}
\left(
\cos\Delta_0\,\eta
+
s\cos\Delta_0\,d_+
-
q_{0,+}s\sin\Delta_0\,\eta
\right),
\]

\[
\delta N_{21}^{\lin}
=
-\frac{1}{\pi s^2}
\left(
\cos\Delta_0\,\eta
+
s\cos\Delta_0\,d_-
-
q_{0,-}s\sin\Delta_0\,\eta
\right),
\]

and

\[
\delta N_{22}^{\lin}
=
\frac{1}{2\pi s^3}
\left(
\partial_{q_-}F_0\,d_-
+
\partial_{q_+}F_0\,d_+
+
\partial_\Delta F_0\,\eta
\right),
\]

where

\[
F(q_-,q_+,\Delta;s)
=
(q_-+q_+)s\cos\Delta
+
(2-q_-q_+s^2)\sin\Delta.
\]

Thus the normalized grade-5 mixed block is

\[
\boxed{
M^{[5]}
=
[z^5]\,
\mathfrak D_Q
\begin{pmatrix}
-\dfrac{2\cos\Delta_0}{\pi s}\eta
&
\dfrac{\cos\Delta_0\,\eta+s\cos\Delta_0\,d_+-q_{0,+}s\sin\Delta_0\,\eta}{\pi s^2}
\\[2ex]
-\dfrac{\cos\Delta_0\,\eta+s\cos\Delta_0\,d_- -q_{0,-}s\sin\Delta_0\,\eta}{\pi s^2}
&
\dfrac{\partial_{q_-}F_0\,d_-+\partial_{q_+}F_0\,d_++\partial_\Delta F_0\,\eta}{2\pi s^3}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
M^{[5]}
=
[z^5]\left(
\mathcal A_-(z)U_-(z)
+
\mathcal A_+(z)U_+(z)
+
\mathcal A_\Delta(z)V(z)
\right),
}
\]

for explicit bounded baseline coefficient matrices \(\mathcal A_-,\mathcal A_+,\mathcal A_\Delta\) determined by \(q_{0,\pm},\Delta_0,s,Q\). The draft already states this mixed-block Taylor expansion is linear in \(U_-,U_+,V\) modulo terms of pair-kernel degree at least two. 

By contrast, the same-point linear perturbation is

\[
\delta G_\pm^{\lin}
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2d_\pm & \frac12e_\pm\\[1ex]
\frac12e_\pm &
\frac1{12}\left(g_\pm+6q_{0,\pm}^2d_\pm\right)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

So the grade-1 and grade-5 same-point pieces entering \(\mathsf L_2^{1,5}\) and \(\mathsf R_2^{1,5}\) are extracted from

\[
[z^1]\mathfrak D_Q\delta G_\pm^{\lin},
\qquad
[z^5]\mathfrak D_Q\delta G_\pm^{\lin},
\]

and therefore from coefficient lists of

\[
U_\pm,\quad E_\pm,\quad G_\pm
\]

with baseline multipliers. The staged block confirms that same-point entries are linear in \(d_\pm,e_\pm,g_\pm\), with the \((2,2)\) entry having the form

\[
g_\pm+\text{baseline}\cdot d_\pm+\text{higher pair-kernel degree}.
\]

It also confirms the mixed block is linear in \((d_-,d_+,\eta)\) at \(\mathcal K\)-degree one. 

Therefore the source identity being tested is not automatic. It is exactly the assertion that, after applying the second Fréchet derivative of \(G^{-1/2}\), multiplying by \(N_0\) and the first Fréchet output on the opposite side, and taking \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^7]\), the resulting same-point grade-\((1,5)\) object agrees modulo \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\) with the mixed-block grade-5 object \(M^{[5]}\).

In formula form, the missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
&\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^7]\Bigl(
D^2(G_-^{-1/2})_{G_-^{(0)}}[
\delta G_-^{[1]},\delta G_-^{[5]}]
\,N_0\,
D(G_+^{-1/2})_{G_+^{(0)}}[\delta G_+^{[1]}]
\\
&\qquad\qquad+
D(G_-^{-1/2})_{G_-^{(0)}}[\delta G_-^{[1]}]
\,N_0\,
D^2(G_+^{-1/2})_{G_+^{(0)}}[
\delta G_+^{[1]},\delta G_+^{[5]}]
\Bigr)
\\
&\equiv
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^7]\Bigl(
\text{the }M^{[5]}\text{-middle-slot correction}
\Bigr)
\pmod{\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)}.
\end{aligned}
}
\]

The current ledgers say precisely that the needed \([z^r]\Lambda_{i,\pm}\) and \([z^s]M_i^{[5]}\) coefficient lists are still missing, and that \(L_2YR_0/L_0YR_2\) require second-Fréchet identities coupled to \(M^{[1]}/M^{[5]}\) in the same normalization. turn10file9

Exact refs

The relevant source facts are:

1. UV-025 supplies a tagged pre-whitening source block using \(d_\pm,e_\pm,g_\pm,\eta\), but explicitly does not assert \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\), \(Q_{7,m}^q\), \(\Pi_{1,1}\), or the UV-026 gauge theorem. 

2. The current UV-026 ledger requires coefficient lists \([z^r]\Lambda_{i,\pm}\) and \([z^s]M_i^{[5]}\), and separately flags \(L_2YR_0/L_0YR_2\) as requiring second-Fréchet inverse-square-root identities coupled to grade-one/grade-five mixed input. 

3. The source provenance audit says the paper contains notation near the target but not the actual grade \(1/5/1\) cubic matrices, fixed-sector projection, or \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-proportionality theorem. 

4. The current findings summarize the gap as a missing UV-023/UV-024 source-bidegree quotient package: the tagged source block is canonical, but UV-026 still reduces to seven pre-\(\Phi_K\) families, with gauge/vanishing available only after a term is identified as one-pair \(K_5\), \(K_3\), or pure. 

Dependencies

The smallest coefficient list needed is now clear.

For \(M^{[5]}\), one needs:

\[
[z^j]U_-,\quad [z^j]U_+,\quad [z^j]V
\]

for all \(j\) that can contribute to \([z^5]\) after multiplication by the baseline coefficient matrices

\[
\mathcal A_-(z),\quad \mathcal A_+(z),\quad \mathcal A_\Delta(z).
\]

Equivalently, one needs

\[
[z^5]\mathfrak D_Q\delta N^{\lin}
\]

entry-by-entry.

For the side contribution, one needs:

\[
[z^1]\mathfrak D_Q\delta G_\pm^{\lin},
\qquad
[z^5]\mathfrak D_Q\delta G_\pm^{\lin},
\]

hence the relevant coefficients of

\[
U_\pm,\quad E_\pm,\quad G_\pm.
\]

Then one needs the second-Fréchet inverse-square-root coefficients

\[
D^2(G_\pm^{-1/2})_{G_\pm^{(0)}}[
\delta G_\pm^{[1]},\delta G_\pm^{[5]}],
\]

and the first-Fréchet coefficients

\[
D(G_\pm^{-1/2})_{G_\pm^{(0)}}[\delta G_\pm^{[1]}].
\]

Finally, one must form

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^7]
\left(
\mathsf L_2^{1,5}N_0\mathsf R_1^1+
\mathsf L_1^1N_0\mathsf R_2^{1,5}
-
M^{[5]}\text{-middle correction}
\right)
\]

and test membership in

\[
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

Strongest objection

There is a plausible hidden relation: since both \(M^{[5]}\) and the side grade-\((1,5)\) terms come from the same corrected phase variables, they may satisfy a nontrivial source identity after \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^7]\). But this is not visible at the level of definitions. The mixed slot sees only \(d_-,d_+,\eta\), while the same-point side slot sees \(d_\pm,e_\pm,g_\pm\). The relation would have to use the analytic identities

\[
e_\pm=\partial_t d_\pm,\qquad
g_\pm=\partial_t^2 d_\pm,\qquad
\eta=\int_{t_+}^{t_-}r_\rho(u)\,du,
\]

converted into \(z\)-coefficients and then passed through the Fréchet inverse-square-root map. That coefficient theorem is not present in the current source.

Scalar-base counterexample after source constraints

The previous scalar-base counterexample treated

\[
Y,\quad \dot Y,\quad N_0
\]

as independent symbols. After imposing actual source relations, that counterexample is no longer decisive. In the actual source package,

\[
Y=M^{[5]}
\]

is constrained by

\[
U_-,U_+,V,
\]

and the \(N_0\)-side grade-5 contribution is constrained by

\[
U_\pm,E_\pm,G_\pm.
\]

So the scalar-base witness survives only if one can choose a legitimate one-pair source kernel with the same scalar-base simplification and still make

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^7]
\left(
\mathsf L_2^{1,5}N_0\mathsf R_1^1+
\mathsf L_1^1N_0\mathsf R_2^{1,5}
-
M^{[5]}\text{-middle correction}
\right)
\notin
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

The current files do not provide enough coefficient data to run that constrained test. So the free-symbol scalar-base witness should be demoted from “counterexample to the source theorem” to “counterexample to any proof that treats \(Y,\dot Y,N_0\) as independent formal symbols.”

Needed for promotion

Promotion requires an explicit finite-order coefficient computation:

\[
\boxed{
M^{[5]}
=
[z^5]\mathfrak D_Q\delta N^{\lin}
}
\]

from \(U_-,U_+,V\), plus

\[
\boxed{
\mathsf L_2^{1,5},\mathsf R_2^{1,5}
}
\]

from \(U_\pm,E_\pm,G_\pm\), followed by the fixed-sector quotient test

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^7]
\left(
\mathsf L_2^{1,5}N_0\mathsf R_1^1+
\mathsf L_1^1N_0\mathsf R_2^{1,5}
-
M^{[5]}\text{-middle correction}
\right)
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
}
\]

The exact entries required are:

\[
[z^j]U_\pm,\quad [z^j]E_\pm,\quad [z^j]G_\pm,\quad [z^j]V
\]

through the finite orders contributing to \([z^7]\) in the cubic product; practically, this means up to order \(5\) for the grade-5 block and up to order \(1\) for the grade-1 Fréchet factors, with baseline coefficient expansions included to the remaining order required by the \(r+s+t=7\) convolution.

Honest verdict

The target theorem remains open. The actual corrected block variables sharpen the problem but do not close it.

The real state is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The }N_0\text{-to-}M^{[5]}\text{ identity is not formal.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{It is conditional on an explicit }[z^5]\text{ mixed-block and grade-}(1,5)\text{ same-point coefficient computation.}
}
\]

The previous scalar-base counterexample does not refute the actual source theorem after imposing \(Y=M^{[5]}\), but the current paper does not provide the coefficient tables needed to prove the theorem either. Do not move to \(C_3\); the next productive attack is the finite coefficient table for

\[
[z^5]\mathfrak D_Q\delta N^{\lin}
\quad\text{and}\quad
D^2(G_\pm^{-1/2})[\delta G_\pm^{[1]},\delta G_\pm^{[5]}].
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-24 14:40:45)

_Thought for 14s_

Claim

The smallest source theorem needed is a **grade-5 middle/side compatibility theorem**. It should not be stated as “\(N_0=Y\)” or as a generic Fréchet identity. It should be stated as a fixed-sector coefficient identity after the actual source substitutions:

\[
M^{[5]}=[z^5]\,\mathfrak D_Q\,\delta N^{\lin}
\]

and

\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{side}}^{[7]}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^7]\left(
\mathsf L_2^{1,5}N_0\mathsf R_1^1
+
\mathsf L_1^1N_0\mathsf R_2^{1,5}
\right)
\]

must induce the same obstruction-covector contribution as the \(M^{[5]}\)-middle correction, modulo \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\).

A precise theorem statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^7]\left(
\mathsf L_2^{1,5}N_0\mathsf R_1^1
+
\mathsf L_1^1N_0\mathsf R_2^{1,5}
-
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{corr}}^{[5]}
\right)
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
}
\]

where \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{corr}}^{[5]}\) is the corresponding seven-order contribution generated by inserting \(M^{[5]}\) into the middle slot of the \(C_2\) obstruction.

Status

Open. This is a **new source-normalization theorem**, not already implied by the corrected mixed block formula.

More sharply:

\[
\boxed{
\text{False in free-symbol algebra, but possibly true under actual source constraints.}
}
\]

It is not likely false yet; the free-symbol counterexample no longer applies once \(M^{[5]}\) and the side grade-\((1,5)\) terms are both forced by the same source variables. But the current paper/work files do not provide the coefficient list needed to verify it.

Evidence

The canonical UV-025 block defines the actual source perturbations before whitening by additive substitution into

\[
d_\pm,\qquad e_\pm,\qquad g_\pm,\qquad \eta,
\]

or equivalently into the tagged kernels

\[
U_\pm,\qquad E_\pm,\qquad G_\pm,\qquad V.
\]

It also states the guardrail: this block is pre-whitening and does **not** assert \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\), \(Q_{7,m}^q\), \(\Pi_{1,1}\), or UV-026 gauge. 

The mixed block \(M^{[5]}\) is the grade-5 coefficient of the \(\mathcal K\)-linear mixed perturbation:

\[
\boxed{
M^{[5]}
=
[z^5]\,\mathfrak D_Q\,\delta N^{\lin}(d_-,d_+,\eta).
}
\]

Equivalently, using source kernels,

\[
\boxed{
M^{[5]}
=
[z^5]\left(
\mathcal A_-(z)U_-(z)
+
\mathcal A_+(z)U_+(z)
+
\mathcal A_V(z)V(z)
\right),
}
\]

for baseline coefficient matrices \(\mathcal A_-,\mathcal A_+,\mathcal A_V\) coming from the corrected mixed block Taylor formula.

The side terms use the same source family, but through the same-point blocks:

\[
\delta G_\pm^{\lin}
=
\delta G_\pm^{\lin}(d_\pm,e_\pm,g_\pm)
=
\delta G_\pm^{\lin}(U_\pm,E_\pm,G_\pm).
\]

Define the coefficient pieces

\[
G_\pm^{[1]}:=[z^1]\,\mathfrak D_Q\,\delta G_\pm^{\lin},
\qquad
G_\pm^{[5]}:=[z^5]\,\mathfrak D_Q\,\delta G_\pm^{\lin},
\]

and

\[
N^{[5]}:=[z^5]\,\mathfrak D_Q\,\delta N^{\lin}=M^{[5]}.
\]

Let

\[
\Lambda_\pm^{[1]}
=
D(G_\pm^{(0)-1/2})[G_\pm^{[1]}],
\]

and

\[
\Lambda_\pm^{[1,5]}
=
D^2(G_\pm^{(0)-1/2})[G_\pm^{[1]},G_\pm^{[5]}],
\]

up to the paper’s common Taylor/polarization normalization.

Then the hidden side contribution is

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{side}}^{[7]}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^7]\left(
\Lambda_-^{[1,5]}N_0\Lambda_+^{[1]}
+
\Lambda_-^{[1]}N_0\Lambda_+^{[1,5]}
\right).
}
\]

The explicit middle-slot contribution is

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{mid}}^{[7]}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^7]\left(
\Lambda_-^{[1]}M^{[5]}\Lambda_+^{[1]}
\right)
}
\]

or, more exactly for the \(C_2\)-residual formulation,

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{mid},C_2}^{[7]}
=
\text{the fixed-sector coefficient whose obstruction pairing is }
Y\cdot R_{C_2}^{Y}+\dot Y\cdot R_{C_2}^{\dot Y}.
}
\]

The minimal theorem is therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{side}}^{[7]}
+
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{mid},C_2}^{[7]}
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
}
\]

This is exactly the coefficient-level \(N_0\)-to-\(M^{[5]}\) compatibility required to finish \(C_2\).

Exact refs

The staged source block defines the corrected two-atom source perturbations using \(d_\pm,e_\pm,g_\pm,\eta\), and defines \(\mathcal B_2=(G_{2,-}^{\corr},N_2^{\corr},G_{2,+}^{\corr})\) by the same corrected same-point and mixed block formulas, before whitening. 

The same block states that \(\mathcal K\)-linear same-point entries depend on \(d_\pm,e_\pm,g_\pm\), while the mixed block depends linearly on \((d_-,d_+,\eta)\) at \(\mathcal K\)-degree one. 

The current ledger says the \(L_1YR_1\) gate still requires \([z^r]\Lambda_{i,\pm}\), \([z^s]M_i^{[5]}\), and determinant identities against \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\); those coefficient tables remain missing. 

The UV ledger frames UV-026 as a pre-\(\Phi_K\) source-linear corrected-whitening gauge theorem and specifically lists the required coefficient lists for Fréchet inverse-square-root outputs and \(M_i^{[5]}\). 

Dependencies

### Required entries of \(M^{[5]}\)

All four entries of

\[
M^{[5]}=
\begin{pmatrix}
m_{11}^{[5]} & m_{12}^{[5]}\\
m_{21}^{[5]} & m_{22}^{[5]}
\end{pmatrix}
\]

are needed, but only through their fixed-sector projection after multiplication by the grade-1 whitening factors.

Equivalently, one needs the four coefficients

\[
[z^5](\mathfrak D_Q\delta N^{\lin})_{11},\quad
[z^5](\mathfrak D_Q\delta N^{\lin})_{12},\quad
[z^5](\mathfrak D_Q\delta N^{\lin})_{21},\quad
[z^5](\mathfrak D_Q\delta N^{\lin})_{22}.
\]

In source kernels, these are the coefficients of

\[
U_-,\quad U_+,\quad V
\]

through

\[
[z^5]\left(
\mathcal A_-(z)U_-(z)
+
\mathcal A_+(z)U_+(z)
+
\mathcal A_V(z)V(z)
\right).
\]

### Required entries of the hidden side term

The side term needs the fixed-sector projection of

\[
\Lambda_-^{[1,5]}N_0\Lambda_+^{[1]}
+
\Lambda_-^{[1]}N_0\Lambda_+^{[1,5]}.
\]

Thus the required entries are:

\[
(\Lambda_-^{[1,5]})_{11},\quad
(\Lambda_-^{[1,5]})_{12},\quad
(\Lambda_-^{[1,5]})_{21},\quad
(\Lambda_-^{[1,5]})_{22},
\]

and the analogous four entries for \(\Lambda_+^{[1,5]}\), together with the four entries of \(\Lambda_\pm^{[1]}\) and \(N_0\).

But \(\Lambda_\pm^{[1,5]}\) itself is determined by

\[
G_\pm^{[1]}=[z^1]\mathfrak D_Q\delta G_\pm^{\lin}(U_\pm,E_\pm,G_\pm)
\]

and

\[
G_\pm^{[5]}=[z^5]\mathfrak D_Q\delta G_\pm^{\lin}(U_\pm,E_\pm,G_\pm)
\]

through

\[
D^2(G_\pm^{(0)-1/2})[G_\pm^{[1]},G_\pm^{[5]}].
\]

### Minimal identity in entry form

Let

\[
\mathcal P_{\mathfrak f}(X):=\pi_{\mathfrak f}X
\]

and write

\[
\mathcal P_{\mathfrak f}(X)=x_0I+x_1S
\]

in the fixed sector relevant to \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S\). Then the exact quotient condition is the single scalar identity

\[
\boxed{
v_5x_0-u_5x_1=0
}
\]

for

\[
\boxed{
X=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{side}}^{[7]}
-
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{mid},C_2}^{[7]}.
}
\]

Equivalently, entrywise:

\[
\boxed{
v_5\,\pi_I
\left[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^7]
\left(
\Lambda_-^{[1,5]}N_0\Lambda_+^{[1]}
+
\Lambda_-^{[1]}N_0\Lambda_+^{[1,5]}
-
\Lambda_-^{[1]}M^{[5]}\Lambda_+^{[1]}
\right)
\right]
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
-
u_5\,\pi_S
\left[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^7]
\left(
\Lambda_-^{[1,5]}N_0\Lambda_+^{[1]}
+
\Lambda_-^{[1]}N_0\Lambda_+^{[1,5]}
-
\Lambda_-^{[1]}M^{[5]}\Lambda_+^{[1]}
\right)
\right]
=0.
}
\]

That is the smallest coefficient form. It avoids determinant scalarization as the definition; it only states membership in the quotient line \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\).

Strongest objection

The expression

\[
\Lambda_-^{[1]}M^{[5]}\Lambda_+^{[1]}
\]

is a compressed notation for the middle-slot contribution. The actual \(C_2\)-operator may place coefficients \(1,2\), or signs depending on the chosen Taylor/polarization normalization and whether the full

\[
\frac38D^2-\sum_{i<j}D_iD_j
\]

operator is retained. Those common normalization constants must be aligned before the theorem is committed.

But the theorem’s content is unaffected: the missing identity is exactly that the grade-\((1,5)\) side insertion through \(N_0\) and the grade-5 mixed insertion through \(M^{[5]}\) differ only by an \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-gauge vector.

Needed for promotion

To promote this, the paper needs a coefficient table with:

\[
[z^5]\mathfrak D_Q\delta N^{\lin}(d_-,d_+,\eta),
\]

\[
[z^1]\mathfrak D_Q\delta G_\pm^{\lin}(d_\pm,e_\pm,g_\pm),
\]

\[
[z^5]\mathfrak D_Q\delta G_\pm^{\lin}(d_\pm,e_\pm,g_\pm),
\]

and the corresponding first/second Fréchet inverse-square-root outputs

\[
\Lambda_\pm^{[1]},
\qquad
\Lambda_\pm^{[1,5]}.
\]

Then compute

\[
X=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^7]\left(
\Lambda_-^{[1,5]}N_0\Lambda_+^{[1]}
+
\Lambda_-^{[1]}N_0\Lambda_+^{[1,5]}
-
\Lambda_-^{[1]}M^{[5]}\Lambda_+^{[1]}
\right)
\]

and verify

\[
X\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

Honest verdict

The minimal source theorem is now isolated:

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^7]
\left(
\Lambda_-^{[1,5]}N_0\Lambda_+^{[1]}
+
\Lambda_-^{[1]}N_0\Lambda_+^{[1,5]}
-
\Lambda_-^{[1]}M^{[5]}\Lambda_+^{[1]}
\right)
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
}
\]

This is not implied by the corrected mixed block formula alone. It is a new finite coefficient theorem about the source-linear block after whitening. It is false in free-symbol algebra, possibly true under actual source constraints, and currently open.

## Explicit \(I,S\)-coordinate extraction

For any \(2\times2\) matrix

\[
X=
\begin{pmatrix}
x_{11}&x_{12}\\
x_{21}&x_{22}
\end{pmatrix},
\]

use

\[
\boxed{
\pi_I(X)=\frac{x_{11}+x_{22}}2,\qquad
\pi_S(X)=\frac{x_{12}+x_{21}}2.
}
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
u_{111}^{(2)}
=
\frac{(X_{111}^{(2)})_{11}+(X_{111}^{(2)})_{22}}2,
\qquad
v_{111}^{(2)}
=
\frac{(X_{111}^{(2)})_{12}+(X_{111}^{(2)})_{21}}2.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
u_{111}^{(3)}
=
\frac{(X_{111}^{(3)})_{11}+(X_{111}^{(3)})_{22}}2,
\qquad
v_{111}^{(3)}
=
\frac{(X_{111}^{(3)})_{12}+(X_{111}^{(3)})_{21}}2.
}
\]

These are the explicit \(I,S\)-coordinate formulas compatible with Agent 1’s six-row table.

\[
E_\pm=\mathcal E_\pm[U_\pm;r],\qquad
G_\pm=\mathcal G_\pm[U_\pm;r],\qquad

are not supplied at the coefficient level needed for the \(111\)-row. L114-L120

Status: open.

## Evidence

### 1. \(\Lambda_\pm^{[1]}\) depends on \(U_\pm,E_\pm,G_\pm\)

The same-point source-linear perturbation is

\[
X_\varepsilon(z)=\mathfrak D_Q(\delta G_\varepsilon^{\lin})(z)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
\dfrac{2z^2}{Q^2}U_\varepsilon(z)
&
\dfrac{z}{2Q}E_\varepsilon(z)
\\[1ex]
\dfrac{z}{2Q}E_\varepsilon(z)
&
\dfrac1{12}G_\varepsilon(z)
+
\dfrac{q_\varepsilon(z)^2z^2}{2Q^4}U_\varepsilon(z)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

So, for \(\varepsilon=\pm\),

\[
[z^n]X_\varepsilon
\quad\text{depends on}\quad
[z^{n-2}]U_\varepsilon,\ [z^{n-1}]E_\varepsilon,\ [z^n]G_\varepsilon,
\]

with baseline \(q_\varepsilon\)-coefficients. L274-L305

Then

\[
\Lambda_\varepsilon^{[1]}
=
D(G_\varepsilon^{(0)-1/2})[X_\varepsilon]
\]

is obtained by the first Sylvester recursion using \(P_{\varepsilon}=G_\varepsilon^{(0)1/2}\). Thus

\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_{\pm,0..2}^{[1]}
\text{ are functions of }
U_{\pm,-2..0},\ E_{\pm,-1..1},\ G_{\pm,0..2}
}
\]

with negative-index terms set to zero and baseline coefficients included.

More concretely, since negative indices vanish:

\[
X_{\pm,0}\text{ uses }G_{\pm,0},
\]

\[
X_{\pm,1}\text{ uses }E_{\pm,0},G_{\pm,1},
\]

\[
X_{\pm,2}\text{ uses }U_{\pm,0},E_{\pm,1},G_{\pm,2},
\]

plus the \(q_\pm^2U_\pm\) baseline term at \(n=2\).

The dotted coefficients use the corresponding dotted kernels:

\[
\dot U_\pm,\quad \dot E_\pm,\quad \dot G_\pm.
\]

### 2. \(Y_5\) depends on \(U_\pm,V\), not \(E_\pm,G_\pm\)

The mixed grade-five matrix is

\[
Y_5=[z^5]\mathfrak D_Q\delta N^{\lin}.
\]

Agent 3’s extraction gives:

\[
(Y_5)_{11}
=
-\frac{2}{\pi Q^2}[z^3](cV),
\]

\[
(Y_5)_{12}
=
\frac1\pi\left[
\frac1Q[z^4]\bigl(c(V+U_+)\bigr)
-
\frac1{Q^3}[z^3]\bigl(q_+\ell V\bigr)
\right],
\]

\[
(Y_5)_{21}
=
-\frac1\pi\left[
\frac1Q[z^4]\bigl(c(V+U_-)\bigr)
-
\frac1{Q^3}[z^3]\bigl(q_-\ell V\bigr)
\right],
\]

and a \((2,2)\)-entry depending on \(U_-,U_+,V\) with baseline \(q_\pm,c,\ell\). Thus \(Y_5\) depends only on

\[
U_-,\quad U_+,\quad V
\]

and not on \(E_\pm,G_\pm\). L317-L351

Likewise,

\[

\]

is obtained by replacing

\[
U_\pm,V
\quad\text{with}\quad
\dot U_\pm,\dot V
\]

while keeping \(q_\pm,c,\ell\) as baseline midpoint quantities. L352-L362

### 3. Are \(E_\pm,G_\pm,V\) constrained by \(U_\pm\) or a single \(r=q^{(7)}\)?

At the **formal source-block level currently in the paper**, the answer is no. The UV-025 block defines the \(\mathcal K\)-filtration with separate tagged kernels

\[
\tau_iU_{i,\pm},\quad \tau_iE_{i,\pm},\quad \tau_iG_{i,\pm},\quad \tau_iV_i,
\]

all as degree-one source kernels, and proves only tagged pair-kernel linearity. It explicitly does not assert \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\), \(Q_{7,m}^q\), \(\Pi_{1,1}\), or the UV-026 gauge theorem. L42-L57 L89-L103

However, the broader findings record says that if the bridge theorem is local, it should run through a single explicit source

\[
r=q^{(7)}
\]

via \(\lambda^{[1]}\) / \(\mathcal G^{[1]}\), with no second primitive pointwise field. L114-L120

So the correct audit conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Single-tower compression is expected structurally, but not proved for the }111\text{ coefficient row.}
}
\]

## Minimal source-normal-form theorem needed

The missing theorem should be stated as an order-two finite normal-form theorem for the \(111\)-row:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
&U_{\pm,0..4},\ E_{\pm,0..1},\ G_{\pm,0..2},\ V_{0..4}
\\
&\quad\text{and their }h\text{-derivatives are all linear transforms of one primitive tower }
r_0,r_1,r_2,r_3,r_4
\text{,}
\end{aligned}
}
\]

where \(r\) is the local highest-new source, expected to be \(q^{(7)}\), and the transforms use only baseline coefficients.

More concretely, for the \(111\)-row we need finite identities of the form

\[
U_{\pm,j}=\mathcal U_{\pm,j}(r_0,\ldots,r_j),
\]

\[
E_{\pm,j}=\mathcal E_{\pm,j}(r_0,\ldots,r_{j+1}),
\]

\[
G_{\pm,j}=\mathcal G_{\pm,j}(r_0,\ldots,r_{j+2}),
\]

\[
V_j=\mathcal V_j(r_0,\ldots,r_j),
\]

for the finite range actually used by \(r+t=2\):

\[
U_{\pm,0..4},\quad E_{\pm,0..1},\quad G_{\pm,0..2},\quad V_{0..4}.
\]

The range \(U_{\pm,0..4},V_{0..4}\) is needed because \(Y_5\) uses \([z^4](c(V+U_\pm))\) and \([z^3](q_\pm\ell V)\), while \(\Lambda_{\pm,0..2}^{[1]}\) uses \(U_{\pm,0},E_{\pm,0..1},G_{\pm,0..2}\).

Then the \(111\)-row becomes a quadratic/cubic expression in that one primitive tower:

\[
X_{111}^{(2)}
=
\sum_{r+t=2}
\left(
\dot\Lambda_{-,r}[r]\;Y_5[r]\;\dot\Lambda_{+,t}[r]
+
\Lambda_{-,r}[r]\;\dot Y_5[r]\;\dot\Lambda_{+,t}[r]
+
\dot\Lambda_{-,r}[r]\;\dot Y_5[r]\;\Lambda_{+,t}[r]
\right),
\]

\[
X_{111}^{(3)}
=
\sum_{r+t=2}
\dot\Lambda_{-,r}[r]\;\dot Y_5[r]\;\dot\Lambda_{+,t}[r],
\]

followed by

\[
u_{111}^{(i)}=\pi_I\pi_{\mathfrak f}X_{111}^{(i)},\qquad
v_{111}^{(i)}=\pi_S\pi_{\mathfrak f}X_{111}^{(i)}.
\]

## Classification

The \(111\)-row source dependence is:

\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\pm^{[1]}\leftarrow U_\pm,E_\pm,G_\pm,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
Y_5\leftarrow U_-,U_+,V.
}
\]

So the row currently depends on the union

\[
\boxed{
U_\pm,E_\pm,G_\pm,V
}
\]

and their \(h\)-derivatives.

It is **not yet reduced to a single primitive tower** inside the source block. The paper’s guarded source block treats these kernels as separate degree-one \(\mathcal K\)-generators, and the active UV-026 ledger still asks for coefficient lists before the \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-gauge theorem can be tested. L42-L57 L143-L157

but those identities are not included in the audited coefficient table for the \(111\)-row. Without them, treating \(U,E,G,V\) as one tower would silently assume the bridge theorem being tested.

where every entry is a \(2\times2\) baseline matrix.

Then the two block tests are direct polynomial identities in \(r_\rho,\dot r_\rho\).

## Strongest finite consequence

The \(111\)-row cannot involve \(r_5\) or \(r_6\) in the left/right source positions \(a,c\). Therefore any monomial with \(r_5\) or \(r_6\) in \(a\) or \(c\) in Agent 1’s \(201/102\) rows must cancel internally inside \(201/102\), not against \(111\).

Conversely, the \(111\)-row can contain \(r_5,r_6\) only in the middle position \(b\), through \(Y^5,Y^6\). So the only \(111\)-visible \(r_5,r_6\) monomial types are:

\[

\]

\]

and

\dot r_a\dot r_6\dot r_c,
\]

with

\[
a,c\in\{2,3,4\}.
\]

This is a useful audit constraint for Agent 1’s \(201/102\) rows.

## 2. Monomial types \(111\) cannot cancel

A monomial cannot be canceled by \(111\) if its left/right endpoint pair is not in

\[
S_{111}
=
\{(2,2),(2,3),(2,4),(3,2),(3,3),(4,2)\}.
\]

This excludes all cases with \(5\) or \(6\) in an endpoint slot, but it also excludes three endpoint pairs inside \(\{2,3,4\}^2\):

\[
(3,4),\qquad (4,3),\qquad (4,4).
\]

Thus \(111\) has no coefficient for any of the following, regardless of the middle index \(b\):

\[
\dot r_5 r_b\dot r_c,\quad
\dot r_6 r_b\dot r_c,\quad
\dot r_a r_b\dot r_5,\quad
\dot r_a r_b\dot r_6,
\]

\[
r_5\dot r_b\dot r_c,\quad
r_6\dot r_b\dot r_c,\quad
r_a\dot r_b\dot r_5,\quad
r_a\dot r_b\dot r_6,
\]

\[
\dot r_5\dot r_b r_c,\quad
\dot r_6\dot r_b r_c,\quad
\dot r_a\dot r_b r_5,\quad
\dot r_a\dot r_b r_6,
\]

and similarly

\[
\dot r_5\dot r_b\dot r_c,\quad
\dot r_6\dot r_b\dot r_c,\quad
\dot r_a\dot r_b\dot r_5,\quad
\dot r_a\dot r_b\dot r_6.
\]

More generally, replace \((5,6)\) above by any endpoint pair outside \(S_{111}\), including \((3,4),(4,3),(4,4)\).

These terms must either vanish inside Agent 1’s \(201/102\) rows or be passed forward as residuals. They cannot be canceled by \(111\).

Therefore the only \(111\)-visible \(r_5,r_6\) terms are:

with

(a,c)\in S_{111}.

Any \(r_5,r_6\) occurrence outside the middle slot is invisible to \(111\).

## 5. Checklist for future \((\alpha,\beta)\) rows

Use missing-support terms as zero.

For each ordered triple \((p,q,r)\), the \(C_2\) coefficient tests are:

### Type A: \(\dot r_p r_q\dot r_r\)

\[
\boxed{
d^0_{pqr}+2d^-_{pqr}+d^+_{qpr}=0.
}
\]

Audit conditions:

\[
d^0_{pqr}\neq0
\quad\text{only if}\quad
(p,r)\in S_{111},\ q\in\{2,\ldots,6\}.
\]

\[
d^-_{pqr}\neq0
\quad\text{only if}\quad
p,q\in\{2,3,4\},\ r\in\{2,\ldots,6\}.
\]

\[
d^+_{qpr}\neq0
\quad\text{only if}\quad
q\in\{2,\ldots,6\},\ p,r\in\{2,3,4\}.
\]

### Type B: \(r_p\dot r_q\dot r_r\)

\[
\boxed{
d^0_{pqr}+d^+_{pqr}=0.
}
\]

Audit conditions:

\[
d^0_{pqr}\neq0
\quad\text{only if}\quad
(p,r)\in S_{111},\ q\in\{2,\ldots,6\}.
\]

\[
d^+_{pqr}\neq0
\quad\text{only if}\quad
p\in\{2,\ldots,6\},\ q,r\in\{2,3,4\}.
\]

So if \(r\in\{5,6\}\), both \(d^0_{pqr}\) and \(d^+_{pqr}\) are zero; if Agent 1’s row shows a surviving such term, it is outside the three-family block.

### Type C: \(\dot r_p\dot r_q r_r\)

\[
\boxed{
d^0_{pqr}+d^-_{pqr}+2d^+_{pqr}=0.
}
\]

Audit conditions:

\[
d^0_{pqr}\neq0
\quad\text{only if}\quad
(p,r)\in S_{111},\ q\in\{2,\ldots,6\}.
\]

\[
d^-_{pqr}\neq0
\quad\text{only if}\quad
p,q\in\{2,3,4\},\ r\in\{2,\ldots,6\}.
\]

\[
d^+_{pqr}\neq0
\quad\text{only if}\quad
p\in\{2,\ldots,6\},\ q,r\in\{2,3,4\}.
\]

For \(C_3\), the ordered monomial \(\dot r_p\dot r_q\dot r_r\) must satisfy

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{\operatorname{ord}(a,b,c)=(p,q,r)}d^0_{abc}
+
\sum_{\substack{a,b\in\{2,3,4\}\\ c\in\{2,\ldots,6\}\\ \operatorname{ord}(a,b,c)=(p,q,r)}}d^-_{abc}
+
\sum_{\substack{a\in\{2,\ldots,6\}\\ b,c\in\{2,3,4\}\\ \operatorname{ord}(a,b,c)=(p,q,r)}}d^+_{abc}
=0.
}
\]

These are exactly Agent 1’s coefficient-level cancellation equations, now annotated with the \(111\)-support restrictions. L494-L557

\]

cannot be canceled by \(111\). In particular, any term with \(p\in\{5,6\}\) or \(r\in\{5,6\}\) in the \(111\)-endpoint positions must be handled entirely by \(201/102\).

### Endpoint pairs \((3,4),(4,3),(4,4)\)

These are also invisible to \(111\). If Agent 1’s \(201/102\) rows generate them, their cancellation must be internal to \(201/102\) or they survive to the five/seven-family audit.

### \(r_5,r_6\) in the middle slot

These can be canceled by \(111\), but only in the precise forms:

\[

r_a\dot r_{5/6}\dot r_c,\quad
\dot r_a\dot r_{5/6}r_c,
\quad
\dot r_a\dot r_{5/6}\dot r_c,

with

\[

## Claim

Agent 1’s coefficient equations are structurally correct, **but the proposed “red flag” equalities**

\[
d^-_{ab5}=d^-_{ab6}=0,\qquad
d^+_{5bc}=d^+_{6bc}=0
\]

are **not valid support rules**.

They are actually **allowed** terms, because in \(201\), the index \(c\) is the \(Y\)-index, and in \(102\), the index \(a\) is the \(Y\)-index. Agent 1’s own support definitions say

\[
d^-_{abc}:\quad a,b\in\{2,3,4\},\quad c\in\{2,\ldots,6\},
\]

and

\[
d^+_{abc}:\quad a\in\{2,\ldots,6\},\quad b,c\in\{2,3,4\}.
\]

So \(d^-_{ab5},d^-_{ab6}\) and \(d^+_{5bc},d^+_{6bc}\) are exactly the allowed \(r_5,r_6\)-through-\(Y\) channels.

## Audit of the three classes

### 1. Monomials \(111\) can cancel

The \(111\)-support is

\[
S_{111}=\{(2,2),(2,3),(2,4),(3,2),(3,3),(4,2)\},
\]

with middle index

\[
b\in\{2,3,4,5,6\}.
\]

Thus \(111\) can contribute to monomials whose endpoint pair \((p,r)\) is in \(S_{111}\), and whose middle index \(q\) may be \(2,\ldots,6\). Agent 1’s expression for the \(111\)-row uses exactly this support. 

So \(111\) can cancel terms of the forms

\[
\dot r_p r_q\dot r_r,\qquad
r_p\dot r_q\dot r_r,\qquad
\dot r_p\dot r_q r_r,\qquad
\dot r_p\dot r_q\dot r_r,
\]

only when

\[
(p,r)\in S_{111}.
\]

In particular, \(111\) can see \(r_5,r_6\) only in the middle \(q\)-slot.

### 2. Monomials that must cancel internally in \(201/102\)

Any term with a \(201/102\) source index outside its own support is forced zero. Agent 1’s supports are:

\[
201:\quad d^-_{abc},\quad a,b\in\{2,3,4\},\quad c\in\{2,\ldots,6\},
\]

\[
102:\quad d^+_{abc},\quad a\in\{2,\ldots,6\},\quad b,c\in\{2,3,4\}.
\]

Therefore the genuine support-forced zeros are:

\[
\boxed{
d^-_{5bc}=d^-_{6bc}=0,\qquad d^-_{a5c}=d^-_{a6c}=0.
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
d^+_{ab5}=d^+_{ab6}=0,\qquad d^+_{a5c}=d^+_{a6c}=0.
}
\]

Those are the “left/right source index is \(5\) or \(6\)” exclusions. But \(d^-_{ab5}\) and \(d^+_{5bc}\) are the \(Y\)-index \(5\) terms and are not excluded.

So, for \(r_5,r_6\), the correct rule is:

\[
\boxed{
201\text{ allows }r_5,r_6\text{ only in index }c.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
102\text{ allows }r_5,r_6\text{ only in index }a.
}
\]

Agent 1 states this same fact later: in \(201\), \(r_5,r_6\) occur only in the \(Y\)-index \(c\), and in \(102\), only in the \(Y\)-index \(a\). 

### 3. Monomials preserved for five/seven-family audit

Endpoint pairs invisible to \(111\) are

\[
(3,4),\qquad (4,3),\qquad (4,4),
\]

as well as any endpoint pair involving \(5\) or \(6\).

For such monomials, if \(201/102\) produces a nonzero coefficient and there is no matching \(201/102\)-internal cancellation, then the monomial must be preserved as a residual for the five/seven-family audit.

The possible later cancellers are:

\[
L_2YR_0+L_0YR_2
\]

for remaining \(C_2\)-level even-Hessian/mixed-slot residuals, and

\[
L_3N_0R_0+L_0N_0R_3
\]

for pure third-Fréchet same-point residuals. Do not relabel such residuals as cocycle/connection effects.

## Corrected coefficient equations

Agent 1’s actual coefficient equations are right, provided missing-support terms are interpreted with the corrected supports.

For \(\Delta_2\), each ordered triple \((p,q,r)\) has three dot-placement equations:

### Type A: \(\dot r_p r_q\dot r_r\)

\[
\boxed{
d^0_{pqr}+2d^-_{pqr}+d^+_{qpr}=0.
}
\]

Here:

\[
d^0_{pqr}\neq0\Rightarrow (p,r)\in S_{111},\ q\in\{2,\ldots,6\}.
\]

\[
d^-_{pqr}\neq0\Rightarrow p,q\in\{2,3,4\},\ r\in\{2,\ldots,6\}.
\]

\[
d^+_{qpr}\neq0\Rightarrow q\in\{2,\ldots,6\},\ p,r\in\{2,3,4\}.
\]

This equation is structurally correct. 

### Type B: \(r_p\dot r_q\dot r_r\)

\[
\boxed{
d^0_{pqr}+d^+_{pqr}=0.
}
\]

Here:

\[
d^0_{pqr}\neq0\Rightarrow (p,r)\in S_{111}.
\]

\[
d^+_{pqr}\neq0\Rightarrow p\in\{2,\ldots,6\},\ q,r\in\{2,3,4\}.
\]

So if \(r\in\{5,6\}\), this type has no \(d^+\) support and also no \(d^0\) support unless \((p,r)\in S_{111}\), which never holds for \(r=5,6\). Such a monomial should be absent from the three-family block; if it appears, it is a residual outside \(111+201+102\).

### Type C: \(\dot r_p\dot r_q r_r\)

\[
\boxed{
d^0_{pqr}+d^-_{pqr}+2d^+_{pqr}=0.
}
\]

Here:

\[
d^-_{pqr}\neq0\Rightarrow p,q\in\{2,3,4\},\ r\in\{2,\ldots,6\},
\]

so \(r=5,6\) is allowed through the \(201\) \(Y\)-slot. This is exactly why \(d^-_{ab5},d^-_{ab6}\) must not be support-forced to zero.

}

while

\boxed{
d^-_{ab5},d^-_{ab6},d^+_{5bc},d^+_{6bc}
\text{ are allowed.}

If a residual appears with \(r_5\) or \(r_6\) in a \(Y\)-slot, it is not automatically a residual. It can still be part of the legitimate three-family test.

Examples that are allowed:

\[

\qquad
d^-_{ab6}\,\dot r_a\dot r_b r_6,
\]

\[
d^+_{5bc}\,r_5\dot r_b\dot r_c,
\qquad
d^+_{6bc}\,r_6\dot r_b\dot r_c.
\]

These must be tested against the relevant \(111\) terms if the endpoint pair lies in \(S_{111}\), or against \(201/102\)-internal cancellation if invisible to \(111\).

A genuine residual-for-five/seven audit occurs if the surviving monomial has:

\[
(p,r)\notin S_{111}
\]

and no matching support in the paired \(201/102\) equation.

Especially watch endpoint pairs

\[
(3,4),(4,3),(4,4),
\]

because \(201/102\) can generate them, but \(111\) cannot. If they survive the finite coefficient equations, they should be preserved for the five-family/seven-family audit.

+

This is the exact finite coefficient expression.

## 1. Compute \(Y^6\)

Agent 1 gives

\[

\begin{cases}
\dfrac{\varepsilon^a}{2^a a!Q^{2a-4}},&j=a-2,\\
0,&j\ne a-2,
\end{cases}
\]

and

\[
v_j^a=
\begin{cases}
-\dfrac{1}{2^a(a+1)!Q^{2a-4}},&j=a-2,\ a\text{ even},\\
0,&\text{otherwise}.
\end{cases}
\]

For \(a=6\), only \(j=4\) contributes:

\[
u_{+,4}^6=u_{-,4}^6=\frac{1}{2^6 6!Q^8},
\]

\[
v_4^6=-\frac{1}{2^6 7!Q^8}.
\]

Set

\[
\mu_6:=u_{\pm,4}^6+v_4^6
=
\frac{1}{2^6Q^8}\left(\frac1{6!}-\frac1{7!}\right)
=
\frac{1}{53760\,Q^8}.
\]

Agent 1’s \(Y^a\) formula gives, for \(a=6\),

\[
(Y^6)_{11}=0,
\]

because \((Y^a)_{11}\) uses \(\sum_{i+j=3}c_iv_j^a\), while \(v_j^6\) is supported only at \(j=4\). Agent 1 explicitly notes \(Y^6_{11}=0\) for this reason. L258-L270

\[

=
\frac{1}{\pi Q}c_0\mu_6,
\]

\[
(Y^6)_{21}
=
-\frac{1}{\pi Q}c_0\mu_6.
\]

The \((2,2)\)-entry is

\[
(Y^6)_{22}
=
\frac{\mu_6}{2\pi}
\left(
2c_1-\frac{(q_{-,0}+q_{+,0})s_0}{Q^2}
\right).
\]

In the collision chart, \(s_0=\sin\Delta_0(0)=0\), \(c_0=\cos\Delta_0(0)=1\), and \(c_1=0\). Hence

\[

\]

and therefore

\[
\boxed{

=
\frac{1}{53760\,\pi Q^9}J.

So \(Y^6\) is not zero; it is pure \(J\).

Agent 1’s table already states that \(Y^6\) is an allowed \(Y\)-slot coefficient and that support does not kill \(d^-_{ab6}\) or \(d^+_{6bc}\). L30-L63

is not killed by parity. Parity reduces it to a pure \(J\)-slot:

\[

But a pure \(J\) middle factor can still produce \(I,S\) fixed-sector output after multiplication by the endpoint factors \(H^\mp\) and \(W_\pm\). So parity alone does not imply

\[
d^-_{226}=0,\qquad d^+_{622}=0.
\]

### \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-gauge

The required gauge tests are exactly:

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(

+

+

+
W_{-,2}JH^+_{0;22}
\right)
\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

These are finite projected coefficient identities, not formal consequences of support.
