## Claim

The tests

\[
d^-_{226}=0,\qquad d^+_{622}=0
\]

are **not proved** by the \(Y^6\)-slot computation alone.

Accepted source computation gives

\[
Y^6=\frac{1}{53760\pi Q^9}J.
\]

This is strong, but it does **not** imply the fixed-sector projections vanish. Since \(H^-_{n;22},H^+_{n;22}\), and \(W_{\pm,n}\) are symmetric \(I,S,D\)-sector matrices, products of the form

\[
H^-_{n;22}JW_{+,t},
\qquad
W_{-,n}JH^+_{t;22}
\]

can have nonzero \(I,S\)-components. Thus \(d^-_{226}\) and \(d^+_{622}\) remain finite \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-gauge tests, not parity-vanishing consequences.

## Status

Open. The two coefficients remain live unless Agent 1 supplies the explicit projected identities

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}M^-_{226}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
\qquad
\pi_{\mathfrak f}M^+_{622}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

---

## 1. Are \(H^-_{n;22},H^+_{n;22},W_{\pm,n}\) symmetric \(I,S,D\)-sector matrices?

Yes.

Agent 1’s same-point primitives \(X_{\varepsilon,n}^a\) for \(n\le2\) are all in the \(I,S,D\)-sector: the listed nonzero entries are combinations of \(I-D\), \(S\), and \(I,D\), with no \(J\)-component. The table also says all other \(X_{\varepsilon,n}^a\) with \(n\le2\) are zero. L13-L69

The Sylvester recursion

\[
P_{\varepsilon,0}Z+ZP_{\varepsilon,0}=C
\]

preserves symmetry when \(P_{\varepsilon,0}\) and \(C\) are symmetric. The first and second Sylvester outputs are therefore symmetric \(I,S,D\)-sector matrices. Agent 1 defines \(S_{\varepsilon,n}^a\) and then \(\Lambda_{\varepsilon,n}^{[1]}\) entirely from \(P_{\varepsilon,0..2},W_{\varepsilon,0..2}\), and the \(X_{\varepsilon,n}^a\)-table. L73-L150

The second-Fréchet kernels \(H^-_{n;22}\) and \(H^+_{n;22}\) are built from those same symmetric Sylvester outputs with equal source index \(22\). Hence they are symmetric \(I,S,D\)-sector matrices.

So we may write

\[
H^-_{n;22}=a_{n,0}^-I+a_{n,1}^-S+a_{n,2}^-D,
\]

\[
H^+_{n;22}=a_{n,0}^+I+a_{n,1}^+S+a_{n,2}^+D,
\]

\[
W_{\pm,n}=b_{n,0}^{\pm}I+b_{n,1}^{\pm}S+b_{n,2}^{\pm}D.
\]

---

## 2. Does multiplication by \(J\) produce fixed-sector components?

Yes. This is the critical point.

For

\[
A=a_0I+a_1S+a_2D,\qquad
B=b_0I+b_1S+b_2D,
\]

one computes

\[
AJB
=
(-a_1b_2+a_2b_1)I
+
(-a_0b_2+a_2b_0)S
\]

\[
\qquad
+
(a_0b_1-a_1b_0)D
+
(a_0b_0-a_1b_1-a_2b_2)J.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(AJB)
=
(-a_1b_2+a_2b_1)I
+
(-a_0b_2+a_2b_0)S.
}
\]

So a pure \(J\)-middle slot is **not invisible** after multiplication by symmetric endpoint factors. It is invisible only under additional endpoint relations such as

\[
a_1b_2=a_2b_1,
\qquad
a_0b_2=a_2b_0.
\]

No such relation is supplied by the \(Y^6\)-slot computation.

Thus

\[
Y^6=\frac{1}{53760\pi Q^9}J
\]

reduces the test to a \(J\)-middle projection test, but does not prove either coefficient vanishes.

---

## 3. Source-constrained forms of the two tests

Using

\[
Y^6=\frac{1}{53760\pi Q^9}J,
\]

we have

\[
M^-_{226}
=
\frac{1}{53760\pi Q^9}
\sum_{n+t=2}H^-_{n;22}JW_{+,t}.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
d^-_{226}
=
\frac{1}{53760\pi Q^9}
\left[
v_5\pi_I\pi_{\mathfrak f}
-
u_5\pi_S\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\right]
\sum_{n+t=2}H^-_{n;22}JW_{+,t}.
}
\]

Similarly,

\[
M^+_{622}
=
\frac{1}{53760\pi Q^9}
\sum_{n+t=2}W_{-,n}JH^+_{t;22},
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
d^+_{622}
=
\frac{1}{53760\pi Q^9}
\left[
v_5\pi_I\pi_{\mathfrak f}
-
u_5\pi_S\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\right]
\sum_{n+t=2}W_{-,n}JH^+_{t;22}.
}
\]

The support audit already says \(d^-_{ab6}\) and \(d^+_{6bc}\) are in support and require actual coefficient identities, not support arguments. L30-L76

---

## 4. Is there a left/right symmetry relating \(d^-_{226}\) and \(d^+_{622}\)?

There is a formal anti-symmetry at the fixed-sector projection level.

For symmetric \(A,B\),

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(BJA)
=
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}(AJB).
\]

This follows immediately from the formula above.

Therefore, if the left/right source tables satisfy the exact mirror relation

\[
H^+_{t;22}\leftrightarrow H^-_{t;22},
\qquad
W_{-,n}\leftrightarrow W_{+,n},
\]

with no additional sign or \(z\mapsto -z\) normalization factor, then one expects

\[
\boxed{
d^+_{622}=-d^-_{226}
}
\]

after the corresponding left/right swap.

But this is **not the same as**

\[
d^-_{226}=0,\qquad d^+_{622}=0.
\]

It only says the two tests may be paired. Under an ordered-slot protocol, the two coefficients occur in different monomial placements. Under a fully commutative polynomial collection, the pair may cancel if the monomials are identified and the sign is exactly opposite. Agent 1’s current support audit treats them as ordered-slot residual candidates, so individual vanishing is still not proved. L177-L244

---

}

and

\[
\boxed{
d^-_{226}\,\dot r_2\dot r_2r_6.
}

If \(d^+_{622}\neq0\), the residual monomials are

d^+_{622}\,r_6\dot r_2\dot r_2
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
2d^+_{622}\,\dot r_6\dot r_2r_2.
}
\]

These are the \(Y^6\)-analogues of the first \(Y^5\)-slot residuals listed in the support audit. The audit states that if \(d^-_{ab5/6}\) or \(d^+_{5/6bc}\) fail to vanish, the residual goes first to the five-family audit; only if the five-family audit cannot cancel them should they move to the seven-family audit. ## Claim

Agent 1’s \(Y^6\)-slot cancellation is valid **at the three-family block level**, provided the standard midpoint parity convention is in force:

\[
W_{+,n}=(-1)^nW_{-,n},
\qquad
H^+_{n;22}=(-1)^nH^-_{n;22}.
\]

Under that convention,

\[
\boxed{
d^+_{622}=-d^-_{226}.
}
\]

So \(d^-_{226}\) and \(d^+_{622}\) are **not individually proved zero**, but their monomial contributions cancel after summing the \(201/102\) pair. They should **not** be carried as residuals to the five-family audit. L1-L18

## Status

Proved modulo the midpoint left/right parity convention.

Not proved as individual \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-gauge vanishings.

## Evidence

Accepted:

\[
Y^6=y_6J,
\qquad
y_6=\frac{1}{53760\pi Q^9}.
\]

Then

\[
M^-_{226}
=
y_6
\left(
H^-_{0;22}JW_{+,2}
+
H^-_{1;22}JW_{+,1}
+
H^-_{2;22}JW_{+,0}
\right).
\]

Using midpoint parity,

\[
W_{+,0}=W_{-,0},\quad
W_{+,1}=-W_{-,1},\quad
W_{+,2}=W_{-,2},
\]

and writing

\[
H_n:=H^-_{n;22},
\qquad
W_n:=W_{-,n},
\]

we get

\[
M^-_{226}
=
y_6(H_0JW_2-H_1JW_1+H_2JW_0).
\]

Similarly,

\[
M^+_{622}
=
y_6(W_0JH_2-W_1JH_1+W_2JH_0).
\]

For symmetric \(I,S,D\)-sector matrices

\[
H=aI+bS+cD,\qquad W=pI+qS+rD,
\]

we have

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HJW)=(cq-br)I+(cp-ar)S,
\]

while

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(WJH)=(rb-qc)I+(ra-pc)S.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(WJH)=-\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HJW).
}
\]

Applying this termwise gives

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}M^+_{622}
=
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}M^-_{226}.
}
\]

The determinant/gauge scalar

\[
v_5\pi_I-u_5\pi_S
\]

is linear, so

\[
\boxed{
d^+_{622}=-d^-_{226}.
}
\]

This is Agent 1’s conclusion, and the algebra checks out. L20-L86

---

## Do they vanish individually?

No. Individual vanishing would require

\[
[v_5\pi_I-u_5\pi_S]
\left(
H_0JW_2-H_1JW_1+H_2JW_0
\right)=0.
\]

The \(Y^6\)-slot parity result only gives

\[
Y^6=y_6J\neq0.
\]

It does not force the displayed \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-gauge scalar to vanish. Agent 1 states the same: individual \(d^-_{226}=0\) or \(d^+_{622}=0\) is not proved. L88-L105

---

## Block-level monomial cancellation

The \(201\)-side terms are

\[
2d^-_{226}\,\dot r_2 r_2\dot r_6
+
d^-_{226}\,\dot r_2\dot r_2 r_6.
\]

The \(102\)-side terms are

\[
d^+_{622}\,r_6\dot r_2\dot r_2
+
2d^+_{622}\,\dot r_6\dot r_2r_2.
\]

Since the residual-source coefficients commute,

\[
\dot r_2 r_2\dot r_6
=
\dot r_6\dot r_2r_2,
\]

and

\[
\dot r_2\dot r_2r_6
=
r_6\dot r_2\dot r_2.
\]

Using

\[
d^+_{622}=-d^-_{226},
\]

the scalar monomial coefficients cancel:

\[
2d^-_{226}+2d^+_{622}=0,
\]

\[
d^-_{226}+d^+_{622}=0.
\]

So the pair \((226)\leftrightarrow(622)\) passes the three-family audit. L107-L132

## 2. Does \(H^+_{n;ab}=(-1)^nH^-_{n;ab}\) hold for all relevant pairs?

Yes, for the relevant source-index range \(a,b\in\{2,3,4\}\), under Agent 1’s midpoint convention.

Agent 1’s primitive table gives

\[
X_{\varepsilon,0}^2=\frac1{24\pi}(I-D),

\[
X_{\varepsilon,1}^2=\frac{\varepsilon}{4\pi Q}S,
\qquad

\left(\frac1{8\pi Q^2}+\frac{q^2}{32\pi Q^4}\right)I
+

\[
X_{\varepsilon,2}^3=\frac1{16\pi Q^3}S,
\qquad
X_{\varepsilon,2}^4=\frac1{192\pi Q^4}(I-D).
\]

Thus the source primitives satisfy

\[
X_{+,n}^a=(-1)^nX_{-,n}^a
\]

for all relevant nonzero entries \(n\le2,\ a\in\{2,3,4\}\). L13-L69

The Sylvester recursions for \(S_{\varepsilon,n}^a\), \(\Lambda_{\varepsilon,n}\), and the second-Fréchet \(H_{\varepsilon,n;ab}\) are built coefficientwise from \(P_{\varepsilon,0..2}\), \(W_{\varepsilon,0..2}\), and the \(X_{\varepsilon,n}^a\) table. Therefore the midpoint parity propagates to

\[

This is the same convention Agent 1 explicitly used for the \(226/622\) computation. L20-L45

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(WJH)=-\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HJW).
}
\]

Agent 1 verified this by direct \(I,S,D,J\) multiplication. L47-L66

Now compute:

\[
M^-_{ab6}
=
y_6\sum_{n+t=2}H^-_{n;ab}JW_{+,t}
=
y_6\sum_{n+t=2}(-1)^tH^-_{n;ab}JW_{-,t}.
\]

Since \(n+t=2\), \((-1)^t=(-1)^n\), so

\[
M^-_{ab6}
=
y_6\sum_{n+t=2}(-1)^nH^-_{n;ab}JW_{-,t}.
\]

Similarly,

\[
M^+_{6ab}
=
y_6\sum_{n+t=2}W_{-,n}JH^+_{t;ab}
=
y_6\sum_{n+t=2}(-1)^tW_{-,n}JH^-_{t;ab}.
\]

Reindex \(n\leftrightarrow t\):

\[
M^+_{6ab}
=
y_6\sum_{n+t=2}(-1)^nW_{-,t}JH^-_{n;ab}.
\]

Projecting to \(\mathfrak f\),

\[

=

Therefore

\boxed{

}

and

So the endpoint-pair support matches the cancellation equations exactly.

\[

}

for the residual-source coefficients.

## 1. Substitute \(Y^2,Y^3,Y^4\)

Agent 1’s \(Y^a\)-row gives \(Y^a\) explicitly in terms of

\[
u_{\pm,j}^a,\qquad v_j^a,\qquad q_{\pm,j},\qquad c_j,\qquad s_j,
\]

where

\[
u_{\varepsilon,j}^a
=
\begin{cases}
\dfrac{\varepsilon^a}{2^aa!Q^{2a-4}},&j=a-2,\\
0,&j\ne a-2,
\end{cases}
\]

and

\[
v_j^a
=
\begin{cases}
-\dfrac{1}{2^a(a+1)!Q^{2a-4}},&j=a-2,\ a\text{ even},\\
0,&\text{otherwise}.
\end{cases}
\]

The table also states the parity facts used earlier: \(V\)-terms vanish for \(a=3,5\), while \(Y^6\) has the special \(J\)-slot behavior. L152-L270

For the present gate:

### \(Y^2\)

Here \(j=0\). We have

\[
u_{+,0}^2=u_{-,0}^2=\frac1{8Q^0}=\frac18,
\qquad
v_0^2=-\frac1{24}.
\]

So \(Y^2\) is the matrix obtained from Agent 1’s \(Y^a\) formula using only \(u_{\pm,0}^2\) and \(v_0^2\). It has generally nonzero \(I,S,D,J\)-components.

### \(Y^3\)

Here \(j=1\). We have

\[
u_{+,1}^3=\frac1{48Q^2},\qquad
u_{-,1}^3=-\frac1{48Q^2},
\qquad
v_1^3=0.
\]

So \(Y^3\) is a pure \(U_\pm\)-driven row. It is not zero by source parity; only the \(V\)-integral part vanishes.

### \(Y^4\)

Here \(j=2\). We have

\[
u_{+,2}^4=u_{-,2}^4=\frac1{384Q^4},
\qquad
v_2^4=-\frac1{1920Q^4}.
\]

So \(Y^4\) again has both \(U_\pm\)- and \(V\)-driven contributions and is generally nonzero.

Thus none of \(Y^2,Y^3,Y^4\) is eliminated by the parity arguments that closed \(Y^5/Y^6\).

This is a finite baseline coefficient identity, but the required \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-formula is not supplied in the current extraction data.

---

## Evidence

The current coefficient framework requires an actual fixed-sector vector

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^7](T)=uI+vS
\]

and a determinant check

\[
uv_5-u_5v=0
\]

against the matching

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=u_5I+v_5S.
\]

The dispatch explicitly says a positive result must prove proportionality to \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\), not merely scalar or formal invisibility. 

The available finite extraction reports also state that the coefficient rows are computable from finite normal-form tables, but those reports do not supply final numeric/projected values. They isolate the finite table as the remaining computation rather than a closed identity. turn39file15

The source notes identify the determinant pairing with \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) as the quotient test, but they warn that the actual quotient class/coefficient map must be controlled, not assumed from representative or determinant bookkeeping alone. turn39file0

---

## Explicit reduction

Write

\[
H^-_{1;32}=a_1I+b_1S+c_1D,
\qquad
H^-_{2;32}=a_2I+b_2S+c_2D,
\]

\[
W_1=p_1I+q_1S+r_1D,
\qquad
W_0=p_0I+q_0S+r_0D.
\]

For symmetric \(I,S,D\)-sector matrices,

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HJW)
=
(cq-br)I+(cp-ar)S.
\]

Therefore

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(H^-_{2;32}JW_0-H^-_{1;32}JW_1)
=
U_{324}I+V_{324}S,
\]

where

\[
\boxed{
U_{324}
=
-(c_1q_1-b_1r_1)+(c_2q_0-b_2r_0)
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
V_{324}
=
-(c_1p_1-a_1r_1)+(c_2p_0-a_2r_0).
}
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\Xi_{324}=v_5U_{324}-u_5V_{324}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\Xi_{324}
=
v_5[-(c_1q_1-b_1r_1)+(c_2q_0-b_2r_0)]
-
u_5[-(c_1p_1-a_1r_1)+(c_2p_0-a_2r_0)].
}
\]

This is already the simplest baseline-coordinate form.

---

## What would be needed to close it

To prove \(\Xi_{324}=0\), we need an explicit formula or identity showing

\[
(U_{324},V_{324})
\]

is proportional to

\[
(u_5,v_5).
\]

Equivalently, one must prove

\[
\boxed{
\frac{U_{324}}{V_{324}}=\frac{u_5}{v_5}
}
\]

on a \(v_5\neq0\) patch, or directly

\[
\boxed{
v_5U_{324}-u_5V_{324}=0.
}
\]

The currently available \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) material defines \(u_5,v_5\) and gives some fixed-sector/quintic structural information, but it does not give the needed baseline-coordinate equality for this specific \((3,4)\) second-Fréchet channel.

So the requested task stops at:

\[
\boxed{
\text{required missing identity: }
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
\parallel
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(H^-_{2;32}JW_0-H^-_{1;32}JW_1).
}
\]

---

## Classification

\[
\boxed{
\Xi_{324}=0
\text{ is not proved by the current }A_5^{\mathfrak f}\text{ data.}
}
\]

It is not closed by:

- support;
- \(Y^5=0\);
- \(Y^6\)-pairing;
- midpoint parity;
- Sylvester recursion alone;
- determinant scalarization as a bookkeeping device.

It remains a genuine finite coefficient identity.

The current source-constrained data do not prove this scalar vanishes. Therefore the three-family audit does **not** close at \((3,4)\) unless an additional explicit \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-parallelism identity is supplied.

}
\]

\[
\boxed{
R^{(C)}_5
=
y_4\Xi_{324}+E^-_{324}+2E^+_{324}.
}
\]

Five-family closure is exactly

\[
R^{(A)}_5=0,\qquad R^{(C)}_5=0.
\]

---

## 2. Finite support ranges

### \(E^-_{324}\)

\[
E^-_{324}
=
\mathcal D
\left(
\sum_{n+s+t=7}H^-_{n;32}N^{(0)}_s\Lambda^+_{t;4}
\right).
\]

The first nonzero \(H^-_{n;32}\) occurs at \(n=1\), because the \(r_3\)-source starts at order \(1\) and the \(r_2\)-source starts at order \(0\). The first nonzero \(\Lambda^+_{t;4}\) occurs at \(t=2\), because the \(r_4\)-source first appears in \(\Lambda_{\pm,2}\). Agent 1’s finite table explicitly shows \(\Lambda_{\pm,2}\) has an \(r_4\)-column while \(\Lambda_{\pm,0},\Lambda_{\pm,1}\) do not. 

Thus the required finite ranges are:

\[
\boxed{
H^-_{n;32}: n=1,\ldots,5,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\Lambda^+_{t;4}: t=2,\ldots,6,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
N^{(0)}_s: s=0,\ldots,4.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
E^-_{324}
=
\mathcal D
\left(
\sum_{\substack{1\le n\le5\\0\le s\le4\\2\le t\le6\\n+s+t=7}}
H^-_{n;32}N^{(0)}_s\Lambda^+_{t;4}
\right).
}
\]

### \(E^+_{234}\)

\[
E^+_{234}
=
\mathcal D
\left(
\sum_{n+s+t=7}
\Lambda^-_{n;2}N^{(0)}_sH^+_{t;34}
\right).
\]

Here \(\Lambda^-_{n;2}\) starts at \(n=0\), while \(H^+_{t;34}\) starts at \(t=3\), because \(r_3\) starts at order \(1\) and \(r_4\) starts at order \(2\). Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\Lambda^-_{n;2}: n=0,\ldots,4,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
H^+_{t;34}: t=3,\ldots,7,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
N^{(0)}_s: s=0,\ldots,4.
}
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
E^+_{234}
=
\mathcal D
\left(
\sum_{\substack{0\le n\le4\\0\le s\le4\\3\le t\le7\\n+s+t=7}}
\Lambda^-_{n;2}N^{(0)}_sH^+_{t;34}
\right).
}
\]

### \(E^+_{324}\)

\[
E^+_{324}
=
\mathcal D
\left(
\sum_{n+s+t=7}
\Lambda^-_{n;3}N^{(0)}_sH^+_{t;24}
\right).
\]

Here \(\Lambda^-_{n;3}\) starts at \(n=1\), while \(H^+_{t;24}\) starts at \(t=2\), because \(r_2\) starts at order \(0\) and \(r_4\) starts at order \(2\). Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\Lambda^-_{n;3}: n=1,\ldots,5,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
H^+_{t;24}: t=2,\ldots,6,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
N^{(0)}_s: s=0,\ldots,4.
}
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
E^+_{324}
=
\mathcal D
\left(
\sum_{\substack{1\le n\le5\\0\le s\le4\\2\le t\le6\\n+s+t=7}}
\Lambda^-_{n;3}N^{(0)}_sH^+_{t;24}
\right).
}
\]

## 3. Midpoint parity reductions

The plus-side terms can be reduced using midpoint parity:

\[
\boxed{
\Lambda^+_{t;4}=(-1)^t\Lambda^-_{t;4},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
H^+_{t;34}=(-1)^tH^-_{t;34},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
H^+_{t;24}=(-1)^tH^-_{t;24}.
}
\]

This is the same midpoint parity convention used in the \(Y^6\)-slot cancellation audit. The earlier support audit also fixed the \(201/102\) polynomial convention and the relevant row supports. 

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
E^-_{324}
=
\mathcal D
\left(
\sum_{\substack{1\le n\le5\\0\le s\le4\\2\le t\le6\\n+s+t=7}}
(-1)^t
H^-_{n;32}N^{(0)}_s\Lambda^-_{t;4}
\right).
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
E^+_{234}
=
\mathcal D
\left(
\sum_{\substack{0\le n\le4\\0\le s\le4\\3\le t\le7\\n+s+t=7}}
(-1)^t
\Lambda^-_{n;2}N^{(0)}_sH^-_{t;34}
\right).
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
E^+_{324}
=
\mathcal D
\left(
\sum_{\substack{1\le n\le5\\0\le s\le4\\2\le t\le6\\n+s+t=7}}
(-1)^t
\Lambda^-_{n;3}N^{(0)}_sH^-_{t;24}
\right).
}
\]

This is the reduced minus-side form of the five-family gate.

one needs the finite identity

\[

\[

\]

and the scalar

\[

=

This is acceptable only on the good patch

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\neq0.
\]

The constant baseline \(q_0(t)=1\) with \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\) is therefore quotient-inconclusive, exactly as you stated. The actual multiplicities in \(R^{(A)}_{300/003},R^{(C)}_{300/003}\) must be taken from the same ordered \(C_2\)-operator used in Agent 1’s row table. I would not hard-code a factor here without that row convention for \(L_3\), because the whole error we just corrected was a family-labeling/sign convention error.

---

## 4. What would constitute closure

Seven-family closure requires the two finite identities

\[
\boxed{
R^{(A)}_{300/003}=-R^{(A)}_5,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
R^{(C)}_{300/003}=-R^{(C)}_5.
}
\]

Equivalently, after expanding in the residual-source tower, the coefficients of

\[
\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4,\qquad
\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4
\]

must vanish.

If either does not vanish, preserve

\[
\boxed{
R^{(A)}_7\,\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4
+
R^{(C)}_7\,\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4
}
\]

as the seven-family residual.

---

Not from the current source material in the uploaded files.

- the \(Y^a\) grade-five row;

=

=

\]

plus \(N^{(0)}_{0..4}\) and \(W_{\pm,0..4}\).

Those \(L_3/R_3\) coefficient lists are not supplied. The current project state explicitly identifies \(L_3N_0R_0/L_0N_0R_3\) as needing actual third-Fréchet inverse-square-root coefficient identities, and warns not to close this route with generic matrix algebra. turn44file9

# 1. \(L_2/L_3\) normalization audit

## Finding

This is the only simple possible rescue. It must be checked before anything else.

There are two conventions:

### Derivative-normalized Fréchet tensors

\[
L_2=D^2W,\qquad L_3=D^3W.
\]

### Homogeneous Taylor coefficients

\[
L_2=\frac{1}{2!}D^2W,\qquad
L_3=\frac{1}{3!}D^3W.
\]

Your row work has mostly followed a **derivative-normalized / source-tag coefficient convention**, because the row equations explicitly carry multiplicity factors such as

\[
\alpha_1+2\alpha_2,\qquad 2\alpha_5+\alpha_7,
\]

and the second-Fréchet coefficient formulas used earlier include the raw second-derivative-type factors. The attached work states that recurrence/convolution gates are finite bookkeeping, not a proof, and that coefficient-table lanes must use the same \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\) normalization. 

## Exact audit

Let

\[
\rho_{111}
\]

be the \(111\) contribution,

\[
\rho_{2}
\]

the sum of all \(L_2/R_2\)-family contributions,

\[
\rho_{3}
\]

the sum of all \(L_3/R_3\)-family contributions.

Then the tested residual has the form

\[
\boxed{
\rho(\lambda_2,\lambda_3)
=
\rho_{111}
+
\lambda_2\rho_2
+
\lambda_3\rho_3.
}
\]

If the numeric script used derivative tensors while the paper uses homogeneous Taylor coefficients, then rerun with

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_2=\frac12,\qquad \lambda_3=\frac16.
}
\]

If the script already used the paper’s row convention, then

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_2=1,\qquad \lambda_3=1.
}
\]

## Diagnosis

A normalization mismatch is possible only if

\[
\rho(1,1)\ne0
\quad\text{but}\quad
\rho\!\left(\frac12,\frac16\right)=0.
\]

This is easy to test from the existing script if it retains per-family residuals. If it does not vanish under \((1/2,1/6)\), normalization is not the rescue.

**Rank:** possible but narrow. Check once.

# 2. Quotient-line audit

## Finding

The script’s quotient line

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(X_0JX_4-X_4JX_0+X_3JX_1-X_1JX_3)
\]

is plausible as the canonical fixed midpoint line **if** the \(X_i\) are the same one-pair midpoint fixed-sector coefficients used to define

\[
Q_{7,m}^q(C)=[B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C)]
\in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

The project target has consistently been the fixed quotient

\[
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
\]

with determinant pairing used only as a coordinate after the quotient object exists, not as the definition. 

## Exact audit

Let the script line be

\[
A_{5,\rm scr}^{\mathfrak f}=u_{\rm scr}I+v_{\rm scr}S.
\]

Let the true package line be

\[
A_{5,\rm pkg}^{\mathfrak f}=u_{\rm pkg}I+v_{\rm pkg}S.
\]

The determinant functional should be

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D_{\rm pkg}(Z)
=
v_{\rm pkg}\pi_I(Z)-u_{\rm pkg}\pi_S(Z).
}
\]

If the script used

\[
\mathcal D_{\rm scr}(Z)
=
v_{\rm scr}\pi_I(Z)-u_{\rm scr}\pi_S(Z),
\]

then the correction is

\[
\boxed{
(\mathcal D_{\rm pkg}-\mathcal D_{\rm scr})(Z)
=
(v_{\rm pkg}-v_{\rm scr})\pi_I(Z)
-
(u_{\rm pkg}-u_{\rm scr})\pi_S(Z).
}
\]

If

\[
A_{5,\rm pkg}^{\mathfrak f}=\lambda A_{5,\rm scr}^{\mathfrak f},
\]

then there is no quotient-line mismatch, only an irrelevant scalar rescaling of the determinant test. If the two lines are not proportional, the entire raw residual test must be rerun.

## Diagnosis

No uploaded evidence indicates a different normalized quintic line. The current target is explicitly \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}((1-\Pi_{1,1})C_{\mathcal W})\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\), equivalently \(Q_{7,m}^q(C_{\mathcal W})=Q_{7,m}^q(\Pi_{1,1}C_{\mathcal W})\). 

**Rank:** unlikely, unless the script’s \(X_i\) are not the true midpoint-trivialized one-pair coefficients.

# 3. Source-bidegree projection audit

## Finding

This is a serious separator.

The raw residuals are cubic finite-order source terms of type \((1,1,5)\). The working theorem was not supposed to be “all raw cubic terms vanish”; it was supposed to be a source-bidegree quotient-compatibility theorem:

\[
Q_7^q(C)=Q_7^q(\Pi_{1,1}C),
\]

or equivalently

\[
Q_7^q((1-\Pi_{1,1})C)=0.
\]

The record already says the formal \((1,1)\) projection mechanism kills higher homogeneous transfer pieces, but the paper does not define the needed source projector, fixed-target quotient extractor, or compatibility theorem. 

## Does \((1-\Pi_{1,1})\) remove these residual monomials?

Only if \(\Pi_{1,1}\) is being defined to discard all cubic source-degree terms before \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\).

But under the UV-026 raw test, these monomials are precisely in the non-\((1,1)\) sector. Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
(1-\Pi_{1,1})\text{ keeps them, not removes them.}
}
\]

If a new projection rule removes them, then the theorem has changed. The rule would need to be:

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\le 2}^{\rm source}\text{ or }\Pi_{1,1}^{\rm transfer}
\text{ kills all cubic source-degree }(1,1,5)\text{ monomials before }B_7^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

That is not the current UV-026 statement. It would be a UV-023/UV-024 projection theorem: source-defined projection before quotient extraction, plus proof that \(Q_7^q\) commutes with the projection. The file record explicitly says post-quotient or post-determinant projection is invalid; the projector must be pre-quotient and source-defined. 

## Diagnosis

The raw residuals survive the old UV-026 \((1-\Pi_{1,1})\) test. Projection can rescue the program only by replacing raw UV-026 with a stronger, explicitly defined source-bidegree quotient package.

**Rank:** likely part of the corrected theorem, but not currently available as a proof.

---

# 4. Package counterterm audit

## Finding

This is the main diagnosis.

The raw seven-family expansion is not the actual normalized quotient package. The corrected object must include the order-7 package correction terms coming from:

\[
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2},
\]

fixed-target midpoint trivialization,

moving quotient-line connection,

and corrected reduced-package normalization.

The project record already separates the raw coefficient work from the actual quotient-valued edge package: UV-010 needs an actual order-7 quotient defect as an analytic section in a fixed quotient bundle, and a trivialization from the moving \(h_1\) quotient to the midpoint quotient. 

The same record says the actual package layer should use the corrected-whitening cross-effect and that diagonal/collision vanishing of the order-7 quotient component is the obstruction; a diagonal counterterm alone is not promotion-ready. 

## Minimal quotient-level counterterm

Let

\[
Z_{\rm raw}
=
B_7^{\mathfrak f}\left((1-\Pi_{1,1})C_{\rm raw}\right)
\in\mathfrak f.
\]

Let

\[
\rho_{\rm raw}
=
\mathcal D(Z_{\rm raw}).
\]

Then the required correction is any \(C_{\rm corr}\) satisfying

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D\left(
B_7^{\mathfrak f}\left((1-\Pi_{1,1})C_{\rm corr}\right)
\right)
=
-\rho_{\rm raw}.
}
\]

Equivalently, in quotient form,

\[
\boxed{
\left[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}\left((1-\Pi_{1,1})C_{\rm corr}\right)
\right]
=
-
[Z_{\rm raw}]
\quad\text{in}\quad
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
}
\]

This is the only invariant statement; matrix-level representatives are not unique.

## Concrete decomposition

The correction should be decomposed as

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm corr}
=
C_{\rm amp}
+
C_{\rm triv}
+
C_{\rm conn}
+
C_{\rm red}
+
C_{\rm proj}.
}
\]

where:

### Amplitude normalization

\[
C_{\rm amp}
\]

comes from expanding

\[
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}
\]

against lower-order raw coefficients. If

\[
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}
=
\mu_{-2}\delta^{-2}+\mu_{-1}\delta^{-1}+\mu_0+\mu_1\delta+\cdots,
\]

then order-7 receives contributions of the schematic form

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm amp}^{(7)}
=
\mu_1 B_6^{\rm raw}
+
\mu_2 B_5^{\rm raw}
+\cdots
}
\]

restricted to the same source-bidegree sector. The exact \(\mu_i\) depend on the amplitude chart.

### Fixed-target midpoint trivialization

\[
C_{\rm triv}
\]

comes from replacing a moving quotient line

\[
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h_1)
\]

by the fixed midpoint line

\[
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

If

\[
A_5(h_1)=A_5(m)+\epsilon \dot A_5+\frac{\epsilon^2}{2}A_5''+\cdots,
\]

then determinant functionals satisfy

\[
\mathcal D_{h_1}(Z)
=
\mathcal D_m(Z)
+
\det(Z,\epsilon\dot A_5+\cdots).
\]

So the correction must include the connection terms generated by derivatives of the quotient line.

### Moving quotient-line connection

\[
C_{\rm conn}
\]

is the same effect expressed intrinsically: the quotient bundle

\[
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)
\]

has a connection under midpoint trivialization. The connection term is exactly what raw fixed-line determinant testing omits.

### Corrected reduced-package normalization

\[
C_{\rm red}
\]

comes from the fact that the corrected reduced package is not simply the raw whitened matrix coefficient. Earlier C-work repeatedly found that reduced-package blow-up hypotheses leave a free determinant slot unless an actual diagonal-merger / collision-functoriality theorem kills it. 

### Projection correction

\[
C_{\rm proj}
\]

is required if \(\Pi_{1,1}\) does not commute strictly with \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\). The record says this commutation is missing and must be proved before projection-based quotient invisibility can be promoted. 

---

# Ranked diagnosis

## 1. Required counterterm / package normalization — most likely

The raw seven-family package is missing the order-7 quotient package correction. This is the main diagnosis.

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm corr}=C_{\rm amp}+C_{\rm triv}+C_{\rm conn}+C_{\rm red}+C_{\rm proj}.
}
\]

## 2. Source-bidegree projection mismatch — likely part of the corrected theorem

The current residuals are exactly non-\((1,1)\) cubic terms, so raw \((1-\Pi_{1,1})\) retains them. A projection can rescue the theorem only if a source-defined projector and \(Q_7^q\)-compatibility lemma are added before \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\). This is not currently in the paper. 

## 3. \(L_2/L_3\) normalization mismatch — possible, check once

Run the residual with

\[
\lambda_2=\frac12,\qquad \lambda_3=\frac16.
\]

If the residual persists, eliminate this separator. If it vanishes, the failure was a script convention error.

## 4. Quotient-line mismatch — less likely

The script line is probably correct if it computes the same midpoint \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\). If there is a mismatch, the determinant functional correction is

\[
(v_{\rm pkg}-v_{\rm scr})\pi_I-(u_{\rm pkg}-u_{\rm scr})\pi_S.
\]

No current evidence points to a different package line.

## 5. Raw UV-026 genuinely false — yes, under old wording

If UV-026 means

\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}\left((1-\Pi_{1,1})C_{\rm raw}\right)
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
\]

then it is false under the current source-constrained numerical tests.

The corrected theorem must be:

\[
\boxed{
B_7^{\mathfrak f}\left((1-\Pi_{1,1})(C_{\rm raw}+C_{\rm corr})\right)
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
}
\]

## Honest verdict

The raw seven-family failure should now be promoted to a negative result for old UV-026. The next proof obligation is not another family expansion; it is the construction of the quotient-package counterterm \(C_{\rm corr}\), with the normalization and projection layers made explicit.

## Claim

The fixed-target quotient-line connection correction is exactly

\[
q_{\mathrm{conn},k}
=
\sum_{i=1}^{k}\omega(B_{k-i},A_i),
\]

provided \(A_i,B_j\) are **coefficient-normalized Taylor coefficients** in the expansion

\[
A(h)=\sum_{i\ge0}(h-m)^iA_i,\qquad
B(h)=\sum_{j\ge0}(h-m)^jB_j.
\]

If \(A_i,B_j\) are derivative-normalized instead, i.e.

\[
A(h)=\sum_{i\ge0}\frac{(h-m)^i}{i!}\partial_h^iA(m),
\]

then the correction has binomial/factorial weights. Since your target formula explicitly asks for

\[
q_{\mathrm{conn},k}=\sum_{i=1}^k\omega(B_{k-i},A_i),
\]

I use the coefficient-normalized convention below.

This connection term **can in principle cancel** the raw seven-family residual, but it is not computable yet without lower-order fixed-sector package data

\[
B_j\quad(j<7)
\]

in the same non-\((1,1)\) source sector.

---

## Derivation

Let

\[
A(h)=A_0+(h-m)A_1+(h-m)^2A_2+\cdots
\]

and

\[
B(h)=B_0+(h-m)B_1+(h-m)^2B_2+\cdots.
\]

Use the two-dimensional determinant pairing on

\[
\mathfrak f=\operatorname{span}\{I,S\}.
\]

If

\[
B=u_BI+v_BS,\qquad A=u_AI+v_AS,
\]

then

\[
\omega(B,A)=u_Bv_A-u_Av_B.
\]

The moving quotient coordinate is

\[
\omega(B(h),A(h)).
\]

The raw fixed-target test used

\[
\omega(B(h),A_0).
\]

Therefore the omitted connection piece is

\[
\omega(B(h),A(h))-\omega(B(h),A_0)
=
\omega(B(h),A(h)-A_0).
\]

Since

\[
A(h)-A_0=\sum_{i\ge1}(h-m)^iA_i,
\]

we get

\[
\omega(B(h),A(h))-\omega(B(h),A_0)
=
\sum_{j\ge0}\sum_{i\ge1}(h-m)^{i+j}\omega(B_j,A_i).
\]

Thus the coefficient of \((h-m)^k\) is

\[
\boxed{
q_{\mathrm{conn},k}
=
\sum_{i=1}^{k}\omega(B_{k-i},A_i).
}
\]

This is the quotient-line connection counterterm.

---

## Specialization to the two residual monomials

Let

\[
M_A:=\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4,
\qquad
M_C:=\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4.
\]

The raw seven-family residual has determinant coefficients

\[
R_7^{(A)}
\quad\text{on}\quad
M_A,
\]

and

\[
R_7^{(C)}
\quad\text{on}\quad
M_C.
\]

To cancel them by quotient-line connection, we need

\[
\boxed{
q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[M_A]=-R_7^{(A)},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[M_C]=-R_7^{(C)}.
}
\]

Write

\[
A_i=u_i^AI+v_i^AS,
\]

and write the coefficient of monomial \(M\) in \(B_j\) as

\[
B_j[M]=u_{j,M}^BI+v_{j,M}^BS.
\]

Then

\[
\omega(B_j[M],A_i)
=
u_{j,M}^Bv_i^A-u_i^Av_{j,M}^B.
\]

Therefore the connection corrections for the two monomials are

\[
\boxed{
q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[M_A]
=
\sum_{i=1}^{7}
\left(
u_{7-i,M_A}^Bv_i^A
-
u_i^Av_{7-i,M_A}^B
\right),
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[M_C]
=
\sum_{i=1}^{7}
\left(
u_{7-i,M_C}^Bv_i^A
-
u_i^Av_{7-i,M_C}^B
\right).
}
\]

So the connection cancels the residual iff

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{i=1}^{7}
\left(
u_{7-i,M_A}^Bv_i^A
-
u_i^Av_{7-i,M_A}^B
\right)
=
-R_7^{(A)},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{i=1}^{7}
\left(
u_{7-i,M_C}^Bv_i^A
-
u_i^Av_{7-i,M_C}^B
\right)
=
-R_7^{(C)}.
}
\]

---

## What must be constructed

To test this for

\[
q_0(t)=1+\frac12(t-m),
\qquad
q_0(t)=1+(t-m),
\]

we need two coefficient tables.

### 1. Moving quotient-line table

We need

\[
A_i=[(h-m)^i]A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)
\]

for

\[
i=1,\ldots,7.
\]

In coordinates:

\[
A_i=u_i^AI+v_i^AS.
\]

If \(A(h)\) is low-degree for the tested linear baselines, many \(A_i\) will vanish. That should be checked from the actual \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)\) formula.

### 2. Lower fixed-sector representative table

For each residual monomial

\[
M_A=\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4,
\qquad
M_C=\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4,
\]

we need

\[
B_j[M_A],\qquad B_j[M_C]
\]

for

\[
j=0,\ldots,6.
\]

In coordinates:

\[
B_j[M_A]=u_{j,A}^BI+v_{j,A}^BS,
\]

\[
B_j[M_C]=u_{j,C}^BI+v_{j,C}^BS.
\]

These \(B_j\) are **lower-order fixed-sector representatives in the same source sector**, before quotienting. They are not the raw \(B_7\) residual; they are lower-order package coefficients whose moving-line coordinate was omitted by the fixed-target determinant test.

---

## Does this compute from the current raw seven-family data?

No. The raw seven-family computation gives

\[
R_7^{(A)},\qquad R_7^{(C)}
\]

at order \(7\). It does not by itself give the lower-order representatives

\[
B_0,\ldots,B_6
\]

in the same source monomials.

So the connection correction is now derived, but not evaluable without a lower-order package table.

---

## Minimal missing coefficient tables

For the two residual monomials, construct:

\[
\boxed{
A_i=A_{5,i}^{\mathfrak f}
\quad (i=1,\ldots,7).
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
B_j[\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4],
\quad
B_j[\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4]
\quad (j=0,\ldots,6).
}
\]

Then compute:

\[
\boxed{
q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4]
=
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega(B_{7-i}[\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4],A_i).
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4]
=
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega(B_{7-i}[\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4],A_i).
}
\]

Then test:

\[
\boxed{
R_7^{(A)}+q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4]=0.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
R_7^{(C)}+q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4]=0.
}
\]

---

## Important convention check

If the script used derivative-normalized \(A_i\) and \(B_j\), then the correction is not the unweighted sum. It is:

\[
\boxed{
q_{\mathrm{conn},k}
=
\sum_{i=1}^{k}
\binom{k}{i}
\omega(B_{k-i},A_i)
}
\]

where

\[
A_i=\partial_h^iA(m),\qquad B_j=\partial_h^jB(m).
\]

If the script used coefficient-normalized Taylor coefficients, then the unweighted formula is correct.

This convention must match the residual computation before testing cancellation.

---

## Classification

The quotient-line connection is a plausible missing counterterm.

It is not another raw Fréchet family. It is the correction from comparing

\[
\omega(B(h),A(h))
\]

to

\[
\omega(B(h),A_0).
\]

The exact counterterm is:

\[
\boxed{
C_{\mathrm{conn},7}
\text{ such that }
\mathcal D(C_{\mathrm{conn},7})=
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega(B_{7-i},A_i).
}
\]

More invariantly:

\[
\boxed{
[B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C_{\mathrm{conn}})]
=
\sum_{i=1}^{7}[B_{7-i}]\cdot[A_i]
\quad\text{as the quotient-line connection correction.}
}
\]

But it cannot yet be confirmed to cancel the nonconstant-baseline residuals without the lower-order \(B_j\) table.

---

## Honest verdict

The fixed-target quotient-line connection counterterm is:

\[
\boxed{
q_{\mathrm{conn},7}
=
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega(B_{7-i},A_i).
}
\]

For the two surviving monomials:

\[
\boxed{
q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4]
=
\sum_{i=1}^{7}
\omega(B_{7-i}[\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4],A_i),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4]
=
\sum_{i=1}^{7}
\omega(B_{7-i}[\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4],A_i).
}
\]

The required missing data are exactly:

\[
\boxed{
A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f},\ldots,A_{5,7}^{\mathfrak f}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
B_0,\ldots,B_6
\text{ in the two residual source monomials.}
}
\]

Without those, the connection counterterm is derived but not numerically testable against the two nonconstant baselines.

## 1. What can be constructed now

=

or the paper’s equivalent canonical definition of the quintic line. If the script’s \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is exactly this midpoint-trivialized line, then \(A_i\) is computable by expanding those \(X_j(h)\). If the script uses only \(A_0=A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\), then it lacks precisely the connection data

## 5. Why I cannot honestly fill the table now

The current source materials support the recursive extraction of raw coefficient tables, but repeatedly mark the actual \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\) coefficient map and normalized quotient package as missing. The UV ledger states that UV-024 is to define the pre-determinant fixed-sector order-7 coefficient \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C)\) before \(\Phi_K\) or determinant scalarization, and to prove the non-\((1,1)\) quotient-gauge statement; it is not already in the source. 

The project notes also say the guarded source block is pre-whitening only and does not assert \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\), \(Q_{7,m}^q\), or cubic gauge. 

Therefore any concrete \(B_j\)-values I wrote now would be invented unless they come from a newly specified package representative.

---

## 6. Correct next theorem statement

The missing lemma should be:

```tex
\begin{lemma}[Moving quotient-line connection table]
Let \(C_{\mathrm{pkg}}(h)\) be the actual normalized corrected-whitening
cross-effect representative before quotienting, and write
\[
B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}(h)
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f} C_{\mathrm{pkg}}(h)
=
\sum_{j\ge0}(h-m)^jB_j.
\]
Let
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)=\sum_{i\ge0}(h-m)^iA_i.
\]
For each residual monomial \(M\), the fixed-target determinant differs from
the moving quotient determinant at order \(7\) by
\[
q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[M]
=
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega(B_{7-i}[M],A_i).
\]
\end{lemma}
```

Then add the finite table for

\[
A_i,\quad B_j[M_A],\quad B_j[M_C].
\]

## Claim

The object you want,

\[
B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}(h)
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^{\le 7}]\,
(1-\Pi_{1,1})C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}(h),
\]

is **not yet well-defined in the current source**. It can be specified as a definition target, but the paper/work files still lack the definitions needed to make it an actual computable object.

The precise failure is not at \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}\), nor at the formal quotient line. It fails earlier: the current source has a guarded **pre-whitening tagged source block** and a conditional matrix-cross-effect template, but it does not define the normalized corrected-whitening package representative after source-bidegree projection, amplitude normalization, midpoint trivialization, and quotient-line connection. The guarded source block explicitly says it does not assert \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\), \(Q_{7,m}^q\), \(\Pi_{1,1}\), or UV-026 gauge. 

## Status

A correct definition can be drafted, but the current paper does not yet supply enough structure to compute

\[
B_j[M_A],\quad B_j[M_C],\qquad j=0,\ldots,6.

# Proposed definition scaffold

## 1. Actual corrected-whitening cross-effect

Start with the tagged pre-whitening source block

\[
\mathcal B_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
(G_{2,-}^{\corr},N_2^{\corr},G_{2,+}^{\corr}),
\]

already defined by substituting tagged corrected source perturbations into the corrected same-point and mixed block formulas. 

Let

\[
\mathcal W
\]

denote the corrected-whitening transfer that maps a pre-whitening block triple

\[
(G_-,N,G_+)
\]

to the whitened matrix

\[
G_-^{-1/2}NG_+^{-1/2}.
\]

Then the natural matrix cross-effect is

\[
\boxed{
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
\mathcal W(\mathcal B_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2))
-
\mathcal W(\mathcal B_1(a_1,h_1))
-
\mathcal W(\mathcal B_1(a_2,h_2))
+
\mathcal W(\mathcal B_0).
}
\]

This is the same conditional definition template the current notes identify:

\[
C_{\mathcal W}
=
W(B+a_1L_1+a_2L_2)-W(B+a_1L_1)-W(B+a_2L_2)+W(B),
\]

available before \(\Phi_K\), but not yet promoted to the normalized quotient package. 

At this point the object is still **raw**. It is not \(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}\).

---

## 2. Source-bidegree projection before quotienting

The source-bidegree projection must be defined **before** fixed-sector extraction and before determinant testing. The current source repeatedly rejects post-quotient or post-determinant projection and says the missing package needs a source-defined \(\Pi_{1,1}\) plus compatibility with \(Q_7^q\). 

Define source tags \(\tau_1,\tau_2\). Then, for any tagged matrix series \(F(\tau_1,\tau_2)\), define

\[
\Pi_{1,1}F:=[\tau_1\tau_2]F.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
(1-\Pi_{1,1})F
\]

keeps every source-bidegree except the exactly bilinear cross term. In the present failure, the residual monomials are non-\((1,1)\) cubic terms; the old raw UV-026 was precisely testing whether these are quotient-gauge. The current files state UV-024/UV-026 as requiring \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}((1-\Pi_{1,1})C)\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\), not scalar hiding. 

So the projected raw object is

\[
\boxed{
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw,\nonlin}
:=
(1-\Pi_{1,1})C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}.
}
\]

But this is still not normalized.

---

## 3. Amplitude normalization

The package convention used throughout the recent calculations is

\[
\operatorname{Triv}_{1\to m}
\left(
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}
\right).
\]

Thus the normalized matrix-level object must include the amplitude factor

\[
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}.
\]

Define

\[
\boxed{
\widehat C_{\mathcal W}^{\amp}
:=
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}\,
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw,\nonlin}.
}
\]

This operation is **not innocent**: expanding \(-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}\) can mix lower-order coefficients into the order-7 slot. Therefore the lower moving representatives \(B_0,\ldots,B_6\) required by the connection formula cannot be taken from the raw seven-family \(z^7\) table. They must come from this amplitude-normalized package.

The UV-010 formulation notes likewise state that the normalized fixed-target theorem requires applying moving-to-midpoint trivialization to \(a_1^{-1}\overline{\mathcal E}_{12}^{(7;1)}\), with descent and merger kept downstream. 

---

## 4. Midpoint fixed-target trivialization

Let the moving quotient line be

\[
A(h)=A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),
\]

and the midpoint line be

\[
A_0=A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

On the good patch \(A_0\neq0\), determinant pairing gives a local moving-to-midpoint quotient chart. The current project notes say this trivialization is locally solved on the good patch, while the \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\) locus is a rank jump needing exclusion or a separate convention. 

Define a quotient-line trivialization operator

\[
\operatorname{Triv}_{h\to m}.
\]

At representative level, the only invariant requirement is:

\[
\left[
\operatorname{Triv}_{h\to m}Z(h)
\right]_{\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_0}
=
[Z(h)]_{\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A(h)}.
\]

A convenient determinant-coordinate formulation is:

\[
\omega(\operatorname{Triv}_{h\to m}Z(h),A_0)
=
\omega(Z(h),A(h)).
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\operatorname{Triv}_{h\to m}Z(h)
=
Z(h)+\Theta_{\mathrm{conn}}(Z,A;h),
\]

where \(\Theta_{\mathrm{conn}}\) is any representative-level correction whose determinant coordinate realizes

\[
\omega(Z(h),A(h))-\omega(Z(h),A_0).
\]

This is exactly the connection term you derived:

\[
q_{\mathrm{conn},k}
=
\sum_{i=1}^k \omega(B_{k-i},A_i).
\]

---

## 5. Quotient-line connection convention

For a moving representative

\[
B(h)=\sum_{j\ge0}(h-m)^jB_j
\]

and

\[
A(h)=\sum_{i\ge0}(h-m)^iA_i,
\]

coefficient-normalized convention gives

\[
\boxed{
q_{\mathrm{conn},k}
=
\sum_{i=1}^k\omega(B_{k-i},A_i).
}
\]

Derivative-normalized convention gives

\[
\boxed{
q_{\mathrm{conn},k}
=
\sum_{i=1}^k\binom{k}{i}\omega(B_{k-i},A_i).
}
\]

This connection is part of the package definition if the package is meant to live in the fixed midpoint quotient. It is not a raw Fréchet family.

---

## 6. Fixed-sector extraction and \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\)

Only after steps 1–5 define:

\[
\boxed{
C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}(h)
:=
\operatorname{Triv}_{h\to m}
\left(
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}(h)
\right).
}
\]

Then define the moving package representative

\[
\boxed{
B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}(h)
:=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^{\le7}]
C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}(h).
}
\]

And finally

\[
\boxed{
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
:=
[z^7]\,B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}(m)
}
\]

or, in the moving \(h\)-coefficient version needed for the connection table,

\[
\boxed{
B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}(h)
=
\sum_{j=0}^7(h-m)^jB_j+O((h-m)^8).
}
\]

This is the first point where \(B_j\) can be defined.

---

# Lower moving representative coefficients

For

\[
M_A=\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4,
\qquad
M_C=\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4,
\]

define

\[
\boxed{
B_j[M_A]
:=
[(h-m)^jM_A]\,
B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}(h),
\qquad
j=0,\ldots,6,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
B_j[M_C]
:=
[(h-m)^jM_C]\,
B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}(h),
\qquad
j=0,\ldots,6.
}
\]

Here \([(h-m)^jM]\) means: extract the coefficient of the source monomial \(M\) in the \((h-m)^j\)-coefficient of the moving fixed-sector representative. If

\[
B_j[M_\bullet]=u_{j,\bullet}^BI+v_{j,\bullet}^BS,
\]

then the connection correction is

\[
\boxed{
q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[M_\bullet]
=
\sum_{i=1}^7
(u_{7-i,\bullet}^Bv_i^A-u_i^Av_{7-i,\bullet}^B).
}
\]

This is the correct table target.

---

# Is the displayed formula currently well-defined?

Only as a **definition schema**, not as a computable object.

The current source supports the ingredients up to the tagged pre-whitening source block and a conditional raw matrix cross-effect. It does **not** yet define all of:

1. an actual source-weight-linear two-atom input \(X^{[1]}\) after whitening;
2. a source-bidegree projector \(\Pi_{1,1}\) compatible with \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\);
3. the pre-determinant coefficient map \(C\mapsto B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C)\) for the actual corrected-whitening cross-effect;
4. the normalized package representative including \(-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}\);
5. the representative-level midpoint trivialization \( \operatorname{Triv}_{h\to m}\);
6. the moving lower representatives \(B_j\) for \(j<7\).

These are not merely missing coefficient tables. They are missing definitions/theorems. The current ledger explicitly states that the paper does not define \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C)\) for the actual corrected-whitening cross-effect, though it has enough infrastructure to draft a minimal definition block. 

The UV ledger similarly defines UV-024 as the task of defining \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C)\), \(Q_{7,m}^q(C)\), and proving the non-\((1,1)\) quotient-gauge theorem; it is not recorded as already present.

C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}

with the actual \(\mathcal W\), \(\mathcal B_2\), \(\mathcal B_1^{(i)}\), source tags, amplitude variables, and collision chart fixed.

on tagged matrix series, with the rule

## Assistant (2026-04-24 16:37:52)

_Thought for 9s_

Below is a paper-ready conditional layer. It is deliberately **definition-first**: it does not claim UV-026 is proved. It defines the normalized package object that the raw seven-family computation failed to model.

```tex
\begin{definition}[Corrected-whitening matrix cross-effect before scalarization]
\label{def:corrected-whitening-matrix-cross-effect}
Let
\[
\mathcal B_0=(G_-^{(0)},N^{(0)},G_+^{(0)})
\]
be the baseline corrected block, and let
\[
\mathcal B_1(a_i,h_i)
\]
denote the one-source tagged corrected block obtained by substituting only the
\(i\)-th tagged source perturbation into the corrected same-point and mixed
block formulae.  Let
\[
\mathcal B_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
\]
be the tagged two-source corrected block.

Let
\[
\mathcal W(G_-,N,G_+):=G_-^{-1/2}NG_+^{-1/2}
\]
be the corrected-whitening transfer, defined on the good analytic patch where
the inverse square roots are holomorphic.

Define the matrix cross-effect before applying \(\Phi_K\), determinant
scalarization, or quotient extraction by
\[
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathcal W(\mathcal B_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2))
-\mathcal W(\mathcal B_1(a_1,h_1))
-\mathcal W(\mathcal B_1(a_2,h_2))
+\mathcal W(\mathcal B_0).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Source-bidegree projection before quotient extraction]
\label{def:source-bidegree-projection-before-quotient}
Work with formal source tags \(\tau_1,\tau_2\) retained through the matrix
cross-effect.  For a tagged matrix series \(F(\tau_1,\tau_2)\), define
\[
\Pi_{1,1}F:=[\tau_1\tau_2]F.
\]
Thus \(\Pi_{1,1}\) is applied before fixed-sector projection, before
\(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\), before determinant pairing, and before quotienting.

The non-\((1,1)\) source-bidegree component is
\[
(1-\Pi_{1,1})F.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Amplitude-normalized non-\((1,1)\) package representative]
\label{def:amplitude-normalized-non-11-package}
On the collision-cancellation chart, define the amplitude-normalized raw
package representative by
\[
\widehat C_{\mathcal W}^{\amp}
:=
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}.
\]
This is a matrix-valued object before \(\Phi_K\), before determinant
scalarization, and before quotient extraction.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Representative-level midpoint trivialization]
\label{def:representative-level-midpoint-trivialization}
Let
\[
A(h):=A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)
\]
be the moving quintic fixed-sector line, and assume
\[
A_0:=A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\neq0.
\]
For \(Z(h)\in\mathfrak f\), define a representative-level midpoint
trivialization
\[
\operatorname{Triv}_{h\to m}Z(h)
\]
to be any holomorphic representative satisfying
\[
\omega(\operatorname{Triv}_{h\to m}Z(h),A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m))
=
\omega(Z(h),A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)),
\]
where, for
\[
X=x_0I+x_1S,\qquad Y=y_0I+y_1S,
\]
we write
\[
\omega(X,Y):=x_0y_1-y_0x_1.
\]

Equivalently, \(\operatorname{Triv}_{h\to m}\) identifies the moving quotient
\[
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)
\]
with the fixed midpoint quotient
\[
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
\]
on the good patch \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\neq0\).
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Normalized corrected-whitening package representative]
\label{def:normalized-corrected-whitening-package-representative}
Define the normalized corrected-whitening package representative by
\[
C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}(h)
:=
\operatorname{Triv}_{h\to m}
\left(
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}(h)
\right).
\]

Define its moving fixed-sector representative through order \(7\) by
\[
B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}(h)
:=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^{\le7}]\,C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}(h).
\]
Equivalently,
\[
B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}(h)
=
\sum_{j=0}^{7}(h-m)^jB_j+O((h-m)^8),
\qquad
B_j\in\mathfrak f.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Lower moving package coefficients]
\label{def:lower-moving-package-coefficients}
Let \(M\) be a source monomial, for example
\[
M_A=\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4,
\qquad
M_C=\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4.
\]
Define
\[
B_j[M]:=[(h-m)^jM]\,B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}(h),
\qquad
0\le j\le 6.
\]
If
\[
B_j[M]=u_j^B[M]I+v_j^B[M]S,
\]
and
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)=\sum_{i\ge0}(h-m)^iA_i,
\qquad
A_i=u_i^AI+v_i^AS,
\]
then the order-\(7\) quotient-line connection correction on \(M\) is
\[
q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[M]
=
\sum_{i=1}^{7}
\omega(B_{7-i}[M],A_i).
\]
In coordinates,
\[
q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[M]
=
\sum_{i=1}^{7}
\left(
u_{7-i}^B[M]\,v_i^A
-
u_i^A\,v_{7-i}^B[M]
\right).
\]
If \(A_i,B_j\) are derivative-normalized rather than coefficient-normalized,
replace this formula by
\[
q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[M]
=
\sum_{i=1}^{7}
\binom{7}{i}
\omega(B_{7-i}[M],A_i).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Package-level order-\(7\) quotient extractor]
\label{def:package-level-order-7-quotient-extractor}
For the normalized package representative, define
\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
:=
[z^7]\,B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
The quotient-valued order-\(7\) extractor is
\[
Q_{7,m}^q(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
:=
\left[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
\right]
\in
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
\end{definition}
```

## Theorem obligations separated from definitions

### Definition-level material

The following are definitions, not claims of vanishing:

\[
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw},
\qquad
\Pi_{1,1},
\qquad
\widehat C_{\mathcal W}^{\amp},
\qquad
\operatorname{Triv}_{h\to m},
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}(h),
\qquad
B_j[M],
\qquad
Q_{7,m}^q.
\]

These definitions deliberately keep the work before \(\Phi_K\), before determinant scalarization, and before quotient shortcuts.

### Theorem obligation 1 — edge divisibility

One must prove that the normalized corrected package has the required collision edge law:

\[
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\]

extends holomorphically through the collision chart after midpoint trivialization, at least through the order needed to define \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\).

A typical target statement is:

\[
\operatorname{Triv}_{h\to m}
\left(
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\right)
=
\mathcal H_7^{\pkg}(m,\kappa,\delta^2)
\]

with holomorphic dependence on \((m,\kappa,\delta^2)\) on the good patch.

### Theorem obligation 2 — source-bidegree compatibility

The source-bidegree projection must be compatible with the order-\(7\) fixed-sector extractor:

\[
Q_{7,m}^q(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
=
Q_{7,m}^q(\Pi_{1,1}C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
\]

or equivalently

\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}
\bigl((1-\Pi_{1,1})C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}\bigr)
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

The raw seven-family computation shows this is false if \(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}\) is replaced by the raw seven-family object.

### Theorem obligation 3 — holomorphic extension at \(\delta=0\)

The definitions above assume that all pieces remain holomorphic after the normalization

\[
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}.
\]

This must be proved. The obstruction is exactly the sort of lower-order collision residue exposed by the raw seven-family failure.

### Theorem obligation 4 — quotient-line connection cancellation

For each residual monomial \(M\), one must prove

\[
R_7[M]+q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[M]=0,
\]

where \(R_7[M]\) is the raw fixed-target residual and

\[
q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[M]
=
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega(B_{7-i}[M],A_i).
\]

For the two current monomials, the targets are:

\[
R_7^{(A)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}
\omega(B_{7-i}[\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4],A_i)
=0,
\]

\[
R_7^{(C)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}
\omega(B_{7-i}[\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4],A_i)
=0.
\]

### Theorem obligation 5 — corrected UV-026

The corrected UV-026 statement should be:

\[
\boxed{
B_7^{\mathfrak f}
\left(
(1-\Pi_{1,1})C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}
\right)
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
Q_{7,m}^q(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
=
Q_{7,m}^q(\Pi_{1,1}C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}).
}
\]

This replaces the false raw theorem:

\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}
\left(
(1-\Pi_{1,1})C_{\raw}
\right)
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

## Exact missing definitions still needed for computability

The above makes the package layer precise as a conditional definition, but to compute the connection table one still needs:

\[
A_i=[(h-m)^i]A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),
\qquad
i=1,\ldots,7,
\]

and

\[
B_j[\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4],
\qquad
B_j[\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4],
\qquad
j=0,\ldots,6.
\]

These must be extracted from

\[
B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}(h)
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^{\le7}]
\operatorname{Triv}_{h\to m}
\left(
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}(h)
\right),
\]

not from the raw seven-family rows.

## Honest verdict

This definition layer is now clean:

\[
\boxed{
B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}(h)
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}[z^{\le7}]
\operatorname{Triv}_{h\to m}
\left(
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}(h)
\right).
}
\]

The raw seven-family failure is reclassified as evidence that the theorem must use \(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}\), not \(C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}\). The next proof obligation is the connection-cancellation theorem for the lower moving coefficients \(B_j[M]\).

\begin{remark}[Negative shortcuts not to reuse]
\label{rem:negative-shortcuts-not-to-reuse-package-frontier}
The following routes do not prove the corrected package quotient theorem.

\[

two-source cubic whitening families without an identification theorem.

Definition~\ref{def:tagged-two-atom-prewhitening-source-block} is
pre-whitening source data only.  It does not imply \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\)-gauge,
diagonal merger, quotient-output package coincidence, or UV-026.

\item The raw seven-family Fréchet package is not quotient-gauge in the tested
source-constrained nonconstant baselines.  The theorem object is the corrected
package representative
\[
C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr},
\]
not the raw seven-family sum.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}

## 1. Replace the normalized package representative definition

**Reason:** \(\operatorname{Triv}_{h\to m}\) is defined for \(Z(h)\in\mathfrak f_h\), not for a full \(2\times2\) matrix. So define a fixed-sector moving representative first.

**Replace the current `definition` named `Normalized corrected-whitening package representative` with:**

```tex
\begin{definition}[Normalized corrected-whitening fixed-sector package representative]
\label{def:normalized-corrected-whitening-package-representative}
Assume the amplitude-normalized package
\[
\widehat C_{\mathcal W}^{\mathrm{amp}}
\]
extends holomorphically to \(\delta=0\) through ordinary order \(7\).

First extract the moving fixed-sector representative
\[
Z_{\mathcal W}^{\mathfrak f}(h)
:=
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}[z^{\le7}]
\widehat C_{\mathcal W}^{\mathrm{amp}}(h)
\in\mathfrak f_h .
\]
Then define the normalized fixed-target package representative by
\[
B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}(h)
:=
\operatorname{Triv}_{h\to m}
\left(
Z_{\mathcal W}^{\mathfrak f}(h)
\right)
\in\mathfrak f_m .
\]
Equivalently,
\[
B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}(h)
=
\sum_{j=0}^{7}(h-m)^jB_j+O((h-m)^8),
\qquad
B_j\in\mathfrak f_m.
\]
Although the coefficients still depend on the moving parameter \(h\), the
representatives themselves have already been transported to the fixed
midpoint fiber \(\mathfrak f_m\).

When we write \(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}\) below, we mean this normalized
fixed-sector package representative \(B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}\), not
the full unprojected matrix cross-effect.
\end{definition}
```

This also makes the package-level \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\) definition cleaner.

## 2. Patch the package-level quotient extractor wording

**Reason:** after the replacement above, \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\) should be defined from \(B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}\), not from a full matrix object.

**Replace the current `Package-level order-\(7\) quotient extractor` definition with:**

```tex
\begin{definition}[Package-level order-\(7\) quotient extractor]
\label{def:package-level-order-7-quotient-extractor}
For the normalized fixed-target package representative, define
\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
:=
[z^7]\,B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}(m)
\in \mathfrak f_m .
\]
The quotient-valued order-\(7\) extractor is
\[
Q_{7,m}^q(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
:=
\left[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
\right]
\in
\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
\end{definition}
```

This keeps \(Q_{7,m}^q\) pre-determinant and quotient-valued, consistent with the UV-024 target. turn64file11

## 3. Add a Fréchet normalization convention

**Reason:** you already quarantined the \(L_2/L_3\) normalization rescue, but the finite coefficient section should explicitly say what convention its \(H_{\varepsilon,n}^{ab}\) and \(G_{\varepsilon,n}^{abc}\) use. Otherwise future agents will re-open the \(D^2\) vs \(D^2/2!\) issue.

**Insert near the start of `sec:finite-frechet-coefficient-calculus`, after the opening paragraph:**

```tex
\begin{remark}[Fr\'echet coefficient normalization]
\label{rem:frechet-coefficient-normalization}
The finite tables in this section use homogeneous Taylor coefficients in the
ordinary \(z\)-expansion of the inverse-square-root transfer.  Thus
\(\Lambda\), \(H\), and \(G\) denote the actual coefficient contributions to
the expanded matrix series, not raw multilinear derivatives \(D,D^2,D^3\)
unless explicitly stated.

Equivalently, if a separate computation uses derivative-normalized tensors,
then the dictionary is
\[
H_{\mathrm{Taylor}}=\frac{1}{2!}H_{\mathrm{deriv}},
\qquad
G_{\mathrm{Taylor}}=\frac{1}{3!}G_{\mathrm{deriv}}.
\]
All determinant tests in this paper use the Taylor-coefficient convention
unless the contrary is explicitly stated.
\end{remark}
```

This is consistent with the raw-package status note that both derivative-normalized and Taylor-normalized weights were tested and failed, but it fixes the convention for the paper’s own tables.

## 4. Add the missing UV-022 / source-weight-linear obligation

**Reason:** the theorem obligations currently cover edge divisibility, source-bidegree compatibility, midpoint trivialization, connection cancellation, and corrected UV-026. They should also explicitly include the upstream UV-022 obligation: the actual source-weight-linear input / exact one-amplitude collapse. The current work state repeatedly identifies this as a blocker. turn63file9

**Insert as a new first item in `rem:definition-level-material-and-theorem-obligations`:**

```tex
\item \textbf{Source-weight-linear package input.}
One must prove that the tagged pre-whitening source block induces the actual
source-weight-linear input used by the corrected-whitening cross-effect.  In
particular, the construction must not reintroduce the rejected signed-lift
shortcut in which multiplying an even whitened package by the source amplitude
leaves higher \(a^3,a^5,\ldots\) terms.  The package input must be invariant,
functorial through the corrected-whitening transfer, and compatible with
the quotient extractor \(Q_{7,m}^q\).
```

Then renumbering is automatic in LaTeX.

## 5. Add a residual-source tower vs highest-new tower guardrail

**Reason:** the current draft has homogeneous scalar grade and mentions grade-zero, but it should explicitly say the \(r_\rho\)-tower test comes before any \(q^{(7)}\)/highest-new collapse. This prevents agents from killing residuals prematurely by invoking same-tower closure too early. The findings say the best bridge data run through a single highest-new source only after the package bridge is established; it is not a license to skip residual-source tests. 

**Insert after `rem:grade-zero-sector-remains-open`:**

```tex
\begin{remark}[Residual-source tower before highest-new reduction]
\label{rem:residual-source-tower-before-highest-new-reduction}
The homogeneous scalar-grade convention organizes the local residual source
tower, but it does not by itself identify all residual-source coefficients with
the highest-new tower \(q^{(7)}\).  Finite quotient-gauge identities must first
be tested in the residual-source variables supplied by the corrected source
block.  Only a residual that survives this package-level test should be passed
to the later same-tower / highest-new reduction.

Thus the statement that the eventual local bridge should run through the
single highest-new source \(q^{(7)}\) is a downstream package-to-jet bridge
claim.  It is not a substitute for the pre-\(\Phi_K\), pre-determinant
fixed-sector quotient-gauge calculation.
\end{remark}
```

## 6. Add a short “representative choices are harmless only after quotienting” guardrail

**Reason:** the representative-level trivialization uses \(E_m,\ell_h\). The current definition says changes alter the representative by a multiple of \(A_m\). Add a theorem-obligation/remark that computations of \(B_j[M]\) must track representatives until the final quotient coordinate.

**Insert after `def:lower-moving-package-coefficients`:**

```tex
\begin{remark}[Representative choices and lower coefficient tables]
\label{rem:representative-choices-lower-coefficient-tables}
The lower coefficients \(B_j[M]\) are representative-dependent as elements of
\(\mathfrak f_m\), but the order-\(7\) connection coordinate
\[
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(B_{7-i}[M],A_i)
\]
is independent of changes of \(B_j[M]\) by multiples of \(A_m\).  Therefore
coefficient tables may choose any analytic section used by
Definition~\ref{def:representative-level-midpoint-trivialization}, but they
must keep that section fixed until the final quotient-coordinate calculation.
Changing representatives in the middle of a finite table is not a valid
simplification.
\end{remark}
```

---

## 7. Optional: update the UV ledger remark to avoid “UV-026 = seven-family” drift

The draft’s `rem:current-uv-chain-and-status` is already good, but I’d add one sentence at the end.

**Append to `rem:current-uv-chain-and-status`:**

```tex
In this formulation, UV-026 is a theorem about the normalized corrected
package representative.  The raw seven-family Fr\'echet sum is only a
diagnostic object; its failure under a matrix-output \(M^{[5]}\) convention
is recorded in Remark~\ref{rem:computational-status-raw-package} and does not
replace the corrected package theorem.
```

This reinforces the quarantine. The note already recommends treating the raw numerical failure as a warning, not the active theorem path. turn62file3

## Net

I would add **six small edits**, not another section:

1. Replace normalized package representative definition so trivialization acts on \(\mathfrak f_h\), not the full matrix.
2. Patch the \(Q_{7,m}^q\) extractor wording accordingly.
3. Add Fréchet coefficient normalization convention.
4. Add source-weight-linear package-input theorem obligation.
5. Add residual-source tower before highest-new reduction guardrail.
6. Add representative-choice guardrail for \(B_j[M]\).

Everything else looks structurally aligned with the latest frontier.

_Thought for 1m 27s_

Final pass: I would not add another substantive section. The current draft already has the two necessary layers: corrected package definitions and finite Fréchet/Sylvester coefficient contracts. The remaining edits are small consistency/guardrail insertions.

I would add three patches.

---

## 1. Add a good-patch quotient-line convention remark

**Placement:** immediately after `def:package-level-order-7-quotient-extractor`.

This makes explicit that determinant coordinates are valid only on the \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\neq0\) patch. It also prevents future agents from treating \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\) numerical tests as meaningful quotient tests. This matches the current working rule that determinant pairing is a good-patch coordinate, not the quotient definition itself. 

```tex
\begin{remark}[Good-patch convention for the quotient coordinate]
\label{rem:good-patch-convention-quotient-coordinate}
The quotient
\[
Q_{7,m}^q(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
\in
\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
\]
is the invariant object.  On a good patch where
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=u_5I+v_5S\ne0,
\]
the determinant coordinate
\[
\mathcal D_m(Z):=(v_5\pi_I-u_5\pi_S)\pi_{\mathfrak f_m}(Z)
\]
identifies this one-dimensional quotient with \(\mathbf C\).  This coordinate
is not available on the rank-jump locus
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=0.
\]
Consequently, baseline tests for which \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=0\) are
quotient-inconclusive, not evidence for or against the quotient-gauge theorem.
\end{remark}
```

---

## 2. Add the homogeneous scalar-grade theorem as an explicit theorem obligation

**Placement:** inside `rem:definition-level-material-and-theorem-obligations`, after the existing “Source-weight-linear package input” item.

You already have `rem:status-homogeneous-grade-lemmas`, but the theorem-obligation list should explicitly say that the homogeneous scalar-grade convention is not merely notation; it is a proof obligation. This avoids treating the \(Y\)-slot absence theorem as final rather than conditional on the source-grade normalization.

```tex
\item \textbf{Homogeneous scalar-grade source theorem.}
One must prove that the residual scalar source convention
\[
\operatorname{Gr}_a r
=
\frac{r^{(a+2)}(m)}{(a+2)!}(t-m)^{a+2}
\]
is the correct source-grade decomposition for the actual corrected package.
In particular, the absence of the \(Y\)-slot families at
\(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\) relies on this homogeneous scalar-grade convention.
If a different convention defines \(M^{[5]}\) as an ordinary matrix-output
order-\(5\) projection, then the \(Y\)-slot families
\[
L_1YR_1,\qquad L_2YR_0,\qquad L_0YR_2
\]
must be reopened and audited separately, as noted in
Remark~\ref{rem:quarantined-matrix-output-M5-convention}.
```

---

## 3. Fix a minor wording issue in the finite coefficient section

**Placement:** at the opening paragraph of `sec:finite-frechet-coefficient-calculus`.

The section says “This appendix” even though it is currently a `\section`, not necessarily in an appendix. Replace the first sentence with this neutral wording.

```tex
This section records the finite Fr\'echet/Sylvester coefficient recurrences
and finite gates used by the corrected-whitening package frontier of
Remark~\ref{rem:wip-first-cubic-source-transfer-target}.  These are table
contracts, not completed source tables.  Their role is to make the finite
computations auditable by agents and scripts without re-opening convention
choices already fixed in the main text.
```

---

## 4. Optional but useful: strengthen the raw-package failure remark by pointing to the quotient-line convention

**Placement:** append to `rem:computational-status-raw-package`.

This reinforces that the constant baseline result is inconclusive for structural reasons, while the nonconstant tests reject only the raw shortcut.

```tex
The word ``inconclusive'' for the constant baseline is meant in the precise
sense of Remark~\ref{rem:good-patch-convention-quotient-coordinate}: when
\(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\), the determinant coordinate does not define the
fixed-target quotient.  The nonconstant baseline failures occur on
nondegenerate good patches and therefore reject the raw Fr\'echet shortcut
under the tested convention.  They do not replace the corrected package
theorem, whose object is \(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}\).
```

---

## Net result

No more large structural insertions are needed. The final cleanups are:

1. good-patch quotient coordinate guardrail;
2. homogeneous scalar-grade theorem obligation;
3. minor wording fix from “appendix” to “section”;
4. optional reinforcement in the raw-package failure remark.

Everything else now looks aligned with the latest frontier: raw Fréchet paths are quarantined, the corrected package object is defined conditionally, the finite coefficient calculus is a toolkit, and the next real missing data are the moving package tables \(A_i\) and \(B_j[M]\).

## Order-count verification

Under the homogeneous scalar-grade convention,

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_a r
=
\frac{r^{(a+2)}(m)}{(a+2)!}(t-m)^{a+2},
\]

the draft’s accepted status is that the \(Y\)-slot families are absent at \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\). The first live non-\(Y\) gate is \(L_2N_0R_1/L_1N_0R_2\).

\[

\quad\Rightarrow\quad

\quad\Rightarrow\quad

So the order count is valid.

## Coefficient conventions from the draft

The finite Fréchet section uses homogeneous Taylor coefficients in the ordinary \(z\)-expansion, not raw derivative-normalized tensors. Therefore \(H\) and \(G\) already include the Taylor \(1/2!\) and \(1/3!\) normalization if those would appear in a raw derivative convention. 

The first-Fréchet table is:

\[
\Lambda_{\varepsilon,n}^{a}
=
-\sum_{i+j+k=n}
W_{\varepsilon,i}S_{\varepsilon,j}^aW_{\varepsilon,k},
\]

where \(S_{\varepsilon,n}^a\) solves

\[
S_{\varepsilon,n}^a
=
\Sigma_\varepsilon
\left(
X_{\varepsilon,n}^a
-
\sum_{j=1}^{n}
(P_{\varepsilon,j}S_{\varepsilon,n-j}^a+
S_{\varepsilon,n-j}^aP_{\varepsilon,j})
\right).
\]

The second-Fréchet table is:

\[
H_{\varepsilon,n}^{ab}
=
\sum_{i+j+k+\ell+m=n}
\left(
W_{\varepsilon,i}S_{\varepsilon,j}^bW_{\varepsilon,k}
S_{\varepsilon,\ell}^aW_{\varepsilon,m}
+
W_{\varepsilon,i}S_{\varepsilon,j}^aW_{\varepsilon,k}
S_{\varepsilon,\ell}^bW_{\varepsilon,m}
\right)
-
\sum_{i+j+k=n}
W_{\varepsilon,i}T_{\varepsilon,j}^{ab}W_{\varepsilon,k}.
\]

The \(T_{\varepsilon,n}^{ab}\) are defined by the second Sylvester recursion. 

---

## Required coefficient formulas

To keep notation compact, write

\[
\Lambda_{\varepsilon,n}^{[1]}:=\Lambda_{\varepsilon,n}^{a=1},
\qquad
\Lambda_{\varepsilon,n}^{[5]}:=\Lambda_{\varepsilon,n}^{a=5},
\]

and

\[
\mathcal L_{\varepsilon,n}^{\{1,1\}}:=H_{\varepsilon,n}^{1,1},
\qquad
\mathcal L_{\varepsilon,n}^{\{1,5\}}:=H_{\varepsilon,n}^{1,5}.
\]

For the right side, use \(\mathcal R_{+,n}^{\{\cdot,\cdot\}}\) for the same construction with \(+\)-side baseline tables.

### First-Fréchet rows

\[
\boxed{
[z^1]\Lambda_\pm^{[1]}
=
\Lambda_{\pm,1}^{[1]}
=
-\sum_{i+j+k=1}W_{\pm,i}S_{\pm,j}^{[1]}W_{\pm,k}.
}
\]

Expanded:

\[
\Lambda_{\pm,1}^{[1]}
=
-\left(
W_{\pm,1}S_{\pm,0}^{[1]}W_{\pm,0}
+
W_{\pm,0}S_{\pm,1}^{[1]}W_{\pm,0}
+
W_{\pm,0}S_{\pm,0}^{[1]}W_{\pm,1}
\right).
\]

If homogeneous grade \(1\) starts at ordinary order \(1\), then typically \(S_{\pm,0}^{[1]}=0\), reducing this to

\[
\Lambda_{\pm,1}^{[1]}
=
-W_{\pm,0}S_{\pm,1}^{[1]}W_{\pm,0}.
\]

But I leave the general formula above, because the draft says the grade-zero sector remains a separate obligation.

\[
\boxed{
[z^5]\Lambda_\pm^{[5]}
=
\Lambda_{\pm,5}^{[5]}
=
-\sum_{i+j+k=5}W_{\pm,i}S_{\pm,j}^{[5]}W_{\pm,k}.
}
\]

If homogeneous grade \(5\) starts at ordinary order \(5\), this reduces to

\[
\Lambda_{\pm,5}^{[5]}
=
-W_{\pm,0}S_{\pm,5}^{[5]}W_{\pm,0}.
\]

### Second-Fréchet rows

\[
\boxed{
[z^2]\mathcal L_-^{\{1,1\}}
=
H_{-,2}^{1,1}.
}
\]

Explicitly:

\[
H_{-,2}^{1,1}
=
\sum_{i+j+k+\ell+m=2}
\left(
W_{-,i}S_{-,j}^{[1]}W_{-,k}S_{-,\ell}^{[1]}W_{-,m}
+
W_{-,i}S_{-,j}^{[1]}W_{-,k}S_{-,\ell}^{[1]}W_{-,m}
\right)
-
\sum_{i+j+k=2}W_{-,i}T_{-,j}^{1,1}W_{-,k}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
H_{-,2}^{1,1}
=
2\sum_{i+j+k+\ell+m=2}
W_{-,i}S_{-,j}^{[1]}W_{-,k}S_{-,\ell}^{[1]}W_{-,m}
-
\sum_{i+j+k=2}W_{-,i}T_{-,j}^{1,1}W_{-,k}.
\]

\[
\boxed{
[z^6]\mathcal L_-^{\{1,5\}}
=
H_{-,6}^{1,5}.
}
\]

Explicitly:

\[
H_{-,6}^{1,5}
=
\sum_{i+j+k+\ell+m=6}
\left(
W_{-,i}S_{-,j}^{[5]}W_{-,k}S_{-,\ell}^{[1]}W_{-,m}
+
W_{-,i}S_{-,j}^{[1]}W_{-,k}S_{-,\ell}^{[5]}W_{-,m}
\right)
-
\sum_{i+j+k=6}W_{-,i}T_{-,j}^{1,5}W_{-,k}.
\]

If the homogeneous grade starts exactly at ordinary orders \(1\) and \(5\), the leading contribution simplifies to

\[
H_{-,6}^{1,5}
=
W_{-,0}S_{-,5}^{[5]}W_{-,0}S_{-,1}^{[1]}W_{-,0}
+
W_{-,0}S_{-,1}^{[1]}W_{-,0}S_{-,5}^{[5]}W_{-,0}
-
W_{-,0}T_{-,6}^{1,5}W_{-,0}.
\]

The right-side coefficients are the same construction with \(+\)-side data:

\[
\boxed{
[z^2]\mathcal R_+^{\{1,1\}}
=
H_{+,2}^{1,1},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
[z^6]\mathcal R_+^{\{1,5\}}
=
H_{+,6}^{1,5}.
}
\]

### Baseline middle

\[
\boxed{
N_0[0]=[z^0]N^{(0)}(z).
}
\]

The draft’s baseline mixed block coefficient contract gives \(N^{(0)}_j\) in terms of \(q_\pm(z)\), \(C(z)=\cos\Delta_0(z)\), and \(S(z)=\sin\Delta_0(z)\). For \(j=0\), the needed entries are the \(j=0\) specializations of those formulas. 

So the required baseline \(q_0\)-data for \(N_0[0]\) are whichever midpoint jets determine

\[
[z^1]S(z),\quad [z^2]S(z),\quad [z^3]S(z),
\]

\[
[z^1](q_\pm C),\quad [z^2]((q_-+q_+)C),\quad [z^1](q_-q_+S).
\]

The draft’s Stage 1 contract asks for baseline jets \(q_0^{(k)}(m),0\le k\le9\), which is more than enough for \(N_0[0]\). 

---

## Midpoint parity reductions

The draft permits midpoint parity in this coefficient calculus. For ordinary \(z\)-coefficients:

\[
\Lambda_{+,n}^{[a]}=(-1)^n\Lambda_{-,n}^{[a},
\]

and

\[
H_{+,n}^{a,b}=(-1)^nH_{-,n}^{a,b},
\]

when the \(+\)-side and \(-\)-side are related by \(z\mapsto -z\) in the midpoint chart.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
[z^1]\Lambda_+^{[1]}=-[z^1]\Lambda_-^{[1]},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
[z^5]\Lambda_+^{[5]}=-[z^5]\Lambda_-^{[5]},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
[z^2]\mathcal R_+^{\{1,1\}}
=
[z^2]\mathcal L_-^{\{1,1\}},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
[z^6]\mathcal R_+^{\{1,5\}}
=
[z^6]\mathcal L_-^{\{1,5\}}.
}
\]

The signs are \((-1)^1=-1\), \((-1)^5=-1\), \((-1)^2=+1\), and \((-1)^6=+1\). This is consistent with the draft’s midpoint-parity convention for finite coefficient tables. 

---

## Determinant tests

Once the vectors are computed, write

\[
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}=u_{112}^{L}I+v_{112}^{L}S,
\]

\[
C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}=u_{122}^{L}I+v_{122}^{L}S,
\]

\[
C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}=u_{112}^{R}I+v_{112}^{R}S,
\]

\[
C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}=u_{122}^{R}I+v_{122}^{R}S.
\]

Then the four determinant tests are:

\[
\boxed{
u_{112}^{L}v_5-u_5v_{112}^{L}=0,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
u_{122}^{L}v_5-u_5v_{122}^{L}=0,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
u_{112}^{R}v_5-u_5v_{112}^{R}=0,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
u_{122}^{R}v_5-u_5v_{122}^{R}=0.
}
\]

No determinant test can be honestly evaluated until those four \(u,v\) pairs are computed.

## Minimal missing coefficient table

The minimal missing table is:

### 1. First-Fréchet grade-one input

\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_{-,1}^{[1]}
=
-\sum_{i+j+k=1}W_{-,i}S_{-,j}^{[1]}W_{-,k}.
}
\]

Required primitives:

\[
W_{-,0},W_{-,1},\quad
S_{-,0}^{[1]},S_{-,1}^{[1]}.
\]

If homogeneous grade \(1\) starts at \(z^1\), this reduces to:

\[
W_{-,0},\quad S_{-,1}^{[1]}.
\]

### 2. First-Fréchet grade-five input

\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_{-,5}^{[5]}
=
-\sum_{i+j+k=5}W_{-,i}S_{-,j}^{[5]}W_{-,k}.
}
\]

Required primitives:

\[
W_{-,0..5},\quad S_{-,0..5}^{[5]}.
\]

If homogeneous grade \(5\) starts at \(z^5\), this reduces to:

\[
W_{-,0},\quad S_{-,5}^{[5]}.
\]

### 3. Second-Fréchet \((1,1)\) input

\[
\boxed{
H_{-,2}^{1,1}
=
2\sum_{i+j+k+\ell+m=2}
W_{-,i}S_{-,j}^{[1]}W_{-,k}S_{-,\ell}^{[1]}W_{-,m}
-
\sum_{i+j+k=2}W_{-,i}T_{-,j}^{1,1}W_{-,k}.
}
\]

Required primitives:

\[
W_{-,0..2},\quad S_{-,0..2}^{[1]},\quad T_{-,0..2}^{1,1}.
\]

If grade \(1\) starts at \(z^1\), this reduces to:

\[
W_{-,0},\quad S_{-,1}^{[1]},\quad T_{-,2}^{1,1}.
\]

### 4. Second-Fréchet \((1,5)\) input

\[
\boxed{
H_{-,6}^{1,5}
=
\sum_{i+j+k+\ell+m=6}
\left(
W_{-,i}S_{-,j}^{[5]}W_{-,k}S_{-,\ell}^{[1]}W_{-,m}
+
W_{-,i}S_{-,j}^{[1]}W_{-,k}S_{-,\ell}^{[5]}W_{-,m}
\right)
-
\sum_{i+j+k=6}W_{-,i}T_{-,j}^{1,5}W_{-,k}.
}
\]

Required primitives:

\[
W_{-,0..6},\quad
S_{-,0..6}^{[1]},\quad
S_{-,0..6}^{[5]},\quad
T_{-,0..6}^{1,5}.
\]

If grades \(1\) and \(5\) start sharply at \(z^1,z^5\), this reduces to:

\[
W_{-,0},\quad
S_{-,1}^{[1]},\quad
S_{-,5}^{[5]},\quad
T_{-,6}^{1,5}.
\]

### 5. Baseline middle

\[
\boxed{
N_0[0]=[z^0]N^{(0)}(z).
}
\]

Required baseline data:

\[
q_0^{(k)}(m)
\]

sufficient to compute the \(j=0\) baseline mixed-block coefficients. The draft’s Stage 1 contract asks for \(q_0^{(0)},\ldots,q_0^{(9)}\), which covers this. 

### 6. Source-grade inputs

The source-grade primitives needed are:

\[
\boxed{
(r_i^{[1]})^{(k)}(m),\qquad
(r_i^{[5]})^{(k)}(m)
}
\]

for the ranges needed to build

\[
S_{-,1}^{[1]},\quad S_{-,5}^{[5]},\quad
T_{-,2}^{1,1},\quad T_{-,6}^{1,5}.
\]

The draft’s Stage 1 contract requests

\[
(r_i^{[a]})^{(k)}(m),\qquad
i=1,2,\ a\in\{1,5\},\ 2\le k\le9,
\]

which is sufficient but not yet supplied as a theorem. 

### 7. Quintic quotient line

Finally, to run the determinant test, one needs

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=u_5I+v_5S.
\]

If this line is on the rank-jump locus \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\), the determinant coordinate is unavailable and the test is quotient-inconclusive. The good-patch determinant coordinate is only valid when \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\ne0\).
