## Claim

Gate A is reduced to four explicit fixed-sector vectors built from the Taylor-coefficient Fréchet tables:

\[
\Lambda_{-,1}^{[1]},\quad
\Lambda_{-,5}^{[5]},\quad
H_{-,2}^{1,1},\quad
H_{-,6}^{1,5},\quad
N_0[0].
\]

Under the homogeneous scalar-grade convention, the order placements

\[
2+0+5=7,\qquad 6+0+1=7
\]

are correct. The four tag vectors can be written explicitly in the draft’s Taylor-coefficient normalization, but the determinant tests are **blocked** until the finite source table supplies the actual matrices

\[
S_{-,1}^{[1]},\quad S_{-,5}^{[5]},\quad T_{-,2}^{1,1},\quad T_{-,6}^{1,5},\quad W_{-,0},\quad N_0[0],\quad A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

This is a finite coefficient-table problem, not a formal gauge proof. The draft’s coefficient calculus defines the Sylvester/Fréchet recurrences, but recurrence alone is not a determinant identity. 

## Status: reduced

The gate is reduced to a minimal finite table. It is not yet proved.

## Order-count verification

The active homogeneous scalar-grade route accepts that the \(Y\)-slot families are absent at \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\), so the first live non-\(Y\) cubic gate is

\[
L_2N_0R_1,\qquad L_1N_0R_2.
\]

The two possible order placements are:

\[
[z^2]\mathcal L_-^{\{1,1\}}\cdot N_0[0]\cdot[z^5]\Lambda_+^{[5]}
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
2+0+5=7,
\]

and

\[
[z^6]\mathcal L_-^{\{1,5\}}\cdot N_0[0]\cdot[z^1]\Lambda_+^{[1]}
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
6+0+1=7.
\]

The right-side \(L_1N_0R_2\) terms are the mirror placements:

\[
[z^1]\Lambda_-^{[1]}\cdot N_0[0]\cdot[z^6]\mathcal R_+^{\{1,5\}}
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
1+0+6=7,
\]

\[
[z^5]\Lambda_-^{[5]}\cdot N_0[0]\cdot[z^2]\mathcal R_+^{\{1,1\}}
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
5+0+2=7.
\]

So the order count is proved.

## Explicit formulas

Let

\[
A:=S_{-,1}^{[1]},\qquad B:=S_{-,5}^{[5]},
\]

and let \(W:=W_{-,0}\). Under the homogeneous scalar-grade convention, the grade-one and grade-five inputs first appear at ordinary orders \(1\) and \(5\), respectively. Therefore

\[
S_{-,j}^{[1]}=0\quad(j<1),
\qquad
S_{-,j}^{[5]}=0\quad(j<5).
\]

### First-Fréchet coefficients

Using

\[
\Lambda_{\varepsilon,n}^{a}
=
-\sum_{i+j+k=n}
W_{\varepsilon,i}S_{\varepsilon,j}^{a}W_{\varepsilon,k},
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_{-,1}^{[1]}
=
-W_{-,0}S_{-,1}^{[1]}W_{-,0}
=
-WAW.
}
\]

Likewise,

\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_{-,5}^{[5]}
=
-W_{-,0}S_{-,5}^{[5]}W_{-,0}
=
-WBW.
}
\]

These are Taylor-coefficient Fréchet entries, not raw derivative-normalized tensors. The draft’s finite Fréchet section uses Taylor coefficients for determinant tests. 

### Second-Fréchet coefficient \(H_{-,2}^{1,1}\)

The paper’s recurrence is

\[
H_{\varepsilon,n}^{ab}
=
\sum_{i+j+k+\ell+m=n}
\left(
W_{\varepsilon,i}S_{\varepsilon,j}^{b}W_{\varepsilon,k}
S_{\varepsilon,\ell}^{a}W_{\varepsilon,m}
+
W_{\varepsilon,i}S_{\varepsilon,j}^{a}W_{\varepsilon,k}
S_{\varepsilon,\ell}^{b}W_{\varepsilon,m}
\right)
-
\sum_{i+j+k=n}W_{\varepsilon,i}T_{\varepsilon,j}^{ab}W_{\varepsilon,k}.
\]

For \(a=b=1,n=2\), only \(S_{-,1}^{[1]}\) contributes. Thus

\[
\boxed{
H_{-,2}^{1,1}
=
2WAWAW-WT_{-,2}^{1,1}W.
}
\]

Here

\[
T_{-,2}^{1,1}
\]

is the second Sylvester coefficient determined by

\[
\boxed{
P_{-,0}T_{-,2}^{1,1}+T_{-,2}^{1,1}P_{-,0}
=
-2AA.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
T_{-,2}^{1,1}
=
\Sigma_-\!\left(-2AA\right).
\]

### Second-Fréchet coefficient \(H_{-,6}^{1,5}\)

For \(a=1,b=5,n=6\), only \(S_{-,1}^{[1]}\) and \(S_{-,5}^{[5]}\) contribute. Hence

\[
\boxed{
H_{-,6}^{1,5}
=
WBWAW+WAWBW-WT_{-,6}^{1,5}W.
}
\]

The corresponding second Sylvester coefficient satisfies

\[
\boxed{
P_{-,0}T_{-,6}^{1,5}+T_{-,6}^{1,5}P_{-,0}
=
-(AB+BA).
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
T_{-,6}^{1,5}
=
\Sigma_-\!\left(-(AB+BA)\right).
\]

### Baseline middle coefficient \(N_0[0]\)

From the baseline mixed block, the \(z^0\)-coefficient is the diagonal-limit same-point block at \(m\):

\[
\boxed{
N_0[0]
=
\frac{1}{\pi}
\begin{pmatrix}
2q & \frac12 q'\\[0.6ex]
\frac12 q' & \frac1{12}(q''+2q^3)
\end{pmatrix},
}
\]

where

\[
q=q_0(m),\qquad q'=q_0'(m),\qquad q''=q_0''(m).
\]

This is the same expression obtained by taking \(z\to0\) in the baseline mixed block coefficient formulas. The draft’s baseline mixed-block table gives \(N^{(0)}_j\) from \(q_\pm,\cos\Delta_0,\sin\Delta_0\); \(j=0\) specializes to the above same-point coefficient. 

---

## Midpoint parity reductions

Using midpoint parity,

\[
\Lambda_{+,1}^{[1]}=-\Lambda_{-,1}^{[1]},
\qquad
\Lambda_{+,5}^{[5]}=-\Lambda_{-,5}^{[5]},
\]

and

\[
H_{+,2}^{1,1}=H_{-,2}^{1,1},
\qquad
H_{+,6}^{1,5}=H_{-,6}^{1,5}.
\]

The signs are \((-1)^1=-1\), \((-1)^5=-1\), \((-1)^2=+1\), and \((-1)^6=+1\). This is the same midpoint parity convention used in the finite coefficient calculus. 

---

## Four tag-vector formulas

Define

\[
N:=N_0[0],
\]

\[
H_{11}:=H_{-,2}^{1,1}=2WAWAW-WT_{-,2}^{1,1}W,
\]

\[
H_{15}:=H_{-,6}^{1,5}=WBWAW+WAWBW-WT_{-,6}^{1,5}W,
\]

\[
\Lambda_1:=\Lambda_{-,1}^{[1]}=-WAW,
\]

\[
\Lambda_5:=\Lambda_{-,5}^{[5]}=-WBW.
\]

Then the four vectors are:

### 1. \(C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}\)

\[
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
H_{11}N\Lambda_5
\right).
\]

Since \(\Lambda_5=-WBW\), this is

\[
\boxed{
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
H_{11}NWBW
\right).
}
\]

### 2. \(C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}\)

\[
C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
H_{15}N\Lambda_1
\right).
\]

Since \(\Lambda_1=-WAW\),

\[
\boxed{
C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
H_{15}NWAW
\right).
}
\]

### 3. \(C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}\)

\[
C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
\Lambda_1NH_{15}
\right),
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
WAWNH_{15}
\right).
}
\]

### 4. \(C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}\)

\[
C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
\Lambda_5NH_{11}
\right),
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
WBWNH_{11}
\right).
}
\]

These are the four fixed-sector vectors in the paper’s midpoint/Taylor convention.

## Order-count verification

The accepted homogeneous scalar-grade route removes the \(Y\)-slot families from \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\), so the first live non-\(Y\) gate is

\[
L_2N_0R_1,\qquad L_1N_0R_2.
\]

The live placements are:

\[
[z^2]\mathcal L_-^{\{1,1\}}\cdot N_0[0]\cdot [z^5]\Lambda_+^{[5]},
\]

so

\[
2+0+5=7,
\]

and

\[
[z^6]\mathcal L_-^{\{1,5\}}\cdot N_0[0]\cdot [z^1]\Lambda_+^{[1]},
\]

so

\[
6+0+1=7.
\]

The right-side \(L_1N_0R_2\) placements are the same orders reversed:

\[
1+0+6=7,\qquad 5+0+2=7.
\]

This matches the draft’s first live non-\(Y\) gate description and its listed leading coefficients. 

---

## Explicit formulas

Let

\[
W:=W_{-,0}=G_-^{(0)}(m)^{-1/2}.
\]

Let

\[
\Sigma_-(C)
\]

be the Sylvester inverse defined by

\[
P_{-,0}Z+ZP_{-,0}=C,\qquad P_{-,0}=G_-^{(0)}(m)^{1/2}.
\]

Set

\[
A:=S_{-,1}^{[1]}=\Sigma_-(X_{-,1}^{[1]}),
\]

\[
B:=S_{-,5}^{[5]}=\Sigma_-(X_{-,5}^{[5]}).
\]

Then

\[
T_2^{1,1}=\Sigma_-(-2AA),
\]

\[
T_6^{1,5}=\Sigma_-\bigl(-(AB+BA)\bigr).
\]

These are in the paper’s Taylor-coefficient Fréchet normalization, not raw derivative normalization.

### First-Fréchet coefficients

Using

\[
\Lambda_{\varepsilon,n}^{a}
=
-\sum_{i+j+k=n}
W_{\varepsilon,i}S_{\varepsilon,j}^{a}W_{\varepsilon,k},
\]

and the homogeneous grade support, we get

\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_{-,1}^{[1]}=-WAW.
}
\]

Similarly,

\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_{-,5}^{[5]}=-WBW.
}
\]

### Second-Fréchet coefficients

Using the paper’s second-Fréchet/Sylvester recurrence,

\[
\boxed{
H_{-,2}^{1,1}=2WAWAW-WT_2^{1,1}W.
}
\]

And

\[
\boxed{
H_{-,6}^{1,5}=WBWAW+WAWBW-WT_6^{1,5}W.
}
\]

These are the exact leading Taylor-coefficient formulas.

---

## Baseline middle coefficient \(N_0[0]\)

The baseline mixed block at \(z=0\) is the same-point limit:

\[
\boxed{
N_0[0]
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2q_0(m) & \frac12q_0'(m)\\[0.6ex]
\frac12q_0'(m) & \frac1{12}\bigl(q_0''(m)+2q_0(m)^3\bigr)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

This is the \(j=0\) specialization of the baseline mixed-block coefficient contract. The draft’s baseline contract expresses \(N^{(0)}_j\) entrywise from the coefficients of \(q_\pm\), \(\cos\Delta_0\), and \(\sin\Delta_0\). 

Set

\[
N:=N_0[0].
\]

---

## Midpoint parity signs

Using midpoint parity,

\[
\Lambda_{+,1}^{[1]}=-\Lambda_{-,1}^{[1]},
\qquad
\Lambda_{+,5}^{[5]}=-\Lambda_{-,5}^{[5]},
\]

because orders \(1\) and \(5\) are odd.

Also,

\[
\mathcal R_{+,2}^{\{1,1\}}=\mathcal L_{-,2}^{\{1,1\}},
\qquad
\mathcal R_{+,6}^{\{1,5\}}=\mathcal L_{-,6}^{\{1,5\}},
\]

because orders \(2\) and \(6\) are even. This is the midpoint parity convention used by the finite coefficient tables. 

---

## Four fixed-sector vectors

Define

\[
H_{11}:=H_{-,2}^{1,1}=2WAWAW-WT_2^{1,1}W,
\]

\[
H_{15}:=H_{-,6}^{1,5}=WBWAW+WAWBW-WT_6^{1,5}W.
\]

Then the four tag vectors reduce to:

### 1. \(C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}\)

\[
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}\left(H_{11}N\Lambda_{-,5}^{[5]}\right).
\]

Since

\[
\Lambda_{-,5}^{[5]}=-WBW,
\]

\[
\boxed{
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\left(H_{11}NWBW\right).
}
\]

### 2. \(C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}\)

\[
C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}\left(H_{15}N\Lambda_{-,1}^{[1]}\right).
\]

Since

\[
\Lambda_{-,1}^{[1]}=-WAW,
\]

\[
\boxed{
C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\left(H_{15}NWAW\right).
}
\]

### 3. \(C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}\)

\[
C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\left(\Lambda_{-,1}^{[1]}NH_{15}\right),
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}\left(WAWNH_{15}\right).
}
\]

### 4. \(C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}\)

\[
C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\left(\Lambda_{-,5}^{[5]}NH_{11}\right),
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}\left(WBWNH_{11}\right).
}
\]

These are the requested four fixed-sector vectors.

---

## Determinant tests

For each vector, write:

\[
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}=u_{112}^{L}I+v_{112}^{L}S,
\]

\[
C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}=u_{122}^{L}I+v_{122}^{L}S,
\]

\[
C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}=u_{112}^{R}I+v_{112}^{R}S,
\]

\[
C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}=u_{122}^{R}I+v_{122}^{R}S.
\]

The four quotient-gauge tests are:

\[
\boxed{
u_{112}^{L}v_5-u_5v_{112}^{L}=0,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
u_{122}^{L}v_5-u_5v_{122}^{L}=0,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
u_{112}^{R}v_5-u_5v_{112}^{R}=0,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
u_{122}^{R}v_5-u_5v_{122}^{R}=0.
}
\]

These cannot be evaluated from the current draft because \(u_5,v_5\) and the concrete \(I,S\)-coordinates of the four products are not provided as a completed table. The draft’s target requires actual vectors and determinant identities before promotion; determinant scalarization is not a substitute for constructing the pre-\(\Phi_K\) fixed-sector coefficient. 

---

## Minimal missing coefficient table

The smallest missing table is:

### 1. Baseline inverse square root and Sylvester inverse

\[
\boxed{
W=W_{-,0}=G_-^{(0)}(m)^{-1/2}.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\Sigma_-: C\mapsto Z,\qquad P_{-,0}Z+ZP_{-,0}=C.
}
\]

Equivalently, supply \(P_{-,0}=G_-^{(0)}(m)^{1/2}\).

### 2. Grade-one source input

\[
\boxed{
X_{-,1}^{[1]}.
}
\]

Then

\[
A=\Sigma_-(X_{-,1}^{[1]}).
\]

### 3. Grade-five source input

\[
\boxed{
X_{-,5}^{[5]}.
}
\]

Then

\[
B=\Sigma_-(X_{-,5}^{[5]}).
\]

### 4. Second Sylvester terms

No independent table is required after \(A,B,\Sigma_-\) are known:

\[
\boxed{
T_2^{1,1}=\Sigma_-(-2AA),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
T_6^{1,5}=\Sigma_-\bigl(-(AB+BA)\bigr).
}
\]

### 5. Baseline middle

\[
\boxed{
N_0[0]
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2q_0(m)&\frac12q_0'(m)\\[0.6ex]
\frac12q_0'(m)&\frac1{12}\bigl(q_0''(m)+2q_0(m)^3\bigr)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

### 6. Quotient line

\[
\boxed{
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=u_5I+v_5S.
}
\]

The determinant coordinate is valid only on the good patch \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\ne0\).

### Minimal list

\[
\boxed{
W_{-,0},\quad
\Sigma_-,\quad
X_{-,1}^{[1]},\quad
X_{-,5}^{[5]},\quad
N_0[0],\quad
u_5,\quad v_5.
}
\]

Everything else in Gate A follows from those entries.

---

## Honest verdict

Gate A is reduced to a small, concrete fixed-sector table. The four vectors are:

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\left((2WAWAW-WT_2^{1,1}W)NWBW\right),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\left((WBWAW+WAWBW-WT_6^{1,5}W)NWAW\right),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}\left(WAWN(WBWAW+WAWBW-WT_6^{1,5}W)\right),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}\left(WBWN(2WAWAW-WT_2^{1,1}W)\right).
}
\]

The draft does not yet supply \(X_{-,1}^{[1]}\), \(X_{-,5}^{[5]}\), or \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=u_5I+v_5S\) as concrete fixed-sector data. Therefore the quotient-gauge determinant tests are blocked, not proved.

## Assistant (2026-04-24 18:16:01)

_Thought for 42s_

## 1. Claim

Gate A is reduced to a minimal finite table, but it is **not computable from the latest draft alone**. The paper gives the correct homogeneous-grade setup, the Fréchet/Sylvester recurrences, and the four leading tag-vector formulas, but it does **not** give concrete values for

\[
X_{-,1}^{[1]},\qquad X_{-,5}^{[5]},\qquad A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=u_5I+v_5S.
\]

Thus the four fixed-sector vectors can be expressed in closed algebraic form in terms of

\[
W,\ \Sigma_-,\ X_{-,1}^{[1]},\ X_{-,5}^{[5]},\ N_0[0],
\]

but the determinant tests cannot yet be run. This is consistent with the draft’s own instruction that the first live homogeneous non-\(Y\) gate requires finite coefficient tables, not recurrence formulas treated as determinant identities. 

## 2. Status: reduced / blocked

The gate is reduced to:

\[
W_{-,0},\quad
\Sigma_-,\quad
X_{-,1}^{[1]},\quad
X_{-,5}^{[5]},\quad
N_0[0],\quad
u_5,\quad v_5.
\]

The draft supplies \(N_0[0]\) from the baseline mixed block and gives recurrences for \(W\), \(\Sigma\), \(\Lambda\), and \(H\), but it does not supply the actual source-grade matrices \(X_{-,1}^{[1]}\), \(X_{-,5}^{[5]}\), nor the explicit \(u_5,v_5\) quotient-line coordinates. The coefficient-calculus layer is a table contract, not a completed source table. turn81file5

---

## 3. Order-count verification

Under the homogeneous scalar-grade convention,

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_a r=\frac{r^{(a+2)}(m)}{(a+2)!}(t-m)^{a+2},
\]

grade \(1\) first appears in the same-point Fréchet input at ordinary order \(1\), and grade \(5\) first appears at ordinary order \(5\). The draft accepts that the \(Y\)-slot families

\[
L_1YR_1,\quad L_2YR_0,\quad L_0YR_2
\]

are absent at \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\), so the first live non-\(Y\) gate is

\[
L_2N_0R_1,\qquad L_1N_0R_2.
\]

The live placements are:

\[
[z^2]\mathcal L_-^{\{1,1\}}\cdot N_0[0]\cdot[z^5]\Lambda_+^{[5]},
\]

so

\[
2+0+5=7,
\]

and

\[
[z^6]\mathcal L_-^{\{1,5\}}\cdot N_0[0]\cdot[z^1]\Lambda_+^{[1]},
\]

so

\[
6+0+1=7.
\]

The right-side terms are the same placements reversed:

\[
1+0+6=7,\qquad 5+0+2=7.
\]

No other \(Y\)-slot placement is active unless the homogeneous scalar-grade convention is abandoned. The draft explicitly warns that changing to an ordinary matrix-output \(M^{[5]}\) convention would reopen the \(Y\)-slot audit. 

---

## 4. Minimal table entries found or missing

### 4.1 \(N_0[0]\): computed

Let

\[
q=q_0(m),\qquad q'=q_0'(m),\qquad q''=q_0''(m).
\]

The baseline same-point/mixed limit is

\[
\boxed{
N_0[0]
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2q & \frac12q'\\[0.6ex]
\frac12q' & \frac1{12}(q''+2q^3)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

This is the \(j=0\) specialization of the baseline mixed block coefficient contract. 

### 4.2 \(W_{-,0}\): reducible to baseline square-root, not numerically tabulated

Set

\[
G_0:=G_-^{(0)}(m)=N_0[0].
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
W:=W_{-,0}=G_0^{-1/2}.
}
\]

If one wants an explicit \(2\times2\) formula, write

\[
G_0=\frac1\pi M,\qquad
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
2q & \frac12q'\\[0.6ex]
\frac12q' & \frac1{12}(q''+2q^3)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

For a positive definite \(2\times2\) matrix \(M\), set

\[
\tau=\operatorname{tr}M,\qquad
\Delta=\det M,\qquad
s=\sqrt{\Delta}.
\]

Then

\[
M^{-1/2}=\sqrt{\tau+2s}\,(M+sI)^{-1},
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
W=\sqrt{\pi}\,\sqrt{\tau+2s}\,(M+sI)^{-1}.
}
\]

This is computable once \(q,q',q''\) are fixed.

### 4.3 \(\Sigma_-\): reducible to the Sylvester inverse

Let

\[
P:=P_{-,0}=G_0^{1/2}=W^{-1}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\Sigma_-(C)=Z
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
PZ+ZP=C.
}
\]

Equivalently, in vectorized form,

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{vec}(\Sigma_-(C))
=
(I\otimes P+P^T\otimes I)^{-1}\operatorname{vec}(C).
}
\]

So \(\Sigma_-\) is computable once \(W\) or \(P\) is fixed.

### 4.4 \(X_{-,1}^{[1]}\): missing

The draft’s homogeneous-grade contract says the grade-one same-point input starts at ordinary order \(1\), but it does not give the actual matrix

\[
\boxed{
X_{-,1}^{[1]}.
}
\]

This is the first missing source-grade datum.

### 4.5 \(X_{-,5}^{[5]}\): missing

Similarly, the grade-five same-point input starts at ordinary order \(5\), but the draft does not give the actual matrix

\[
\boxed{
X_{-,5}^{[5]}.
}
\]

This is the second missing source-grade datum.

### 4.6 \(u_5,v_5\): missing as explicit coordinates

The determinant test requires

\[
\boxed{
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=u_5I+v_5S.
}
\]

The draft defines the good-patch quotient line and determinant coordinate, but the concrete \(u_5,v_5\) values for Gate A are not supplied as a completed table. The good-patch convention is essential: if \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=0\), the determinant coordinate is quotient-inconclusive rather than a successful gauge test.

---

## 5. Explicit Gate A formulas

Define

\[
A:=S_{-,1}^{[1]}=\Sigma_-(X_{-,1}^{[1]}),
\]

\[
B:=S_{-,5}^{[5]}=\Sigma_-(X_{-,5}^{[5]}).
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
T_2^{1,1}:=\Sigma_-(-2AA),
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
T_6^{1,5}:=\Sigma_-\bigl(-(AB+BA)\bigr).
}
\]

Using the paper’s Taylor-coefficient Fréchet normalization, define

\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_{-,1}^{[1]}=-WAW,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_{-,5}^{[5]}=-WBW.
}
\]

The two second-Fréchet coefficients are

\[
\boxed{
H_{-,2}^{1,1}=2WAWAW-WT_2^{1,1}W,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
H_{-,6}^{1,5}=WBWAW+WAWBW-WT_6^{1,5}W.
}
\]

These formulas use the Taylor-coefficient convention; if one used raw derivative-normalized tensors, the \(H\)-entries would differ by factorial factors. The draft’s coefficient section fixes the Taylor convention for determinant tests.

## 6. Four fixed-sector vectors

Set

\[
N:=N_0[0],
\]

\[
H_{11}:=2WAWAW-WT_2^{1,1}W,
\]

\[
H_{15}:=WBWAW+WAWBW-WT_6^{1,5}W.
\]

Midpoint parity gives

\[
\Lambda_{+,1}^{[1]}=-\Lambda_{-,1}^{[1]},
\qquad
\Lambda_{+,5}^{[5]}=-\Lambda_{-,5}^{[5]},
\]

and

\[
H_{+,2}^{1,1}=H_{-,2}^{1,1},
\qquad
H_{+,6}^{1,5}=H_{-,6}^{1,5}.
\]

Thus the four vectors reduce to:

\[
\boxed{
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}

=

}
\]

\[
\boxed{
C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}\left(WBWN H_{11}\right).
}
\]

These are the requested fixed-sector vectors. They are pre-\(\Phi_K\), pre-determinant-scalarization, and use no raw seven-family substitution.

## Honest verdict

Gate A is reduced, not proved. The four vectors are known as explicit products in

\[
W,\quad \Sigma_-,\quad X_{-,1}^{[1]},\quad X_{-,5}^{[5]},\quad N_0[0].
\]

But the latest draft does not provide \(X_{-,1}^{[1]}\), \(X_{-,5}^{[5]}\), or the concrete \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) coordinates \(u_5,v_5\). Therefore the determinant tests cannot yet be run.

## Assistant (2026-04-24 18:17:01)

I’ll do a focused second pass on the latest draft for the four blockers: \(X_{-,1}^{[1]}\), \(X_{-,5}^{[5]}\), \(u_5,v_5\), and whether \(W,\Sigma,N_0[0]\) are actually derivable from existing formulas. If the draft does not contain a table, I’ll derive the smallest usable formula from its definitions.

_Thought for 1m 48s_

## Claim

A second pass finds that the Gate A blocker is **smaller than previously stated**.

The draft does not explicitly tabulate

\[
X_{-,1}^{[1]},\qquad X_{-,5}^{[5]},
\]

but these two entries **are derivable** from the homogeneous scalar-grade convention and the source-linear same-point formula. In fact,

\[
\boxed{
X_{-,1}^{[1]}=-\frac{1}{48\pi Q^2}(I-D),
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
X_{-,5}^{[5]}=-\frac{1}{92160\pi Q^{10}}(I-D).
}
\]

Consequently,

\[
\boxed{
X_{-,5}^{[5]}=\frac{1}{1920Q^8}X_{-,1}^{[1]}.
}
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
B=S_{-,5}^{[5]}=\frac{1}{1920Q^8}A
}
\]

where

\[
A=S_{-,1}^{[1]}.
\]

This collapses Gate A from a two-input \((A,B)\) problem to a **single same-point source matrix \(A\)** problem.

The remaining genuine blocker is not \(X_{-,1}^{[1]}\) or \(X_{-,5}^{[5]}\). It is the quotient line

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=u_5I+v_5S
\]

unless the draft supplies a concrete \(u_5,v_5\) table in the same convention as Gate A.

## Status: reduced further

Gate A is reduced to:

\[
W_{-,0},\quad \Sigma_-,\quad A=\Sigma_-\!\left(-\frac{1}{48\pi Q^2}(I-D)\right),\quad
N_0[0],\quad u_5,\quad v_5.
\]

The baseline pieces \(W_{-,0},\Sigma_-,N_0[0]\) are derivable from \(q_0(m),q_0'(m),q_0''(m)\). The concrete \(u_5,v_5\) line is still missing unless one imports the paper’s one-pair \(X_0,\ldots,X_4\) coefficient table.

---

## Derivation of \(X_{-,1}^{[1]}\) and \(X_{-,5}^{[5]}\)

The draft’s same-point source-linear formula has the form

\[
X_\varepsilon(z)
=
\mathfrak D_Q(\delta G_\varepsilon^{\lin})(z)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac{2z^2}{Q^2}U_\varepsilon(z)
&
\frac{z}{2Q}E_\varepsilon(z)
\\[0.8ex]
\frac{z}{2Q}E_\varepsilon(z)
&
\frac1{12}G_\varepsilon(z)
+
\frac{q_\varepsilon(z)^2z^2}{2Q^4}U_\varepsilon(z)
\end{pmatrix},
\]

with \(I,S,D\)-coordinates obtained from the matrix entries. 

Under the homogeneous scalar-grade convention,

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_a r
=
\frac{r^{(a+2)}(m)}{(a+2)!}(t-m)^{a+2}.
\]

For the minus endpoint,

\[
t_-=m-\frac{z}{2Q^2}.
\]

### Grade \(1\)

For grade \(1\), the source is proportional to

\[
\frac{(t-m)^3}{3!}.
\]

Its second \(t\)-derivative is

\[
(t-m).
\]

At \(t=t_-\),

\[
g_-(z)=-\frac{z}{2Q^2}.
\]

The leading contribution to \(X_-(z)\) at ordinary order \(z^1\) is only the \((2,2)\)-entry:

\[
\frac1\pi\cdot\frac1{12}g_-(z)
=
-\frac{z}{24\pi Q^2}.
\]

Thus the \(z^1\)-coefficient matrix is

\[
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0\\
0&-\frac{1}{24\pi Q^2}
\end{pmatrix}
=
-\frac{1}{48\pi Q^2}(I-D).
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
X_{-,1}^{[1]}=-\frac{1}{48\pi Q^2}(I-D).
}
\]

This agrees with the residual-source table pattern \(X_{\varepsilon,1}^3=\varepsilon(48\pi Q^2)^{-1}(I-D)\) when grade \(1\) is read as the cubic source. 

### Grade \(5\)

For grade \(5\), the source is proportional to

\[
\frac{(t-m)^7}{7!}.
\]

Its second \(t\)-derivative is

\[
\frac{(t-m)^5}{5!}.
\]

At \(t=t_-\),

\[
g_-(z)
=
-\frac{z^5}{2^5\,5!\,Q^{10}}.
\]

Again the leading ordinary order \(z^5\) same-point contribution is only the \((2,2)\)-entry:

\[
\frac1\pi\cdot \frac1{12}g_-(z)
=
-\frac{z^5}{12\cdot 2^5\cdot 5!\,\pi Q^{10}}.
\]

Thus

\[
[z^5]X_-^{[5]}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0\\
0&-\frac{1}{46080\pi Q^{10}}
\end{pmatrix}
=
-\frac{1}{92160\pi Q^{10}}(I-D).
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
X_{-,5}^{[5]}=-\frac{1}{92160\pi Q^{10}}(I-D).
}
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
X_{-,5}^{[5]}=\lambda X_{-,1}^{[1]},
\qquad
\lambda:=\frac{1}{1920Q^8}.
}
\]

---

## Consequences for \(A,B,T_2,T_6,H_{11},H_{15}\)

Let

\[
A:=S_{-,1}^{[1]}=\Sigma_-(X_{-,1}^{[1]}).
\]

Then

\[
B:=S_{-,5}^{[5]}=\Sigma_-(X_{-,5}^{[5]})
=
\lambda A,
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{1}{1920Q^8}.
\]

Therefore

\[
T_2^{1,1}
=
\Sigma_-(-2AA),
\]

and

\[
T_6^{1,5}
=
\Sigma_-\bigl(-(AB+BA)\bigr)
=
\lambda\Sigma_-(-2AA)
=
\lambda T_2^{1,1}.
\]

Set

\[
H_{11}:=2WAWAW-WT_2^{1,1}W.
\]

Then

\[
H_{15}
:=
WBWAW+WAWBW-WT_6^{1,5}W
=
\lambda H_{11}.
\]

Also

\[
\Lambda_{-,1}^{[1]}=-WAW,
\]

and

\[
\Lambda_{-,5}^{[5]}=-WBW
=
-\lambda WAW
=
\lambda\Lambda_{-,1}^{[1]}.
\]

So the four Gate A vectors collapse strongly.

---

## Four fixed-sector vectors after the collapse

Let

\[
N:=N_0[0].
\]

Let

\[
M:=WAW.
\]

Then

\[
H:=H_{11}=2MAM-WT_2^{1,1}W.
\]

Since

\[
B=\lambda A,
\qquad
H_{15}=\lambda H,
\qquad
WBW=\lambda WAW=\lambda M,
\]

the four vectors become:

### 1. \(C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}\)

\[
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HNW B W)
=
\boxed{
\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HNM).
}
\]

### 2. \(C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}\)

\[
C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(H_{15}NWAW)
=
\boxed{
\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HNM).
}
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}.
}
\]

### 3. \(C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}\)

\[
C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}(WAWNH_{15})
=
\boxed{
-\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(MNH).
}
\]

### 4. \(C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}\)

\[
C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}(WBWNH)
=
\boxed{
-\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(MNH).
}
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}.
}
\]

So Gate A has only **two distinct fixed-sector vectors**, not four:

\[
\boxed{
C_L:=\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HNM),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
C_R:=-\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(MNH).
}
\]

The four determinant tests reduce to two:

\[
\boxed{
C_L\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
\qquad
C_R\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
}
\]

---

## Baseline pieces

### \(N_0[0]\)

The baseline middle is

\[
\boxed{
N_0[0]
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2q & \frac12q'\\[0.6ex]
\frac12q' & \frac1{12}(q''+2q^3)
\end{pmatrix},
}
\]

where

\[
q=q_0(m),\qquad q'=q_0'(m),\qquad q''=q_0''(m).
\]

This is derivable from the baseline mixed block. 

### \(W\) and \(\Sigma_-\)

Let

\[
G_0:=N_0[0].
\]

Then

\[
W=G_0^{-1/2}.
\]

Equivalently, if

\[
G_0=\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2q & \frac12q'\\
\frac12q' & \frac1{12}(q''+2q^3)
\end{pmatrix},
\]

then \(W\) is explicitly computable as the inverse square root of this positive \(2\times2\) matrix.

Let

\[
P=G_0^{1/2}=W^{-1}.
\]

Then

\[
\Sigma_-(C)=Z
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
PZ+ZP=C.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\operatorname{vec}(\Sigma_-(C))
=
(I\otimes P+P^T\otimes I)^{-1}\operatorname{vec}(C).
\]

Thus \(W\), \(P\), and \(\Sigma_-\) are not missing once \(q,q',q''\) are specified.

---

## What is still missing?

The remaining blocker is the quotient line

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=u_5I+v_5S.
\]

The draft defines this line abstractly as the fixed-sector quintic coefficient of the normalized one-pair quotient odd germ, but it does not provide \(u_5,v_5\) in the same explicit Gate A baseline coordinates. It gives the structural quotient definition and good-patch convention, not a completed \(u_5,v_5\) table. 

If the paper intends the explicit formula

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
X_0JX_4-X_4JX_0+X_3JX_1-X_1JX_3
\right),
\]

then write

\[
X_j=a_jI+b_jS+c_jD.
\]

For symmetric fixed-sector \(X_i\), using

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(X_iJX_j-X_jJX_i)
=
2\bigl((c_i b_j-b_i c_j)I+(c_i a_j-a_i c_j)S\bigr),
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
u_5
=
2\bigl(
c_0b_4-b_0c_4+c_3b_1-b_3c_1
\bigr),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
v_5
=
2\bigl(
c_0a_4-a_0c_4+c_3a_1-a_3c_1
\bigr).
}
\]

But the draft must state that the \(X_j\) here are exactly the canonical one-pair coefficients defining \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\). Otherwise this remains a conditional reconstruction.

---

## Determinant tests after the collapse

Let

\[
C_L=\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HNM)=u_LI+v_LS,
\]

\[
C_R=-\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(MNH)=u_RI+v_RS.
\]

Then the four tests reduce to:

\[
\boxed{
u_Lv_5-u_5v_L=0
}
\]

for both \(C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}\) and \(C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}\), and

\[
\boxed{
u_Rv_5-u_5v_R=0
}
\]

for both \(C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}\) and \(C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}\).

These cannot be resolved without \(u_5,v_5\).

---

## Minimal missing table after derivation

The previous missing list

\[
W_{-,0},\quad
\Sigma_-,\quad
X_{-,1}^{[1]},\quad
X_{-,5}^{[5]},\quad
N_0[0],\quad
u_5,\quad v_5
\]

can now be sharpened to:

\[
\boxed{
u_5,\quad v_5.
}
\]

plus, if not already fixed in a computation, the baseline scalars

\[
\boxed{
q_0(m),\quad q_0'(m),\quad q_0''(m)
}
\]

needed to instantiate \(W,\Sigma_-,N_0[0]\).

Everything else is derived:

\[
X_{-,1}^{[1]}=-\frac{1}{48\pi Q^2}(I-D),
\]

\[
X_{-,5}^{[5]}=-\frac{1}{92160\pi Q^{10}}(I-D),
\]

\[
B=\frac{1}{1920Q^8}A,
\]

\[
H_{15}=\frac{1}{1920Q^8}H_{11}.
\]

## Honest verdict

The second pass improves Gate A substantially.

The source-grade inputs are **not missing**:

\[
\boxed{
X_{-,1}^{[1]}=-\frac{1}{48\pi Q^2}(I-D),
\qquad
X_{-,5}^{[5]}=-\frac{1}{92160\pi Q^{10}}(I-D).
}
\]

This collapses the four tag vectors to two:

\[
\boxed{
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HNM),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
-\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(MNH),
}
\]

where

\[
\lambda=\frac1{1920Q^8},\qquad
M=WAW,\qquad
H=2WAWAW-W\Sigma_-(-2AA)W.
\]

The only remaining nontrivial table needed to run the quotient-gauge test is the explicit Gate A-compatible formula for

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=u_5I+v_5S.
\]

If that formula is supplied, Gate A becomes a two-vector determinant computation.

## Claim

A second pass finds one more usable derivation from the draft: the source-grade same-point inputs

\[
X_{-,1}^{[1]},\qquad X_{-,5}^{[5]}
\]

are not genuinely missing. They are derivable from the homogeneous scalar-grade convention and the source-linear same-point formula. The remaining obstruction is the explicit Gate-A-compatible quotient line

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=u_5I+v_5S.
\]

The draft contains partial and local formulas for \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), including the commutator channel and centered-branch formulas, but I do not find a single globally applicable Gate-A table for \(u_5,v_5\) in terms of the same baseline \(W,\Sigma_-,A\) data used in Gate A. So Gate A is now blocked only on \(u_5,v_5\), not on \(X_{-,1}^{[1]}\) or \(X_{-,5}^{[5]}\).

---

## Status: reduced further

Previously missing:

\[
W_{-,0},\quad
\Sigma_-,\quad
X_{-,1}^{[1]},\quad
X_{-,5}^{[5]},\quad
N_0[0],\quad
u_5,\quad v_5.

After this pass:

W_{-,0},\quad \Sigma_-,\quad N_0[0]

are baseline-derived;

are source-grade-derived;

only

remain as the minimal missing Gate A table.

## Derived source-grade entries

The draft’s homogeneous scalar-grade convention is

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_a r
=
\frac{r^{(a+2)}(m)}{(a+2)!}(t-m)^{a+2}.
\]

The source-linear same-point perturbation has the form

\[
X_\varepsilon(z)
=
\mathfrak D_Q(\delta G_\varepsilon^{\lin})(z)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac{2z^2}{Q^2}U_\varepsilon(z)
&
\frac{z}{2Q}E_\varepsilon(z)
\\[0.8ex]
\frac{z}{2Q}E_\varepsilon(z)
&
\frac1{12}G_\varepsilon(z)
+
\frac{q_\varepsilon(z)^2z^2}{2Q^4}U_\varepsilon(z)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

This same source-linear table is present in the finite-table notes and is consistent with the draft’s finite Fréchet coefficient contracts. 

### Grade \(1\)

For \(\operatorname{Gr}_1 r\),

\[
r(t)=\frac{(t-m)^3}{3!}.
\]

Then

\[
r''(t)=t-m.
\]

At the minus endpoint

\[
t_-=m-\frac{z}{2Q^2},
\]

so

\[
r''(t_-)
=
-\frac{z}{2Q^2}.
\]

The first nonzero same-point contribution is in the \((2,2)\)-entry:

\[
\frac1\pi\cdot\frac1{12}r''(t_-)
=
-\frac{z}{24\pi Q^2}.
\]

Therefore

\[
[z^1]X_-^{[1]}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0\\
0&-\frac{1}{24\pi Q^2}
\end{pmatrix}
=
-\frac{1}{48\pi Q^2}(I-D).
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
X_{-,1}^{[1]}
=
-\frac{1}{48\pi Q^2}(I-D).
}
\]

### Grade \(5\)

For \(\operatorname{Gr}_5 r\),

\[
r(t)=\frac{(t-m)^7}{7!}.
\]

Then

\[
r''(t)=\frac{(t-m)^5}{5!}.
\]

At the minus endpoint,

\[
r''(t_-)
=
-\frac{z^5}{2^5\,5!\,Q^{10}}.
\]

Again, the leading same-point contribution is in the \((2,2)\)-entry:

\[
\frac1\pi\cdot\frac1{12}r''(t_-)
=
-\frac{z^5}{12\cdot 2^5\cdot 5!\,\pi Q^{10}}.
\]

Thus

\[
[z^5]X_-^{[5]}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0\\
0&-\frac{1}{46080\pi Q^{10}}
\end{pmatrix}
=
-\frac{1}{92160\pi Q^{10}}(I-D).
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
X_{-,5}^{[5]}
=
-\frac{1}{92160\pi Q^{10}}(I-D).
}
\]

Consequently,

\[
\boxed{
X_{-,5}^{[5]}
=
\lambda X_{-,1}^{[1]},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{1}{1920Q^8}.
}
\]

This is stronger than a “missing coefficient” answer.

## Consequence for \(A,B,T_2,T_6\)

Let

\[
A:=S_{-,1}^{[1]}=\Sigma_-(X_{-,1}^{[1]}).
\]

Then

\[
B:=S_{-,5}^{[5]}=\Sigma_-(X_{-,5}^{[5]})
=
\lambda A,
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{1}{1920Q^8}.
\]

Therefore

\[
T_2^{1,1}=\Sigma_-(-2AA),
\]

and

\[
T_6^{1,5}
=
\Sigma_-\bigl(-(AB+BA)\bigr)
=
\lambda\Sigma_-(-2AA)
=
\lambda T_2^{1,1}.
\]

Set

\[
M:=WAW,
\]

and

\[
H:=2WAWAW-WT_2^{1,1}W.
\]

Then

\[
\Lambda_{-,1}^{[1]}=-M,
\]

\[
\Lambda_{-,5}^{[5]}=-\lambda M,
\]

and

\[
H_{-,6}^{1,5}=\lambda H_{-,2}^{1,1}=\lambda H.

## Gate A four-vector collapse

The four Gate A vectors become only two distinct vectors.

### Left pair

\[
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\left(HNWBW\right)
=
\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HNM).
\]

Also

\[
C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\left(H_{15}NWAW\right)
=
\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HNM).
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HNM).
}
\]

### Right pair

\[
C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}(WAWNH_{15})
=
-\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(MNH).
\]

And

\[
C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}(WBWNH)
=
-\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(MNH).
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
-\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(MNH).
}
\]

So the four determinant tests reduce to two:

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HNM)\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(MNH)\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
}
\]

The scalar factor \(\lambda\) is irrelevant on \(\lambda\neq0\), which holds for finite nonzero \(Q\).

---

## Baseline pieces are derivable

The baseline middle is

\[
\boxed{
N_0[0]
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2q_0(m) & \frac12q_0'(m)\\[0.6ex]
\frac12q_0'(m) & \frac1{12}\bigl(q_0''(m)+2q_0(m)^3\bigr)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

The same expression is the coincident baseline same-point block \(G_0\), so

\[
W=G_0^{-1/2},
\]

and

\[
\Sigma_-(C)=Z
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
G_0^{1/2}Z+ZG_0^{1/2}=C.
\]

Thus \(W,\Sigma_-\), and \(N_0[0]\) are not independent missing data once \(q_0(m),q_0'(m),q_0''(m)\) are given. The baseline mixed block formula in the draft gives the relevant \(N^{(0)}_j\) coefficients; \(j=0\) gives the displayed same-point limit. 

---

## The remaining \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) issue

The draft defines

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)=u_5(h)I+v_5(h)S
\]

as the fixed-sector quintic coefficient of the normalized one-pair quotient odd germ. It also gives an explicit commutator-channel formula:

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(X_3JX_1-X_1JX_3)
=
\bigl(v(\gamma-\alpha)+\beta(u-w)\bigr)I
+
(\gamma u-\alpha w)S.
\]

This supplies the \(X_3JX_1-X_1JX_3\) part of \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), but Gate A needs the complete canonical \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) line in the same normalization. 

From the draft’s quintic trace witness, the full relevant channel includes

\[
X_0JX_4-X_4JX_0
+
X_3JX_1-X_1JX_3.
\]

Therefore, if

\[
X_j=a_jI+b_jS+c_jD,
\]

then the full fixed-sector expression is derivable by the identity

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(X_iJX_j-X_jJX_i)
=
2\bigl((c_i b_j-b_i c_j)I+(c_i a_j-a_i c_j)S\bigr).
\]

So the complete conditional formula is:

\[
\boxed{
u_5
=
2\bigl(
c_0b_4-b_0c_4+c_3b_1-b_3c_1
\bigr),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
v_5
=
2\bigl(
c_0a_4-a_0c_4+c_3a_1-a_3c_1
\bigr).
}
\]

This is a valid derivation **if** the \(X_j\) are the canonical one-pair coefficients used in \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\). The draft clearly defines \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) abstractly and provides channel formulas, but I do not see a single Gate-A-ready table for the coefficients

\[
X_0,\quad X_1,\quad X_3,\quad X_4
\]

in the same baseline notation

\[
W,\quad A=\Sigma_-(X_{-,1}^{[1]}),\quad q_0(m),q_0'(m),q_0''(m).
\]

So \(u_5,v_5\) are **conditionally derivable** from the \(X_j\) table, but the \(X_j\)-to-Gate-A baseline table remains missing.

The minimal missing table is now:

\[
\boxed{

}
\]

for the canonical one-pair quintic line \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), or directly

\[
\boxed{

}
\]

Everything else in Gate A is derivable from the draft.

More explicitly, to finish the determinant tests we need either:

### Option A — direct quotient-line table

A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=u_5I+v_5S.
\]

### Option B — one-pair coefficient table

\[

\]

for \(j=0,1,3,4\). Then use

\[

=

\]

\[

=

\]

Option B requires \(X_0,X_1,X_3,X_4\) in the same normalization as the \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) definition.

## 1. Claim

Pushing one step further, Gate A has a **pre-determinant aggregate cancellation**.

Under the homogeneous scalar-grade convention, the source-grade inputs satisfy

\[
X_{-,5}^{[5]}=\lambda X_{-,1}^{[1]},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{1}{1920Q^8}.
\]

Therefore

\[
B=S_{-,5}^{[5]}=\lambda A,
\qquad
T_6^{1,5}=\lambda T_2^{1,1},
\qquad
H_{-,6}^{1,5}=\lambda H_{-,2}^{1,1}.
\]

Consequently the four Gate A vectors collapse to two opposite pairs:

\[
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}=C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HNM),
\]

\[
C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}=C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
-\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(MNH),
\]

where

\[
M=WAW,
\qquad
H=2WAWAW-W\Sigma_-(-2AA)W.
\]

Since \(W,A,H,N\) are symmetric,

\[
MNH=(HNM)^T,
\]

and fixed-sector projection to \(\mathfrak f=\operatorname{span}\{I,S\}\) is transpose-invariant. Hence

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(MNH)=\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HNM).
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}+C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}=0,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}+C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}=0.
}
\]

So if Gate A is the **aggregate** \(L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2\) package gate, then Gate A closes before determinant testing. If the draft insists on **family-by-family** gauge for each of the four displayed vectors separately, that stronger statement remains blocked on the explicit \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) line.

---

## 2. Status: proved for aggregate Gate A / blocked for family-by-family gauge

The aggregate cancellation is proved from the draft’s homogeneous-grade convention and the finite Fréchet/Sylvester recurrence structure. It does not use \(\Phi_K\), determinant scalarization, or raw seven-family shortcuts.

The individual family tests

\[
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\quad
C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

and similarly for \(L_1N_0R_2\), still require \(u_5,v_5\). But the natural package gate should be aggregate, because \(L_2N_0R_1\) and \(L_1N_0R_2\) are the left/right pair in the same corrected-whitening cross-effect. The draft itself identifies the live non-\(Y\) gate as the pair \(L_2N_0R_1\) and \(L_1N_0R_2\), with the four tag vectors formed from these two families. 

---

## 3. Order-count verification

The accepted homogeneous scalar-grade convention removes the \(Y\)-slot families from \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\). The first live non-\(Y\) placements are

\[
[z^2]\mathcal L_-^{\{1,1\}}\cdot N_0[0]\cdot [z^5]\Lambda_+^{[5]},
\]

and

\[
[z^6]\mathcal L_-^{\{1,5\}}\cdot N_0[0]\cdot [z^1]\Lambda_+^{[1]}.
\]

Thus

\[
2+0+5=7,
\qquad
6+0+1=7.
\]

The right-side mirror placements are

\[
1+0+6=7,
\qquad
5+0+2=7.
\]

No \(Y\)-slot placement is active unless the homogeneous scalar-grade convention is abandoned. The draft’s \(Y\)-absence lemma is explicitly scoped to that convention.

## 4. Minimal table entries found

### 4.1 \(X_{-,1}^{[1]}\)

Under

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_1 r=\frac{r^{(3)}(m)}{3!}(t-m)^3,
\]

the second derivative of the source is \(t-m\). At the minus endpoint

\[
t_-=m-\frac{z}{2Q^2},
\]

so the leading same-point source-linear contribution is the \((2,2)\)-entry

\[
-\frac{z}{24\pi Q^2}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
X_{-,1}^{[1]}
=
-\frac{1}{48\pi Q^2}(I-D).
}
\]

This is consistent with the source-linear same-point table: the \(r_3\)-type cubic source has \(X_{\varepsilon,1}^{3}=\varepsilon(48\pi Q^2)^{-1}(I-D)\), and \(\varepsilon=-1\) for the minus side. 

### 4.2 \(X_{-,5}^{[5]}\)

Under

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_5 r=\frac{r^{(7)}(m)}{7!}(t-m)^7,
\]

the second derivative is

\[
\frac{(t-m)^5}{5!}.
\]

At the minus endpoint,

\[
(t_--m)^5=-\frac{z^5}{2^5Q^{10}}.
\]

Thus the leading same-point source-linear contribution is

\[
-\frac{z^5}{12\cdot 2^5\cdot 5!\,\pi Q^{10}}
\]

in the \((2,2)\)-entry, giving

\[
\boxed{
X_{-,5}^{[5]}
=
-\frac{1}{92160\pi Q^{10}}(I-D).
}
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
X_{-,5}^{[5]}
=
\lambda X_{-,1}^{[1]},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{1}{1920Q^8}.
}
\]

### 4.3 \(N_0[0]\)

The baseline middle coefficient is the same-point limit

\[
\boxed{
N=N_0[0]
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2q_0(m)&\frac12q_0'(m)\\[0.6ex]
\frac12q_0'(m)&\frac1{12}(q_0''(m)+2q_0(m)^3)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

The draft’s baseline mixed-block contract gives \(N^{(0)}_j\) from the baseline \(q_\pm,\cos\Delta_0,\sin\Delta_0\) coefficient formulas; the \(j=0\) specialization is this coincident same-point block. 

### 4.4 \(W\) and \(\Sigma_-\)

Let

\[
G_0=N_0[0].
\]

Then

\[
W=W_{-,0}=G_0^{-1/2}.
\]

Let

\[
P=G_0^{1/2}=W^{-1}.
\]

Then

\[
\Sigma_-(C)=Z
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
PZ+ZP=C.
\]

So \(W\) and \(\Sigma_-\) are not independent missing data once \(q_0(m),q_0'(m),q_0''(m)\) are fixed.

---

## 5. Collapse of the Fréchet data

Let

\[
A:=S_{-,1}^{[1]}=\Sigma_-(X_{-,1}^{[1]}),
\]

and

\[
B:=S_{-,5}^{[5]}=\Sigma_-(X_{-,5}^{[5]}).
\]

Since \(\Sigma_-\) is linear,

\[
\boxed{
B=\lambda A,
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{1}{1920Q^8}.
}
\]

Now

\[
T_2^{1,1}=\Sigma_-(-2AA),
\]

and

\[
T_6^{1,5}=\Sigma_-( -(AB+BA)).
\]

Using \(B=\lambda A\),

\[
AB+BA=2\lambda AA,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
T_6^{1,5}=\lambda T_2^{1,1}.
}
\]

Set

\[
M:=WAW,
\]

and

\[
H:=2WAWAW-WT_2^{1,1}W.
\]

Then

\[
\Lambda_{-,1}^{[1]}=-M,
\qquad
\Lambda_{-,5}^{[5]}=-\lambda M,
\]

and

\[
H_{-,2}^{1,1}=H,
\qquad
H_{-,6}^{1,5}=\lambda H.
\]

These formulas use the paper’s Taylor-coefficient Fréchet normalization, not derivative-normalized tensors. 

---

## 6. Four fixed-sector vectors

Using the reduced midpoint-parity formulas in the prompt:

\[
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
H_{-,2}^{1,1}N\Lambda_{-,5}^{[5]}
\right),
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HNM).
}
\]

Similarly,

\[
C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
H_{-,6}^{1,5}N\Lambda_{-,1}^{[1]}
\right),
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}
=
\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HNM).
}
\]

For the right family,

\[
C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
\Lambda_{-,1}^{[1]}NH_{-,6}^{1,5}
\right),
\]

hence

\[
\boxed{
C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
-\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(MNH).
}
\]

And

\[
C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
\Lambda_{-,5}^{[5]}NH_{-,2}^{1,1}
\right),
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=
-\lambda\,\pi_{\mathfrak f}(MNH).
}
\]

Thus the four vectors reduce to two.

---

## 7. Aggregate cancellation

The matrices \(W,A,T_2,H,M,N\) are symmetric:

- \(W\) is the inverse square root of the symmetric positive baseline;
- \(A=\Sigma_-(X_{-,1}^{[1]})\) is symmetric because \(X_{-,1}^{[1]}\) and \(P\) are symmetric;
- \(T_2=\Sigma_-(-2AA)\) is symmetric;
- \(H\), \(M\), and \(N\) are products arranged palindromically or baseline symmetric.

Therefore

\[
(HNM)^T=MNH.
\]

For any \(2\times2\) matrix \(Z\), the fixed-sector projection to \(\operatorname{span}\{I,S\}\) is invariant under transpose:

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(Z^T)=\pi_{\mathfrak f}(Z).
\]

Hence

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(MNH)
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HNM).
\]

It follows that

\[
\boxed{
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}
+
C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=0,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}
+
C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}
=0.
}
\]

This is a pre-\(\Phi_K\), pre-determinant fixed-sector cancellation.

---

## 8. Determinant tests

If one tests each individual family vector separately, write

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HNM)=u_LI+v_LS.
\]

Then the left-family tests are

\[
\lambda(u_Lv_5-u_5v_L)=0,
\]

and the right-family tests are

\[
-\lambda(u_Lv_5-u_5v_L)=0.
\]

These individual tests are still blocked unless \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=u_5I+v_5S\) is supplied.

But the aggregate Gate A tests are stronger and do not require \(u_5,v_5\), because the aggregate vectors are zero:

\[
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}+C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}=0,
\]

\[
C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}+C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}=0.
\]

Therefore

\[
0\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
\]

on every patch, including the good patch.

---

## 9. Minimal missing table, if blocked

The only remaining missing table applies to the **stronger family-by-family** statement, not to aggregate Gate A.

For family-by-family quotient-gauge, the missing table is:

\[
\boxed{
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=u_5I+v_5S.
}
\]

The draft gives structural definitions and partial quintic commutator formulas, but the complete Gate-A-compatible \(u_5,v_5\) table is not stated as a finished source table. The fixed quotient target must be controlled before determinant scalarization; determinant pairing is a coordinate only after \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\neq0\) is fixed. 

For aggregate Gate A, no missing coefficient table remains.

\text{ contributes zero fixed-sector vector at the leading homogeneous non-}Y

The key derivation is:

which forces

and makes the left/right products transpose-pairs with opposite signs.

Thus the first live homogeneous non-\(Y\) Gate A is not a surviving obstruction if the theorem tests the natural aggregate \(L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2\). Only the stronger, unnatural family-by-family gauge statement remains blocked on \(u_5,v_5\).

\qquad

the Sylvester linearity, and transpose invariance of \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}\). It stays before \(\Phi_K\), before determinant scalarization, and before any raw seven-family shortcut.

## 1. Source-grade proportionality

Under the homogeneous scalar-grade convention,

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_1r=\frac{r^{(3)}(m)}{3!}(t-m)^3,
\qquad
\operatorname{Gr}_5r=\frac{r^{(7)}(m)}{7!}(t-m)^7.
\]

At the minus endpoint,

\[
t_-=m-\frac{z}{2Q^2}.
\]

The source-linear same-point formula gives the leading grade-one matrix

\[
X_{-,1}^{[1]}
=
-\frac{1}{48\pi Q^2}(I-D),
\]

and the leading grade-five matrix

\[
X_{-,5}^{[5]}
=
-\frac{1}{92160\pi Q^{10}}(I-D).
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
X_{-,5}^{[5]}
=
\lambda X_{-,1}^{[1]},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{1}{1920Q^8}.
}
\]

This is consistent with the finite source-linear table, where the same-point primitives are source-constrained and not free variables.

## 2. Sylvester consequences

Let

\[
W=W_{-,0},\qquad
A=S_{-,1}^{[1]}=\Sigma_-(X_{-,1}^{[1]}),

\[

\boxed{
B=\lambda A.
}

Then

\[
T_2^{1,1}=\Sigma_-(-2AA),

and

T_6^{1,5}=\Sigma_-\bigl(-(AB+BA)\bigr)
=\lambda\Sigma_-(-2AA)
=\lambda T_2^{1,1}.

\Lambda_{-,1}^{[1]}=-M,
\qquad

and

H_{-,2}^{1,1}=H,
\qquad
H_{-,6}^{1,5}=\lambda H.

All of this is in the draft’s Taylor-coefficient Fréchet normalization, not raw derivative-normalized notation. The finite Fréchet/Sylvester section defines these coefficient recurrences and is explicitly a coefficient table contract, not a post-\(\Phi_K\) scalarization.

## 4. Transpose cancellation

The matrices \(W,A,T_2,H,M,N\) are symmetric:

- \(W\) is the inverse square root of a symmetric baseline same-point block;
- \(A=\Sigma_-(X_{-,1}^{[1]})\) is symmetric because \(X_{-,1}^{[1]}\) and the Sylvester operator are symmetric;
- \(T_2=\Sigma_-(-2AA)\) is symmetric;
- \(M=WAW\), \(H=2WAWAW-WT_2W\), and \(N=N_0[0]\) are symmetric.

Therefore

\[
(HNM)^T=MNH.
\]

The fixed-sector projection

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}:\operatorname{Mat}_{2\times2}\to\operatorname{span}\{I,S\}
\]

is transpose-invariant, since it keeps the diagonal trace component and the symmetric off-diagonal component. Hence

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(HNM)=\pi_{\mathfrak f}(MNH).
}
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
C_{112}^{L_2N_0R_1}+C_{112}^{L_1N_0R_2}=0,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
C_{122}^{L_2N_0R_1}+C_{122}^{L_1N_0R_2}=0.
}
\]

This is a fixed-sector cancellation before quotienting.

---

## 5. Determinant tests

For the aggregate Gate A package, the determinant tests are automatic:

\[
0\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

So the aggregate gate does **not** need \(u_5,v_5\).

If someone insists on testing each individual vector separately, then one still needs the explicit quotient line

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=u_5I+v_5S.
\]

But that family-by-family requirement is stronger than the package-level gate and is not the natural UV-026 object. The active package theorem concerns the combined corrected-whitening cross-effect, not isolated left/right family fragments. The source-bidegree quotient package target is explicitly pre-\(\Phi_K\) and pre-determinant, and determinant scalarization alone is not the definition of \(Q_{7,m}^q\). 

---

\quad\text{in fixed-sector at the leading homogeneous non-}Y\text{ gate.}

The key mechanism is not \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-gauge. It is stronger:

\qquad\text{and}\qquad
L_0N_0R_3,
\]

with the same discipline: aggregate package first, family-by-family gauge only if the aggregate fails.

## Order placements

Under homogeneous scalar grade,

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_1 r=\frac{r^{(3)}(m)}{3!}(t-m)^3,
\qquad
\operatorname{Gr}_5 r=\frac{r^{(7)}(m)}{7!}(t-m)^7.

The first live all-left/all-right source-grade multiset is

1+1+5=7.
\]

Since the all-left/all-right families have baseline middle and opposite-side baseline factors, the leading placements are

\[
L_3N_0R_0:
\qquad
[z^7]\mathcal L_-^{\{1,1,5\}}\,N_0[0]\,W_{+,0},
\]

and

\[
L_0N_0R_3:
\qquad
W_{-,0}\,N_0[0]\,[z^7]\mathcal R_+^{\{1,1,5\}}.
\]

So the order placements are

\[
\boxed{7+0+0=7}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{0+0+7=7.}
\]

There are no \(Y\)-slot terms here, and the accepted \(Y\)-slot absence theorem remains untouched. The draft’s third-Fréchet table states that the all-left/all-right audit uses third-Fréchet coefficient ranges such as \(G^-_{324,3..7}\) and \(G^+_{324,3..7}\); the leading homogeneous \((1,1,5)\) gate is the \(n=7\) case. 

---

## Required third-Fréchet coefficients

Let

\[
A:=S_{-,1}^{[1]},
\qquad
B:=S_{-,5}^{[5]}.
\]

From Gate A we already have

\[
B=\lambda A,\qquad \lambda=\frac{1}{1920Q^8}.
\]

The third Sylvester coefficient for the source triple \((1,1,5)\) is

\[
U_{-,7}^{1,1,5},
\]

defined by the draft’s third-Fréchet/Sylvester recurrence. In leading homogeneous order, only the source coefficients

\[
S_{-,1}^{[1]},
\qquad
S_{-,5}^{[5]},
\qquad
T_{-,2}^{1,1},
\qquad
T_{-,6}^{1,5}
\]

enter. The draft’s third Sylvester recurrence is

\[
P_{\varepsilon,0}U_{\varepsilon,n}^{abc}
+
U_{\varepsilon,n}^{abc}P_{\varepsilon,0}
=
-\sum_{i+j=n}
\Bigl(
S_{\varepsilon,i}^{a}T_{\varepsilon,j}^{bc}
+S_{\varepsilon,i}^{b}T_{\varepsilon,j}^{ac}
+S_{\varepsilon,i}^{c}T_{\varepsilon,j}^{ab}
+
T_{\varepsilon,i}^{bc}S_{\varepsilon,j}^{a}
+T_{\varepsilon,i}^{ac}S_{\varepsilon,j}^{b}
+T_{\varepsilon,i}^{ab}S_{\varepsilon,j}^{c}
\Bigr)
-\cdots ,
\]

where the omitted terms are the baseline-recursion terms involving \(P_{\varepsilon,j}U_{\varepsilon,n-j}^{abc}\). At the leading homogeneous order \(n=7\), the only source-degree contributions are exactly the \((1,1,5)\) ones. 

Because

\[
B=\lambda A,
\qquad
T_{-,6}^{1,5}=\lambda T_{-,2}^{1,1},
\]

the same recurrence gives

\[
\boxed{
U_{-,7}^{1,1,5}=\lambda\,U_{-,3}^{1,1,1}
}
\]

in the leading homogeneous table. Consequently the all-left third-Fréchet coefficient satisfies

\[
\boxed{
G^-_{7;1,1,5}=\lambda\,G^-_{3;1,1,1}.
}
\]

I will write

\[
G:=G^-_{7;1,1,5}.
\]

This \(G\) is the Taylor-coefficient third-Fréchet matrix, not a raw \(D^3\) tensor. The draft explicitly fixes the finite tables to Taylor-coefficient normalization. 

---

## Plus-side coefficient and midpoint parity

Midpoint parity gives

\[
\boxed{
G^+_{7;1,1,5}=(-1)^7G^-_{7;1,1,5}=-G.
}
\]

Also

\[
W_{+,0}=W_{-,0}=W,
\]

and

\[
N_0[0]=N
\]

is common.

Therefore the all-left contribution is

\[
\boxed{
C_L:=\pi_{\mathfrak f}(G\,N\,W).
}
\]

The all-right contribution is

\[
\boxed{
C_R:=\pi_{\mathfrak f}(W\,N\,G^+)
=
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}(W\,N\,G).
}
\]

The midpoint parity lemma in the draft states the same sign pattern for third-Fréchet coefficients once the \(G^\pm\)-table is defined. 

---

## Aggregate cancellation

The matrices \(G,N,W\) are symmetric:

- \(W\) is the inverse square root of the symmetric baseline same-point block;
- \(N=N_0[0]\) is the symmetric same-point baseline middle coefficient;
- \(G\) is a coefficient of the inverse square root of a symmetric same-point block and is therefore symmetric.

Hence

\[
(GNW)^T=WNG.
\]

The fixed-sector projection is transpose-invariant:

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(Z^T)=\pi_{\mathfrak f}(Z),
\]

because \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}\) keeps the trace/diagonal \(I\)-part and the symmetric off-diagonal \(S\)-part.

Therefore

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(GNW)=\pi_{\mathfrak f}(WNG).
\]

So

\[
C_L+C_R
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(GNW)-\pi_{\mathfrak f}(WNG)
=
0.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
C^{L_3N_0R_0}_{(1,1,5)}
+
C^{L_0N_0R_3}_{(1,1,5)}
=0
\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f.
}
\]

This is an aggregate fixed-sector cancellation before quotienting.

---

## Residual / determinant test

There is no aggregate residual.

Since the aggregate fixed-sector vector is zero,

\[
0\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
\]

on every good patch, and even at rank-jump points in the trivial sense that no determinant coordinate is needed to see the vector is zero.

If one insists on testing \(L_3N_0R_0\) or \(L_0N_0R_3\) family-by-family, then a determinant test against

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=u_5I+v_5S
\]

would still be needed. But that is stronger than the package-level UV-026 gate and is not the natural object. Prior audits already warned that all-left/all-right families should not be closed by scalarization or generic algebra family-by-family; aggregate matrix/fixed-sector cancellation is the correct level. 

---

## Honest verdict

The all-left/all-right homogeneous third-Fréchet gate closes as an aggregate:

\[
\boxed{
L_3N_0R_0+L_0N_0R_3=0
\quad\text{in fixed sector at the leading homogeneous non-}Y\text{ order.}
}
\]

Together with the prior Gate A result,

\[
L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2=0,
\]

the leading homogeneous non-\(Y\) UV-026 cubic gates close at the aggregate package level. No \(Y\)-slot reopening, post-\(\Phi_K\) scalarization, or family-by-family determinant test is involved.

## Claim

G^+_{7;1,1,5}=(-1)^7G^-_{7;1,1,5}=-G^-_{7;1,1,5}.

at the leading homogeneous non-\(Y\) \((1,1,5)\) order.

## Status: proved conditionally on the stated third-Fréchet midpoint parity

The proof is fixed-sector, pre-\(\Phi_K\), pre-determinant, and does not require \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).

---

## Parity sign check

The draft’s midpoint parity rule is:

\[
\text{plus-side coefficient at ordinary order }n
=
(-1)^n
\text{ minus-side coefficient at ordinary order }n.
\]

For the leading third-Fréchet coefficient,

\[
n=7,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
G^+_{7;1,1,5}=(-1)^7G^-_{7;1,1,5}=-G^-_{7;1,1,5}.
}
\]

Set

\[
G:=G^-_{7;1,1,5},\qquad
W:=W_{-,0}=W_{+,0},\qquad
N:=N_0[0].
\]

Because \(W_{\pm,0}\) is order \(0\), midpoint parity gives no sign:

\[
W_{+,0}=W_{-,0}.
\]

---

## Aggregate cancellation proof

The leading all-left placement is

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\left(G^-_{7;1,1,5}N_0[0]W_{+,0}\right)
=
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(GNW).
}
\]

The leading all-right placement is

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\left(W_{-,0}N_0[0]G^+_{7;1,1,5}\right)
=
\boxed{
-\pi_{\mathfrak f}(WNG).
}
\]

Now \(G,N,W\) are symmetric:

- \(W\) is the inverse square root of the symmetric baseline same-point block.
- \(N=N_0[0]\) is the symmetric baseline mixed/same-point limit.
- \(G=G^-_{7;1,1,5}\) is a third-Fréchet coefficient of the inverse square root of a symmetric same-point block in symmetric source directions, so it remains symmetric.

Hence

\[
(GNW)^T=WNG.
\]

The projection

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}:\operatorname{Mat}_{2\times2}\to\operatorname{span}\{I,S\}
\]

is transpose-invariant:

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(Z^T)=\pi_{\mathfrak f}(Z),
\]

because it keeps only the diagonal trace component and the symmetric off-diagonal component.

Therefore

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(GNW)
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}((GNW)^T)
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(WNG).
\]

Thus

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(GNW)-\pi_{\mathfrak f}(WNG)=0.
\]

So the aggregate all-left/all-right fixed-sector vector is zero:

\[
\boxed{
C^{L_3N_0R_0}_{1,1,5}
+
C^{L_0N_0R_3}_{1,1,5}
=0.
}
\]

---

## Caveats

1. **Third-Fréchet parity must be explicitly part of the draft.** If the draft only proves midpoint parity for first- and second-Fréchet tables, then this cancellation is conditional on extending that parity to \(G^\pm_{7;1,1,5}\). The sign must be \((-1)^7=-1\).

2. **Taylor normalization matters.** The cancellation uses the same Taylor-coefficient normalization on both left and right. A global \(1/3!\) factor would appear on both \(G^-\) and \(G^+\), so it would not affect cancellation, but inconsistent left/right normalization would break the argument.

3. **Source-tag ordering must be symmetrized consistently.** The argument assumes \(G_{7;1,1,5}\) is the symmetric third-Fréchet coefficient for the multiset \((1,1,5)\). If the table uses ordered triples rather than symmetric multilinear coefficients, the aggregate must include all ordered permutations with the same convention on both sides. The transpose cancellation then applies to the symmetrized aggregate.

4. **This is aggregate cancellation only.** It does not imply

\[
L_3N_0R_0\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

or

\[
L_0N_0R_3\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

family-by-family. It says their sum has zero fixed-sector representative.

## Honest verdict

The all-left/all-right homogeneous \((1,1,5)\) third-Fréchet gate closes at the natural aggregate level:

\[
\boxed{
L_3N_0R_0+L_0N_0R_3=0
\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f.
}
\]

The proof is robust once the draft’s third-Fréchet midpoint parity convention is accepted.

## Expansion of \(F_1\)

Start from the raw matrix cross-effect before \(\Phi_K\):

\[
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
\mathcal W(\mathcal B_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2))
-\mathcal W(\mathcal B_1(a_1,h_1))
-\mathcal W(\mathcal B_1(a_2,h_2))
+\mathcal W(\mathcal B_0),
\]

where source tags are retained until

\[
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
\]

is applied. This is the draft’s pre-\(\Phi_K\), pre-determinant package object. 

On the collision chart,

\[
h_1=h-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
h_2=h+\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]

define

\[
\mathcal C(h,\delta)
:=
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\left(a_1,h-\frac{\delta}{2};
-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),h+\frac{\delta}{2}\right).
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
F_1=[z^7][\delta^1]\mathcal C(h,\delta).
}
\]

Equivalently, at \(\delta=0\),

\[
\boxed{
F_1
=
[z^7]\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial\delta}
\mathcal C(h,\delta)
\right|_{\delta=0}.
}
\]

By the chain rule, this derivative decomposes schematically into

\[
\boxed{
F_1
=
F_{1,h}
+
F_{1,a}
+

+

where:

\[

=

=

\left(
-\kappa a_1\partial_{a_2}
\right)
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}\Big|_{\delta=0},

and \(F_{1,\mathrm{source}}\) denotes the induced derivative of the homogeneous source inputs under \(h_1,h_2\) motion. The term \(F_{1,\mathrm{proj}}\) is zero only if the source-bidegree projector is fixed and commutes with the coefficient extraction in the required sense; that compatibility is explicitly a theorem obligation in the package layer. 

This is the exact formal expansion of the first-collision obstruction. What remains is the finite coefficient evaluation of its \([z^7]\)-part.

Because the \(L_2N_0R_1/L_1N_0R_2\) and \(L_3N_0R_0/L_0N_0R_3\) cancellations are **aggregate fixed-sector cancellations**, not merely determinant-gauge identities, their contribution to the first collision derivative vanishes provided the cancellation is tagwise and holds as a function of the moving midpoint \(h\). ## Remaining possible sources of \(F_1\)

After removing the Gate A aggregate, any remaining \(F_1\) must come from outside the leading homogeneous cubic \(B_7\)-inventory.

### 1. Non-leading homogeneous grades

Gate A closes the leading \((1,1,5)\) homogeneous cubic sector. It does not by itself classify all non-leading homogeneous combinations that can feed a \([z^7][\delta^1]\) edge coefficient. Any such term must be represented in a separate first-collision table.

### 2. Grade \(0,2,4\) lower shadows

The homogeneous \(Y\)-slot absence is scoped. The draft warns that ordinary matrix-output or parity-corrected non-homogeneous conventions reopen \(Y\)-slot gates and require no-double-counting against the natural grade \(0,2,4\) same-point shadows. 

Under the active homogeneous convention, those lower shadows still need an explicit “edge-divisibility does not receive \([z^7][\delta^1]\) from grade \(0,2,4\)” theorem. The draft’s current text does not provide that full table.

### 3. Baseline \(h\)-motion / \(q_0\)-derivatives

The derivative

\[
-\frac12\partial_{h_1}+\frac12\partial_{h_2}
\]

acts not only on source positions but also on the moving baseline coefficients:

\[
G_\pm^{(0)}(h_i),\quad
N^{(0)}(h_1,h_2),\quad
W_\pm(h_i).
\]

Gate A’s leading homogeneous cancellation is pointwise in \(h\), but a full proof that all baseline-motion contributions vanish in \(F_1\) requires a first-collision table for the raw package, not just the \(B_7\) leading cubic table.

### 4. Amplitude-weight derivative

For the closed leading Gate A aggregates, amplitude derivatives are harmless. But for any non-leading non-\((1,1)\) source-bidegree term not already shown to vanish, the derivative of

\[
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta)
\]

can contribute to \([z^7][\delta^1]\). This is not ruled out by the leading homogeneous gate.

### 5. Source-bidegree projection leakage

The source-bidegree projector must be compatible with pre-determinant fixed-sector extraction. The draft lists this as a theorem obligation and explicitly says projection after determinant scalarization or quotienting is invalid. 

Thus, unless compatibility is proved, a \([z^7][\delta^1]\) residual can arise as projection leakage between the tagged source expansion and the coefficient extractor.

### 6. Missing diagonal / edge counterterm

If

\[
F_1\neq0,
\]

then

\[
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\]

has a \(\delta^{-1}\)-pole. The update note states that such a case requires a canonical edge/first-collision counterterm or a source-bidegree quotient-invisibility theorem. 

---

## Remaining residual or proof of zero

From the current draft, I can prove only:

This is exactly the “Gate B / edge-divisibility” theorem, not a continuation of Gate A.

## Exact missing theorem if blocked

The missing theorem should be stated as:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
&[z^7][\delta^1]\,
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\left(a_1,h-\frac{\delta}{2};
-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),h+\frac{\delta}{2}\right)
=0.
\end{aligned}
}
\]

A useful paper-ready form is:

```tex
\begin{lemma}[First-collision edge divisibility through order \(7\)]
\label{lem:first-collision-edge-divisibility-order-seven}
On the collision chart
\[
h_1=h-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
h_2=h+\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]
one has
\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\,
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\mathrm{mix}}
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}=0.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\mathrm{mix}}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
=
O(a_1\delta^2)
\]
through ordinary order \(z^7\) in fixed sector.
\]
\end{lemma}
```

The proof requires a new coefficient table:

```tex
\begin{itemize}
\item the \([z^7]\) first-collision derivative of every non-\((1,1)\)
```

## Formula for \(F_1\)

Let

\[
\mathcal C(h,\delta)
:=
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\left(a_1,h-\frac{\delta}{2};
-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),h+\frac{\delta}{2}\right).
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
F_1=[z^7]\left.\frac{\partial}{\partial\delta}\mathcal C(h,\delta)\right|_{\delta=0}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
F_1
=
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
\left[
\left(
-\frac12\partial_{h_1}
+\frac12\partial_{h_2}
-\kappa a_1\partial_{a_2}
\right)
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\right]_{\substack{h_1=h_2=h\\a_2=-a_1}}.
}
\]

The first two derivatives are the collision motion

\[
h_1=h-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad h_2=h+\frac{\delta}{2},
\]

and the last derivative is the amplitude-weight motion

\[
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta).
\]

This formula is pre-\(\Phi_K\), pre-determinant, and keeps source tags until the projection is applied. The raw corrected-whitening cross-effect and pre-quotient source-bidegree projection are defined at the matrix level in the package layer. 

If one expands the projected tagged cross-effect as

\[
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
=
\sum_{\mu\in\mathcal I_{\rm mix}}
a_1^{p_\mu}a_2^{q_\mu} C_\mu(h_1,h_2;z),
\]

where \(\mathcal I_{\rm mix}\) is the set of retained non-\((1,1)\) source-bidegree components, then

\[
\boxed{
F_1
=
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\sum_{\mu\in\mathcal I_{\rm mix}}
(-1)^{q_\mu}a_1^{p_\mu+q_\mu}
\left(
q_\mu\kappa C_\mu
+
\left(-\frac12\partial_{h_1}+\frac12\partial_{h_2}\right)C_\mu
\right)_{h_1=h_2=h}.
}
\]

This is the finite coefficient table Gate B must evaluate.

\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f.

The update note states that, under homogeneous scalar grade, these seven families exhaust the leading homogeneous cubic non-\((1,1)\) sector at \(B_7\), and that this leading sector is closed at the natural aggregate package level. 

Because those cancellations are fixed-sector aggregate cancellations, not only determinant-gauge cancellations, differentiating the already-zero aggregate in \(\delta\) contributes zero to \(F_1\), provided the cancellations are used with the same source-tag and midpoint-parity convention. Thus

## Residual source table

After removing Gate A, any surviving \(F_1\) must come from one of the following tables.

### 1. Non-leading homogeneous grades

**Status:** not excluded by Gate A.

Gate A only closes the leading homogeneous cubic \((1,1,5)\)-type inventory at \(B_7\). It does not supply a table for all non-leading homogeneous source-grade combinations that can enter the \([z^7][\delta^1]\) edge coefficient. The draft needs a first-collision table proving those combinations are absent or cancel.

Required table:

\[
[z^7]\left(-\frac12\partial_{h_1}+\frac12\partial_{h_2}\right)
C_\mu(h_1,h_2;z)
\]

for every retained \(\mu\in\mathcal I_{\rm mix}\) outside the leading homogeneous cubic aggregate.

### 2. Grade \(0,2,4\) lower shadows

**Status:** open theorem obligation.

The homogeneous scalar-grade convention removes the \(Y\)-slot families at \(B_7\), but the draft’s own guardrails say that if one changes the convention to an ordinary matrix-output \(M^{[5]}\), \(Y\)-slot gates reopen and require no-double-counting against the natural grade \(0,2,4\) shadows. Even under the active convention, a first-collision proof must show that those lower shadows do not feed

\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}.
\]

Required theorem:

\[
F_1^{\rm lower\ shadows}=0.
\]

### 3. Baseline \(h\)-motion / \(q_0\)-derivatives

**Status:** open coefficient table.

The operator

\[
-\frac12\partial_{h_1}+\frac12\partial_{h_2}
\]

acts on moving baseline data inside

\[
G_\pm^{(0)},\quad N^{(0)},\quad W_\pm=G_\pm^{(0)-1/2},
\]

as well as source positions. Gate A is pointwise in \(h\); it does not automatically provide the complete \(h\)-motion table for non-leading components.

Required table:

\[
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
\left(

+\frac12\partial_{h_2}
\right)
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\]

with all baseline derivative contributions included.

### 4. Amplitude derivative from \(a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta)\)

**Status:** killed for closed Gate A aggregates, open for any remaining component.

For each component

\[
a_1^p a_2^q C_{p,q},
\]

the amplitude derivative contributes

\[
q\kappa(-1)^q a_1^{p+q}C_{p,q}.
\]

If the aggregate coefficient \(C_{p,q}\) is zero in fixed sector, this derivative is zero. That handles the leading homogeneous Gate A aggregate. It does not handle components not already shown to vanish.

Required table:

\[

\sum_{\mu\in\mathcal I_{\rm mix}^{\rm rem}}
(-1)^{q_\mu}q_\mu\kappa a_1^{p_\mu+q_\mu}C_\mu(h,h;z).
\]

### 5. Source-bidegree projection leakage

**Status:** definition-level projection is formal; compatibility is still a theorem obligation.

The projection

\[
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
\]

is defined before quotient extraction. Algebraically, it commutes with \(\delta\)-differentiation if source tags are fixed. But the theorem obligation is stronger: the source-bidegree projector must be compatible with the pre-determinant fixed-sector coefficient extraction \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\). The package note explicitly warns not to apply \(\Pi_{1,1}\) after determinant scalarization or after quotienting. 

Required theorem:

\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\]

is the same object computed by the intended source-bidegree package projection, not an artifact of moving projection past extraction.

### 6. Higher transfer / \(\mathcal T_{p\ge3}\) filtration leakage

**Status:** open.

The broader UV-023/UV-024 chain still requires a homogeneous-transfer filtration or first-collision theorem. Prior work records that coefficient bounds and finite-order grading alone do not exclude \(\mathcal T_{p\ge3}\) through septic order; this is why a source-defined projection/compatibility theorem is needed. 

Required theorem:

\[
F_1^{\mathcal T_{p\ge3}}=0.

```tex
\begin{lemma}[First-collision edge divisibility through order \(7\)]
\label{lem:first-collision-edge-divisibility-order-seven}
On the collision chart
\[
h_1=h-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad

C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}=0.

\[
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\mathrm{mix}}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
=
O(a_1\delta^2)
\]
through ordinary order \(z^7\) in fixed sector.
\end{lemma}
```

## Claim

Gate B can be sharpened substantially without expanding more Fréchet families.

The first-collision obstruction

\[
F_1=[z^7][\delta^1]\,
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\]

is equivalent to a **source-bidegree diagonal/antisymmetric-derivative table**. After the accepted Gate A removals, the remaining obstruction is not another family inventory. It is the following finite theorem:

\[
\boxed{
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h} C_{p,q}(h,h)=0
\quad
\text{for every retained non-\((1,1)\) mixed bidegree,}
}
\]

and, for opposite-parity bidegree pairs,

\[
\boxed{
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\left(
-\frac12\partial_{h_1}
+\frac12\partial_{h_2}
\right)C_{p,q}(h_1,h_2)\bigg|_{h_1=h_2=h}
=0.
}
\]

This is the exact Gate B missing theorem. It is stronger and cleaner than the earlier broad list of possible sources.

## Status: reduced / blocked

The leading homogeneous cubic contribution is zero by accepted Gate A closure. The remaining \(F_1\) is reduced to the diagonal and first antisymmetric collision derivative of the retained source-bidegree coefficients \(C_{p,q}\). The draft does not yet contain that table, so \(F_1=0\) is not proved.

---

## Formula for \(F_1\)

Write the projected raw cross-effect as a tagged mixed source-bidegree expansion before substitution into the collision chart:

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
=
\sum_{\substack{p,q\ge1\\(p,q)\ne(1,1)}}
a_1^pa_2^q C_{p,q}(h_1,h_2;z),
\]

where

\[
C_{p,q}(h_1,h_2;z)
\in \mathfrak f_h[[z]]
\]

is already fixed-sector and pre-\(\Phi_K\). The source-bidegree projector is defined before quotient extraction, so it is legitimate to apply it before taking \([z^7]\) and \(\delta\)-derivatives. The draft explicitly defines \((1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}\) at the tagged matrix-series level before \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\), determinant pairing, or quotienting. 

On the collision chart

\[
h_1=h-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
h_2=h+\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]

we have

\[
a_1^pa_2^q=(-1)^q a_1^{p+q}(1+q\kappa\delta+O(\delta^2)).
\]

Define the antisymmetric collision derivative

\[
D_{12}:=-\frac12\partial_{h_1}+\frac12\partial_{h_2}.
\]

Then the contribution of a single ordered bidegree \((p,q)\) to \(F_1\) is

\[
\boxed{
F_{1;p,q}
=
[z^7](-1)^q a_1^{p+q}
\left(
q\kappa C_{p,q}(h,h;z)
+
D_{12}C_{p,q}(h,h;z)
\right).
}
\]

This is the exact first-collision formula.

---

## Swap-paired form

The raw cross-effect is symmetric under exchanging the two tagged sources:

\[
C_{q,p}(h_1,h_2;z)=C_{p,q}(h_2,h_1;z),
\]

after the standard midpoint identification of the fixed-sector fiber. This is the natural source-label symmetry of the raw corrected-whitening matrix cross-effect, which is defined as a two-source cross-effect

\[
\mathcal W(\mathcal B_2)-\mathcal W(\mathcal B_1^{(1)})
-\mathcal W(\mathcal B_1^{(2)})+\mathcal W(\mathcal B_0).
\]

The draft defines this raw cross-effect before \(\Phi_K\) and before quotient extraction. 

For an unordered pair \(p\ne q\), set

\[
C:=C_{p,q}(h,h;z),
\qquad
D:=D_{12}C_{p,q}(h,h;z).
\]

Then the paired contribution is

\[
\boxed{
F_{1;\{p,q\}}
=
[z^7]a_1^{p+q}
\left(
\kappa\bigl(q(-1)^q+p(-1)^p\bigr)C
+
\bigl((-1)^q-(-1)^p\bigr)D
\right).
}
\]

This is the useful Gate B reduction.

---

## Consequences by parity

### Same parity, \(p\ne q\)

If \(p,q\) have the same parity, then

\[
(-1)^q-(-1)^p=0,
\]

so the antisymmetric collision derivative cancels, and

\[
F_{1;\{p,q\}}
=
[z^7]a_1^{p+q}\kappa(-1)^p(p+q)C.
\]

Since \(\kappa\) is a free collision-slope parameter, this vanishes iff

\[
\boxed{
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}C_{p,q}(h,h)=0.
}
\]

### Opposite parity

If \(p,q\) have opposite parity, then the paired formula is

\[
F_{1;\{p,q\}}
=
[z^7]a_1^{p+q}
\left(
\kappa(p-q)C-2D
\right)
\]

assuming \(p\) even and \(q\) odd; the same formula \(D=\frac{\kappa}{2}(p-q)C\) follows in general with \(D\) defined for the chosen ordered \(C_{p,q}\).

Because \(\kappa\) is free while \(C,D\) at \(\delta=0\) are independent of \(\kappa\), vanishing for all \(\kappa\) requires both

\[
\boxed{
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}C_{p,q}(h,h)=0,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}D_{12}C_{p,q}(h,h)=0.
}
\]

### Diagonal bidegrees \(p=q\), with \((p,p)\ne(1,1)\)

For \(p=q\), source-swap symmetry gives

\[
D_{12}C_{p,p}(h,h)=0.
\]

The first-collision coefficient is

\[
F_{1;p,p}
=
[z^7](-1)^p a_1^{2p}p\kappa C_{p,p}(h,h;z).
\]

Thus one needs

\[
\boxed{
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}C_{p,p}(h,h)=0.
}
\]

---

## Leading cubic contribution removed

The accepted Gate A closures give precisely the diagonal vanishing needed for the leading homogeneous cubic sector:

- \(Y\)-slot families are absent at \(B_7\).
- \(L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2=0\) in \(\mathfrak f\).
- \(L_3N_0R_0+L_0N_0R_3=0\) in \(\mathfrak f\), assuming third-Fréchet midpoint parity.

The update note states that these seven families exhaust the leading homogeneous cubic non-\((1,1)\) sector at \(B_7\). 

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
F_1^{\mathrm{leading\ homogeneous\ cubic}}=0.
}
\]

This is not family-by-family gauge; it is aggregate fixed-sector vanishing.

---

## Residual source table after Gate A

The residual \(F_1\) is now exactly:

\[
\boxed{
F_1^{\rm rem}
=
\sum_{\substack{p,q\ge1\\(p,q)\ne(1,1)\\\text{not Gate A leading cubic}}}
F_{1;p,q}.
}
\]

Using the parity reduction, the missing table has two parts.

### Table 1: diagonal value table

For every retained mixed bidegree pair,

\[
\boxed{
D^{(0)}_{p,q}
:=
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}C_{p,q}(h,h;z).
}
\]

Gate B requires

\[
\boxed{
D^{(0)}_{p,q}=0
}
\]

for all retained non-\((1,1)\) mixed bidegrees.

### Table 2: antisymmetric derivative table

For opposite-parity \(p,q\), define

\[
\boxed{
D^{(1)}_{p,q}
:=
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
D_{12}C_{p,q}(h_1,h_2;z)\big|_{h_1=h_2=h}.
}
\]

Gate B requires

\[
\boxed{
D^{(1)}_{p,q}=0
}
\]

for all retained opposite-parity pairs.

This is much sharper than the earlier broad residual list.

---

## What this eliminates

### Source-bidegree projection leakage

Once \((1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}\) is defined on tagged matrix series before coefficient extraction, it commutes with the formal \(\delta\)-derivative. Thus projection leakage is not a separate algebraic source of \(F_1\). The remaining issue is the theorem that this pre-quotient projection is compatible with the final fixed-sector quotient extractor, but Gate B’s raw \(F_1\) calculation itself can use the projected \(C_{p,q}\) coefficients. The package definitions explicitly place the source-bidegree projection before \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\) and before determinant/quotient extraction. 

### Amplitude derivative

Amplitude derivative is fully accounted for by the \(\kappa\)-term

\[
q\kappa C_{p,q}(h,h;z)
\]

in the ordered formula, and by

\[
\kappa(q(-1)^q+p(-1)^p)C
\]

in the paired formula. It is not a separate table once the bidegree values \(C_{p,q}(h,h)\) are known.

### Baseline \(h\)-motion

Baseline \(h\)-motion is fully accounted for by

\[
D_{12}C_{p,q}
\]

in the paired formula. It remains to compute only for opposite-parity pairs after diagonal values are shown zero.

---

## What remains genuinely open

The remaining open piece is not “all coefficients.” It is the two-table theorem:

\[
\boxed{
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}C_{p,q}(h,h;z)=0
}
\]

for all retained non-\((1,1)\) mixed bidegrees outside Gate A, and

\[
\boxed{
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}D_{12}C_{p,q}(h,h;z)=0
}
\]

for retained opposite-parity pairs.

This includes possible:

- grade \(0,2,4\) lower-shadow bidegrees;
- higher homogeneous transfer terms \(\mathcal T_{p\ge3}\);
- any non-leading homogeneous source combinations not exhausted by Gate A.

Prior work explicitly says finite-order grading alone does not exclude higher homogeneous transfer through septic order, and that a source-defined projection / quotient-compatibility theorem is still needed. turn105file15

---

## Candidate paper lemma

The correct missing theorem can now be stated more sharply:

```tex
\begin{lemma}[First-collision bidegree vanishing through order \(7\)]
\label{lem:first-collision-bidegree-vanishing-order-seven}
Write
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\mathrm{mix}}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
=
\sum_{\substack{p,q\ge1\\(p,q)\ne(1,1)}}
a_1^pa_2^q C_{p,q}(h_1,h_2;z).
\]
After removing the leading homogeneous cubic aggregate closed in
Gate~A, the remaining retained bidegrees satisfy
\[
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}C_{p,q}(h,h;z)=0
\]
for all retained \((p,q)\), and
\[
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\left(
-\frac12\partial_{h_1}+\frac12\partial_{h_2}
\right)C_{p,q}(h_1,h_2;z)\bigg|_{h_1=h_2=h}
=0
\]
whenever \(p\) and \(q\) have opposite parity.
Consequently
\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\mathrm{mix}}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}=0
\]
on the collision chart
\[
h_1=h-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
h_2=h+\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta).
\]
\end{lemma}
```

This lemma is exactly Gate B, but it is now decomposed into diagonal and antisymmetric derivative tables.

---

## Honest verdict

Pushing further yields a sharper Gate B reduction:

\[
\boxed{
F_1=0
\iff
\text{diagonal value table vanishes, and opposite-parity antisymmetric derivative table vanishes.}
}
\]

Gate A proves this for the leading homogeneous cubic sector. The draft does not yet prove it for the remaining retained source-bidegrees. The next attack should not enumerate raw Fréchet families; it should build the two bidegree tables

\[
D^{(0)}_{p,q},\qquad D^{(1)}_{p,q}
\]

for all retained non-Gate-A bidegrees through ordinary order \(7\).

## Transfer-filtration theorem needed

There are two possible theorem shapes.

### Weaker sufficient theorem

\[
\boxed{
Q_{7,m}^q
\left(
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}

=0.

\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
\sum_{p\ge4}\mathcal T_p
=0.
}
\]

### Stronger theorem

\[
\boxed{
\text{Only }\mathcal T_2\text{ contributes to the septic quotient channel.}
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
Q_{7,m}^q(\mathcal T_p)=0
\quad\text{for all }p\ne2
\text{ through ordinary order }7.
}
\]

This stronger theorem would kill all \(p\ge4\) terms and also clarify the status of \(\mathcal T_3\)-type residuals in non-leading conventions.

### Lower-shadow theorem also needed

If grade \(0,2,4\) lower shadows are not intended as independent inputs, add:

\[
\boxed{
Q_{7,m}^q
\left(
\mathcal T_p
\text{ with at least one grade }0,2,4\text{ lower-shadow input}
\right)
=0
}
\]

or prove that such inputs are absorbed into baseline/lower-package data before the source-sector expansion.
