## Claim

Gate B can be sharpened further by deriving the first-collision formula for each homogeneous transfer degree \(p\) directly. After Gate A is removed, the obstruction is not an unstructured “all remaining terms” problem. For each \(p\ge4\), the first-collision coefficient of the mixed source cross-effect has the universal form

\[
\boxed{
F_{1,p}
=
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\left[
(-1)^{p+1}p\,\kappa\,\mathcal T_p(X^p)
+
\frac{p}{2}(1-(-1)^p)\,
\mathcal T_p(X^{p-1},X_h)
\right],
}
\]

where \(X\) is the diagonal source-linear input and

\[
X_h:=\partial_h X
\]

is the antisymmetric collision derivative direction. Therefore:

- for **even \(p\)**, Gate B requires
  \[
  [z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_p(X^p)=0;
  \]
- for **odd \(p\)**, Gate B requires both
  \[
  [z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_p(X^p)=0
  \]
  and
  \[
  [z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_p(X^{p-1},X_h)=0.
  \]

This is the precise transfer-filtration theorem needed after Gate A.

## Status: reduced / blocked

The paper/draft does not prove these vanishings. Existing source notes say the analytic homogeneous expansion and coefficient bounds do not imply quotient-invisibility of \(\mathcal T_{p\ge3}\), and that finite-order grading alone still permits septic witnesses unless a source-bidegree projection or quotient-invisibility theorem is added. turn111file15

---

## Derivation of the homogeneous first-collision formula

For a homogeneous transfer term \(\mathcal T_p\), the mixed source cross-effect at degree \(p\) is

\[
C_p^{\mathrm{mix}}(\delta)
=
\sum_{i=1}^{p-1}
\binom{p}{i}
a_1^i a_2^{p-i}
\mathcal T_p(X_1^i,X_2^{p-i}).
\]

On the collision chart,

\[
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]

\[
X_1=X-\frac{\delta}{2}X_h+O(\delta^2),
\qquad
X_2=X+\frac{\delta}{2}X_h+O(\delta^2).
\]

At \(\delta=0\),

\[
a_2=-a_1,\qquad X_1=X_2=X.
\]

### Amplitude derivative

The amplitude part of \([ \delta^1 ] C_p^{\mathrm{mix}}\) is

\[
a_1^p\kappa
\sum_{i=1}^{p-1}
\binom{p}{i}
(-1)^{p-i}(p-i)\,
\mathcal T_p(X^p).
\]

The full binomial sum over \(i=0,\ldots,p\) is zero for \(p>1\), and the only removed nonzero endpoint is \(i=0\):

\[
\sum_{i=1}^{p-1}
\binom{p}{i}
(-1)^{p-i}(p-i)
=
-p(-1)^p
=
(-1)^{p+1}p.
\]

Hence the amplitude term is

\[
\boxed{
(-1)^{p+1}p\,a_1^p\kappa\,\mathcal T_p(X^p).
}
\]

### Collision \(h\)-motion derivative

The \(h\)-motion part is

\[
a_1^p
\sum_{i=1}^{p-1}
\binom{p}{i}
(-1)^{p-i}
\left(
-\frac{i}{2}+\frac{p-i}{2}
\right)
\mathcal T_p(X^{p-1},X_h).
\]

Again the full sum over \(i=0,\ldots,p\) is zero, so the mixed sum is minus the two endpoint contributions:

\[
-\left[
(-1)^p\frac{p}{2}
-\frac{p}{2}
\right]
=
\frac{p}{2}(1-(-1)^p).
\]

Therefore the \(h\)-motion term is

\[
\boxed{
\frac{p}{2}(1-(-1)^p)a_1^p\mathcal T_p(X^{p-1},X_h).
}
\]

Combining gives the universal formula above.

This derivation uses only the source-tagged mixed cross-effect and the collision chart. It stays before \(\Phi_K\), before determinant scalarization, and before quotienting. The raw matrix cross-effect and \((1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}\) are defined in the package layer precisely at this pre-quotient source-tag level. turn111file3

---

## Partition table after this reduction

The transfer-degree formula shows that the remaining task is to control

\[
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_p(X^p)
\]

for \(p\ge4\), plus the odd-\(p\) derivative term.

### If grade \(0\) is excluded or absorbed

Then \(p\le7\) and the positive-grade partitions are finite.

#### \(p=4\)

\[
(1,1,1,4),
\qquad
(1,1,2,3),
\qquad
(1,2,2,2).
\]

Gate B requires

\[
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_4(X^4)=0
\]

on all these source-grade components.

#### \(p=5\)

\[
(1,1,1,1,3),
\qquad
(1,1,1,2,2).
\]

Gate B requires

\[
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_5(X^5)=0
\]

and

\[
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_5(X^4,X_h)=0
\]

on these components.

#### \(p=6\)

\[
(1,1,1,1,1,2).
\]

Gate B requires

\[
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_6(X^6)=0.
\]

#### \(p=7\)

\[
(1,1,1,1,1,1,1).
\]

Gate B requires

\[
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_7(X^7)=0
\]

and

\[
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_7(X^6,X_h)=0.
\]

### If grade \(0\) is active

Then zero-padding makes the inventory non-finite:

\[
(0,\ldots,0,7),
\quad
(0,\ldots,0,1,1,5),
\quad
(0,\ldots,0,1,1,2,3),
\]

and so on.

Thus the paper must either:

\[
\boxed{
\text{exclude grade }0\text{ as an independent source sector,}
}
\]

or prove

\[
\boxed{
\text{all grade-zero insertions are absorbed into baseline/lower-package data and are quotient-invisible.}
}
\]

Without this, Gate B is not a finite coefficient problem.

---

## Source-sector convention

The active homogeneous scalar-grade convention excludes the ordinary matrix-output \(M^{[5]}\) \(Y\)-slot route, but it does **not** by itself eliminate \(p\ge4\) transfer terms. The existing notes are explicit: coefficient bounds and finite-order grading do not prove \(\mathcal T_{p\ge3}\) invisibility, and a formal \((1,1)\) bidegree projection would kill higher source degrees only if it were actually defined and compatible with \(Q_7^q\). turn111file18

So the current source-sector convention is incomplete for Gate B. It must be extended with one of the following.

---

## Transfer-filtration theorem needed

### Option A: \(\mathcal T_2\)-only theorem

The strongest clean theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_p(X^p)=0
\quad(p\ge4),
}
\]

and, for odd \(p\),

\[
\boxed{
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_p(X^{p-1},X_h)=0
\quad(p\ge5,\ p\text{ odd}).
}
\]

This implies the septic quotient channel receives only the quadratic transfer \(\mathcal T_2\), after Gate A has closed the leading cubic sector.

### Option B: quotient-invisibility theorem

A weaker theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
Q_{7,m}^q
\left(
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
\sum_{p\ge4}\mathcal T_p
\right)=0,
}
\]

plus the first-collision derivative version

\[
\boxed{
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
\sum_{p\ge4}\mathcal T_p
=0.
}
\]

### Option C: source-bidegree compatibility theorem

The formal source-bidegree route would show that only the \((1,1)\) component contributes to \(Q_7^q\):

\[
\boxed{
Q_{7,m}^q(C)=Q_{7,m}^q(\Pi_{1,1}C).
}
\]

Since \((1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}\) removes the \((1,1)\) component, this would kill all retained higher source-degree terms. But the source notes say this is not yet a theorem: the actual source-weight-linear input \(X^{[1]}\), pre-quotient \(\Pi_{1,1}\), fixed-target \(Q_7^q\), and compatibility proof are still missing. turn111file11

---

If grade \(0\) remains active, add zero-padded versions, including:

\quad

\quad

\]

and arbitrarily longer zero-padded partitions.

\[

[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_p(X^p)=0
\quad(p\ge4),

and for odd \(p\),

\[

The current draft does not prove this. It must either be proved directly as \(\mathcal T_2\)-only septic contribution, or indirectly via source-bidegree quotient compatibility.

## Grade-zero treatment

If grade \(0\) is active as an independent source input, order exhaustion is not finite, because zeros can be padded indefinitely:

\[
(0,\ldots,0,7),
\]

\[
(0,\ldots,0,1,1,5),
\]

\[
(0,\ldots,0,1,1,2,3),
\]

and so on.

Thus the draft needs a grade-zero absorption theorem, such as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{grade }0\text{ source directions are baseline/lower-package data, not independent transfer inputs.}
}
\]

or a quotient-invisibility theorem:

\[
\boxed{
Q_{7,m}^q
\left(
\mathcal T_p
\text{ with any grade }0\text{ lower-shadow input}
\right)
=0.
}
\]

The same issue applies, though finitely, to lower-shadow grades \(2,4\). The current draft warns that matrix-output \(M^{[5]}\) conventions require a no-double-counting theorem against grades \(0,2,4\), but it does not prove a general absorption theorem for those lower shadows.

}

\[
\boxed{

and their longer zero-padded variants. These cannot be ignored until grade-zero absorption is proved.

## Does the draft already prove invisibility?

No.

But the paper does not yet provide the required theorem package: an actual source-weight-linear \(X^{[1]}\), a pre-quotient \(\Pi_{1,1}\), a fixed-target quotient extractor \(Q_7^q\), and compatibility

\[
Q_7^q(C)=Q_7^q(\Pi_{1,1}C).
\]

This gap is explicitly recorded in the source audits. turn112file9

The draft also does not prove the alternative \(\mathcal T_2\)-only septic theorem. Prior work says coefficient bounds and \(\mathfrak D_Q\)/finite-order grading alone do not close this route.

## Transfer-filtration theorem needed

A minimal paper-ready statement is:

```tex
\begin{lemma}[Septic homogeneous-transfer filtration]
\label{lem:septic-homogeneous-transfer-filtration}
For the actual source-weight-linear corrected-whitening input \(X^{[1]}\),
one has
\[
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}\mathcal T_p(X^{[1]},\ldots,X^{[1]})=0
\qquad(p\ge4).
\]
Moreover, for odd \(p\ge5\),
\[
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
\mathcal T_p((X^{[1]})^{p-1},\partial_hX^{[1]})=0.
\]
Consequently
\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
\sum_{p\ge4}\mathcal T_p=0.
\]
\end{lemma}
```

If grade \(0,2,4\) lower shadows are not independent source inputs, add:

```tex
\begin{lemma}[Lower-shadow absorption]
\label{lem:lower-shadow-absorption}
The grade \(0,2,4\) lower-shadow source directions are absorbed into the
baseline/lower corrected package data before applying the homogeneous transfer
expansion.  Equivalently, any term in the septic quotient channel containing
a lower-shadow input lies in \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\), and hence
vanishes in \(Q_{7,m}^q\).
\end{lemma}
```

## Claim

Pushing from the draft and the current source audits, Gate B reduces to an even sharper statement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate B is equivalent to source-bidegree quotient compatibility for the actual source-linear input.}
}
\]

The formal transfer-degree computation shows exactly why:

\[
\mathcal T_{p\ge4}
\]

cannot be killed by coefficient bounds, \(\mathfrak D_Q\)-scaling, or finite-order grading alone. But if the actual corrected package is projected to source bidegree \((1,1)\) **before quotient extraction**, then all \(\mathcal T_{p\ge3}\) terms are removed by source degree. Gate A closes. Gate B reduces to a missing theorem, not a coefficient family audit.

## Derived transfer-degree obstruction

For a homogeneous transfer term \(\mathcal T_p\), the mixed cross-effect contains

\[
C_p^{\mathrm{mix}}
=
\sum_{i=1}^{p-1}
\binom{p}{i}
a_1^ia_2^{p-i}
\mathcal T_p(X_1^i,X_2^{p-i}).
\]

On the collision chart,

\[
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]

\[
X_1=X-\frac{\delta}{2}X_h+O(\delta^2),
\qquad
X_2=X+\frac{\delta}{2}X_h+O(\delta^2).
\]

Therefore the first-collision coefficient is

\[
\boxed{
F_{1,p}
=
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\left[
(-1)^{p+1}p\,\kappa\,\mathcal T_p(X^p)
+
\frac{p}{2}(1-(-1)^p)\mathcal T_p(X^{p-1},X_h)
\right].
}
\]

Thus:

- for even \(p\ge4\), Gate B requires
  \[
  [z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_p(X^p)=0;
  \]
- for odd \(p\ge5\), Gate B requires both
  \[
  [z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_p(X^p)=0
  \]
  and
  \[
  [z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_p(X^{p-1},X_h)=0.
  \]

This derivation is pre-\(\Phi_K\) and pre-determinant.

---

## Why coefficient bounds / scaling do not close it

The current source audits already tested this route:

\[
\mathfrak D_Q\text{-scaling and finite-order grading do not exclude } \mathcal T_{p\ge3}.
\]

In particular, finite-order grading permits septic witnesses such as \((1,1,5)\), and coefficient bounds permit homogeneous transfer terms through order \(7\) unless the actual input has a stronger source-degree/projection constraint. turn114file18

Gate A removed the leading homogeneous cubic \((1,1,5)\) aggregate by explicit fixed-sector cancellation, but this does not imply general \(\mathcal T_{p\ge4}\) invisibility.

So the positive proof cannot be:

\[
\text{``orders are too high.''}
\]

It must be:

\[
\text{``source-bidegree projection removes them before }Q_7^q\text{ sees them.''}
\]

---

## Source-bidegree route

The formal source-bidegree mechanism is clean.

Let \(X^{[1]}\) be the actual source-weight-linear corrected block input, with source tags retained. Then a homogeneous transfer term \(\mathcal T_p((X^{[1]})^p)\) has source degree \(p\). The projection

\[
\Pi_{1,1}
\]

keeps only source bidegree \((1,1)\), i.e. total source degree \(2\).

Therefore:

\[
p\ge3
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\Pi_{1,1}\mathcal T_p=0.
\]

In particular,

\[
p\ge4
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\Pi_{1,1}\mathcal T_p=0.
\]

So if the paper proved

\[
\boxed{
Q_{7,m}^q(C)=Q_{7,m}^q(\Pi_{1,1}C),
}
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
Q_{7,m}^q((1-\Pi_{1,1})C)=0
}
\]

and every \(\mathcal T_{p\ge3}\), hence every \(\mathcal T_{p\ge4}\), would be quotient-invisible.

This is exactly the frontier stated in the source audits: the formal \((1,1)\) projection kills higher transfers, but the paper lacks the actual source-defined projector, source-weight-linear input, and compatibility theorem for \(Q_7^q\). turn114file18

---

## What still needs to be proved

The missing theorem is not merely

\[
Q_{7,m}^q(\mathcal T_{p\ge4})=0
\]

as a black box. The precise theorem is:

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Source-bidegree quotient compatibility through order \(7\)]
Let \(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}\) be the normalized corrected-whitening package
representative, built from the actual source-weight-linear corrected-block
input \(X^{[1]}\) with source tags retained.  Then
\[
Q_{7,m}^q(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
=
Q_{7,m}^q(\Pi_{1,1}C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}).
\]
Equivalently,
\[
Q_{7,m}^q((1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\mathrm{mix}}C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})=0.
\]
\end{theorem}
```

For Gate B first-collision, the needed corollary is:

```tex
\begin{corollary}[Gate B first-collision vanishing]
On the collision chart
\[
h_1=h-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
h_2=h+\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]
one has
\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}=0.
\]
\end{corollary}
```

This theorem would kill the entire residual list of transfer partitions.

---

## What is missing for that theorem

The current source audits name the exact missing objects:

1. **Actual source-weight-linear input**
   \[
   X^{[1]}
   \]
   for the corrected two-atom block before whitening.

2. **Pre-quotient source-bidegree projector**
   \[
   \Pi_{1,1}
   \]
   defined on the actual tagged package, not after determinant scalarization.

3. **Fixed-target order-7 quotient extractor**
   \[
   Q_{7,m}^q
   \]
   defined before determinant scalarization.

4. **Compatibility theorem**
   \[
   Q_{7,m}^q(C)=Q_{7,m}^q(\Pi_{1,1}C).
   \]

The source audits explicitly reject post-quotient projection, determinant scalarization, finite-order grading alone, diagonal merger, and downstream package coincidence as justifications. turn114file4

---

## Partition residuals if compatibility is not proved

If the compatibility theorem is not available, the positive-grade residual partitions remain:

\[
p=4:\quad
(1,1,1,4),\quad
(1,1,2,3),\quad
(1,2,2,2).
\]

\[
p=5:\quad
(1,1,1,1,3),\quad
(1,1,1,2,2).
\]

\[
p=6:\quad
(1,1,1,1,1,2).
\]

\[
p=7:\quad
(1,1,1,1,1,1,1).
\]

If grade \(0\) is active, zero-padding creates infinitely many formal partitions unless grade-zero directions are absorbed into baseline/lower-package data. So the additional required theorem is:

```tex
\begin{lemma}[Lower-shadow absorption]
The grade \(0,2,4\) lower-shadow inputs are not independent source factors in
the normalized corrected package, or else any transfer term containing such an
input is killed in \(Q_{7,m}^q\) through order \(7\).
\end{lemma}
```

## Claim

The structural compatibility theorem

\[
Q_{7,m}^q(C)=Q_{7,m}^q(\Pi_{1,1}C)
\]

is **not proved in the current draft**. The formal source-bidegree mechanism is correct—\(\Pi_{1,1}\) kills \(\mathcal T_{p\ge3}\) by source degree—but the draft does not yet prove that the quotient extractor \(Q_{7,m}^q\) commutes with this projection for the actual normalized corrected package.

\[
\boxed{

}

\[
\boxed{
\text{Source-bidegree quotient compatibility remains a theorem obligation.}
}
\]

This is exactly the recorded UV-023/UV-024 frontier: the formal \((1,1)\) projection route is plausible, but promotion needs the actual source-weight-linear \(X^{[1]}\), the pre-quotient projector \(\Pi_{1,1}\), the fixed-target \(Q_7^q\), and a proof that quotient extraction commutes with projection.

## Correct package layer for \(\Pi_{1,1}\)

The projection must be applied to the **tagged, pre-quotient matrix package**, not after fixed-sector extraction, determinant scalarization, or quotienting.

The correct layer is:

\[
\boxed{
C=C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
}
\]

or, equivalently, the corresponding **pre-trivialization, amplitude-normalized matrix package** if one is proving a holomorphic edge statement. But for defining source bidegree, the tags live naturally on the raw matrix cross-effect

\[
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
=
\mathcal W(\mathcal B_2)
-\mathcal W(\mathcal B_1^{(1)})
-\mathcal W(\mathcal B_1^{(2)})
+\mathcal W(\mathcal B_0).
\]

The paper’s package layer defines this raw corrected-whitening matrix cross-effect before \(\Phi_K\), determinant scalarization, or quotient extraction. It also defines \((1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}\) before fixed-sector extraction and before \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\). 

So the correct order is:

\[
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\;\xrightarrow{\Pi_{1,1}}\;
\Pi_{1,1}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\;\xrightarrow{\text{normalization/trivialization}}\;
C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}
\;\xrightarrow{B_7^{\mathfrak f}}\;
Q_{7,m}^q.
\]

It is **not**:

\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C)
\;\xrightarrow{\Pi_{1,1}}\;
\text{projected quotient},
\]

and it is not projection after determinant pairing.

---

## Projection definition

Write the tagged matrix series as

\[
C=\sum_{p,q\ge0}\tau_1^p\tau_2^q C_{p,q}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{1,1}C=C_{1,1}.
}
\]

For the mixed part,

\[
\boxed{
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C
=
\sum_{\substack{p,q\ge1\\(p,q)\ne(1,1)}}C_{p,q}.
}
\]

This keeps mixed bidegrees other than \((1,1)\), and removes pure one-source terms and the exact \((1,1)\) mixed term. The update note’s Gate B target uses precisely this projected raw corrected-whitening package. 

---

## Projection-compatibility proof or obstruction

### Formal source-degree mechanism

Let the corrected-whitening transfer have homogeneous expansion

\[
\mathcal T(X)=\sum_{p\ge1}\mathcal T_p(X).
\]

If \(X^{[1]}\) is the actual source-weight-linear input, then

\[
\mathcal T_p((X^{[1]})^p)
\]

has total source degree \(p\).

Therefore:

- \(\mathcal T_2\) can contain source bidegree \((1,1)\);
- \(\mathcal T_{p\ge3}\) has total source degree \(p\ge3\), so it cannot have bidegree \((1,1)\);
- hence

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{1,1}\mathcal T_{p\ge3}=0.
}
\]

This is the formal reason the source-bidegree route would kill all higher transfers, including all \(p\ge4\) Gate B partitions.

### Obstruction

The draft does not yet prove that the quotient extractor sees only the \((1,1)\) source bidegree:

\[
\boxed{
Q_{7,m}^q(C)=Q_{7,m}^q(\Pi_{1,1}C).
}
\]

The source audits explicitly state that the paper lacks the objects needed to promote this formal mechanism: actual source-weight-linear \(X^{[1]}\), source projector \(\Pi_{1,1}\) before quotient extraction, fixed-target \(Q_7^q\), and the compatibility theorem. 

So the proof is blocked exactly at:

\[
\boxed{
B_7^{\mathfrak f}((1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
}
\]

This is also the corrected UV-026 theorem obligation in the package layer. 

---

## Effect on \(\mathcal T_{p\ge3}\), especially \(p\ge4\)

If the compatibility theorem holds, then every \(p\ge3\) transfer term is quotient-invisible:

\[
Q_{7,m}^q(\mathcal T_p)=0,\qquad p\ge3.
\]

Therefore it kills all \(p\ge4\) Gate B residual partitions, including:

\[
(1,1,1,4),\quad (1,1,2,3),\quad (1,2,2,2),
\]

\[
(1,1,1,1,3),\quad (1,1,1,2,2),
\]

\[
(1,1,1,1,1,2),
\]

\[
(1,1,1,1,1,1,1).
\]

It also kills zero-padded higher-transfer partitions if grade \(0\) is encoded as part of \(X^{[1]}\), provided the source-degree/projector theorem is stated for the actual package input.

If the compatibility theorem does **not** hold, then all these partitions remain live residual classes. The source audits already record that \(\mathfrak D_Q\) scaling and finite-order grading do not exclude them. 

---

## Treatment of grade \(0,2,4\) lower shadows

This remains a separate issue.

### If lower shadows are independent source inputs

Then \(\Pi_{1,1}\) removes any term whose source bidegree is not \((1,1)\), but the theorem still needs to prove that \(Q_7^q\) is compatible with that removal. Also, if grade \(0\) is active, zero-padding creates an infinite formal partition inventory unless the source-degree expansion is bounded by some other rule.

### If lower shadows are baseline/lower-package data

Then they should not be counted as independent source factors in \(\mathcal T_p\). This is the cleaner convention. But the draft needs a no-double-counting theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{grade }0,2,4\text{ lower shadows are absorbed into baseline/lower-package data before source-bidegree projection.}
}
\]

or a quotient-invisibility theorem:

\[
\boxed{
Q_{7,m}^q
\left(
\text{terms containing grade }0,2,4\text{ lower-shadow inputs}
\right)=0.
}
\]

The current draft warns that reviving a matrix-output \(M^{[5]}\) convention would require a no-double-counting theorem against grades \(0,2,4\), but it does not prove that theorem. 

Thus grade \(0,2,4\) treatment remains open.

---

## Exact missing theorem if blocked

The missing theorem should be stated as follows.

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Source-bidegree quotient compatibility through order \(7\)]
\label{thm:source-bidegree-quotient-compatibility-order-seven}
Let \(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}\) be the normalized corrected-whitening package
constructed from the actual source-weight-linear corrected-block input with
source tags retained.  Then
\[
Q_{7,m}^q(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
=
Q_{7,m}^q(\Pi_{1,1}C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}).
\]
Equivalently,
\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}\left(
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}
\right)
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

For Gate B, add the corollary:

```tex
\begin{corollary}[Gate B transfer-filtration vanishing]
\label{cor:gate-b-transfer-filtration-vanishing}
Under Theorem~\ref{thm:source-bidegree-quotient-compatibility-order-seven},
\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\,
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
\sum_{p\ge4}\mathcal T_p=0.
\]
\end{corollary}
```

And add the lower-shadow theorem if needed:

```tex
\begin{lemma}[Lower-shadow absorption before source-bidegree projection]
\label{lem:lower-shadow-absorption-before-source-bidegree-projection}
The grade \(0,2,4\) lower-shadow directions are absorbed into the baseline and
lower corrected package data before the source-bidegree expansion.  They are
not independent source factors for the homogeneous-transfer filtration through
ordinary order \(7\).
\end{lemma}
```

## Claim

Pushing further exposes a logical separator:

\[
Q_{7,m}^q(C)=Q_{7,m}^q(\Pi_{1,1}C)
\]

is **not sufficient by itself to prove Gate B edge divisibility**.

Reason: \(Q_{7,m}^q\) is defined for the **normalized corrected package** after the amplitude normalization and midpoint quotient package have been constructed. But Gate B is the condition needed to make that normalization holomorphic:

\[
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
=
O(a_1\delta^2).
\]

If

\[
F_1=[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\neq0,
\]

then

\[
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\]

has a \(\delta^{-1}\)-pole. In that case \(B_7^{\mathfrak f}\) and \(Q_{7,m}^q\) for the normalized package are not yet legitimate objects at \(\delta=0\). So quotient compatibility is downstream of edge divisibility, unless it is reformulated as a **pre-normalization edge theorem**.

## Status: reduced / structural obstruction found

The bidegree compatibility route is still valuable, but it must be split into two logically distinct statements:

1. **Gate B edge divisibility**
   \[
   [z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
   (1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}=0.
   \]

2. **Post-edge quotient compatibility**
   \[
   Q_{7,m}^q(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
   =
   Q_{7,m}^q(\Pi_{1,1}C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}).
   \]

The current draft’s source-bidegree projection definitions support the second statement as the right target, but they do not yet prove the first. The paper’s own theorem-obligation block treats edge divisibility separately from source-bidegree compatibility, which confirms this separation. 

---

## Derivation of the logical obstruction

The package definitions have the sequence:

\[
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\longrightarrow
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\longrightarrow
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\longrightarrow
C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}
\longrightarrow
B_7^{\mathfrak f}
\longrightarrow
Q_{7,m}^q.
\]

The source-bidegree projection is correctly defined before fixed-sector extraction, determinant pairing, and quotienting. 

But the amplitude-normalized object exists holomorphically only if

\[
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
=
O(a_1\delta^2).
\]

The update note states exactly this: if the \(\delta^1\) coefficient is nonzero, the normalized package has a \(\delta^{-1}\)-pole, and one needs an edge/first-collision counterterm or source-bidegree quotient-invisibility theorem. 

Therefore:

\[
Q_{7,m}^q(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
\]

cannot be used to prove the holomorphic existence of \(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}\) unless the theorem is reformulated at the raw edge level.

---

## Corrected Gate B theorem shape

The source-bidegree route needs a **raw edge-level compatibility theorem**, not only a quotient theorem.

A precise statement is:

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Raw source-bidegree edge divisibility through order \(7\)]
\label{thm:raw-source-bidegree-edge-divisibility-order-seven}
On the collision chart
\[
h_1=h-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
h_2=h+\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]
one has
\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\,
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}=0.
\]
Equivalently, the non-\((1,1)\) mixed component of the raw corrected-whitening
cross-effect is \(O(a_1\delta^2)\) through ordinary order \(7\) in fixed
sector.
\end{theorem}
```

Then, after this is proved, define

\[
C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}
=
\operatorname{Triv}_{h\to m}
\left(
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\right)
\]

and prove the post-edge quotient statement:

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Post-edge source-bidegree quotient compatibility]
\label{thm:post-edge-source-bidegree-quotient-compatibility}
For the holomorphic normalized corrected package,
\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}
\bigl(
C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}
\bigr)
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
Equivalently,
\[
Q_{7,m}^q(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})=0
\]
for the non-\((1,1)\) mixed package component.
\end{theorem}
```

This avoids circularity.

---

## What can still be derived from source bidegree?

The formal bidegree projection still gives a real reduction.

For a source-linear input \(X^{[1]}\),

\[
\mathcal T_p((X^{[1]})^p)
\]

has total source degree \(p\). Hence:

\[
p\ge3 \quad\Rightarrow\quad \Pi_{1,1}\mathcal T_p=0.
\]

So if the raw first-collision theorem can be reduced to **only the projected \((1,1)\) bidegree**, then all \(\mathcal T_{p\ge3}\) leakage is killed. But the missing step is exactly to prove that the \([z^7][\delta^1]\) raw edge coefficient is controlled by this source-bidegree projection.

The currently documented frontier says the formal projection is clean, but current source lacks the actual \(X^{[1]}\), pre-quotient \(\Pi_{1,1}\), \(Q_7^q\), and the compatibility theorem.

This theorem must be pre-\(\Phi_K\), pre-determinant, and pre-quotient.

## Why post-quotient compatibility is not enough

The theorem

\[
Q_{7,m}^q(C)=Q_{7,m}^q(\Pi_{1,1}C)
\]

is meaningful only after \(C\) is a holomorphic normalized corrected package. But Gate B is testing whether that holomorphic package exists. Therefore the quotient compatibility theorem cannot be the first proof of Gate B unless it is backed by a raw edge-divisibility theorem.

In short:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Edge divisibility first; quotient compatibility second.}
}
\]

The attack finds an important correction to the strategy.

The formal source-bidegree route is not wrong, but it is **one layer too late** if stated only as

\[
Q_{7,m}^q(C)=Q_{7,m}^q(\Pi_{1,1}C).
\]

For Gate B, the required theorem is a raw edge-level source-bidegree filtration:

\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}=0.
\]

The current draft does not prove this. The live residuals are the \(p\ge4\) transfer partitions and lower-shadow sectors listed above.

\[

=

\]
through order \(z^7\) in fixed sector.

## Claim

The raw Gate B first-collision identity is **not proved by the current draft**. It is reduced to a precise source-weight-linear / bidegree-compatibility obstruction.

The formal calculation gives:

\[
F_1=
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
\left[
\left(
-\frac12\partial_{h_1}
+\frac12\partial_{h_2}
-\kappa a_1\partial_{a_2}
\right)
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\right]_{\substack{h_1=h_2=h\\a_2=-a_1}}.
\]

The leading homogeneous cubic non-\((1,1)\) contribution is zero by accepted Gate A. The remaining possible \(F_1\) contributions are exactly higher-transfer / non-leading source-sector leakage terms. The draft does not contain the theorem that kills them. The current source audits state this sharply: the formal \((1,1)\) projection kills higher source degrees, but the paper still lacks the actual source-weight-linear input, pre-quotient projector, fixed-target quotient extractor, and compatibility theorem needed to promote that formal mechanism. 

## Status: reduced / blocked

Gate A is closed. Gate B is blocked on a raw edge-level source-sector theorem.

## Expression for \(F_1\)

Start with the raw corrected-whitening cross-effect:

\[
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
=
\mathcal W(\mathcal B_2)
-\mathcal W(\mathcal B_1(a_1,h_1))
-\mathcal W(\mathcal B_1(a_2,h_2))
+\mathcal W(\mathcal B_0).
\]

Apply \((1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}\) while source tags are still present, then restrict to the collision chart

\[
h_1=h-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
h_2=h+\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta).
\]

Define

\[
\mathcal C(h,\delta)
:=
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\left(a_1,h-\frac{\delta}{2};
-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),h+\frac{\delta}{2}\right).
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
F_1=[z^7]\left.\frac{\partial}{\partial\delta}\mathcal C(h,\delta)\right|_{\delta=0}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
F_1=
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
\left[
\left(
-\frac12\partial_{h_1}
+\frac12\partial_{h_2}
-\kappa a_1\partial_{a_2}
\right)
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\right]_{\substack{h_1=h_2=h\\a_2=-a_1}}.
}
\]

This is the raw edge-level obstruction. It is before amplitude normalization, before midpoint trivialization, before determinant scalarization, and before \(\Phi_K\).

The package definition layer already treats the raw cross-effect and edge divisibility as theorem-level data rather than definition-level facts. 

---

## Removed Gate A contribution

Accepted Gate A gives:

\[
L_1YR_1,\quad L_2YR_0,\quad L_0YR_2
\]

absent at \(B_7\) under homogeneous scalar grade;

\[
L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2=0
\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f;
\]

and, assuming third-Fréchet midpoint parity,

\[
L_3N_0R_0+L_0N_0R_3=0
\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f.
\]

The update note states that these seven families exhaust the leading homogeneous cubic non-\((1,1)\) sector at \(B_7\), and therefore the leading homogeneous cubic obstruction is closed at the aggregate package level. 

Because these are fixed-sector aggregate cancellations, their contribution to the first-collision coefficient is zero:

\[
\boxed{
F_1^{\mathrm{lead\ cubic}}=0.
}
\]

This statement does not require family-by-family gauge and does not use \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).

---

## Remaining residual source table

After removing Gate A, the remaining source is:

\[
\boxed{
F_1^{\rm rem}
=
[z^7][\delta^1]\,
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
\left(
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
-
C_{\rm GateA}^{\rm lead}
\right).
}
\]

The remaining source classes are not another seven-family inventory. They are source-sector / transfer-filtration leakage.

### 1. Higher transfer terms \(p\ge4\)

For a homogeneous transfer term \(\mathcal T_p\), the first-collision coefficient has the universal form

\[
F_{1,p}
=
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\left[
(-1)^{p+1}p\,\kappa\,\mathcal T_p(X^p)
+
\frac{p}{2}(1-(-1)^p)\mathcal T_p(X^{p-1},X_h)
\right].
\]

Thus Gate B requires:

\[
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_p(X^p)=0
\quad(p\ge4),
\]

and, for odd \(p\),

\[
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_p(X^{p-1},X_h)=0.
\]

The current audits say this is not proved from the analytic expansion or coefficient bounds alone. turn118file17

The live positive-grade partitions include:

\[
p=4:\quad
(1,1,1,4),\ (1,1,2,3),\ (1,2,2,2),
\]

\[
p=5:\quad
(1,1,1,1,3),\ (1,1,1,2,2),
\]

\[
p=6:\quad
(1,1,1,1,1,2),
\]

\[
p=7:\quad
(1,1,1,1,1,1,1).
\]

### 2. Grade \(0,2,4\) lower shadows

If grade \(0\) is active as an independent input, zero-padding makes the partition inventory non-finite:

\[
(0,\ldots,0,7),\quad
(0,\ldots,0,1,1,5),\quad
(0,\ldots,0,1,1,2,3),\ldots
\]

So a lower-shadow theorem is required:

\[
\boxed{
\text{grade }0,2,4\text{ lower shadows are absorbed into baseline/lower-package data}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
Q_{7,m}^q(\text{terms containing grade }0,2,4\text{ lower-shadow inputs})=0.
}
\]

The draft warns that lower shadows are a no-double-counting issue if one revives non-homogeneous matrix-output conventions, but it does not prove a general lower-shadow absorption theorem. 

### 3. Baseline \(h\)-motion

Baseline \(h\)-motion is contained in

\[
-\frac12\partial_{h_1}+\frac12\partial_{h_2}.
\]

Gate A closes only the leading homogeneous cubic aggregate. It does not automatically kill all \(h\)-motion derivatives of non-leading terms. These remain part of the \(\mathcal T_{p\ge4}\) / lower-shadow table.

### 4. Amplitude derivative

The amplitude derivative is contained in

\[
-\kappa a_1\partial_{a_2}.
\]

For the already-zero Gate A aggregate, this contributes zero. For remaining non-leading source sectors, it contributes the \(\kappa\mathcal T_p(X^p)\) term in the formula above.

### 5. Source-bidegree projection compatibility

The formal source-degree argument is simple:

\[
\mathcal T_p((X^{[1]})^p)
\quad\text{has total source degree }p.
\]

So

\[
\Pi_{1,1}\mathcal T_{p\ge3}=0.
\]

But the draft still lacks the theorem that the fixed-target order-7 quotient extractor sees only the source-bidegree \((1,1)\) component. The current UV ledger states exactly this as the UV-023/UV-024 frontier.

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Raw source-bidegree edge divisibility through order \(7\)]

\[

Equivalently,
\[

=
O(a_1\delta^2)
\]
through ordinary order \(7\) in fixed sector.
\end{theorem}
```

A sharper sufficient theorem is:

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Raw transfer-filtration edge theorem]
\label{thm:raw-transfer-filtration-edge-theorem}

\[

\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
\sum_{p\ge4}\mathcal T_p=0.
\]
Moreover, grade \(0,2,4\) lower shadows are absorbed into baseline/lower-package
```

## Claim

\[

\[
\boxed{

\text{ are not currently proved absorbed, excluded, or quotient-invisible.}
}

## Status: blocked

The draft has the homogeneous scalar-grade convention and the \(Y\)-slot absence theorem, but the scoped remark only says that changing to a matrix-output \(M^{[5]}\) convention would require a no-double-counting theorem against grades \(0,2,4\). It does not prove that no-double-counting / absorption theorem. 

---

## Lower-shadow convention

The active convention is:

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_a r
=
\frac{r^{(a+2)}(m)}{(a+2)!}(t-m)^{a+2}.
\]

Thus:

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_0 r=\frac{r^{(2)}(m)}{2!}(t-m)^2,
\]

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_2 r=\frac{r^{(4)}(m)}{4!}(t-m)^4,
\]

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_4 r=\frac{r^{(6)}(m)}{6!}(t-m)^6.
\]

From the current draft material, the only established exclusion is:

\[
L_1YR_1,\quad L_2YR_0,\quad L_0YR_2
\]

are absent at \(B_7\) under homogeneous scalar grade. That is an order-count absence theorem for the \(Y\)-slot families, not a global lower-shadow absorption theorem. 

Therefore:

### Are grade \(0,2,4\) part of the tagged source input?

The draft does not definitively state the global convention. Two readings remain possible:

1. **Active-source reading:** \(\operatorname{Gr}_0,\operatorname{Gr}_2,\operatorname{Gr}_4\) are allowed homogeneous source inputs in \(X\).
2. **Lower-package reading:** \(\operatorname{Gr}_0,\operatorname{Gr}_2,\operatorname{Gr}_4\) are absorbed into baseline/lower corrected package data and are not independent source factors for Gate B.

The current draft does not prove the second reading. So for Gate B, they must be treated as **live unless an absorption theorem is added**.

---

## Zero-padding analysis

If \(\operatorname{Gr}_0\) is active, order exhaustion is not finite.

Examples:

\[
(0,1,1,5),
\]

\[
(0,0,1,1,5),
\]

\[
(0,0,0,1,1,5),
\]

and in general

\[
(\underbrace{0,\ldots,0}_{N\text{ times}},1,1,5)
\]

all have ordinary order \(7\), regardless of \(N\). Thus transfer degree \(p\) is unbounded.

So if grade \(0\) remains an independent source input, Gate B cannot be closed by a finite partition inventory. It needs either:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{Gr}_0\text{ is not an independent source factor;}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{all transfer terms containing }\operatorname{Gr}_0
\text{ are killed in the fixed-target quotient through }B_7.
}
\]

This is exactly why the draft’s scoped \(Y\)-absence remark says a no-double-counting theorem against grades \(0,2,4\) is needed if the matrix-output route is revived. The same issue appears for Gate B if lower shadows are treated as active inputs. 

---

## Residual list if lower shadows are not absorbed

If \(\operatorname{Gr}_0,\operatorname{Gr}_2,\operatorname{Gr}_4\) remain active, the first live lower-shadow partitions include:

\[
\boxed{(0,1,1,5)}
\]

\[
\boxed{(0,0,1,1,5)}
\]

\[
\boxed{(0,1,2,4)}
\]

\[

\]

and further zero-padded versions:

\[
(0,0,0,1,1,5),
\]

\[
(0,0,1,2,4),
\]

\[
(0,0,2,2,3),
\]

etc.

If grade \(0\) is excluded but grades \(2,4\) remain active, then the positive-grade partition list is finite but still includes lower-shadow patterns such as:

\[
(1,1,2,3),
\]

\[
(1,2,2,2),
\]

\[
(1,1,1,4),
\]

\[
(1,1,1,2,2),
\]

\[
(1,1,1,1,3),
\]

\[
(1,1,1,1,1,2).
\]

Some of these also appear in the general \(p\ge4\) positive-grade residual list; what makes them lower-shadow-relevant is the presence of grade \(2\) or grade \(4\) as an input factor.

---

## Absorption or quotient-invisibility theorem needed

The clean theorem to add is:

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Lower-shadow absorption before Gate B]
\label{thm:lower-shadow-absorption-before-gate-b}
Under the homogeneous scalar-grade convention, the grade \(0,2,4\) scalar
directions are absorbed into the baseline and lower corrected package data
before applying the source-bidegree expansion for Gate B.  They are not
independent source factors in
\[
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\]
through ordinary order \(7\).
\end{theorem}
```

If absorption is too strong, use the quotient-invisibility form:

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Lower-shadow quotient invisibility through order \(7\)]
\label{thm:lower-shadow-quotient-invisibility-order-seven}
Every term in the Gate B first-collision coefficient containing at least one
lower-shadow input
\[
\operatorname{Gr}_0 r,\qquad
\operatorname{Gr}_2 r,\qquad
\operatorname{Gr}_4 r
\]
has fixed-sector order-\(7\) coefficient in
\[
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
Equivalently,
\[
Q_{7,m}^q
\left(
\text{Gate B terms containing a lower-shadow input}
\right)=0.
\]
\end{theorem}
```

For raw edge-divisibility, the pre-quotient version is even sharper:

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Lower-shadow raw edge invisibility]
\label{thm:lower-shadow-raw-edge-invisibility}
On the collision chart,
\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\,
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\big|_{\text{at least one lower-shadow input}}
=0.
\]
\end{theorem}
```

This last theorem is the one Gate B actually needs before normalization.

---

The lower-shadow lane is not closed by the current draft.

The draft excludes the \(Y\)-slot families at \(B_7\) under homogeneous scalar grade, and Gate A closes the leading homogeneous cubic aggregate. But there is no theorem yet saying grades \(0,2,4\) are absorbed into baseline/lower-package data or quotient-invisible. If \(\operatorname{Gr}_0\) is active, zero-padding makes the Gate B partition inventory non-finite.

The next required theorem is lower-shadow absorption or raw edge invisibility for grades \(0,2,4\).

## Status: blocked

Lower-shadow absorption is a missing theorem. Until it is proved, grades \(0,2,4\) must be treated as live Gate B inputs or explicitly quarantined by a new source-sector convention.

---

## Source-sector decomposition

The decomposition we need is:

\[
X_{\mathrm{corr}}
=
X_{\mathrm{active}}\oplus X_{\mathrm{base/lower}},
\]

where

\[
X_{\mathrm{active}}
=
\bigoplus_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{active}}} \operatorname{Gr}_a r
\]

contains only the source factors intended to enter the Gate B homogeneous transfer expansion, while

\[
X_{\mathrm{base/lower}}
\]

contains baseline-renormalization and lower-shadow material.

The target convention would be:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{Gr}_0 r,\operatorname{Gr}_2 r,\operatorname{Gr}_4 r
\in X_{\mathrm{base/lower}}.
}
\]

That would mean these grades do **not** appear as independent arguments in

\[
\mathcal T_p(X,\ldots,X)
\]

for Gate B.

But the current draft does not establish this. It defines/uses homogeneous scalar grade and proves the \(Y\)-slot absence under that convention, but it does not state a global rule assigning \(\operatorname{Gr}_0,\operatorname{Gr}_2,\operatorname{Gr}_4\) to baseline/lower-package data. The package-definition layer lists edge divisibility and source-bidegree compatibility as theorem obligations, not as proved facts. 

---

## Lower-shadow treatment

### \(\operatorname{Gr}_0 r\)

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_0 r=\frac{r^{(2)}(m)}{2!}(t-m)^2.
\]

If this is active as an independent source input, then Gate B does **not** have finite order exhaustion, because zeros can be inserted indefinitely:

\[
(0,1,1,5),
\]

\[
(0,0,1,1,5),
\]

\[
(0,0,0,1,1,5),
\]

and in general

\[
(\underbrace{0,\ldots,0}_{N\text{ times}},1,1,5).
\]

All have ordinary order \(7\). So either \(\operatorname{Gr}_0\) is absorbed, or Gate B is not reducible to a finite partition audit.

### \(\operatorname{Gr}_2 r\)

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_2 r=\frac{r^{(4)}(m)}{4!}(t-m)^4.
\]

If active, it produces finite but live partitions such as

\[
(1,2,2,2),\qquad (1,1,2,3),\qquad (0,1,2,4),\qquad (0,2,2,3).
\]

No current theorem in the draft proves these are baseline artifacts or quotient-invisible.

### \(\operatorname{Gr}_4 r\)

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_4 r=\frac{r^{(6)}(m)}{6!}(t-m)^6.
\]

If active, it contributes to partitions such as

\[
(1,1,1,4),\qquad (0,1,2,4).
\]

Again, the current draft does not prove a general absorption or quotient-invisibility theorem for these terms.

## Zero-padding analysis

If grade \(0\) is live, partitions of ordinary order \(7\) with transfer degree \(p\ge4\) are not finite. Examples include:

\[
(0,1,1,5),
\]

\[
(0,0,1,1,5),
\]

\[
(0,\ldots,0,1,1,5),
\]

and also

\[
(0,1,2,4),\qquad (0,2,2,3),
\]

plus longer zero-padded variants.

Therefore the source-sector theorem must first decide whether grade \(0\) is an independent source input. If it is, a finite Gate B partition table is impossible without a separate cap on transfer degree or a zero-grade invisibility theorem.

---

## Residual list if blocked

If lower shadows are not absorbed, the first live residual classes include:

\[

\]

\]

\[

\]

If grade \(0\) is excluded but grades \(2,4\) remain live, then the positive-grade residuals still include:

\[

\]

and higher \(p\)-degree positive partitions such as

\[

\]

These are precisely the transfer-filtration residual classes that remain live unless the source-bidegree projection theorem or \(\mathcal T_2\)-only theorem is proved. Existing project notes say coefficient bounds, \(\mathfrak D_Q\)-scaling, and finite-order grading do not prove \(\mathcal T_{p\ge3}\) invisibility; a source-defined \((1,1)\) projection or quotient-invisibility theorem is still needed. turn123file15

## Exact theorem needed

The cleanest theorem is an absorption theorem:

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Lower-shadow absorption for the corrected package]
\label{thm:lower-shadow-absorption-corrected-package}
For the actual corrected-whitening package, the homogeneous scalar-grade
directions
\[
\operatorname{Gr}_0 r,\qquad \operatorname{Gr}_2 r,\qquad \operatorname{Gr}_4 r
\]
are absorbed into the baseline and lower corrected package data before the
source-bidegree expansion.  Equivalently, they are not independent source
arguments of
\[
\mathcal T_p(X,\ldots,X)
\]
in the Gate B first-collision calculation through ordinary order \(7\).
\end{theorem}
```

If absorption is too strong, the needed replacement is a raw edge-invisibility theorem:

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Lower-shadow raw edge invisibility through order \(7\)]
\label{thm:lower-shadow-raw-edge-invisibility-order-seven}
On the collision chart
\[
h_1=h-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
h_2=h+\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]
all terms in
\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\]
containing at least one lower-shadow input
\[
\operatorname{Gr}_0 r,\qquad \operatorname{Gr}_2 r,\qquad \operatorname{Gr}_4 r
\]
vanish.
\end{theorem}
```

A quotient-only version would be weaker and downstream:

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Lower-shadow quotient invisibility]
\label{thm:lower-shadow-quotient-invisibility}
Every Gate B term containing at least one lower-shadow input
\[
\operatorname{Gr}_0 r,\qquad \operatorname{Gr}_2 r,\qquad \operatorname{Gr}_4 r
\]
has order-\(7\) fixed-sector coefficient in
\[
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

For raw Gate B edge divisibility, the raw edge-invisibility version is the most relevant, because \(Q_{7,m}^q\) is downstream of holomorphic normalization. The update note explicitly warns that if the \(\delta^1\) raw edge coefficient is nonzero, the normalized package has a \(\delta^{-1}\)-pole and the later quotient package is not yet holomorphic. 

---

## Honest verdict

The draft does **not** yet prove the source-sector decomposition

\[
X_{\mathrm{corr}}
=
X_{\mathrm{active}}\oplus X_{\mathrm{base/lower}}
\]

with

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_0,\operatorname{Gr}_2,\operatorname{Gr}_4
\in X_{\mathrm{base/lower}}.
\]

Gate A only excludes the \(Y\)-slot families under homogeneous scalar grade and closes the leading homogeneous cubic aggregate. It does not prove lower-shadow absorption for Gate B. If grade \(0\) remains live, zero-padding makes order exhaustion non-finite.

The next theorem needed is lower-shadow absorption or raw edge invisibility for grades \(0,2,4\), stated before \(\Phi_K\), before determinant scalarization, and before quotienting.

The desired decomposition is:

\[
X_{\mathrm{corr}}

The draft/source material supports the following weaker statements:

1. The homogeneous scalar-grade convention is the active convention for the current Gate A route.
2. Under that convention, the \(Y\)-slot cubic families are absent at \(B_7\).

   \[

## Claim

The lower-shadow **absorption** theorem is refuted for the current source-linear input convention.

The finite source table treats the lower grades as **tagged source inputs**, not as baseline data:

\[
X_{\varepsilon,0}^{2}=\frac{1}{24\pi}(I-D)\ne0,
\]

\[
X_{\varepsilon,1}^{2}=\frac{\varepsilon}{4\pi Q}S\ne0,
\]

\[
X_{\varepsilon,2}^{2}
=
\left(
\frac{1}{8\pi Q^2}
+
\frac{q^2}{32\pi Q^4}
\right)I
+
\left(
\frac{1}{8\pi Q^2}
-
\frac{q^2}{32\pi Q^4}
\right)D,
\]

and

\[
X_{\varepsilon,2}^{4}=\frac{1}{192\pi Q^4}(I-D)\ne0.
\]

These are explicitly source-indexed coefficients in the same source-linear table used to build the Fréchet/Sylvester coefficients. They are not part of \(G^{(0)}\), \(N^{(0)}\), or \(W^{(0)}\). So, under the currently displayed source table, \(\operatorname{Gr}_0,\operatorname{Gr}_2,\operatorname{Gr}_4\) are **live tagged inputs** unless a new projection/absorption theorem removes them. 

## Status: reduced / absorption refuted under current source table

The theorem

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_0,\operatorname{Gr}_2,\operatorname{Gr}_4
\in X_{\mathrm{base/lower}}
\]

does **not** follow from the draft. In fact, the visible coefficient table points the other way: it places these lower shadows inside the tagged source-linear same-point perturbation.

The raw edge-invisibility theorem remains open; no current table proves those live lower-shadow terms vanish in

\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}.

## Absorption proof or obstruction

### Obstruction to absorption

A baseline/lower-package datum should be independent of source tags and should be present already in the baseline block

\[
\mathcal B_0=(G_-^{(0)},N^{(0)},G_+^{(0)}).
\]

But the source-linear table is explicitly written as

\[
X_{\varepsilon,n}
=
[z^n]\mathfrak D_Q\delta G_\varepsilon^{\lin}
=
\sum_{a=2}^{6}X_{\varepsilon,n}^a r_a.
\]

The lower-shadow coefficients \(a=2,4\), corresponding to homogeneous scalar grades \(0,2\), occur as \(X_{\varepsilon,n}^a r_a\). The table even defines Sylvester coefficients

\[
S_{\varepsilon,n}^a=\Sigma_\varepsilon(X_{\varepsilon,n}^a-\cdots)
\]

for each \(a=2,\ldots,6\), so these are treated as inputs to the source-linear Fréchet calculus, not as baseline terms. 

Thus the currently documented decomposition is closer to

\[
X_{\mathrm{corr}}
=
X_{\mathrm{source}}^{(0,1,2,3,4,\ldots)}
\oplus X_{\mathrm{baseline}},
\]

not

\[
X_{\mathrm{corr}}
=
X_{\mathrm{active}}\oplus X_{\mathrm{base/lower}}
\]

with \(0,2,4\) removed.

### What this refutes

It refutes this absorption statement as a theorem from the current table:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{Gr}_0,\operatorname{Gr}_2,\operatorname{Gr}_4
\text{ are already baseline/lower-package data.}
}
\]

The paper may still **choose** to define a new convention that reclassifies them, but that would be a new source-sector theorem/definition, not something already proved by the displayed finite source table.

---

## Zero-padding impact

Because \(\operatorname{Gr}_0\) is live under the current source-table reading, order exhaustion is non-finite.

The table has

\[
X_{\varepsilon,0}^{2}\ne0,
\]

which is exactly the grade-zero source at ordinary order \(0\). Therefore one can insert arbitrary grade-zero factors into transfer partitions without increasing ordinary order.

Examples:

\[
(0,1,1,5),
\]

\[
(0,0,1,1,5),
\]

\[
(0,0,0,1,1,5),
\]

and in general

\[
(\underbrace{0,\ldots,0}_{N},1,1,5)
\]

all have ordinary order \(7\). So if grade \(0\) is an independent source input, Gate B cannot be closed by a finite partition enumeration.

This is not a cosmetic issue. It means the transfer expansion

\[
\mathcal T=\sum_{p\ge1}\mathcal T_p
\]

can receive ordinary-order \(7\) contributions from arbitrarily high transfer degree \(p\) unless grade-zero inputs are either removed from the source sector or proved invisible at the raw edge level.

---

Under the current source-table reading, the first live lower-shadow partitions are:

\[
\boxed{(0,1,1,5)}
\]

\[
\boxed{(0,0,1,1,5)}
\]

\[
\boxed{(0,1,2,4)}

\[

Additional live classes include all zero-padded versions of these.

(1,1,2,3),

(1,2,2,2),

These are not killed by Gate A, because Gate A only closed the leading homogeneous cubic aggregate. The update note explicitly says Gate B remains the next target after the leading homogeneous cubic sector closes.

## Raw edge-invisibility theorem still needed

Since absorption fails under the currently visible source table, the next possible theorem is raw edge invisibility:

\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\big|_{\text{terms containing }\operatorname{Gr}_0,\operatorname{Gr}_2,\operatorname{Gr}_4}
=0.
\]

The draft/source notes do not prove this. They instead warn that finite coefficient recurrences and source tables are computation tools, not quotient-gauge proofs. turn126file16

A precise theorem needed is:

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Lower-shadow raw edge invisibility]
\label{thm:lower-shadow-raw-edge-invisibility}
On the collision chart
\[
h_1=h-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
h_2=h+\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]
one has
\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\big|_{\text{at least one lower-shadow input}}
=0,
\]
where the lower-shadow inputs are
\[
\operatorname{Gr}_0 r,\qquad
\operatorname{Gr}_2 r,\qquad
\operatorname{Gr}_4 r.
\]
\end{theorem}
```

If the intended strategy is absorption instead, the theorem must explicitly override the current table:

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Lower-shadow reclassification]
\label{thm:lower-shadow-reclassification}
Although the finite source-linear table records coefficients
\[
X_{\varepsilon,n}^{2},\quad X_{\varepsilon,n}^{4},
\]
the corresponding homogeneous scalar-grade directions
\[
\operatorname{Gr}_0r,\quad \operatorname{Gr}_2r,\quad \operatorname{Gr}_4r
\]
are not independent Gate B source inputs.  They are absorbed into the baseline
and lower corrected package before the homogeneous transfer expansion used for
Gate B.
\end{theorem}
```

That theorem would need to explain how the tagged entries \(X_{\varepsilon,n}^{2},X_{\varepsilon,n}^{4}\) are removed or reinterpreted.

---

## Honest verdict

I can refute lower-shadow absorption **as something already implied by the draft/source table**.

The current finite source-linear table explicitly includes lower-shadow source coefficients:

\[
X_{\varepsilon,0}^{2}\ne0,\quad
X_{\varepsilon,1}^{2}\ne0,\quad
X_{\varepsilon,2}^{2}\ne0,\quad
X_{\varepsilon,2}^{4}\ne0.
\]

Therefore \(\operatorname{Gr}_0,\operatorname{Gr}_2,\operatorname{Gr}_4\) are live source inputs under the displayed convention. If grade \(0\) remains live, zero-padding makes Gate B non-finite.

The only remaining ways out are new theorems:

1. a reclassification theorem moving lower shadows into \(X_{\mathrm{base/lower}}\), despite their current tagged source-table appearance; or
2. a raw edge-invisibility theorem proving all lower-shadow terms vanish in the \([z^7][\delta^1]\) fixed-sector coefficient.

is also not proved by the current draft. The source audits explicitly say the homogeneous expansion and coefficient bounds do not prove the needed transfer filtration, and that \(\mathcal T_{p\ge3}\) quotient-invisibility through order \(7\) is missing. turn131file16

## Status: blocked

The target has been reduced to a finite fourth-transfer coefficient table:

\[

The current finite Fréchet/Sylvester calculus in the draft defines first-, second-, and third-Fréchet table contracts, but it does **not** define a fourth homogeneous transfer table \(\mathcal T_4\) or provide its \(I,S\)-fixed-sector projection at order \(7\). The earlier notes also warn that coefficient recurrences are tools, not quotient-gauge proofs. turn130file5

## Three \(p=4\) vectors

Let the fourth homogeneous transfer be denoted by

\[
\mathcal T_4(X_1,X_2,X_3,X_4).
\]

In the active homogeneous scalar-grade convention, the positive-grade \(p=4\) partitions of ordinary order \(7\) are exactly:

\[
(1,1,1,4),\qquad (1,1,2,3),\qquad (1,2,2,2).

For Gate B, since these are total source degree \(4\), they lie in the retained complement

\[

Thus \((1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}\) does **not** remove them. The formal \(\Pi_{1,1}\) route would remove them only if we had a theorem saying the quotient extractor sees only source bidegree \((1,1)\). That theorem is currently missing.

## \(A_5\)-line test

The fixed-target quotient line is

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)=u_5I+v_5S.
\]

The quotient-line test for any vector

\[
C=uI+vS
\]

is

\[
uv_5-u_5v=0.
\]

This determinant coordinate is only a good-patch coordinate for the quotient

\[
\mathfrak f_h/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),
\]

not the quotient definition itself. The source notes emphasize that \(Q_{7,m}^q\) is quotient-valued before determinant scalarization and that determinant scalarization is not a valid substitute for defining/proving the pre-determinant fixed-sector coefficient. turn131file17

For the three \(p=4\) partitions, the three determinant tests are:

\boxed{

\boxed{
u_{1222}v_5-u_5v_{1222}=0.
}
\]

No current draft theorem proves these.

## Why the current draft does not close the \(p=4\) gate

The draft/source material supports:

1. a raw corrected-whitening cross-effect before \(\Phi_K\);
2. a source-bidegree projector before quotient extraction;
3. a quotient-valued \(Q_{7,m}^q\) target;
4. finite Fréchet/Sylvester coefficient contracts through the leading cubic gates.

But the source audits state that the paper still lacks the theorem that \(Q_{7,m}^q\) is insensitive to non-\((1,1)\) source bidegrees, and that homogeneous expansion / coefficient bounds do not kill \(\mathcal T_{p\ge3}\) through order \(7\). turn130file0

More specifically, the available coefficient calculus gives first-, second-, and third-Fréchet recurrences. It does not give the fourth homogeneous transfer coefficient table needed for \(\mathcal T_4\). turn130file5

So the \(p=4\) gate is not presently computable.

# Part A — positive-grade \(p=4\)

## \(V_4\) computation / reduction

The positive-grade \(p=4\) ordinary-order \(7\) partitions are exactly:

\[
(1,1,1,4),\qquad
(1,1,2,3),\qquad
(1,2,2,2).
\]

Because each partition already has total ordinary order \(7\), only the **leading ordinary coefficient** of each homogeneous grade input can contribute. Define

\[
X_a:=[z^a]X^{[a]}
\]

for the actual full source-linear corrected-block input \(X^{[a]}\). Then the three vectors reduce to:

\[
\boxed{
V_{1114}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}\mathcal T_4(X_1,X_1,X_1,X_4).
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
V_{1123}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}\mathcal T_4(X_1,X_1,X_2,X_3).
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
V_{1222}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}\mathcal T_4(X_1,X_2,X_2,X_2).
}
\]

Thus

\[

=
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\left[
\operatorname{Sym}\mathcal T_4(X_1,X_1,X_1,X_4)
+
\operatorname{Sym}\mathcal T_4(X_1,X_1,X_2,X_3)
+
\operatorname{Sym}\mathcal T_4(X_1,X_2,X_2,X_2)
\right].
}
\]

Write

\[
V_4=u_4I+v_4S.
\]

The line-membership test is

\[
\boxed{

\qquad
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)=u_5I+v_5S.
}
\]

## What can be derived about the inputs

For the same-point side of the source-linear input, the homogeneous scalar-grade convention gives the leading same-point coefficient

\[
[z^a]X_{\varepsilon}^{[a]}
=
\frac{\varepsilon^a}{24\pi\,2^a a!Q^{2a}}(I-D),
\]

where \(\varepsilon=-1\) on the minus side and \(+1\) on the plus side. This matches the finite source table, e.g.

\[
X_{\varepsilon,0}^{2}=\frac{1}{24\pi}(I-D),
\]

and the previously derived

\[
X_{-,1}^{[1]}=-\frac{1}{48\pi Q^2}(I-D),
\qquad

\]

But this is not enough to compute \(V_4\), because \(\mathcal T_4\) acts on the **full corrected-block input**, not just the same-point component, and the draft does not provide the fourth-transfer table for the full whitening map.

## \(A_5\)-line test for \(V_4\)

## Claim

The lower-shadow absorption theorem is **false under the currently displayed source table**.

The draft/source table does not place

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_0,\operatorname{Gr}_2,\operatorname{Gr}_4
\]

inside baseline/lower-package data. It explicitly includes the corresponding lower-shadow directions as tagged source-linear coefficients. In particular,

\[
X_{\varepsilon,0}^2=\frac{1}{24\pi}(I-D)\ne0,
\]

\[
X_{\varepsilon,1}^2=\frac{\varepsilon}{4\pi Q}S\ne0,
\]

\[
X_{\varepsilon,2}^2\ne0,
\qquad
X_{\varepsilon,2}^4=\frac{1}{192\pi Q^4}(I-D)\ne0.
\]

Thus grades \(0,2,4\) are **live source inputs** in the current finite table unless the paper adds a new reclassification theorem. 

## Status: counterexample to absorption / raw invisibility still open

Absorption is refuted by the table. Raw edge-invisibility of all lower-shadow terms is **not** refuted yet, but it is also not proved. The next live target is a lower-shadow raw edge-invisibility theorem, not an absorption theorem.

---

## Source-sector decomposition

The desired decomposition was

\[
X_{\mathrm{corr}}
=
X_{\mathrm{active}}\oplus X_{\mathrm{base/lower}},
\]

with

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_0,\operatorname{Gr}_2,\operatorname{Gr}_4
\in X_{\mathrm{base/lower}}.
\]

But the finite table gives

\[
X_{\varepsilon,n}
=
[z^n]\mathfrak D_Q\delta G_\varepsilon^{\lin}
=
\sum_{a=2}^{6}X_{\varepsilon,n}^a r_a.
\]

Here \(a=2\) corresponds to \(\operatorname{Gr}_0\), \(a=4\) corresponds to \(\operatorname{Gr}_2\), and \(a=6\) would correspond to \(\operatorname{Gr}_4\) in the residual-source indexing used by that table. The lower-shadow entries are part of the source-linear perturbation and then flow into the Sylvester recursion. 

So the decomposition currently supported by the table is instead:

\[
\boxed{
X_{\mathrm{corr}}
=
X_{\mathrm{source}}
\oplus
X_{\mathrm{baseline}},
}
\]

where \(X_{\mathrm{source}}\) includes the lower-shadow source directions.

If the paper wants

\[
X_{\mathrm{base/lower}}
\]

to contain \(\operatorname{Gr}_0,\operatorname{Gr}_2,\operatorname{Gr}_4\), it must explicitly override the present table with a reclassification/absorption theorem.

---

## Zero-padding impact

Because

\[
X_{\varepsilon,0}^2\ne0,
\]

grade \(0\) is active under the displayed source-table convention.

Therefore ordinary-order exhaustion is not finite. For every \(N\ge0\),

\[
(\underbrace{0,\ldots,0}_{N},1,1,5)
\]

has total ordinary order \(7\). Thus there are infinitely many formal transfer degrees contributing at ordinary order \(7\), unless grade-zero insertions are killed or absorbed.

Concrete live zero-padded families include:

\[

\]

\[
(0,0,1,1,5),
\]

\[
(0,0,0,1,1,5),
\]

and so on.

This means Gate B cannot be closed by finite partition enumeration while grade \(0\) is active.

## What theorem is still possible?

Since absorption is refuted by the displayed table, the remaining viable theorem is raw edge-invisibility:

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Lower-shadow raw edge invisibility through order \(7\)]
On the collision chart
\[
h_1=h-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
h_2=h+\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]
one has
\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\big|_{\text{at least one lower-shadow input}}
=0,
\]
where the lower-shadow inputs are
\[
\operatorname{Gr}_0,\qquad \operatorname{Gr}_2,\qquad \operatorname{Gr}_4.
\]
\end{theorem}
```

A quotient-only version is too late for raw edge divisibility; Gate B needs the pre-normalization, raw-edge version. The update note says if the \(\delta^1\) coefficient is nonzero, the normalized package has a \(\delta^{-1}\)-pole.

}

## Claim

The lower-shadow raw-invisibility attack reduces to a **fourth homogeneous transfer table** for the corrected-whitening map

\[
\mathcal W(G_-,N,G_+)=G_-^{-1/2}NG_+^{-1/2}.
\]

The paper/source currently does **not** contain that fourth-transfer table. It contains source-linear same-point primitives and first/second/third Fréchet/Sylvester recurrences, but not the fourth Fréchet/Sylvester recurrence or the associated \(\mathcal T_4\) table needed for

\[
R_{0115}
=
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
\operatorname{Sym}\mathcal T_4(X^{[0]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[5]}).
\]

## Status: blocked, but now reduced to a concrete \(\mathcal T_4\) table

Absorption is refuted by the displayed source table; raw invisibility is not proved. The missing primitive is the fourth homogeneous coefficient of the inverse-square-root factors and its insertion into the corrected-whitening product. The current sources state that higher homogeneous-transfer filtration is missing and cannot be obtained from coefficient bounds or finite-order grading alone. turn139file5

---

## 1. What \(\mathcal T_4\) must be

Let a source-linear perturbation be

\[
X=(A,Y,B),
\]

where

\[
A=\delta G_-^{\lin},\qquad
Y=\delta N^{\lin},\qquad
B=\delta G_+^{\lin}.
\]

The corrected-whitening map is

\[
\mathcal W(G_-,N,G_+)
=
G_-^{-1/2}NG_+^{-1/2}.
\]

Write the homogeneous inverse-square-root expansions as

\[
(G_-^{(0)}+A)^{-1/2}
=
L_0+L_1[A]+L_2[A,A]+L_3[A,A,A]+L_4[A,A,A,A]+\cdots,
\]

\[
(G_+^{(0)}+B)^{-1/2}
=
R_0+R_1[B]+R_2[B,B]+R_3[B,B,B]+R_4[B,B,B,B]+\cdots,
\]

in the paper’s Taylor-coefficient normalization.

Since the corrected mixed block is source-linear at this stage,

\[
N=N_0+Y
\]

for the homogeneous transfer bookkeeping. Hence the fourth homogeneous transfer is

\[
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
\mathcal T_4(X_1,X_2,X_3,X_4)
=&
\sum_{i+k=4}
L_i(A_{\bullet})\,N_0\,R_k(B_{\bullet})
\\
&+
\sum_{i+k=3}
L_i(A_{\bullet})\,Y_{\bullet}\,R_k(B_{\bullet}),
\end{aligned}
}
\]

symmetrized over the four source inputs. More explicitly, the \(N_0\)-middle part contains

\[
L_4N_0R_0,\quad
L_3N_0R_1,\quad
L_2N_0R_2,\quad
L_1N_0R_3,\quad
L_0N_0R_4,
\]

and the \(Y\)-middle part contains

\[
L_3YR_0,\quad
L_2YR_1,\quad
L_1YR_2,\quad
L_0YR_3.
\]

This is the full raw \(\mathcal T_4\) table schema for the corrected-whitening transfer.

The current draft has finite recurrences for first, second, and third Fréchet coefficients, but not for \(L_4/R_4\) or the full fourth homogeneous transfer table. turn139file8

---

## 2. Fourth Sylvester coefficient required

The missing fourth inverse-square-root coefficient can be written recursively.

The square-root coefficients satisfy

\[
P^2=G.
\]

For a fourth source tuple \((a,b,c,d)\), let

\[
V_n^{abcd}
\]

denote the fourth Sylvester coefficient of the square root. It must solve a recursion of the form

\[
\boxed{
P_0V_n^{abcd}+V_n^{abcd}P_0
=
-\mathcal R_n^{abcd},
}
\]

where \(\mathcal R_n^{abcd}\) is the coefficient of the fourth source monomial in

\[
P^2
\]

assembled from lower Sylvester coefficients:

- products of \(S^a\) with \(U^{bcd}\);
- products of \(T^{ab}\) with \(T^{cd}\);
- products of \(U^{abc}\) with \(S^d\);
- plus baseline recurrence terms \(P_jV_{n-j}^{abcd}+V_{n-j}^{abcd}P_j\) for \(j\ge1\).

A concrete ordered version is:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
P_0V_n^{abcd}+V_n^{abcd}P_0
=&
-\sum_{i+j=n}
\Big(
S_i^aU_j^{bcd}+S_i^bU_j^{acd}+S_i^cU_j^{abd}+S_i^dU_j^{abc}
\\
&\qquad
+U_i^{bcd}S_j^a+U_i^{acd}S_j^b+U_i^{abd}S_j^c+U_i^{abc}S_j^d
\\
&\qquad
+T_i^{ab}T_j^{cd}+T_i^{ac}T_j^{bd}+T_i^{ad}T_j^{bc}
\\
&\qquad
+T_i^{bc}T_j^{ad}+T_i^{bd}T_j^{ac}+T_i^{cd}T_j^{ab}
\Big)
\\
&-
\sum_{j=1}^{n}
\left(
P_jV_{n-j}^{abcd}+V_{n-j}^{abcd}P_j
\right).
\end{aligned}
}
\]

Then the fourth inverse-square-root coefficient \(K_n^{abcd}\) is the coefficient of the fourth source monomial in

\[
P^{-1}=W.
\]

Equivalently, it is obtained by expanding

\[
W=(P_0+\text{source})^{-1}
\]

through fourth source degree using \(S,T,U,V\). The paper does not currently provide this \(K_n^{abcd}\) table.

This is the exact missing Sylvester recurrence layer needed for \(\mathcal T_4\).

---

## 6. Minimal missing primitive coefficients

### Fourth square-root Sylvester table

V_n^{abcd}

for grade multisets:

### Fourth inverse-square-root table

## Definitions

Let a source-linear perturbation be
\[
X=(A,Y,B),
\]
where
\[
A=\delta G_-^{\lin},\qquad
Y=\delta N^{\lin},\qquad
B=\delta G_+^{\lin}.
\]

Write
\[
(G_-^{(0)}+A)^{-1/2}
=
L_0+L_1[A]+L_2[A,A]+L_3[A,A,A]+L_4[A,A,A,A]+\cdots,
\]
\[
(G_+^{(0)}+B)^{-1/2}
=
R_0+R_1[B]+R_2[B,B]+R_3[B,B,B]+R_4[B,B,B,B]+\cdots,
\]
using the paper’s Taylor-coefficient normalization.

The middle block is source-linear:
\[
N=N_0+Y.
\]

Therefore the full fourth homogeneous corrected-whitening transfer is:
\[
\mathcal T_4(X_1,X_2,X_3,X_4)
=
\sum_{i+k=4}L_i(A_\bullet)N_0R_k(B_\bullet)
+
\sum_{i+k=3}L_i(A_\bullet)Y_\bullet R_k(B_\bullet),
\]
symmetrized over the four source inputs.

So the active placement families are:
\[
L_4N_0R_0,\quad L_3N_0R_1,\quad L_2N_0R_2,\quad L_1N_0R_3,\quad L_0N_0R_4,
\]
and
\[
L_3YR_0,\quad L_2YR_1,\quad L_1YR_2,\quad L_0YR_3.
\]

## Claim

It cannot yet be evaluated to \(I,S\)-coordinates because the paper does not provide the fourth Sylvester / fourth inverse-square-root coefficient tables, nor the full \(Y\)-middle leading-order table needed for \(\mathcal T_4\).

The deliverable below gives the missing table schema:

\[
\mathcal T_4
=
(L_4N_0R_0+L_3N_0R_1+L_2N_0R_2+L_1N_0R_3+L_0N_0R_4)
\]

\[
\qquad
+
(L_3YR_0+L_2YR_1+L_1YR_2+L_0YR_3),
\]

with \(L_i,R_i\) in the paper’s Taylor-coefficient normalization.

\[

for membership in

## Status: partially derived / blocked on fourth-order coefficient table

The first-, second-, and third-order Fréchet/Sylvester recurrences are already part of the paper’s coefficient-calculus layer, but the fourth-order recurrence is not yet present. The source notes also say the raw coefficient tables are derivable as finite recurrences, but that recurrences themselves do not prove quotient gauge. turn140file2

# 1. Fourth square-root Sylvester recurrence

Let

\[
P(z;\tau)^2=G(z;\tau),
\]

and expand \(P\) in ordinary \(z\)-degree and source tags. Write:

\[
P_n^\varnothing=P_n,
\]

\[
P_n^a=S_n^a,
\]

\[
P_n^{ab}=T_n^{ab},
\]

\[
P_n^{abc}=U_n^{abc},
\]

\[
P_n^{abcd}=V_n^{abcd}.
\]

Here \(V_n^{abcd}\) is the fourth source coefficient of the square root \(P=G^{1/2}\), not the transfer \(\mathcal T_4\).

Let \(J=\{1,2,3,4\}\) label the ordered source tuple

\[
(a,b,c,d).
\]

For a subset \(I\subset J\), write \(a_I\) for the corresponding ordered subtuple. Then the coefficient of source degree \(4\) in \(P^2=G\) gives:

\[
\boxed{
P_0V_n^{abcd}+V_n^{abcd}P_0
=
-\sum_{j=1}^{n}
\left(
P_jV_{n-j}^{abcd}+V_{n-j}^{abcd}P_j
\right)
-
\sum_{\substack{r+s=n\\
\varnothing\ne I\subsetneq J}}
P_r^{a_I}P_s^{a_{J\setminus I}}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
V_n^{abcd}
=
\Sigma\left(
-\sum_{j=1}^{n}
(P_jV_{n-j}^{abcd}+V_{n-j}^{abcd}P_j)
-
\sum_{\substack{r+s=n\\
\varnothing\ne I\subsetneq J}}
P_r^{a_I}P_s^{a_{J\setminus I}}
\right),
}
\]

where

\[
\Sigma(C)=Z
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
P_0Z+ZP_0=C.
\]

Expanded by source-degree splits, the second sum is:

\[
\sum_{r+s=n}
\Bigl[
S_r^aU_s^{bcd}+S_r^bU_s^{acd}+S_r^cU_s^{abd}+S_r^dU_s^{abc}
\]

\[
+U_r^{abc}S_s^d+U_r^{abd}S_s^c+U_r^{acd}S_s^b+U_r^{bcd}S_s^a
\]

\[
+T_r^{ab}T_s^{cd}+T_r^{ac}T_s^{bd}+T_r^{ad}T_s^{bc}
+T_r^{bc}T_s^{ad}+T_r^{bd}T_s^{ac}+T_r^{cd}T_s^{ab}
\Bigr].
\]

This formula is for **ordered labelled source tags**. If the paper uses symmetric multilinear coefficients, then the symmetric coefficient is obtained by summing this ordered table over distinct permutations of the source multiset and dividing by the usual automorphism factor. The draft’s finite tables use Taylor coefficients, so no extra raw-derivative factorial should be inserted unless a derivative-normalized convention is explicitly chosen. 

---

# 2. Fourth inverse-square-root coefficient recurrence

Let

\[
W=P^{-1}=G^{-1/2}.
\]

Write the source-tagged coefficients of \(W\) as:

\[
W_n^\varnothing=W_n,
\]

\[
W_n^a=L_n^a,
\]

\[
W_n^{ab}=H_n^{ab},
\]

\[
W_n^{abc}=G_n^{abc},
\]

\[
W_n^{abcd}=K_n^{abcd}.
\]

Here \(K_n^{abcd}\) is the fourth source coefficient of \(G^{-1/2}\).

Use

\[
PW=I.
\]

For source tuple \(J=\{1,2,3,4\}\), the coefficient equation is

\[
\sum_{r+s=n}
\sum_{I\subseteq J}
P_r^{a_I}W_s^{a_{J\setminus I}}=0.
\]

The term \(I=\varnothing,r=0\) is \(P_0K_n^{abcd}\). Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
K_n^{abcd}
=
-W_0
\left[
\sum_{r=1}^{n}P_rK_{n-r}^{abcd}
+
\sum_{\substack{r+s=n\\
\varnothing\ne I\subseteq J}}
P_r^{a_I}W_s^{a_{J\setminus I}}
\right].
}
\]

In expanded form, this includes:

- \(P^aG^{bcd}\), \(P^{abc}L^d\);
- \(T^{ab}H^{cd}\);
- \(U^{abc}L^d\);
- \(V^{abcd}W^\varnothing\);
- all ordered labelled subset splittings;
- baseline recurrence terms \(P_rK_{n-r}^{abcd}\).

This is the exact fourth inverse-square-root table. The paper currently has first-, second-, and third-order table contracts, but not this \(K_n^{abcd}\) recurrence as a named table. 

---

# 3. Full \(\mathcal T_4\) placement formula

Let a labelled source input be

\[
X_j=(A_j,Y_j,B_j),
\]

where

\[
A_j=\delta G_{-,j}^{\lin},\qquad
Y_j=\delta N_j^{\lin},\qquad
B_j=\delta G_{+,j}^{\lin}.
\]

Let

\[
L_I^-=W_-^{a_I}
\]

be the inverse-square-root coefficient on the left for the source subset \(I\), and similarly

\[
R_K^+=W_+^{a_K}
\]

on the right.

For four labelled inputs \(J=\{1,2,3,4\}\), the fourth homogeneous transfer is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal T_4(X_1,X_2,X_3,X_4)
=
\sum_{I\subseteq J}
L_I^-\,N_0\,R_{J\setminus I}^+
+
\sum_{m\in J}
\sum_{I\subseteq J\setminus\{m\}}
L_I^-\,Y_m\,R_{J\setminus(I\cup\{m\})}^+.
}
\]

The first sum is the \(N_0\)-middle part:

\[
L_4N_0R_0,\quad
L_3N_0R_1,\quad
L_2N_0R_2,\quad
L_1N_0R_3,\quad
L_0N_0R_4.
\]

The second sum is the \(Y\)-middle part:

\[
L_3YR_0,\quad
L_2YR_1,\quad
L_1YR_2,\quad
L_0YR_3.
\]

For a source multiset, define

\[
\operatorname{Sym}\mathcal T_4
\]

by summing over distinct labelled permutations of the multiset and dividing by the automorphism factor, or equivalently by extracting the coefficient of the corresponding commutative source-tag monomial.

---

# 4. Ordinary coefficient extraction

For a labelled tuple \(J\), the \([z^7]\) coefficient is:

\[
\boxed{
[z^7]\mathcal T_4(J)
=
\sum_{I\subseteq J}
\sum_{\alpha+\beta+\gamma=7}
L_{I,\alpha}^-\,N^{(0)}_{\beta}\,R^+_{J\setminus I,\gamma}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\qquad
+
\sum_{m\in J}
\sum_{I\subseteq J\setminus\{m\}}
\sum_{\alpha+\beta+\gamma=7}
L^-_{I,\alpha}\,Y_{m,\beta}\,R^+_{J\setminus(I\cup\{m\}),\gamma}.
}
\]

This is the extraction-ready table.

If the source-grade orders in the chosen multiset sum exactly \(7\), then the \(N_0\)-middle part usually only requires leading baseline order \(N^{(0)}_0\) and leading source coefficients. However, the \(Y\)-middle part depends on the actual first ordinary order of \(Y_m\); under homogeneous scalar grade, some \(Y\)-middle terms may start too late and vanish at \(z^7\). That must be checked from the mixed source-linear table, not assumed from the cubic \(Y\)-slot result.

---
