## Claim

The missing fourth-transfer table can be derived explicitly as a recursive coefficient table. The table has three layers:

1. fourth square-root coefficients \(V_n^{abcd}\);
2. fourth inverse-square-root coefficients \(K_n^{abcd}\);
3. fourth corrected-whitening placements \(\mathcal T_4\), including the \(N_0\)-middle and \(Y\)-middle pieces.

The remaining numerical/blocking issue is **not** the table formula. It is the instantiation of these recurrences for the target multisets and the fixed-sector line test. The table below is sufficient for a coefficient agent or script to compute

\[
V_4,\qquad R_{0115}
\]

as \(I,S\)-vectors.

## Status: derived as a table contract / not yet numerically evaluated

The fourth-transfer coefficient table is now explicit. Evaluation still needs the instantiated coefficient lists \(S,T,U,V,K\), baseline \(N^{(0)}\), and mixed \(Y\)-middle coefficients for the target grades. The current draft already records that finite recurrences are table contracts and not gauge proofs by themselves. turn141file5

---

# 1. Fourth square-root Sylvester recurrence

Let

\[
P(z;\tau)^2=G(z;\tau)
\]

and expand the square root in ordinary \(z\)-degree and labelled source tags.

For a labelled source tuple \(J=(a,b,c,d)\), write

\[
P_n^\varnothing=P_n,
\]

\[
P_n^{a}=S_n^a,
\]

\[
P_n^{ab}=T_n^{ab},
\]

\[
P_n^{abc}=U_n^{abc},
\]

\[
P_n^{abcd}=V_n^{abcd}.
\]

The source coefficient of \(G\) is source-linear, so the source-degree \(4\) coefficient of \(G\) is zero. Hence the coefficient of source tuple \(J=(a,b,c,d)\) in \(P^2=G\) gives:

\[
\boxed{
P_0V_n^{abcd}+V_n^{abcd}P_0
=
-\sum_{j=1}^{n}
\left(
P_jV_{n-j}^{abcd}+V_{n-j}^{abcd}P_j
\right)
-
\sum_{\substack{r+s=n\\
\varnothing\ne I\subsetneq J}}
P_r^{I}P_s^{J\setminus I}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
V_n^{abcd}
=
\Sigma\!\left(
-\sum_{j=1}^{n}
(P_jV_{n-j}^{abcd}+V_{n-j}^{abcd}P_j)
-
\sum_{\substack{r+s=n\\
\varnothing\ne I\subsetneq J}}
P_r^{I}P_s^{J\setminus I}
\right),
}
\]

where

\[
\Sigma(C)=Z
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
P_0Z+ZP_0=C.
\]

Expanded by lower coefficients, this is:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
P_0V_n^{abcd}+V_n^{abcd}P_0
={}&
-\sum_{j=1}^{n}(P_jV_{n-j}^{abcd}+V_{n-j}^{abcd}P_j)
\\
&-\sum_{r+s=n}
\Big[
S_r^aU_s^{bcd}+S_r^bU_s^{acd}+S_r^cU_s^{abd}+S_r^dU_s^{abc}
\\
&\qquad
+U_r^{abc}S_s^d+U_r^{abd}S_s^c+U_r^{acd}S_s^b+U_r^{bcd}S_s^a
\\
&\qquad
+T_r^{ab}T_s^{cd}+T_r^{ac}T_s^{bd}+T_r^{ad}T_s^{bc}
\\
&\qquad
+T_r^{bc}T_s^{ad}+T_r^{bd}T_s^{ac}+T_r^{cd}T_s^{ab}
\Big].
\end{aligned}
}
\]

This is the labelled-source recurrence. For symmetric multilinear coefficients, sum over distinct labelled permutations and divide by the automorphism factor of the source multiset.

---

# 2. Fourth inverse-square-root recurrence

Let

\[
W=P^{-1}=G^{-1/2}.
\]

Write

\[
W_n^\varnothing=W_n,
\]

\[
W_n^{a}=L_n^a,
\]

\[
W_n^{ab}=H_n^{ab},
\]

\[
W_n^{abc}=G_n^{abc},
\]

\[
W_n^{abcd}=K_n^{abcd}.
\]

Use

\[
PW=I.
\]

For source tuple \(J=(a,b,c,d)\), the source-degree \(4\) coefficient of \(PW=I\) is

\[
\sum_{r+s=n}\sum_{I\subseteq J}P_r^I W_s^{J\setminus I}=0.
\]

The term \(I=\varnothing,r=0\) is \(P_0K_n^{abcd}\). Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
K_n^{abcd}
=
-W_0
\left[
\sum_{r=1}^{n}P_rK_{n-r}^{abcd}
+
\sum_{\substack{r+s=n\\(r,I)\ne(0,\varnothing)\\I\subseteq J}}
P_r^I W_s^{J\setminus I}
\right].
}
\]

Equivalently, expanded by lower source degrees:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
K_n^{abcd}
=-W_0\Bigg[
&\sum_{r=1}^{n}P_rK_{n-r}^{abcd}
+
\sum_{r+s=n}
\Big(
S_r^aG_s^{bcd}+S_r^bG_s^{acd}+S_r^cG_s^{abd}+S_r^dG_s^{abc}
\\
&\quad
+U_r^{abc}L_s^d+U_r^{abd}L_s^c+U_r^{acd}L_s^b+U_r^{bcd}L_s^a
\\
&\quad
+T_r^{ab}H_s^{cd}+T_r^{ac}H_s^{bd}+T_r^{ad}H_s^{bc}
\\
&\quad
+T_r^{bc}H_s^{ad}+T_r^{bd}H_s^{ac}+T_r^{cd}H_s^{ab}
\\
&\quad
+V_r^{abcd}W_s
\Big)
\Bigg],
\end{aligned}
}
\]

with the understanding that the baseline term \(\sum_{r=1}^nP_rK_{n-r}^{abcd}\) is already separated, and the displayed lower-source terms include all nonempty source subsets \(I\subseteq J\).

This recurrence is in Taylor-coefficient normalization.

---

# 3. \(Y\)-middle leading-order table

The source-linear mixed input is determined by the corrected mixed block linearized in

\[
d_-,\quad d_+,\quad \eta.
\]

The source notes give the corrected mixed block formula and its linearization in \((d_-,d_+,\eta)\), with weighted variables

\[
d_\pm(z)=\frac{z^2}{Q^4}U_\pm(z),
\qquad
e_\pm(z)=\frac{z}{Q^2}E_\pm(z),
\qquad
g_\pm(z)=G_\pm(z),
\qquad
\eta(z)=\frac{z^3}{Q^6}V(z).
\]

For the homogeneous scalar grade

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_a r=\frac{(t-m)^{a+2}}{(a+2)!},
\]

at

\[
t_\varepsilon=m+\varepsilon\frac{z}{2Q^2},
\qquad
\varepsilon\in\{-1,+1\},
\]

we get:

\[
\boxed{
U_\varepsilon^{[a]}(z)
=
\frac{\varepsilon^{a+2}}{2^{a+2}(a+2)!Q^{2a}}z^a.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
E_\varepsilon^{[a]}(z)
=
\frac{\varepsilon^{a+1}}{2^{a+1}(a+1)!Q^{2a}}z^a.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
G_\varepsilon^{[a]}(z)
=
\frac{\varepsilon^{a}}{2^{a}a!Q^{2a}}z^a.
}
\]

For the phase-gap perturbation,

\[
\eta^{[a]}(z)
=
\int_{t_+}^{t_-}\frac{(u-m)^{a+2}}{(a+2)!}\,du
=
\frac{((-1)^{a+3}-1)}{2^{a+3}(a+3)!Q^{2a+6}}z^{a+3},
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
V^{[a]}(z)
=
\frac{((-1)^{a+3}-1)}{2^{a+3}(a+3)!Q^{2a}}z^a.
}
\]

Thus \(V^{[a]}=0\) for odd \(a\), and is nonzero for even \(a\).

The linear mixed input is

\[
Y^{[a]}(z)
=
\mathfrak D_Q\,\operatorname{Lin}_{d,\eta}
N^{\corr}(d_-^{[a]},d_+^{[a]},\eta^{[a]}).
\]

The corrected mixed block formula gives the weighted entries \(Y_{11},Y_{12},Y_{21}\) explicitly in terms of \(U_\pm,V\), and the \(Y_{22}\)-entry is obtained from the linearization of

\[
F(q_-,q_+,\Delta;s)
=(q_-+q_+)s\cos\Delta+(2-q_-q_+s^2)\sin\Delta.
\]

For the target fourth-transfer table, the only leading \(Y\)-middle inputs that can contribute at total order \(7\) are:

\[
\boxed{
Y^{[4]}_4=[z^4]Y^{[4]},
\qquad
Y^{[2]}_2=[z^2]Y^{[2]},
\qquad
Y^{[0]}_0=[z^0]Y^{[0]}.
}
\]

The odd-grade \(Y\)-middle leading coefficients needed for the listed targets vanish at the would-be leading order:

\[
\boxed{
[z^1]Y^{[1]}=0,\qquad
[z^3]Y^{[3]}=0,\qquad
[z^5]Y^{[5]}=0.
}
\]

This parity fact is precisely why, in the target multisets:

- \(Y\)-middle contributes to \((1,1,1,4)\) only when \(Y\) takes the grade \(4\) input;
- contributes to \((1,1,2,3)\) only when \(Y\) takes the grade \(2\) input;
- contributes to \((1,2,2,2)\) only when \(Y\) takes one of the grade \(2\) inputs;
- contributes to \((0,1,1,5)\) only when \(Y\) takes the grade \(0\) input.

This is the \(Y\)-middle leading-order table needed for \(\mathcal T_4\).

---

# 4. Full \(\mathcal T_4\) placement formula

Let \(J=\{1,2,3,4\}\) be a labelled source tuple, and write \(X_j=(A_j,Y_j,B_j)\).

For a subset \(I\subseteq J\), let

\[
L^-_I
\]

be the inverse-square-root coefficient on the left built from the \(A\)-inputs in \(I\), and let

\[
R^+_{J\setminus I}
\]

be the right coefficient built from the \(B\)-inputs in \(J\setminus I\).

Then

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal T_4(X_1,X_2,X_3,X_4)
=
\sum_{I\subseteq J}
L^-_I\,N_0\,R^+_{J\setminus I}
+
\sum_{m\in J}
\sum_{I\subseteq J\setminus\{m\}}
L^-_I\,Y_m\,R^+_{J\setminus(I\cup\{m\})}.
}
\]

The first sum is:

\[
L_4N_0R_0,\quad L_3N_0R_1,\quad L_2N_0R_2,\quad
L_1N_0R_3,\quad L_0N_0R_4.
\]

The second sum is:

\[
L_3YR_0,\quad L_2YR_1,\quad L_1YR_2,\quad L_0YR_3.
\]

For ordinary \(z^7\)-extraction:

\[
\boxed{
[z^7]\mathcal T_4(J)
=
\sum_{I\subseteq J}\sum_{\alpha+\beta+\gamma=7}
L^-_{I,\alpha}N^{(0)}_\beta R^+_{J\setminus I,\gamma}
+
\sum_{m\in J}\sum_{I\subseteq J\setminus\{m\}}
\sum_{\alpha+\beta+\gamma=7}
L^-_{I,\alpha}Y_{m,\beta}R^+_{J\setminus(I\cup\{m\}),\gamma}.
}
\]

This is the exact coefficient placement formula.

---

# 5. Specialized formulas

## 5.1 \(V_{1114}\)

Let \(J=(1_a,1_b,1_c,4_d)\).

\[
\boxed{
V_{1114}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\operatorname{Sym}_{1114}
\left[
\sum_{I\subseteq J}
L^-_{I,|I|}N^{(0)}_0R^+_{J\setminus I,7-|I|}
+
\sum_{I\subseteq\{1_a,1_b,1_c\}}
L^-_{I,|I|}Y^{[4]}_4R^+_{\{1_a,1_b,1_c\}\setminus I,3-|I|}
\right].
}
\]

Here \(|I|\) means the sum of homogeneous grades in \(I\). The \(Y\)-middle term only permits \(Y^{[4]}_4\), as explained above.

## 5.2 \(V_{1123}\)

Let \(J=(1_a,1_b,2_c,3_d)\).

\[
\boxed{
V_{1123}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\operatorname{Sym}_{1123}
\left[
\sum_{I\subseteq J}
L^-_{I,|I|}N^{(0)}_0R^+_{J\setminus I,7-|I|}
+
\sum_{I\subseteq\{1_a,1_b,3_d\}}
L^-_{I,|I|}Y^{[2]}_2R^+_{\{1_a,1_b,3_d\}\setminus I,5-|I|}
\right].
}
\]

The \(Y\)-middle term only permits \(Y^{[2]}_2\).

## 5.3 \(V_{1222}\)

Let \(J=(1_a,2_b,2_c,2_d)\).

\[
\boxed{
V_{1222}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\operatorname{Sym}_{1222}
\left[
\sum_{I\subseteq J}
L^-_{I,|I|}N^{(0)}_0R^+_{J\setminus I,7-|I|}
+
\sum_{m\in\{2_b,2_c,2_d\}}
\sum_{I\subseteq J\setminus\{m\}}
L^-_{I,|I|}Y^{[2]}_2R^+_{J\setminus(I\cup\{m\}),5-|I|}
\right].
}
\]

The \(Y\)-middle term only permits a grade \(2\) input as \(Y\).

## 5.4 \(R_{0115}\)

Let \(J=(0_a,1_b,1_c,5_d)\).

\[
\boxed{
R_{0115}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\operatorname{Sym}_{0115}
\left[
\sum_{I\subseteq J}
L^-_{I,|I|}N^{(0)}_0R^+_{J\setminus I,7-|I|}
+
\sum_{I\subseteq\{1_b,1_c,5_d\}}
L^-_{I,|I|}Y^{[0]}_0R^+_{\{1_b,1_c,5_d\}\setminus I,7-|I|}
\right].
}
\]

The \(Y\)-middle term only permits \(Y^{[0]}_0\). The grade-zero source remains live under the displayed source table; lower-shadow absorption has not been proved.

# 6. Primitive coefficient ranges still needed

To evaluate the four target vectors as \(uI+vS\), one needs:

### Inverse-square-root coefficient tables

For each target multiset \(J\), all

\[
L^-_{I,|I|},\qquad R^+_{K,|K|}
\]

for submultisets \(I,K\subseteq J\).

This includes fourth-order coefficients

\[
K^{1114},\quad K^{1123},\quad K^{1222},\quad K^{0115}
\]

through leading ordinary order.

### Baseline middle

For the leading terms listed above, only

\[
N^{(0)}_0
\]

is needed, because the source-grade sums already equal \(7\). Higher \(N^{(0)}_\beta\) would exceed order \(7\) in these leading channels.

### Mixed \(Y\)-middle coefficients

Only:

\[
Y^{[4]}_4,\qquad
Y^{[2]}_2,\qquad
Y^{[0]}_0.
\]

### Fixed-sector projection

For each of

\[
V_{1114},\quad V_{1123},\quad V_{1222},\quad R_{0115},
\]

compute

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}(\cdot)=uI+vS.
\]

### Quotient line

For later line tests:

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)=u_5I+v_5S.
\]

## Claim

The first \(p=4\) Gate B residuals actually cancel at the **raw fixed-sector level** once the fourth-transfer table is written in labelled-subset form and midpoint parity is applied.

For the positive-grade aggregate,

\[
V_4
=
V_{1114}+V_{1123}+V_{1222},
\]

and for the first lower-shadow target,

\[
R_{0115},
\]

one gets

\[
\boxed{V_4=0\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f_h,}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{R_{0115}=0\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f_h.}
\]

So these two \(p=4\) tests pass even before the \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line test. This is stronger than quotient-line membership.

## Status: derived / proved for the listed \(p=4\) targets

The proof is pre-\(\Phi_K\), pre-determinant, and pre-quotient. It uses:

1. labelled-subset expansion of \(\mathcal T_4\);
2. midpoint parity on right-side coefficients;
3. symmetry of same-point inverse-square-root coefficients;
4. symmetry of \(N_0[0]\);
5. leading \(Y\)-middle parity: odd-grade \(Y\)-leading terms vanish; even-grade \(Y\)-leading terms are symmetric.

The source-linear same-point and mixed input tables provide exactly these parity facts: lower shadows are live in the source table, and the corrected mixed input is linear in \(U_\pm,V\) with the displayed parity consequences. turn142file5

---

## Fourth-transfer table in labelled-subset form

Let the four labelled source inputs be

\[
J=\{1,2,3,4\}.
\]

For each subset \(I\subseteq J\), write

\[
L_I^-
\]

for the left inverse-square-root coefficient built from the left same-point source inputs in \(I\), and

\[
R_{J\setminus I}^+
\]

for the right inverse-square-root coefficient built from the right same-point source inputs in the complement.

Then the fourth transfer is

\[
\mathcal T_4(J)
=
\sum_{I\subseteq J}L_I^-\,N_0\,R_{J\setminus I}^+
+
\sum_{m\in J}\sum_{I\subseteq J\setminus\{m\}}
L_I^-\,Y_m\,R_{J\setminus(I\cup\{m\})}^+.
\]

The first sum is the \(N_0\)-middle part. The second is the \(Y\)-middle part.

At leading ordinary order, all target multisets have total grade \(7\). Hence only the leading source-grade coefficient of each factor contributes.

---

## Midpoint parity

For a same-point coefficient built from a source subset \(K\), midpoint parity gives

\[
R_K^+=(-1)^{|K|}L_K^-,
\]

where

\[
|K|:=\sum_{a\in K}a
\]

is the ordinary homogeneous grade sum of the subset.

The total grade of the four-source target is

\[
|J|=7.
\]

Therefore

\[
R_{J\setminus I}^+
=
(-1)^{7-|I|}L_{J\setminus I}^-
=
-(-1)^{|I|}L_{J\setminus I}^-.
\]

---

## \(N_0\)-middle cancellation

The \(N_0\)-middle part is

\[
\sum_{I\subseteq J}L_I^-N_0R_{J\setminus I}^+.
\]

Using midpoint parity,

\[
\sum_{I\subseteq J}
(-1)^{7-|I|}
L_I^-N_0L_{J\setminus I}^-.
\]

Pair \(I\) with \(J\setminus I\). The two paired terms are

\[
(-1)^{7-|I|}L_I^-N_0L_{J\setminus I}^-
+
(-1)^{|I|}L_{J\setminus I}^-N_0L_I^-.
\]

Since \(7\) is odd,

\[
(-1)^{7-|I|}=-(-1)^{|I|}.
\]

So the paired sum is

\[
(-1)^{|I|}
\left(
-L_I^-N_0L_{J\setminus I}^-
+
L_{J\setminus I}^-N_0L_I^-
\right).
\]

Now \(L_I^-\), \(L_{J\setminus I}^-\), and \(N_0\) are symmetric matrices. Therefore

\[
(L_I^-N_0L_{J\setminus I}^-)^T
=
L_{J\setminus I}^-N_0L_I^-.
\]

The fixed-sector projection is transpose-invariant:

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(Z^T)=\pi_{\mathfrak f}(Z).
\]

Hence each paired \(N_0\)-middle contribution has zero fixed-sector projection:

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left[
L_I^-N_0R_{J\setminus I}^+
+
L_{J\setminus I}^-N_0R_I^+
\right]
=0.
}
\]

Thus the entire \(N_0\)-middle part of \([z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f}\mathcal T_4\) vanishes for every target multiset of total grade \(7\).

---

## \(Y\)-middle leading-order table

The corrected mixed input has entries in terms of \(U_\pm,V\). The relevant leading facts are:

- \(V^{[a]}\) is supported only for even \(a\);
- the leading \(Y^{[a]}\) vanishes for odd \(a\);
- for even \(a\), the leading \(Y^{[a]}\) is symmetric and lies in the \(I,D\)-sector.

This follows from the displayed mixed-input formulas: \(Y_{11}\) starts too late, \(Y_{12},Y_{21}\) have cancelling leading symmetric part when \(a\) is odd, and \(Y_{22}\) has the leading even-grade contribution. The source notes explicitly record the mixed input as a source-constrained linear expression in \(U_\pm,V\), with parity consequences such as \(Y^3,Y^5\) losing their \(V\)-integral part and \(Y^6\) having special parity behavior under the non-homogeneous table. turn142file14

For the homogeneous leading-order table, the needed consequence is:

\[
\boxed{
Y^{[a]}_{\mathrm{lead}}=0\quad(a\text{ odd}),
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
Y^{[a]}_{\mathrm{lead}}\in \operatorname{span}\{I,D\}
\quad(a\text{ even}).
}
\]

---

## \(Y\)-middle cancellation

Fix the source chosen for the \(Y\)-middle slot, say \(m\in J\), of grade \(a_m\).

The remaining sources have total grade

\[
7-a_m.
\]

If \(a_m\) is odd, then

\[
Y_m^{\mathrm{lead}}=0,
\]

so the \(Y\)-middle contribution is zero.

If \(a_m\) is even, then \(Y_m^{\mathrm{lead}}\) is symmetric, and

\[
7-a_m
\]

is odd. The same subset-complement parity proof applies to

\[
\sum_{I\subseteq J\setminus\{m\}}
L_I^-Y_mR_{J\setminus(I\cup\{m\})}^+.
\]

Indeed, for \(K:=J\setminus\{m\}\),

\[
|K|=7-a_m
\]

is odd. Pair \(I\subseteq K\) with \(K\setminus I\). The two terms differ by a sign and are transposes after fixed-sector projection:

\[
(L_I^-Y_mL_{K\setminus I}^-)^T
=
L_{K\setminus I}^-Y_mL_I^-.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left[
L_I^-Y_mR_{K\setminus I}^+
+
L_{K\setminus I}^-Y_mR_I^+
\right]=0.
}
\]

Thus every leading \(Y\)-middle contribution to the four target multisets also cancels in fixed sector.

---

# Specialized targets

## 1. \(V_{1114}\)

Here

\[
J=(1,1,1,4),\qquad |J|=7.
\]

The \(N_0\)-middle part cancels by odd total grade.

The \(Y\)-middle part:

- \(Y\) on a grade \(1\) input vanishes at leading order;
- \(Y\) on the grade \(4\) input is symmetric, and the remaining grade total is \(1+1+1=3\), odd, so it cancels by subset-complement transpose pairing.

Hence

\[
\boxed{V_{1114}=0.}
\]

## 2. \(V_{1123}\)

Here

\[
J=(1,1,2,3),\qquad |J|=7.
\]

The \(N_0\)-middle part cancels.

The \(Y\)-middle part:

- \(Y\) on grade \(1\) or grade \(3\) vanishes at leading order;
- \(Y\) on grade \(2\) is symmetric, and the remaining grade total is \(1+1+3=5\), odd, so it cancels.

Thus

\[
\boxed{V_{1123}=0.}
\]

## 3. \(V_{1222}\)

Here

\[
J=(1,2,2,2),\qquad |J|=7.
\]

The \(N_0\)-middle part cancels.

The \(Y\)-middle part:

- \(Y\) on grade \(1\) vanishes;
- \(Y\) on any grade \(2\) source is symmetric, and the remaining grade total is \(1+2+2=5\), odd, so it cancels.

Thus

\[
\boxed{V_{1222}=0.}
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
V_4=V_{1114}+V_{1123}+V_{1222}=0.
}
\]

## 4. \(R_{0115}\)

Here

\[
J=(0,1,1,5),\qquad |J|=7.
\]

The \(N_0\)-middle part cancels by odd total grade.

The \(Y\)-middle part:

- \(Y\) on grade \(1\) or grade \(5\) vanishes at leading order;
- \(Y\) on grade \(0\) is symmetric, and the remaining grade total is \(1+1+5=7\), odd, so it cancels.

Thus

\[
\boxed{
R_{0115}=0.
}
\]

This holds even though \(X^{[0]}\) is live. It is not absorption; it is raw fixed-sector cancellation of this first lower-shadow transfer target.

## \(A_5\)-line tests

Since

\[
V_4=0
\]

and

\[
R_{0115}=0,
\]

both line-membership tests are automatic:

\[
V_4\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),
\qquad
R_{0115}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h).
\]

No determinant coordinate is needed.

---

## Exact mechanism

The cancellation mechanism is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{odd total grade }7
+
\text{midpoint parity}
+
\text{transpose-invariance of }\pi_{\mathfrak f}
}
\]

for \(N_0\)-middle terms, and the same mechanism for \(Y\)-middle terms after observing:

\[
\boxed{
Y^{[a]}_{\mathrm{lead}}=0\text{ for odd }a,
\qquad
Y^{[a]}_{\mathrm{lead}}\text{ symmetric for even }a.
}
\]

This is pre-\(\Phi_K\), pre-determinant, and pre-quotient.

## Honest verdict

The first \(p=4\) positive-grade aggregate and the first lower-shadow residual both close:

\[
\boxed{
V_4=0,\qquad R_{0115}=0.
}
\]

This does not prove all of Gate B, but it removes the first live \(p=4\) and first lower-shadow targets without needing \(A_5\)-line testing.

Your target is to generalize this cancellation.

Claim to test:
For any homogeneous transfer degree \(d\), and any labelled source multiset
\[
J=(g_1,\ldots,g_d),\qquad |J|=\sum_i g_i=7,
\]
the leading ordinary-order \(z^7\) amplitude part
\[
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_d(X^{[g_1]},\ldots,X^{[g_d]})
\]
vanishes in \(\mathfrak f_h\), provided:
\[

\(N_0\) is symmetric, the inverse-square-root coefficients are symmetric, and the leading \(Y\)-middle input satisfies
\[
Y^{[a]}_{\mathrm{lead}}=0\quad(a\text{ odd}),
\qquad
Y^{[a]}_{\mathrm{lead}}\text{ symmetric}\quad(a\text{ even}).
\]

Tasks:
1. Prove the subset-complement cancellation for the \(N_0\)-middle part for arbitrary \(d\), not just \(d=4\).
2. Prove the same for the \(Y\)-middle part using the odd/even leading \(Y\)-table.
3. Apply the result to the remaining positive-grade partitions:
\[
d=5:\ (1,1,1,1,3),\ (1,1,1,2,2),
\]
\[
d=6:\ (1,1,1,1,1,2),
\]
\[
d=7:\ (1,1,1,1,1,1,1).
\]
4. Separately analyze the odd-\(d\) collision-motion terms:
\[
\mathcal T_5(X^4,X_h),
\qquad
\mathcal T_7(X^6,X_h).
\]
Do not assume they vanish from the amplitude-part argument. Check whether \(X_h\) has parity/symmetry properties that allow the same pairing argument.

   - only the amplitude part;
   - both amplitude and \(X_h\)-insertion parts;
   - or neither.

## Claim

The parity/transpose cancellation **does generalize to the amplitude part** of every homogeneous transfer degree \(d\) whose labelled source multiset has total ordinary grade

\[
|J|=\sum_i g_i=7.
\]

So for all such \(J\),

\[
\boxed{
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\mathcal T_d(X^{[g_1]},\ldots,X^{[g_d]})=0
}
\]

under the stated assumptions.

This closes the amplitude part for:

\[
d=5:\ (1,1,1,1,3),\ (1,1,1,2,2),
\]

\[
d=6:\ (1,1,1,1,1,2),
\]

\[
d=7:\ (1,1,1,1,1,1,1).
\]

However, the same proof does **not automatically close** the odd-\(d\) collision-motion terms

\[
\mathcal T_5(X^4,X_h),
\qquad
\mathcal T_7(X^6,X_h).

Those close only after an additional \(X_h\)-parity theorem is proved.

## General \(N_0\)-middle proof

Let \(J=\{1,\ldots,d\}\) be a labelled source multiset with total ordinary grade

\[
|J|=7.
\]

For a subset \(I\subseteq J\), write

\[
L_I^-
\]

for the left inverse-square-root coefficient built from the source labels in \(I\), and write

\[
R_{J\setminus I}^+
\]

for the corresponding right coefficient.

The \(N_0\)-middle contribution to the leading ordinary coefficient is

\[
\sum_{I\subseteq J}
L_I^-\,N_0\,R_{J\setminus I}^+.
\]

By midpoint parity,

\[
R_K^+=(-1)^{|K|}L_K^-.
\]

Thus the term for \(I\) is

\[
(-1)^{|J|-|I|}
L_I^-N_0L_{J\setminus I}^-.
\]

Since

\[
|J|=7,
\]

this is

\[
-(-1)^{|I|}
L_I^-N_0L_{J\setminus I}^-.
\]

Pair \(I\) with its complement \(J\setminus I\). The paired contribution is

\[
(-1)^{|I|}
\left(
-L_I^-N_0L_{J\setminus I}^-
+
L_{J\setminus I}^-N_0L_I^-
\right).
\]

The matrices \(L_I^-\), \(L_{J\setminus I}^-\), and \(N_0\) are symmetric. Therefore

\[
(L_I^-N_0L_{J\setminus I}^-)^T
=
L_{J\setminus I}^-N_0L_I^-.
\]

The fixed-sector projection is transpose-invariant:

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(Z^T)=\pi_{\mathfrak f}(Z).
\]

Hence each subset-complement pair has zero fixed-sector projection:

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left[
L_I^-N_0R_{J\setminus I}^+
+
L_{J\setminus I}^-N_0R_I^+
\right]=0.
}
\]

Therefore the whole \(N_0\)-middle contribution vanishes in \(\mathfrak f_h\).

This is exactly the same mechanism previously used for the all-left/all-right Gate A pair, but now stated for arbitrary transfer degree and arbitrary labelled multiset of odd total grade \(7\). The draft/update notes already use midpoint parity and transpose-invariance as legitimate pre-\(\Phi_K\) fixed-sector tools. turn143file5

---

## General \(Y\)-middle proof

Now fix a source label \(m\in J\) to occupy the \(Y\)-middle slot. Let

\[
a:=g_m
\]

be its homogeneous grade, and set

\[
K:=J\setminus\{m\}.
\]

The \(Y\)-middle contribution for this \(m\) is

\[
\sum_{I\subseteq K}
L_I^-\,Y_m\,R_{K\setminus I}^+.
\]

### Case 1: \(a\) odd

By the assumed leading \(Y\)-table,

\[
Y^{[a]}_{\mathrm{lead}}=0.
\]

So the \(Y\)-middle contribution is zero.

### Case 2: \(a\) even

Then

\[
Y^{[a]}_{\mathrm{lead}}
\]

is symmetric. Also

\[
|K|=|J|-a=7-a.
\]

Since \(7\) is odd and \(a\) is even,

\[
|K|\text{ is odd}.
\]

Using midpoint parity,

\[
R_{K\setminus I}^+
=
(-1)^{|K|-|I|}L_{K\setminus I}^-
=
-(-1)^{|I|}L_{K\setminus I}^-.
\]

Pair \(I\) with \(K\setminus I\). The paired contribution is

\[
(-1)^{|I|}
\left(
-L_I^-Y_mL_{K\setminus I}^-
+
L_{K\setminus I}^-Y_mL_I^-
\right).
\]

Since \(L_I^-\), \(L_{K\setminus I}^-\), and \(Y_m\) are symmetric,

\[
(L_I^-Y_mL_{K\setminus I}^-)^T
=
L_{K\setminus I}^-Y_mL_I^-.
\]

Hence the pair has zero fixed-sector projection.

Thus every \(Y\)-middle contribution also cancels in \(\mathfrak f_h\).

The only assumptions used are the midpoint parity rule and the leading \(Y\)-table:

\[
Y^{[a]}_{\mathrm{lead}}=0\quad(a\text{ odd}),
\qquad
Y^{[a]}_{\mathrm{lead}}\text{ symmetric}\quad(a\text{ even}).
\]

These are consistent with the corrected mixed-block source-linear formulas and the scoped homogeneous scalar-grade \(Y\)-slot absence framework. turn143file15

It has total grade \(7\), so

Thus the amplitude part of all remaining positive-grade \(d=5,6,7\) partitions closes.

## \(X_h\)-insertion audit

The accepted first-collision formula has an additional term for odd \(d\):

\[
\frac{d}{2}(1-(-1)^d)\mathcal T_d(X^{d-1},X_h).
\]

So the \(X_h\)-insertion terms occur for

\[
d=5,\qquad d=7.
\]

They are:

\[
\mathcal T_5(X^4,X_h),
\]

and

\[
\mathcal T_7(X^6,X_h).
\]

The amplitude-part proof does **not** automatically apply to these terms unless \(X_h\) satisfies a compatible parity/symmetry theorem.

The sufficient theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
R^+_{K,h}=(-1)^{|K|}L^-_{K,h}
}
\]

for all source subsets containing an \(X_h\)-insertion, with the same ordinary-grade parity convention, and the \(Y_h\)-middle table satisfies

\[
\boxed{
Y_h^{[a]}=0\quad(a\text{ odd}),\qquad
Y_h^{[a]}\text{ symmetric}\quad(a\text{ even}).
}
\]

If those hold, the same subset-complement proof applies.

However, the current draft/source material does not state this \(X_h\)-parity theorem. \(X_h\) is a midpoint derivative of the source-linear input; such a derivative can introduce baseline \(h\)-motion and source-jet shifts. That may preserve parity, but it is not automatic from the amplitude-part proof.

Therefore the odd-\(d\) collision-motion terms remain live unless the following theorem is added:

```tex id="mi5qo8"
\begin{lemma}[Midpoint parity for first-collision source derivatives]
For the midpoint derivative \(X_h=\partial_hX\) of the source-linear corrected
block input, the left and right coefficient tables satisfy the same parity law
as the undifferentiated input:
\[
R^+_{K,h}=(-1)^{|K|}L^-_{K,h}.
\]
Moreover the mixed middle source derivative satisfies
\[
Y_h^{[a]}=0\quad(a\text{ odd}),\qquad
Y_h^{[a]}\text{ is symmetric}\quad(a\text{ even})
\]
at the leading ordinary order relevant to \(B_7\).
\]
\end{lemma}
```

Without that lemma, we can close only the amplitude part.

---

## Honest verdict

The general cancellation theorem is true for the amplitude part:

\[
\boxed{
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\mathcal T_d(X^{[g_1]},\ldots,X^{[g_d]})=0
}
\]

for every labelled multiset with total ordinary grade \(7\), under the stated parity/symmetry hypotheses.

This closes the amplitude components for all remaining positive-grade \(d=5,6,7\) partitions.

But the full Gate B first-collision theorem is not closed yet, because odd-\(d\) terms contain \(X_h\)-insertions. Those require a separate midpoint-parity theorem for \(X_h\).

## Claim

The remaining Gate B obstruction is now sharply identified:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the odd-transfer collision-motion terms do not close under the amplitude-part parity argument.}
}
\]

The raw collision derivative of a homogeneous scalar-grade source lowers the grade by one:

\[
\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r=-\operatorname{Gr}_{g-1}r
\]

up to the corresponding derivative of the source coefficient. Therefore \(X_h\) introduces lower-shadow inputs. The subset-complement cancellation that killed the amplitude part relied on total ordinary grade \(7\) being odd; after a raw \(X_h\)-insertion, the source-grade sum becomes \(6\), so the parity cancellation mechanism no longer applies at leading order.

There is no covariant source derivative \(\nabla_hX\) defined in the draft that subtracts this grade-lowering part at the raw edge level. Therefore the odd-degree collision-motion channels remain live.

## Status: reduced / blocked

Amplitude part: closed.

Raw \(X_h\)-insertion part: live.

The missing theorem is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{either define a raw-edge covariant source derivative that removes the grade-lowering shadow,}
}
\]

or prove raw edge-invisibility for the resulting lower-shadow \(X_h\)-channels.

## 1. Raw \(X_h\) parity calculation

The homogeneous scalar-grade convention is

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_g r
=
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2}
\]

in a moving midpoint chart. If we hold the scalar source coefficient fixed and differentiate the homogeneous basis with respect to \(h\), then

\[
\partial_h\left(\frac{(t-h)^{g+2}}{(g+2)!}\right)
=
-\frac{(t-h)^{g+1}}{(g+1)!}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r
=
-\operatorname{Gr}_{g-1}r
\quad
\text{on the homogeneous basis part.}
}
\]

More generally,

\[
\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r
=
\frac{r^{(g+3)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2}
-
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+1)!}(t-h)^{g+1}.
\]

The first term differentiates the coefficient and stays in grade \(g\)-type data with a shifted scalar coefficient. The second term is the grade-lowering lower-shadow term.

For Gate B, the dangerous part is the grade-lowering component:

\[
\boxed{
X_h^{[g]}\supset -X^{[g-1]}.
}
\]

This lowers ordinary grade by one and changes midpoint parity. Since midpoint parity is

\[
X_+^{[g]}=(-1)^gX_-^{[g]},
\]

the lowered term has parity

\[
(-1)^{g-1},
\]

not

\[
(-1)^g.
\]

So raw \(X_h\) does not satisfy the same parity rule as \(X^{[g]}\).

---

## 2. Why the amplitude-part proof fails for \(X_h\)

For the amplitude part, each labelled multiset \(J\) had total grade

\[
|J|=7.
\]

Subset-complement pairing gave signs

\[
(-1)^{|J|-|I|}=-(-1)^{|I|}
\]

because \(|J|\) was odd. That created pairwise cancellation after transpose projection.

For an \(X_h\)-insertion into an odd transfer degree, one source grade is lowered by one. Hence the source-grade sum becomes

\[
7-1=6.
\]

Now

\[
(-1)^{6-|I|}=+(-1)^{|I|},
\]

so the two subset-complement terms are transposes with the **same** sign, not opposite signs. Thus the amplitude cancellation becomes a symmetrization, not a cancellation.

This is the structural reason the \(X_h\)-terms survive.

---

## 3. Does the draft define a covariant derivative?

The needed covariant derivative would be something like

\[
\nabla_hX^{[g]}
=
\partial_hX^{[g]}+X^{[g-1]}_{\mathrm{lower}}
\]

so that the grade-lowering component is subtracted and

\[
\nabla_hX^{[g]}
\]

preserves the grade-\(g\) midpoint parity:

\[
(\nabla_hX^{[g]})^+=(-1)^g(\nabla_hX^{[g]})^-.
\]

Equivalently, it would be the derivative of the source coefficient in a fixed homogeneous-frame connection, not the raw derivative of the full Taylor monomial.

I do **not** find such a raw-edge covariant source derivative in the draft. The representative-level midpoint trivialization and quotient-line connection are downstream: they operate on fixed-sector quotient representatives after projection/trivialization. They do not redefine the raw source derivative inside

\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}.
\]

The update note also warns that the \(Z_j[M]\) connection table is not available until edge divisibility / holomorphic extension is proved; using post-trivialization corrections here would double-count or be logically circular. 

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No covariant derivative is currently defined at the raw Gate B layer.}
}
\]

---

## 4. Effect on \(\mathcal T_5(X^4,X_h)\)

The amplitude \(d=5\) positive-grade partitions were:

\[
(1,1,1,1,3),
\qquad
(1,1,1,2,2).
\]

When one source slot is replaced by its raw \(h\)-derivative, the grade-lowering pieces are:

### From \((1,1,1,1,3)\)

Differentiating a grade \(1\) slot gives:

\[
(0,1,1,1,3).
\]

Differentiating the grade \(3\) slot gives:

\[
(1,1,1,1,2).
\]

So the raw \(X_h\)-residual classes include

\[
\boxed{(0,1,1,1,3)}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{(1,1,1,1,2)}.
\]

### From \((1,1,1,2,2)\)

Differentiating a grade \(1\) slot gives:

\[
(0,1,1,2,2).
\]

Differentiating a grade \(2\) slot gives:

\[
(1,1,1,1,2).
\]

So the residual classes include

\[
\boxed{(0,1,1,2,2)}
\]

and again

\[
\boxed{(1,1,1,1,2)}.
\]

The total source-grade sum is \(6\), so a \([z^7]\) coefficient requires one additional ordinary-order unit from baseline motion, non-leading source coefficients, \(N^{(0)}_1\), \(Y\)-middle higher coefficient, or inverse-square-root higher coefficient. Hence these are not killed by leading-order parity.

The corresponding raw edge targets are:

\[
\boxed{
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}\mathcal T_5
(X^{[0]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[3]}),
}

\boxed{
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}\mathcal T_5
(X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[2]}),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}\mathcal T_5
(X^{[0]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[2]},X^{[2]}).
}
\]

These are live unless a covariant derivative or raw invisibility theorem kills them.

## 5. Effect on \(\mathcal T_7(X^6,X_h)\)

The amplitude \(d=7\) positive-grade partition was:

Differentiating any grade \(1\) slot lowers it to grade \(0\), producing:

## 7. Exact theorem needed

The best theorem is now a raw-edge covariant derivative theorem:

```tex id="ko8m1r"
\begin{theorem}[Raw source-frame connection for Gate B]
\label{thm:raw-source-frame-connection-gate-b}
There is a source-frame connection \(\nabla_h\) on the homogeneous scalar-grade
source input such that
\[
\nabla_hX^{[g]}
\]
has the same midpoint parity as \(X^{[g]}\):
\[
(\nabla_hX^{[g]})^+=(-1)^g(\nabla_hX^{[g]})^-.
\]
Moreover the raw first-collision derivative of
\[
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\]
is computed using \(\nabla_hX\), with the grade-lowering component of
\(\partial_hX\) absorbed into baseline/lower-package data or cancelled by a
raw edge counterterm.
\end{theorem}
```

If no such connection exists, the needed invisibility theorem is:

```tex id="k8zkru"
\begin{theorem}[Raw edge invisibility for \(X_h\)-lowered shadows]
\label{thm:raw-edge-invisibility-xh-lowered-shadows}
The raw Gate B first-collision terms containing the grade-lowered component of
\(X_h\) vanish in fixed sector through ordinary order \(7\):
\[
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\mathcal T_5(X^4,X_h^{\mathrm{lower}})=0,
\]
and
\[
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\mathcal T_7(X^6,X_h^{\mathrm{lower}})=0.
\]
\end{theorem}
```

## Claim

The raw \(X_h\)-insertion lane remains live. A direct derivation from the homogeneous source convention shows:

\[
\partial_h X^{[g]}
=
X^{[g]}_{\mathrm{coeff}}
-
X^{[g-1]}_{\mathrm{lower}},
\]

where the second term lowers ordinary grade by one and flips midpoint parity. The draft does **not** define a raw-edge covariant source derivative that removes this lower component. The available package/trivialization machinery is downstream of edge divisibility and cannot be used to cancel a \(\delta^{-1}\)-pole before proving holomorphicity. The update note explicitly warns not to use post-trivialization \(B_j[M]\) before edge divisibility / holomorphic extension exists. 

So the odd-transfer collision-motion terms

\[
\mathcal T_5(X^4,X_h),\qquad \mathcal T_7(X^6,X_h)
\]

remain the next live raw Gate B obstruction.

## Status: reduced / blocked

Amplitude part: closed.

Raw \(X_h\)-insertion part: not closed.

No covariant derivative is currently available at the raw layer.

---

## 1. Raw homogeneous source derivative

The homogeneous scalar-grade source basis is

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_g r(h;t)
=
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2}.
\]

Differentiate with respect to \(h\):

\[
\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r
=
\frac{r^{(g+3)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2}
-
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+1)!}(t-h)^{g+1}.
\]

So there are two pieces:

\[
\boxed{
\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r
=
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r)_{\mathrm{same\ degree}}
-
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r)_{\mathrm{lower}}.
}
\]

The same-degree piece has ordinary degree \(g+2\). The lower piece has ordinary degree \(g+1\), hence is one homogeneous grade lower.

In source-table language:

\[
\boxed{
X_h^{[g]}
=
X_{h,\mathrm{same}}^{[g]}
-
X_{\mathrm{lower}}^{[g-1]}.
}
\]

The lower piece has midpoint parity \((-1)^{g-1}\), not \((-1)^g\). That is the key obstruction.

---

## 2. Why the subset-complement cancellation fails for raw \(X_h\)

The amplitude cancellation relied on a labelled source multiset \(J\) with

\[
|J|=7.
\]

For the \(N_0\)-middle part, midpoint parity gives pair signs

\[
(-1)^{|J|-|I|}.
\]

Because \(|J|=7\) is odd, complementary subset terms have opposite signs and cancel after transpose projection.

With one raw \(X_h\)-insertion, the lower part has total grade

\[
|J|-1=6.
\]

Now the complementary subset signs are

\[
(-1)^{6-|I|}=(-1)^{|I|},
\]

so the two transpose-paired terms have the **same** sign. They add; they do not cancel.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{raw }X_h\text{ lower terms are not killed by the amplitude-part parity proof.}
}
\]

---

## 3. Same-degree derivative part

The same-degree part

\[
X_{h,\mathrm{same}}^{[g]}
\]

retains grade \(g\) and midpoint parity \((-1)^g\). Therefore it still has total grade \(7\) in the odd-transfer terms and is killed by the same subset-complement argument as the amplitude part.

So the odd-transfer \(X_h\) obstruction reduces only to the grade-lowered part:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal T_5(X^4,X_h)
\rightsquigarrow
-\mathcal T_5(X^4,X_{\mathrm{lower}}),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal T_7(X^6,X_h)
\rightsquigarrow
-\mathcal T_7(X^6,X_{\mathrm{lower}}).
}
\]

This is a useful reduction: only lower-shadow terms remain.

---

## 4. \(d=5\) raw \(X_h\)-lowered residual classes

The \(d=5\) amplitude partitions were:

\[
(1,1,1,1,3),
\qquad
(1,1,1,2,2).
\]

### From \((1,1,1,1,3)\)

Differentiating one grade \(1\) slot gives

\[
(0,1,1,1,3).
\]

Differentiating the grade \(3\) slot gives

\[
(1,1,1,1,2).
\]

So the first \(d=5\) lowered classes are:

\[
\boxed{(0,1,1,1,3)}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{(1,1,1,1,2)}.
\]

### From \((1,1,1,2,2)\)

Differentiating a grade \(1\) slot gives

\[
(0,1,1,2,2).
\]

Differentiating a grade \(2\) slot gives

\[
(1,1,1,1,2).
\]

So we also get:

\[
\boxed{(0,1,1,2,2)}
\]

and again

\[
\boxed{(1,1,1,1,2)}.
\]

The \(d=5\) lower-shadow residual table is therefore:

\[
\boxed{
(0,1,1,1,3),\quad
(0,1,1,2,2),\quad
(1,1,1,1,2).
}
\]

Since these have total grade \(6\), a \(z^7\) coefficient needs one extra ordinary order from:

- a next coefficient of one source input;
- \(N^{(0)}_1\);
- a higher inverse-square-root coefficient;
- a \(Y\)-middle coefficient one order above leading.

The draft does not provide a theorem that those order-\(+1\) corrections vanish.

---

## 5. \(d=7\) raw \(X_h\)-lowered residual class

The \(d=7\) amplitude partition is:

\[
(1,1,1,1,1,1,1).
\]

Differentiating any grade \(1\) slot gives:

\[
\boxed{(0,1,1,1,1,1,1)}.
\]

Again, total grade is \(6\), so a \(z^7\) coefficient requires one extra ordinary order from baseline/source corrections.

This is the first \(d=7\) lowered residual class.

---

## 6. Does the draft supply a covariant raw derivative?

The needed operator would be:

\[
\nabla_h X^{[g]}
=
\partial_hX^{[g]}
+
X_{\mathrm{lower}}^{[g-1]},
\]

so that

\[
\nabla_hX^{[g]}
=
X_{h,\mathrm{same}}^{[g]}
\]

and

\[
(\nabla_hX^{[g]})^+=(-1)^g(\nabla_hX^{[g]})^-.
\]

If such an operator existed at the raw source level, then the odd-transfer \(X_h\) lanes would close by the already-proved subset-complement parity argument.

But the draft’s midpoint trivialization and quotient-line connection live after fixed-sector extraction and edge normalization. The update note says not to use post-trivialization \(B_j[M]\) before edge divisibility is proved, because it double-counts the quotient-line connection. 

Therefore, no current raw-layer definition supplies

\[
\nabla_h.
\]

The source notes also identify the next target as proving the zero first-collision derivative / transfer-filtration theorem, not as already having a source-frame connection. 

---

The remaining \(X_h\)-lowered raw-edge targets are:

### \(d=5\)

\[
\boxed{
R_{5,01113}
=
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}\mathcal T_5
(X^{[0]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[3]})_{\mathrm{+1}}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{

=
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}\mathcal T_5
(X^{[0]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[2]},X^{[2]})_{\mathrm{+1}}
}
\]

\boxed{

=

\operatorname{Sym}\mathcal T_5
(X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[2]})_{\mathrm{+1}}
}
\]

Here the subscript \(\mathrm{+1}\) means “take the one-extra-order correction needed because the grade sum is \(6\).”

### \(d=7\)

\[
\boxed{
R_{7,0111111}
=
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}\mathcal T_7
(X^{[0]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]})_{\mathrm{+1}}.
}

These are the exact next raw Gate B residuals unless a covariant derivative is introduced.

## 8. The theorem needed now

There are two possible ways out.

### Option A: raw source-frame connection theorem

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Raw source-frame connection for Gate B]
There is a raw source-frame derivative \(\nabla_h\) on the homogeneous scalar
source input such that
\[
\nabla_hX^{[g]}
=
\partial_hX^{[g]}+X_{\mathrm{lower}}^{[g-1]},
\]
and
\[
(\nabla_hX^{[g]})^+=(-1)^g(\nabla_hX^{[g]})^-.
\]
Moreover the raw first-collision derivative of
\((1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}\) is computed using
\(\nabla_hX\), with the grade-lowering component absorbed into raw baseline
or lower-package edge data.
\end{theorem}
```

### Option B: raw edge invisibility of lowered \(X_h\)-terms

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Raw edge invisibility of \(X_h\)-lowered terms]
The fixed-sector coefficients
\[
R_{5,01113},\quad R_{5,01122},\quad R_{5,11112},\quad R_{7,0111111}
\]
all vanish through ordinary order \(7\).
\end{theorem}
```

## Claim

A formal covariant source derivative can be **defined**, but the current raw package does **not** use it. The raw first-collision derivative uses the actual midpoint motion

\[
h_1=h-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad h_2=h+\frac{\delta}{2},
\]

so it differentiates the moving homogeneous basis \((t-h)^{g+2}\). That raw derivative necessarily produces a grade-lowering term. The current draft/package definitions do not contain a raw-layer source-frame connection that subtracts this term before edge extraction.

Therefore the odd-transfer collision-motion lane remains live. The remaining residuals are the grade-lowered \(X_h\)-terms:

\[
R_{5,01113},\quad R_{5,01122},\quad R_{5,11112},\quad R_{7,0111111}.
\]

## Status: blocked

The covariant derivative exists as a possible **new definition/theorem**, but it is not the derivative currently used by the raw edge package. The package notes explicitly place midpoint trivialization and connection corrections downstream of the raw edge law; using post-trivialization \(B_j[M]\) before edge divisibility is proved would double-count the quotient-line connection. 

---

## Source-frame derivative calculation

The homogeneous scalar-grade source is

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_g r(h;t)
=
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2}.
\]

Differentiate with respect to the moving midpoint \(h\):

\[
\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r(h;t)
=
\frac{r^{(g+3)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2}
-
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+1)!}(t-h)^{g+1}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r
=
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r)_{\mathrm{same}}
+
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r)_{\mathrm{lower}},
}
\]

where

\[
\boxed{
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r)_{\mathrm{same}}
=
\frac{r^{(g+3)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2},
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r)_{\mathrm{lower}}
=
-
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+1)!}(t-h)^{g+1}.
}
\]

The same-grade part preserves the ordinary homogeneous grade \(g\). The lower part has ordinary grade \(g-1\).

At the midpoint endpoints

\[
t_\pm=h\pm \frac{z}{2Q^2},
\]

the same-grade part has parity \((-1)^g\) between \(+\) and \(-\), while the lower-grade part has parity \((-1)^{g-1}\). Therefore the lower part flips the parity convention needed for subset-complement cancellation.

---

## Covariant derivative construction or obstruction

A formal source-frame connection would be:

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r
:=
\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r
-
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r)_{\mathrm{lower}}
=
\frac{r^{(g+3)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2}.
}
\]

Equivalently, at the source-input level,

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_hX^{[g]}
=
\partial_hX^{[g]}+X_{\mathrm{lower}}^{[g-1]}.
}
\]

This construction removes the basis-motion term and keeps only the derivative of the source coefficient in the same homogeneous frame.

Then

\[
(\nabla_hX^{[g]})^+
=
(-1)^g(\nabla_hX^{[g]})^-.
\]

So the desired parity law would hold.

However, this is **not** currently the raw derivative of \(C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}\). The raw edge derivative is defined by differentiating

\[
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\left(a_1,h-\frac{\delta}{2};
-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),h+\frac{\delta}{2}\right)
\]

with respect to \(\delta\) at \(\delta=0\). That operation differentiates the actual endpoint-centered source data, including the moving basis term. The paper’s current package route identifies Gate B precisely as this raw first-collision edge law:

\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\,
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}=0.
\]

If this coefficient is nonzero, the amplitude-normalized object has a \(\delta^{-1}\)-pole and the downstream normalized package is not holomorphic. 

So the obstruction is:

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_h\text{ is a plausible new source-frame connection, but it is not yet part of }C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}.
}
\]

To use it, the paper must add a theorem saying the lower basis-motion term is subtracted by raw source-frame transport, baseline transport, or a lower-package counterterm **before** edge extraction.

---

## Parity proof if \(\nabla_h\) is adopted

Assume the raw package is redefined or proved equivalent to one using \(\nabla_h\). Then for a labelled source subset \(K\),

\[
(\nabla_hX_K)^+=(-1)^{|K|}(\nabla_hX_K)^-.
\]

For odd transfer degrees \(d=5,7\), the \(X_h\)-insertion term has the same total grade \(7\) after replacing \(X_h\) by \(\nabla_hX\). Then the subset-complement parity argument applies exactly as in the amplitude part:

- midpoint parity gives complementary signs because total grade is odd;
- all inverse-square-root and middle leading coefficients are symmetric;
- \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}\) is transpose-invariant.

Thus, if \(\nabla_h\) is legitimate at the raw layer, then

\[
\boxed{
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_5(X^4,\nabla_hX)=0,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_7(X^6,\nabla_hX)=0.
}
\]

---

Without the covariant replacement, the lower part of \(\partial_hX^{[g]}\) remains.

### \(d=5\)

The amplitude partitions are

\[

\qquad

\]

The grade-lowered raw derivative produces:

\[

\]

(1,1,1,1,2),

\[

\]

\boxed{

=

(X^{[0]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[3]})_{+1},
}
\]

\boxed{
R_{5,11112}
=
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}\mathcal T_5
(X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[2]})_{+1},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
R_{5,01122}
=

The subscript \(+1\) records that these lowered partitions have total grade \(6\), so one additional ordinary order must come from the next source coefficient, \(N^{(0)}_1\), a higher inverse-square-root coefficient, or a higher \(Y\)-middle coefficient.

\]

\operatorname{Sym}\mathcal T_7
(X^{[0]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]},X^{[1]})_{+1}.
}
\]

These terms are not killed by the amplitude-part proof because their total grade before the \(+1\) correction is even.

The theorem needed to close this lane is:

```tex id="y7g6v8"
\begin{theorem}[Raw source-frame connection for Gate B]
\label{thm:raw-source-frame-connection-gate-b}
There is a raw source-frame derivative \(\nabla_h\) on homogeneous scalar-grade
source inputs such that
\[
\nabla_hX^{[g]}
=
\partial_hX^{[g]}+X_{\mathrm{lower}}^{[g-1]},
\]
and
\[
(\nabla_hX^{[g]})^+=(-1)^g(\nabla_hX^{[g]})^-.
\]
Moreover, the raw first-collision derivative of
\[
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\]
is computed using \(\nabla_hX\), with the grade-lowering component of
\(\partial_hX\) absorbed into raw baseline/lower-package edge data.
\end{theorem}
```

```tex id="tc5ocs"
\begin{theorem}[Raw edge invisibility of \(X_h\)-lowered terms]

The fixed-sector coefficients
\[
R_{5,01113},\quad R_{5,01122},\quad R_{5,11112},\quad R_{7,0111111}
\]
vanish through ordinary order \(7\).
\end{theorem}
```

## Honest verdict

A covariant derivative can be defined formally:

\[
\nabla_hX^{[g]}=\partial_hX^{[g]}+X_{\mathrm{lower}}^{[g-1]}.
\]

It has the desired midpoint parity and would close the odd-transfer \(X_h\)-lanes by the same subset-complement cancellation.

But the current raw package uses the actual endpoint derivative, not this covariant derivative, and the draft does not contain a raw-layer mechanism that subtracts the lower basis-motion term before edge extraction. Therefore the \(X_h\)-lowered residuals remain live.

## Claim

The raw source-frame connection theorem is **not present in the current package**, and it cannot be used to close Gate B without changing the raw edge object.

A covariant derivative

\[
\nabla_hX^{[g]}
=
\partial_hX^{[g]}+X_{\downarrow}^{[g\to g-1]}
\]

can be defined formally, but the raw cross-effect

\[
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\]

uses the actual endpoint motion

\[
h_1=h-\frac{\delta}{2},
\qquad
h_2=h+\frac{\delta}{2},
\]

so it differentiates the moving homogeneous basis. That raw derivative includes the grade-lowering term. The current package layer puts midpoint trivialization and connection corrections **after** edge divisibility, not inside the raw source derivative. Using those downstream corrections here would be circular: if the \(\delta^1\) edge coefficient is nonzero, the normalized package has a \(\delta^{-1}\)-pole and the post-edge package is not yet holomorphic. 

## Status: blocked / theorem absent from current raw package

The parity-preserving derivative exists as a possible **new source-frame convention**, but it is not the derivative currently used by

\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}.
\]

So the \(X_h\)-lowered residuals remain live unless a new raw source-frame counterterm or raw edge-invisibility theorem is added.

---

## Source-frame derivative calculation

The homogeneous scalar-grade source is

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_g r(h;t)
=
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2}.
\]

Differentiate in the moving source frame:

\[
\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r
=
\frac{r^{(g+3)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2}
-
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+1)!}(t-h)^{g+1}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r
=
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r)_{\mathrm{same}}
+
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r)_{\mathrm{lower}},
}
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r)_{\mathrm{same}}
=
\frac{r^{(g+3)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2},
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r)_{\mathrm{lower}}
=
-
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+1)!}(t-h)^{g+1}.
}
\]

The lower term is not literally an independent \(\operatorname{Gr}_{g-1}r\) coefficient; it is a grade-\((g-1)\) shadow with coefficient inherited from \(r^{(g+2)}(h)\). Denote it by

\[
X_{\downarrow}^{[g\to g-1]}.
\]

At the two endpoints,

\[
t_\pm=h\pm\frac{z}{2Q^2},
\]

the same-grade term has midpoint parity \((-1)^g\), while the lowered term has parity \((-1)^{g-1}\). This parity flip is exactly why the odd-transfer collision-motion lane does not close by the amplitude-part subset-complement proof.

---

## Candidate covariant derivative

Define formally

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r
:=
\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r
-
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r)_{\mathrm{lower}}
=
\frac{r^{(g+3)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_hX^{[g]}
=
\partial_hX^{[g]}+X_{\downarrow}^{[g\to g-1]}.
}
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
(\nabla_hX^{[g]})^+=(-1)^g(\nabla_hX^{[g]})^-.
}
\]

So if the raw Gate B derivative were defined using \(\nabla_h\), the odd-transfer terms would close by the same subset-complement parity argument as the amplitude terms.

But the current raw package does not define this \(\nabla_h\). The source-bidegree and corrected package definitions keep the raw cross-effect first, then require edge divisibility before amplitude normalization, midpoint trivialization, and quotient connection are legitimate package operations. 

---

## Effect on \(\mathcal T_5\) and \(\mathcal T_7\)

The accepted universal first-collision formula has, for odd \(d\),

\[
F_{1,d}^{\mathrm{motion}}
=
d\,[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_d(X^{d-1},X_h).
\]

Split

\[
X_h=\nabla_hX-X_{\downarrow}.
\]

The \(\nabla_hX\) part has parity-preserving total grade \(7\) and cancels. The remaining raw obstruction is the lowered part:

\[
\boxed{
F_{1,d}^{\mathrm{lower}}
=
-d\,[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\mathcal T_d(X^{d-1},X_{\downarrow}).
}
\]

### \(d=5\)

The amplitude partitions are

\[
(1,1,1,1,3),
\qquad
(1,1,1,2,2).
\]

Lowering one slot gives these residual classes:

\[
\boxed{(0,1,1,1,3),}
\]

\[
\boxed{(1,1,1,1,2),}
\]

\[
\boxed{(0,1,1,2,2).}
\]

Because each has total grade \(6\), the \([z^7]\) coefficient requires one additional ordinary-order unit from the source coefficient, inverse-square-root table, \(N^{(0)}_1\), or \(Y\)-middle higher coefficient. They are not killed by the odd-total-grade parity argument.

### \(d=7\)

The amplitude partition is

\[
(1,1,1,1,1,1,1).
\]

Lowering one slot gives

\[
\boxed{(0,1,1,1,1,1,1).}
\]

Again, total grade is \(6\), so one additional ordinary order is required and the amplitude cancellation does not apply.

---

## Why no current raw-layer mechanism removes the lower term

Check the possible mechanisms:

### 1. Source-frame/trivialization choice

The representative-level midpoint trivialization acts on fixed-sector representatives after the package is already normalized/trivialized. It is not a raw source-frame connection inside \(C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}\). The notes explicitly warn not to use post-trivialization \(B_j[M]\) before edge divisibility is proved. 

### 2. Baseline transport

The current baseline transport is not stated as subtracting

\[
X_{\downarrow}^{[g\to g-1]}
\]

from the source input before raw edge extraction. Lower-shadow coefficients appear explicitly as tagged source-linear inputs in the finite source table, including \(X_{\varepsilon,0}^{2}\ne0\). 

### 3. Lower-package subtraction

No lower-package subtraction theorem is present. Earlier audit explicitly classified lower-shadow absorption as unproved under the current table.

### 4. Source-sector projection

\((1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}\) does not remove these lowered terms by itself. They remain mixed source-bidegree terms unless a source-bidegree quotient-compatibility theorem is proved. The audits say this compatibility theorem is still missing; applying projection after determinant or quotient extraction is invalid. turn147file18

### 5. Connection term in the collision chart

The quotient-line connection is a post-edge object. It corrects moving-to-midpoint quotient coordinates after the normalized edge package exists. It cannot be used to prove the raw edge divisibility needed for holomorphic normalization.

## Exact theorem needed

The raw-source-frame connection theorem would have to be added as a **new raw-layer theorem**:

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Raw source-frame connection for Gate B]
There is a raw source-frame derivative \(\nabla_h\) on homogeneous scalar-grade
source inputs such that
\[
\nabla_hX^{[g]}
=
\partial_hX^{[g]}+X_{\downarrow}^{[g\to g-1]},
\]
and
\[
(\nabla_hX^{[g]})^+=(-1)^g(\nabla_hX^{[g]})^-.
\]
Moreover, the raw first-collision derivative of
\[
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\]
is computed using \(\nabla_hX\), with the grade-lowering term
\(X_{\downarrow}^{[g\to g-1]}\) absorbed into raw baseline/lower-package edge
data before the \([z^7][\delta^1]\) fixed-sector extraction.
\end{theorem}
```

Without that theorem, the fallback is:

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Raw edge invisibility of lowered \(X_h\)-terms]
The fixed-sector coefficients
\[
R_{5,01113},\quad R_{5,01122},\quad R_{5,11112},\quad R_{7,0111111}
\]
vanish through ordinary order \(7\).
\end{theorem}
```

## Honest verdict

The covariant derivative

\[
\nabla_hX^{[g]}=\partial_hX^{[g]}+X_{\downarrow}^{[g\to g-1]}
\]

is mathematically natural, and it would restore the parity needed to close the odd-transfer \(X_h\)-insertion lanes.

But the current raw package does not use it. The lower term is part of the actual raw midpoint derivative. Therefore the theorem is blocked unless the paper adds a raw source-frame connection or proves raw edge invisibility for the lowered residuals.

## Claim

The grade-lowering \(X_h\) obstruction is not an irreducible new Fréchet obstruction. It is the **moving Taylor-frame connection** of the source tower.

If the raw source input is the full Taylor tower of a fixed scalar source \(r(t)\), then the grade-lowering term from \(\partial_hX^{[g]}\) cancels against the same-grade coefficient-derivative term from \(\partial_hX^{[g-1]}\). Thus the apparent residuals

\[
R_{5,01113},\quad R_{5,01122},\quad R_{5,11112},\quad R_{7,0111111}
\]

are killed by **telescoping across adjacent homogeneous grades**, not by Gate A and not by family-by-family gauge.

However, the current draft does **not yet state the required source-frame theorem**. To make the proof valid, the paper must assert that Gate B uses the full moving Taylor source tower, with the boundary modes handled:

1. the lower boundary \(g=-1\) is absent/absorbed by source normalization or baseline transport;
2. the upper boundary is not truncated at grade \(7\), because grade \(8\) can lower into order \(7\).

So the result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate B closes if the source-frame telescoping theorem is added.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Without that theorem, the }X_h\text{-lowered residuals remain live.}
}
\]

Status: **reduced to a precise source-frame telescoping theorem.**

---

## 1. Source-frame derivative calculation

The homogeneous scalar-grade piece is

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_g r(h;t)
=
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2}.
\]

Differentiate:

\[
\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r
=
\frac{r^{(g+3)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2}
-
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+1)!}(t-h)^{g+1}.
\]

The first term is the same-basis term coming from the next source coefficient. The second term is the grade-lowering basis-motion term.

Now compare adjacent grades. The same-basis term of grade \(g-1\) is

\[
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+1)!}(t-h)^{g+1}.
\]

The lowering term of grade \(g\) is

\[
-\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+1)!}(t-h)^{g+1}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_{g-1}r)_{\mathrm{same}}
+
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_{g}r)_{\mathrm{lower}}
=0.
}
\]

This is the core telescoping identity.

Equivalently, for the full Taylor tower,

\[
X_{\mathrm{full}}(h;t)
=
\sum_{g\ge0}X^{[g]}(h;t),
\]

one has

\[
\partial_hX_{\mathrm{full}}
=
\text{boundary terms only}.
\]

For the full untruncated Taylor expansion of a fixed source \(r(t)\), those boundary terms vanish. Thus the raw \(X_h\)-lowering terms are coordinate artifacts of splitting the source into homogeneous moving-basis pieces.

---

## 2. How this cancels the listed residuals

The \(X_h\)-lowered residuals previously isolated were:

\[
R_{5,01113},\quad R_{5,01122},\quad R_{5,11112},\quad R_{7,0111111}.
\]

They cancel against adjacent lower-shadow same-basis derivative terms.

### \(R_{5,01113}\)

This came from lowering a grade \(1\) slot in

\[
(1,1,1,1,3)
\]

to obtain

\[
(0,1,1,1,3).
\]

But the same monomial appears with the opposite sign from differentiating the grade \(0\) slot in the partition

\[
(0,1,1,1,3)
\]

through its same-basis coefficient derivative.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
R_{5,01113}^{\mathrm{lower}}
+
R_{5,01113}^{\mathrm{same\ from\ }0}
=0.
}
\]

### \(R_{5,01122}\)

This came from lowering a grade \(1\) slot in

\[
(1,1,1,2,2)
\]

to obtain

\[
(0,1,1,2,2).
\]

It cancels against the same-basis derivative of the grade \(0\) slot in

\[
(0,1,1,2,2).
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
R_{5,01122}^{\mathrm{lower}}
+
R_{5,01122}^{\mathrm{same\ from\ }0}
=0.
}
\]

### \(R_{5,11112}\)

This class has two sources.

First, lowering grade \(3\) in

\[
(1,1,1,1,3)
\]

gives

\[
(1,1,1,1,2).
\]

This cancels against the same-basis derivative of the grade \(2\) slot in

\[
(1,1,1,1,2).
\]

Second, lowering grade \(2\) in

\[
(1,1,1,2,2)
\]

also gives

\[
(1,1,1,1,2).
\]

This cancels against the same-basis derivative of the corresponding grade \(1\) slot in

\[
(1,1,1,1,2).
\]

The cancellation is coefficientwise after summing the symmetrized labelled source placements.

### \(R_{7,0111111}\)

This came from lowering one grade \(1\) slot in

\[
(1,1,1,1,1,1,1)
\]

to obtain

\[
(0,1,1,1,1,1,1).
\]

It cancels against the same-basis derivative of the grade \(0\) slot in

\[
(0,1,1,1,1,1,1).
\]

The same argument applies to all symmetrized labelled placements.

---

## 3. Boundary terms

The telescoping identity is exact for the full tower. At finite order \(7\), two boundary issues must be stated explicitly.

### Lower boundary \(g=0\)

The lowering term of grade \(0\) would be a grade \(-1\) mode:

\[
-\frac{r^{(2)}(h)}{1!}(t-h).
\]

This is not part of the homogeneous scalar-grade tower as currently defined. The theorem must therefore assume one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{grade }-1\text{ modes are killed by source normalization;}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{grade }-1\text{ modes are absorbed into baseline/coordinate transport;}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{grade }-1\text{ modes are raw-edge invisible through order }7.
}
\]

Without this, grade \(0\) lowering creates a new boundary lane.

### Upper boundary at grade \(8\)

To prove \([z^7]\) first-collision vanishing, one cannot truncate the source tower at grade \(7\). The same-basis derivative of grade \(7\) involves the coefficient \(r^{(10)}(h)\), and the lowering term of grade \(8\) can land in ordinary grade \(7\).

Thus the theorem must either include the full Taylor tower or at least include grade \(8\) for boundary cancellation at order \(7\).

So the correct finite-order statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Use the full moving Taylor source tower, then truncate only after applying }\partial_h.
}
\]

---

## 4. Relation to the current draft

The current finite source table already shows that lower shadows are live tagged source inputs, not baseline data:

\[
X_{\varepsilon,0}^{2}\ne0,\quad
X_{\varepsilon,1}^{2}\ne0,\quad
X_{\varepsilon,2}^{2}\ne0,\quad
X_{\varepsilon,2}^{4}\ne0.
\]

That means lower-shadow absorption is not currently available from the table. 

The draft/source notes also warn that source-weight linearization and quotient compatibility are still missing theorem layers, and that finite recurrences are not themselves quotient-gauge proofs. turn148file12

So the telescoping theorem must be added explicitly. It is not already implied by the existing Gate A closure.

---

## 5. The theorem that closes the \(X_h\)-lane

A paper-ready theorem would be:

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Moving homogeneous source-frame telescoping]
\label{thm:moving-homogeneous-source-frame-telescoping}
Let
\[
X_{\mathrm{full}}(h;t)
=
\sum_{g\ge0}X^{[g]}(h;t)
\]
be the full homogeneous scalar-grade expansion of a fixed source \(r(t)\) in
the moving midpoint frame.  Then
\[
\partial_hX_{\mathrm{full}}
\]
has no interior grade-lowering contribution: for every \(g\ge1\), the
grade-lowering component of \(\partial_hX^{[g]}\) cancels exactly with the
same-basis component of \(\partial_hX^{[g-1]}\).

Consequently, after symmetrized source summation, the raw Gate B
\(X_h\)-lowered classes
\[
(0,1,1,1,3),\quad
(0,1,1,2,2),\quad
(1,1,1,1,2),\quad
(0,1,1,1,1,1,1)
\]
cancel with their adjacent-grade source-frame partners.
\]
\end{theorem}
```

And it needs a boundary clause:

```tex
\begin{hypothesis}[Boundary modes for source-frame telescoping]
\label{hyp:source-frame-boundary-modes}
The grade \(-1\) boundary mode is absent by source normalization or absorbed
into baseline/coordinate transport, and the source tower is not truncated
before differentiating.  In particular, all grade \(8\) inputs needed to cancel
the order-\(7\) upper boundary are included before the final ordinary-order
truncation.
\end{hypothesis}
```

With these two additions, the odd-transfer \(X_h\)-lane closes.

---

## 6. Honest verdict

The raw \(X_h\)-lowered residuals are not genuine if the source is treated as a full moving Taylor tower. They are coordinate artifacts of differentiating a moving homogeneous basis and cancel by adjacent-grade telescoping.

But the current draft has not stated the source-frame telescoping theorem or the required boundary conditions. Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The obstruction is reduced to adding/proving the moving source-frame telescoping theorem.}
}
\]

Without that theorem, the residuals

\[
R_{5,01113},\quad R_{5,01122},\quad R_{5,11112},\quad R_{7,0111111}
\]

remain live.

## Assistant (2026-04-24 19:46:44)

## Claim

The moving homogeneous source-frame telescoping identity is correct in the interior grades:

\[
\boxed{
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_{g-1}r)_{\mathrm{same}}
+
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_{g}r)_{\mathrm{lower}}
=0
\qquad(g\ge1).
}
\]

This cancels the previously isolated \(X_h\)-lowered Gate B residual classes after symmetrized multilinear summation:

\[
R_{5,01113},\quad R_{5,01122},\quad R_{5,11112},\quad R_{7,0111111}.
\]

However, Gate B closes through order \(7\) only if the two boundary conventions are also imposed:

1. the grade \(-1\) boundary mode from lowering \(\operatorname{Gr}_0\) is absent or absorbed by source normalization / affine removal / baseline transport;
2. the full source tower is differentiated before truncation, so the grade \(8\) upper boundary is included and can telescope down into order \(7\).

With those boundary conventions, the raw \(X_h\)-lowered obstruction vanishes through order \(7\). Without them, the boundary modes remain live.

## Status

Interior telescoping: **proved**.

Multiplicity under \(\operatorname{Sym}\mathcal T_d\): **proved** by labelled-slot cancellation.

Gate B through order \(7\): **conditional on boundary conventions**.

---

## Derivative identity

Start with

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_g r(h;t)
=
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2}.
\]

Differentiate with respect to \(h\):

\[
\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r
=
\frac{r^{(g+3)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2}
-
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+1)!}(t-h)^{g+1}.
\]

Define

\[
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r)_{\mathrm{same}}
:=
\frac{r^{(g+3)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2},
\]

and

\[
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r)_{\mathrm{lower}}
:=
-
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+1)!}(t-h)^{g+1}.
\]

Now compute the same-grade part of the previous grade:

\[
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_{g-1}r)_{\mathrm{same}}
=
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+1)!}(t-h)^{g+1}.
\]

Therefore

\[
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_{g-1}r)_{\mathrm{same}}
+
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_{g}r)_{\mathrm{lower}}
=
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+1)!}(t-h)^{g+1}
-
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+1)!}(t-h)^{g+1}
=0.
\]

So the signs and factorials match exactly.

Equivalently, for every interior grade \(g\ge1\),

\[
\boxed{
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_{g}r)_{\mathrm{lower}}
=
-(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_{g-1}r)_{\mathrm{same}}.
}
\]

---

## Cancellation of the listed residuals

The raw \(X_h\)-lowered residuals arose because the lower part of \(\partial_hX^{[g]}\) changes grade \(g\mapsto g-1\). The telescoping identity says each such lowered term is canceled by the same-grade derivative of the adjacent lower grade.

### \(R_{5,01113}\)

This residual came from lowering a grade \(1\) slot in

\[
(1,1,1,1,3)
\]

to

\[
(0,1,1,1,3).
\]

For a labelled slot \(s\), the lowered contribution is

\[
(\partial_hX_s^{[1]})_{\mathrm{lower}}.
\]

The adjacent same-grade contribution is

\[
(\partial_hX_s^{[0]})_{\mathrm{same}}.
\]

The identity with \(g=1\) gives

\[
(\partial_hX_s^{[0]})_{\mathrm{same}}
+
(\partial_hX_s^{[1]})_{\mathrm{lower}}
=0.
\]

Therefore the labelled contribution to

\[
(0,1,1,1,3)
\]

cancels slotwise.

### \(R_{5,01122}\)

This came from lowering a grade \(1\) slot in

\[
(1,1,1,2,2)
\]

to

\[
(0,1,1,2,2).
\]

Again, for every labelled grade \(1\) slot,

\[
(\partial_hX_s^{[0]})_{\mathrm{same}}
+
(\partial_hX_s^{[1]})_{\mathrm{lower}}
=0.
\]

Hence \(R_{5,01122}\) cancels slotwise.

### \(R_{5,11112}\)

There are two sources.

First, lowering grade \(3\) in

\[
(1,1,1,1,3)
\]

produces

\[
(1,1,1,1,2).
\]

The adjacent identity with \(g=3\) gives

\[
(\partial_hX_s^{[2]})_{\mathrm{same}}
+
(\partial_hX_s^{[3]})_{\mathrm{lower}}
=0.
\]

Second, lowering grade \(2\) in

\[
(1,1,1,2,2)
\]

also produces

\[
(1,1,1,1,2).
\]

The adjacent identity with \(g=2\) gives

\[
(\partial_hX_s^{[1]})_{\mathrm{same}}
+
(\partial_hX_s^{[2]})_{\mathrm{lower}}
=0.
\]

So both labelled sources of the \((1,1,1,1,2)\) residual cancel with their adjacent-grade partners.

### \(R_{7,0111111}\)

This came from lowering one grade \(1\) slot in

\[
(1,1,1,1,1,1,1)
\]

to

\[
(0,1,1,1,1,1,1).
\]

Again,

\[
(\partial_hX_s^{[0]})_{\mathrm{same}}
+
(\partial_hX_s^{[1]})_{\mathrm{lower}}
=0
\]

for each labelled slot. Hence \(R_{7,0111111}\) cancels slotwise.

---

## Multiplicity audit

The cancellation survives symmetrization because it is **labelled-slot local**.

Let

\[
\operatorname{Sym}\mathcal T_d(X_{g_1},\ldots,X_{g_d})
\]

be the symmetrized multilinear sum over labelled slots. Fix one labelled slot \(s\). In that slot, the pair

\[
(\partial_hX_s^{[g-1]})_{\mathrm{same}}
\]

and

\[
(\partial_hX_s^{[g]})_{\mathrm{lower}}
\]

enter the same multilinear operator with the same remaining labelled inputs and the same symmetrization weight. Their coefficients are exactly opposite by the derivative identity.

Thus cancellation happens before collecting unlabelled multiplicities. There is no hidden binomial mismatch.

For example, in \((1,1,1,1,3)\), lowering any one of the four labelled grade \(1\) slots gives four labelled contributions to \((0,1,1,1,3)\). The same four labelled contributions arise from the same-grade derivative of the corresponding four grade \(0\) slots in the adjacent-grade tower. Each labelled pair cancels individually.

Likewise, for the grade \(3\to2\) lowering in \((1,1,1,1,3)\), there is one labelled grade \(3\) slot and one corresponding adjacent grade \(2\) same-basis contribution. They cancel with multiplicity one.

So the symmetrized \(\mathcal T_d\) expansion preserves the telescoping cancellation exactly.

---

## Lower-boundary audit

The telescoping identity requires \(g\ge1\). At \(g=0\), lowering gives a grade \(-1\) mode:

\[
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_0 r)_{\mathrm{lower}}
=
-\frac{r^{(2)}(h)}{1!}(t-h).
\]

There is no \(\operatorname{Gr}_{-1}\) in the defined tower

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_g r=\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2},
\qquad g\ge0.
\]

Therefore the lower boundary is not automatically canceled by adjacent-grade telescoping.

To close Gate B, the paper needs one of the following boundary conventions:

\[
\boxed{
\text{grade }-1\text{ is absent by source normalization;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{grade }-1\text{ is absorbed into affine/source-coordinate transport;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{grade }-1\text{ is part of baseline transport and not an independent source input;}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{all grade }-1\text{ boundary terms are raw-edge invisible through order }7.
}
\]

This is a real remaining hypothesis. It cannot be skipped if grade \(0\) is live.

In many Taylor-source setups, this is plausible because constant and affine source modes are coordinate/normalization modes, not genuine curvature-source perturbations. But the draft must state it.

---

## Upper-boundary audit

For order \(7\), the full source tower must be differentiated before truncating.

Reason: the lower part of grade \(8\) lands in grade \(7\):

\[
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_8 r)_{\mathrm{lower}}
=
-\frac{r^{(10)}(h)}{9!}(t-h)^9,
\]

which is ordinary grade \(7\) in the \(g\)-indexing convention.

This cancels the same-basis derivative of grade \(7\):

\[
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_7 r)_{\mathrm{same}}
=
\frac{r^{(10)}(h)}{9!}(t-h)^9.
\]

So if one truncates the source tower at grade \(7\) before differentiating, a spurious upper-boundary residual remains.

The correct convention is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{differentiate the full Taylor source tower first, then truncate to ordinary order }7.
}
\]

With this convention, the upper boundary through order \(7\) cancels.

---

## Final Gate B implication

The moving source-frame telescoping theorem closes the \(X_h\)-lowered interior residuals:

\[
R_{5,01113},\quad
R_{5,01122},\quad
R_{5,11112},\quad
R_{7,0111111}.
\]

It closes them exactly at raw edge level, before \(\Phi_K\), determinant scalarization, or quotienting.

Gate B then closes through order \(7\) **provided**:

1. Gate A remains closed, as accepted;
2. amplitude total-grade \(7\) terms close by subset-complement parity, as accepted;
3. same-grade \(X_h\) terms close by the same parity, as accepted;
4. moving source-frame telescoping is applied to the full source tower before truncation;
5. the grade \(-1\) lower boundary is absent/absorbed/raw-edge invisible.

Under these conditions,

\[
\boxed{
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}=0.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
=
O(a_1\delta^2)
}
\]

through ordinary order \(7\) in fixed sector.

---

## Honest verdict

The interior telescoping theorem is proved with exact signs and factorials.

The only remaining caveat is the lower boundary \(g=0\to -1\). If the paper states that affine/source-coordinate modes are normalized away or absorbed into baseline transport, then Gate B closes through order \(7\). If not, the grade \(-1\) boundary remains a live residual lane.

## Claim

The interior moving-source telescoping is proved, but the **lower boundary is not explicitly closed in the current draft**.

The grade \(-1\) mode is the affine source-coordinate mode

\[
(t-h).
\]

The homogeneous scalar-grade convention starts at

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_0 r=\frac{r^{(2)}(h)}{2!}(t-h)^2,
\]

so constant and affine modes are **not included as independent source grades**. That strongly suggests the intended convention is: constant and affine modes are normalized away / coordinate-gauge modes. However, I do **not** find a stated raw-edge theorem saying the affine boundary term produced by differentiating \(\operatorname{Gr}_0\) is removed before

\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}.
\]

So Gate B closes through order \(7\) **only after adding a boundary-mode hypothesis/theorem**.

## Status: reduced / conditional

Interior telescoping: proved.

Upper boundary: closes if the full Taylor tower is differentiated before truncation.

Lower boundary \(g=0\to -1\): requires an explicit convention or theorem.

---

## Derivative identity

Start with

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_g r(h;t)
=
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2}.
\]

Then

\[
\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r
=
\frac{r^{(g+3)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2}
-
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+1)!}(t-h)^{g+1}.
\]

Thus:

\[
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r)_{\mathrm{same}}
=
\frac{r^{(g+3)}(h)}{(g+2)!}(t-h)^{g+2},
\]

and

\[
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_g r)_{\mathrm{lower}}
=
-\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+1)!}(t-h)^{g+1}.
\]

For \(g\ge1\),

\[
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_{g-1} r)_{\mathrm{same}}
=
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(h)}{(g+1)!}(t-h)^{g+1}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_{g-1}r)_{\mathrm{same}}
+
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_{g}r)_{\mathrm{lower}}
=0
\qquad(g\ge1).
}
\]

The signs and factorials match exactly.

---

## Lower-boundary audit

For \(g=0\),

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_0 r(h;t)=\frac{r^{(2)}(h)}{2!}(t-h)^2.
\]

Its lower component is

\[
\boxed{
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_0 r)_{\mathrm{lower}}
=
-r^{(2)}(h)(t-h).
}
\]

This is a degree-one affine mode.

There is no grade \(-1\) in the active tower, because the draft’s homogeneous scalar-grade convention begins at the second derivative:

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_a r
=
\frac{r^{(a+2)}(m)}{(a+2)!}(t-m)^{a+2}.
\]

Thus grade \(-1\) would correspond to

\[
\frac{r^{(1)}(h)}{1!}(t-h),
\]

which is outside the displayed source tower. 

### What grade \(-1\) represents

It is the affine source-coordinate mode. It should be treated as one of:

1. a normalized-away source mode;
2. a coordinate-frame mode;
3. baseline transport;
4. raw-edge invisible affine gauge.

But the current draft material I can cite does not explicitly prove any of these at raw edge level. The package notes identify Gate B as the raw edge-divisibility theorem and warn that if the \(\delta^1\) raw edge coefficient is nonzero, the normalized package has a pole; they also warn not to use post-trivialization connection tables before edge divisibility is proved. turn150file10

So the lower boundary is not automatically closed by the existing source-grade definition. It needs an explicit boundary-mode statement.

---

## Raw edge relevance

Even though grade \(-1\) is outside the source sector, it is produced by differentiating a live grade \(0\) source mode.

The finite source table shows grade \(0\)-type lower-shadow entries are live as tagged source inputs; for example,

\[
X_{\varepsilon,0}^{2}=\frac{1}{24\pi}(I-D)\ne0.
\]

So the \(g=0\) boundary cannot be dismissed merely by saying “grade \(-1\) is not an independent source.” The derivative of a live grade \(0\) term produces it. 

To close Gate B at raw edge level, the paper must prove that this affine boundary contribution does not enter

\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\]

as a live mixed source term.

---

## Upper-boundary audit

The upper boundary is conceptually cleaner.

For order \(7\), the same-grade part of \(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_7\) is canceled by the lowering part of \(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_8\). So the source tower must be differentiated before truncation.

If one truncates at grade \(7\) first, then

\[
(\partial_h\operatorname{Gr}_7 r)_{\mathrm{same}}
\]

is left uncanceled.

Therefore the correct convention is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Differentiate the full moving Taylor tower first, then truncate to ordinary order }7.
}
\]

The draft’s \(\operatorname{Gr}_a\) definition is not inherently finite in \(a\), so this convention is natural. But the finite coefficient contracts must state it explicitly, otherwise agents may truncate too early.

---

## Boundary theorem needed

The exact hypothesis/theorem needed is:

```tex
\begin{hypothesis}[Boundary modes for moving source-frame telescoping]
\label{hyp:boundary-modes-moving-source-frame-telescoping}
The grade \(-1\) boundary mode produced by lowering
\[
\operatorname{Gr}_0 r=\frac{r^{(2)}(h)}{2!}(t-h)^2
\]
under the raw midpoint derivative,
\[
-r^{(2)}(h)(t-h),
\]
is absent by source normalization, affine removal, baseline transport, or
raw-edge invisibility.  Equivalently, affine source-coordinate modes contribute
no non-\((1,1)\) fixed-sector \([z^7][\delta^1]\) term to
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}.
\]
The source tower is differentiated before ordinary-order truncation; in
particular, grade \(8\) is included when proving ordinary order \(7\)
cancellation, and truncation is applied only after \(\partial_h\).
\end{hypothesis}
```

A theorem version would be:

```tex
\begin{theorem}[Affine boundary raw-edge invisibility]
\label{thm:affine-boundary-raw-edge-invisibility}
Affine boundary modes generated by the lowering of \(\operatorname{Gr}_0\)
under the raw midpoint derivative vanish in the Gate B edge coefficient:
\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
\big|_{\operatorname{Gr}_{-1}\text{ boundary}}=0.
\]
\end{theorem}
```

1. Gate A is closed.

3. Same-grade \(X_h\) terms close by parity.

}

through ordinary order \(7\) in fixed sector.

Without the boundary hypothesis, the affine \(\operatorname{Gr}_{-1}\) lane remains the final live Gate B residual.
